Chose "Save Offline" over the suggested "Sync to Storage" because the one button does both legs — OneDrive export *and* a verified local offline pin — and "Save Offline" names the outcome a user cares about (works with no network); the export leg still reports "exported to OneDrive ✓". Behavior is unchanged. (3) **The Saturday rule is scoped** in CLAUDE.md: active from the day Brandon starts preaching/working from Ledgr (flip to be tracked here), inactive during build-out.
**Why / alternatives:** Keeping "Pulpit Ready" rejected (the principle is explicit, and the name leaks one use case into a general tool). A literal "Sync to Storage" rejected as inaccurate for the offline-pin leg. Deleting the Saturday rule outright rejected — it's correct once live; it just hasn't started applying yet.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; 23/23 `verify-print.mts` still green (renderer untouched beyond a comment); full `next build` clean. No grep hits for the old name in `src/` user-facing strings.
**Affects:** `src/components/canvas/SaveOffline.tsx` (renamed from `PulpitReady.tsx`), `ItemCanvas.tsx`, comments in `print-html.ts`/`items/[id]/print`/`api/export`/`markdown.ts`/`public/sw.js`/`verify-print.mts`, CLAUDE.md (two working-conventions rules).

## ADR-029: View builder — stored View Definitions with five layout renderers; the filter/sort/grouping jsonb shapes are the same ones the list pages already use
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Slice 27 (PRD §4.2/§4.9), the foundation the embedded views (28) and dashboard (29) build on. The `views` table and the `ViewFilter`/`ViewSort` shapes existed since Phase 1; this turns them into user-built, saved, multi-layout views.
**Decision:** (1) **A view's `filter`/`sort`/`grouping` jsonb store exactly the existing `ViewFilter`/`ViewSort` shapes** plus a new `ViewGrouping` (`{field}` over status/urgency/kind/type/due); `layout` and `date_property` are real columns. So a stored view runs through the same owner-scoped, body-free `viewItemsQuery` as the hardcoded list pages — no second query path. (2) **Hand-rolled validation** (`parseViewInput`, rule 5): unknown filter keys are dropped not rejected (an old client can't wedge a save); calendar/agenda default `dateProperty` to `dueDate`. (3) **One `ViewRenderer` server component dispatches by layout** — list, table, board (columns grouped by the group field, known enums ordered first), calendar (month grid for the current month; out-of-month/undated counted), agenda (day-bucketed sections). Task rows carry the shared check-off control. (4) **CRUD store is owner-scoped; `is_system` views reject edit/delete** (none seeded yet — the hardcoded list pages stay as-is for now). (5) Builder is a client form posting the whole definition; option lists are duplicated as plain arrays so it never imports the DB-backed module.
**Why / alternatives:** Seeding the list pages as system views now rejected — deferred to keep the slice tight; the seam is ready. A per-layout query rejected — the layouts are presentations of one row set. Month-navigation on the calendar deferred (current month only) — enough to prove the layout.
**Verification:** 25/25 in `scripts/verify-views.mts` against live Neon — parse/validate (bad layout/status/entityId/grouping rejected, unknown keys dropped, name trimmed), CRUD round-trip, owner scoping (other owner gets not_found), system-view immutability, and that the view query still carries `owner_id` and selects no body. `tsc` + `next build` clean.
**Affects:** `src/lib/views.ts` (types, validation, store, `viewWhere` refactor), `src/app/api/views/route.ts` + `[id]/route.ts`, `src/app/views/` (index, `[id]`, `[id]/edit`, `new`), `src/components/views/ViewRenderer.tsx` + `ViewBuilder.tsx`, `src/lib/nav.ts` (Views slot), `scripts/verify-views.mts`.

## ADR-030: Embedded query views are an interactive panel on an entity; remove = un-relate, create inherits the relation, check-off edits in place
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Slice 28 (PRD §4.9): the four embedded-view behaviors — editable filter, inline check-off, create-inherits-filters, remove = un-relate. Where they live and what "remove" means had to be pinned down.
**Decision:** (1) **The embedded view mounts on an entity canvas** and runs a filter pinned to items related to that host (confirmed relations, either direction — the existing `entityId` filter). This is the actionable surface for a 1:1 prep (success criterion). (2) **A shared `GET /api/items/query`** runs a `ViewFilter`+sort and returns body-free rows, so the panel (and the dashboard) can refetch after an inline edit without a full reload. (3) **The four behaviors:** filter selects (type/status/due) refetch in place; a task checkbox PATCHes status optimistically and drops the row if it leaves an active status filter; **"+ Add" creates an item of the filtered type and relates it to the host** (so it lands in the view — create-inherits); **"remove" un-relates** the host↔item edge (DELETE relations) and never deletes the item. (4) Kept alongside the existing `RelatedPanel` (backlinks/overview), not replacing it — different jobs.
**Why / alternatives:** Embedding a saved View Definition by reference (storing where each view is embedded) rejected for v1 — heavier plumbing; the standalone entity panel delivers the behaviors now and shares the same filter language. "Remove = soft-delete the item" rejected — un-relate is the PRD's meaning and is non-destructive.
**Verification:** 7/7 in `scripts/verify-embedded-views.mts` against Neon — created+related task appears in the host view, unrelated stays out, status toggle moves it across the status filter, un-relate drops it while the item survives. `tsc` + `next build` clean. In-browser interaction check pending (mirrors slice 24's posture).
**Affects:** `src/app/api/items/query/route.ts` (new), `src/components/views/EmbeddedView.tsx` (new), `src/components/canvas/ItemCanvas.tsx` (mount on entities).

## ADR-031: Widget dashboard — `views.dashboard_order` is the whole config (nullable = pinned + position); native drag-reorder, no DnD library
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Slice 29 (PRD §4.11): drag-and-drop View-Definition cards, item-count badges, content-driven heights with an equal-height option, fill-screen desktop / vertical-scroll mobile. Needed a place to store the dashboard config and a DnD approach that respects the few-dependencies rule.
**Decision:** (1) **A single nullable `views.dashboard_order` integer column is the entire dashboard config** (migration 0005): null = not a widget, a number = grid position. No separate dashboard table — one dashboard per owner in v1, and the config naturally rides the view it shows, owner-scoped. (2) **Native HTML5 drag-and-drop** (draggable + dragOver/drop), no library (rule 5); a drop persists the new order via `PUT /api/dashboard`. (3) **Badge count is `countViewItems`, sharing `viewWhere` with the list** so the number can never disagree with the view; cards show a capped preview (8) with a "+N more" link. (4) **Equal-height is a display preference in localStorage**, not server state — off = content height, on = uniform scrollable cards. (5) **A distinct `/dashboard` route**, not a rebuild of the Phase 1 Today home — pin/unpin from the view detail page; linked from Today and the Views index.
**Why / alternatives:** A `dashboards` table rejected for v1 (one per user; the column is simpler and still multi-user-ready). A DnD library (dnd-kit) rejected (rule 5; native suffices for a small grid, and mobile is scroll-only per the PRD). Replacing the Today home now rejected — the working Phase 1 home stays; merging the dashboard into it is a later call.
**Verification:** 9/9 in `scripts/verify-dashboard.mts` against Neon — pin adds in order, re-pin is a no-op, reorder persists, unpin removes (other fields survive), and the count is the true total independent of the preview limit. Migration 0005 applied to Neon. `tsc` + `next build` clean. In-browser drag check pending.
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (+`dashboard_order`), `drizzle/0005_*`, `src/lib/views.ts` (count, dashboard fns), `src/app/api/dashboard/route.ts` (new), `src/app/dashboard/page.tsx` (new), `src/components/views/DashboardGrid.tsx` + `PinButton.tsx` (new), `src/app/views/[id]/page.tsx` + `src/app/page.tsx` + `src/app/views/page.tsx` (links), `scripts/verify-dashboard.mts`.

## ADR-032: A view's date filter names which date it applies to (default due date, or a meeting's "When"), and adds a within-N-days range
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Review feedback on slices 27/28: a meeting view could only filter by due date, but meetings have no due date — they have "When" (`meeting_at`). So "meetings today" was impossible. Separately, the date window was a fixed preset dropdown; Brandon wanted a range ("meetings in the next N days").
**Decision:** (1) **`ViewFilter` gains `dateField`** (`dueDate` | `meetingAt` | `createdAt` | `updatedAt`, default `dueDate`); the window applies to that column. The day-boundary semantics follow the field: due dates are UTC-midnight calendar days (ADR-008), the timestamp fields use real timezone midnights — the same split `today.ts` already makes, reused via `todayBounds` + `zonedMidnightUtc`. So "overdue" on a meeting means "in the past", "today"/"week"/"none" work on `meeting_at`. (2) **`ViewFilter` gains `withinDays`** (integer 1–366): the window becomes today through today+N (exclusive), winning over `due` when both are set. The existing "week" preset is exactly `withinDays = 7`. (3) **The builder UI** pairs a date-field select with the window select (which gains a "next N days…" option revealing a number input) and **auto-switches the date field to "When" when the type is set to meeting**, so "meetings today" is one obvious path. (4) **The embedded view** derives `dateField` from the selected type (meeting → `meetingAt`), so its window works for meetings too. Backward compatible: the tasks list and everything sending only `due` keep dueDate behavior.
**Why / alternatives:** A separate `meetingDue`-style filter rejected — one date-window concept with a field selector is simpler and generalizes to created/updated. A full arbitrary from/to date-range picker deferred — `withinDays` covers the asked-for case ("next N days") with one number; calendar-range pickers can come if a real need appears (noted, not built).
**Verification:** `verify-views.mts` extended (now 33 checks, all green): meetingAt today/week/withinDays windows include/exclude the right meetings, the default dueDate field correctly *misses* meetings with no due date (the bug, now scoped away), bad `dateField`/`withinDays` rejected, `withinDays` string coerces to a number, and the generated SQL targets `meeting_at`. `tsc` clean.
**Affects:** `src/lib/views.ts` (ViewFilter, `viewWhere` date branch, `parseViewFilter`), `src/app/api/items/query/route.ts`, `src/components/views/ViewBuilder.tsx`, `src/components/views/EmbeddedView.tsx`, `scripts/verify-views.mts`. Also a clarifying hint on the meeting "Agenda" section (`MeetingPrep.tsx`) and two parked explorations (`block-linked-action-items.md`, `dashboard-widgets.md`) for the deferred review items.

## ADR-033: The builder only offers fields a view's type actually has; changing the type reconciles every "by which field" pick
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Follow-up to ADR-032. Brandon hit it live: a calendar view of meetings let him pick "due date" as the placement field, so it rendered blank (meetings have no due date). His point — a bad option shouldn't be offered in the first place; the choice lists should reflect what the view displays.
**Decision:** **Field choices are derived from the selected type, not fixed.** `dateFieldsFor(type)` (task→[dueDate,created,updated]; meeting→[meetingAt,created,updated]; note/link/entity→[created,updated]; any→all) drives the filter date field, the sort field, and the calendar/agenda placement field. `groupFieldsFor(type)` drops urgency + due window for non-tasks (ADR-018) and kind for non-entities. The Urgency and Entity-kind filters hide entirely for types they don't apply to. **Selecting a type reconciles every current pick** to a valid one (a meeting view's placement snaps from due date to "When"). On load, a stored definition's now-invalid picks are clamped the same way, so opening a legacy meeting calendar in the editor and saving repairs it. The server `parseViewInput` also defaults a calendar/agenda's `dateProperty` by type (meeting → `meetingAt`). Principle for future selects: **option lists update based on what the view is displaying.**
**Why / alternatives:** Leaving all fields always-offered + a runtime fallback (place meetings by When even if "due date" is chosen) rejected — it masks a nonsensical choice instead of removing it; Brandon explicitly wanted the option gone. A hard validation error on save rejected — worse UX than simply not offering the field.
**Verification:** Browser-verified with the dev auth stand-in: on a new view, selecting Type=meeting + Layout=calendar removed "due date" from the filter date field, the sort field, and the placement field (all defaulting to "When"), and hid Urgency + Entity kind; creating it rendered the meetings on the correct calendar days (the previously-blank case). `verify-views.mts` adds the meeting-calendar default check (34 checks green); `tsc` + `next build` clean. A one-off check confirmed no stored meeting calendar/agenda views still held `dueDate`.
**Affects:** `src/components/views/ViewBuilder.tsx` (type-aware field lists + `changeType` reconciliation + on-load clamping), `src/lib/views.ts` (`parseViewInput` type-aware `dateProperty` default), `scripts/verify-views.mts`.

## ADR-034: Push notifications — Web Push hand-rolled over node:crypto behind a PushSender; daily agenda on Vercel cron, hourly prep on GitHub Actions
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Slice 30 (PRD §4.5/§4.11): web push for the morning agenda summary and meeting-prep-ready notices (task *reminders* stay Todoist's job). Web Push needs a VAPID keypair, a subscriptions store, a service-worker push handler, and message encryption (RFC 8291). The obvious move is the `web-push` npm package; rule 5 says justify it.
**Decision:** (1) **Hand-rolled over `node:crypto`, no dependency.** The whole protocol is in `node:crypto`: VAPID is an ES256 JWT (`src/lib/push/vapid.ts`), and message encryption is ECDH-P256 + HKDF-SHA256 + AES-128-GCM per RFC 8291/8188 (`src/lib/push/encrypt.ts`). This matches every prior boring-crypto call (hand-rolled HMAC for the Todoist webhook, the PNG icon encoder, the markdown/print serializers, `aws4fetch` over the AWS SDK) and keeps the dep count flat. The risk — fiddly crypto that fails silently — is bought down by a **round-trip self-test** in `verify-push.mts`: encrypt to a freshly generated subscription, decrypt from its side, assert the plaintext matches; plus a VAPID JWT signed then verified with the public key. (2) **A `PushSender` interface** (`WebPushSender` in prod; a stub in verification) — same provider discipline as `CalendarSource`/`MailSource`/`TodoistClient`/`ExportTarget`. `getWebPushSender()` returns null when VAPID keys are unset (the "not configured" path, like Graph/Todoist). (3) **VAPID keys live in env** (`VAPID_PUBLIC_KEY`/`VAPID_PRIVATE_KEY`/`VAPID_SUBJECT`), generated once by `scripts/make-vapid-keys.mjs`; the public key is also the browser's `applicationServerKey`, served at runtime by `GET /api/push` (no `NEXT_PUBLIC_` rebuild needed). (4) **`push_subscriptions` table** (migration 0006), owner-scoped, unique on `endpoint`; subscribe is an idempotent upsert, and a push-service **Gone (404/410) prunes the row** so the table self-heals. (5) **Two triggers, one send path.** The morning agenda is a deterministic count summary (no model — rule 3; the AI-assembled agenda is Phase 3) built from `getTodayData`, sent once/day with a day-guard, on the **Vercel daily cron** (`/api/machine/notify-agenda`, 11:00 UTC ≈ 7am ET — Hobby supports daily). Meeting-prep-ready notifies each meeting coming due within a 2h window **that has a confirmed related entity** (so there's prep worth opening), once per meeting via a `properties.notify.prepNotifiedAt` stamp, on an **hourly GitHub Actions** poll (`/api/machine/notify-prep`) — sub-daily, so it uses the same cron-token door as calendar/email. (6) **SW v3** gains `push` (renders `{title,body,url,tag}`) and `notificationclick` (focus-or-open the url) handlers; it still never touches any cache. (7) `/health` gains `lastAgendaNotifyAt`/`lastPrepNotifyAt` canaries. (8) A `PushToggle` on Today enables/disables for the current browser; renders nothing when push is unsupported/unconfigured (delivery needs the prod-registered SW).
**Why / alternatives:** `web-push` rejected on rule 5 (a dependency + transitive tree to do what `node:crypto` already does, verifiable by round-trip). Inline send-on-save rejected (the existing sync pattern is batched/cron-driven; notifications aren't latency-critical). Notifying every upcoming meeting rejected as noisy — the confirmed-entity gate is the "prep is meaningful" signal. Storing notified meeting ids in `job_state` rejected for the per-item flag (bounded, no growth). Putting the daily agenda on GitHub Actions rejected — Vercel cron does daily natively; only the sub-daily prep poll needs Actions.
**Verification:** 25/25 in `scripts/verify-push.mts` against Neon under a throwaway owner with a stub sender — VAPID keygen shape, JWT sign+verify (and tamper-fails), the **RFC 8291 encryption round-trip**, store CRUD (upsert, unsubscribe), send-and-prune of a Gone endpoint, the agenda day-guard (second same-day run skips), prep gating (in-window+entity notified; no-entity / out-of-window / canceled skipped; re-run doesn't re-notify), and owner scoping. `tsc --noEmit` clean; full `next build` clean (new routes compile). Live end-to-end (a real browser subscription + a delivered notification) is a Brandon-step once VAPID keys are set (runbook §1e).
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (+`push_subscriptions`), `drizzle/0006_*`, `src/lib/push/` (types, vapid, encrypt, web-push, store, notify, owner — new), `src/app/api/push/route.ts` + `subscribe/route.ts`, `src/app/api/machine/notify-agenda/` + `notify-prep/`, `src/components/pwa/PushToggle.tsx`, `src/app/page.tsx`, `public/sw.js` (v3), `src/app/health/route.ts`, `vercel.json`, `.github/workflows/notify-prep.yml`, `scripts/make-vapid-keys.mjs`, `.env.example`, runbook §§1e, 2, 2a, `scripts/verify-push.mts`.

## ADR-035: Public share links — unguessable token → the shared print render; revocation is a stamp; the print document shell is now shared
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Slice 31 (PRD §4.12, a named Notion pain point): read-only, print-friendly, PDF-downloadable public links. The PRD says they're "statically rendered/cached" (§6.5). Open: what the public path renders, how revocation works against caching, and avoiding a second renderer.
**Decision:** (1) **One render, reused.** The self-contained document shell (inline CSS, dark on screen / black-on-white in print, the Print/PDF button) moved from the Save Offline print route into `renderPrintDocument()` in `print-html.ts`; both the owner's `/items/[id]/print` and the public `/share/[token]` call it, so a pinned offline copy and a shared link are byte-identical renders. The share page adds a small "Shared from Ledgr · read-only" footer (dropped under `@media print`). Mentions already render as plain names (no `ledgr://` nav), so a shared page leaks no path into the owner's data. (2) **`share_tokens` table** (migration 0007): an unguessable 24-byte base64url `token` (~192 bits, the same security posture as the machine tokens) maps to one item. Issuance is owner-scoped and mints a fresh token each call; **revocation is a `revoked_at` stamp, not a delete** (auditable, and a revoked string can't be silently reissued). Cascade-deletes with the item at purge. (3) **The public path takes no Clerk** (`/share(.*)` joins the public-route set in `proxy.ts`, alongside the Todoist webhook); the token is the credential. `resolveShareToken` joins token→item in one query so it only yields a live token on a live item — a revoked token or trashed item is a plain 404. **Issuance/listing/revocation (`/api/items/[id]/share`) stays Clerk-protected.** (4) **Caching vs revocation:** the render sets `public, s-maxage=60, stale-while-revalidate=300` — cacheable at the CDN (PRD §6.5, cheap origin) but revocation propagates within ~60s at the edge and is immediate at the origin. Plus `X-Robots-Tag: noindex` and `Referrer-Policy: no-referrer` so a shared link doesn't leak into search or referrers. (5) A `ShareLink` control on every canvas (beside Save Offline) creates/copies/revokes links; the client builds the absolute URL from the returned token (env-agnostic).
**Why / alternatives:** A separate share renderer rejected (forking the print render; extracting the shell unifies them). Revoke-as-delete rejected (loses history; the stamp also blocks reissue races). Long CDN cache rejected (revocation is a security property; 60s is the balance the PRD's "cached" intent allows). Embedding owner-scoped checks on the public path rejected — there's no session; the token + live-item join is the boundary. Storing the share URL base in env rejected (the client knows its own origin).
**Verification:** 18/18 in `scripts/verify-share.mts` against Neon under a throwaway owner — issuance, public resolve (token→item+body), the shared render (full HTML doc, body HTML-escaped, the read-only footer), listing, independent tokens, revocation (then resolves null) + idempotent re-revoke, trashed-item protection, unknown token → null, and owner scoping (a non-owner can't share/list/revoke, and a foreign revoke attempt leaves the link live). `verify-print.mts` still 23/23 after the shell extraction; `tsc` + full `next build` clean.
**Affects:** `src/lib/print-html.ts` (`renderPrintDocument` + shared CSS), `src/app/items/[id]/print/route.ts` (refactored onto it), `src/db/schema.ts` (+`share_tokens`), `drizzle/0007_*`, `src/lib/share.ts` (new), `src/app/share/[token]/route.ts` (new, public), `src/app/api/items/[id]/share/route.ts` (new), `src/proxy.ts` (public route), `src/components/canvas/ShareLink.tsx` (new) + `ItemCanvas.tsx`, `scripts/verify-share.mts`.

## ADR-036: Provider-interface discipline confirmed for auth + scheduler; enforced by a static seam guard
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Slice 32 (roadmap Phase 2 close): confirm the Phase-4 seams hold — auth behind an interface, the scheduler as authenticated endpoints a local cron could call — "mostly an audit + any gaps." The three embedded cloud deps (auth/Clerk, storage/R2, scheduler) and the DB (Drizzle) need to be a packaging change in Phase 4, not a rewrite.
**Decision:** The audit found **no gaps requiring code changes — the seams hold** — so the deliverable is the confirmation plus an *enforceable* guard rather than prose that rots. (1) **Auth:** `@clerk/nextjs` is imported in exactly four files — the provider implementation (`lib/auth/clerk.ts`), its React wrapper (`lib/auth/provider.tsx`), the middleware (`proxy.ts`), and the sign-in page. Every route/component/lib reaches identity only through `authProvider.getCurrentUser()` / `resolveOwner` / `requireOwner`. A Phase-4 local single-user provider is a ~10-line `localAuthProvider` selected in the one switch point (`lib/auth/index.ts`); the dev stand-in already proves that shape. (2) **Scheduler:** every scheduled job (Vercel crons: purge/export/notify-agenda; GitHub Actions: calendar/todoist/email/notify-prep/backup) triggers an authenticated `GET /api/machine/*` with a cron-scoped machine token. The scheduler is interchangeable because the *contract* is "authenticated HTTP call to a machine endpoint" — a local cron runs the identical `curl`. All 9 machine endpoints verify a token. (3) **Storage** is already behind `StorageProvider` (`aws4fetch`/R2 confined to `src/lib/storage/`); **DB** is portable via a Drizzle connection-string change (the pooler guard exempts local Postgres, ADR-002). (4) **The guard:** `scripts/verify-provider-seams.mts` statically asserts (a) only the four auth-seam files import Clerk, (b) only `src/lib/storage` imports the R2 client, (c) every `/api/machine` route calls `verifyMachineToken`, and (d) all Vercel crons target `/api/machine`. It fails loudly if a future file breaks a boundary — turning the discipline into a check, not a hope. Documented in a new runbook "Phase 4 readiness" section (§8).
**Why / alternatives:** A prose-only audit rejected — it goes stale the next time someone adds a route; the static guard is the same posture as the rest of the verify suite. Building the Phase-4 local providers now rejected — Phase 4 is gated/exploratory (roadmap), and the point of this slice is to prove the *shape* is ready, which the guard does without shipping unused code.
**Verification:** 8/8 in `scripts/verify-provider-seams.mts` — Clerk confined to 4 seam files, the `AuthProvider` interface + single selector + `resolveOwner`-through-the-interface present, R2 client confined to the storage seam, the `StorageProvider` interface present, all 9 machine endpoints token-gated, and all Vercel crons targeting `/api/machine`. No code changes were needed; the seams already held.
**Affects:** `scripts/verify-provider-seams.mts` (new), runbook §8 (Phase 4 readiness). No source changes (audit confirmed the existing seams).

## ADR-037: The Markdown epoch — Markdown-canonical body, bespoke-first types, per-type canvas, two-builder model
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted — **the turning point. Supersedes the body-format and "Notion-default" decisions of PRD §10 and revises ADR-006 (serializer role) and ADR-007 (single canvas).** Marked by git tag `v0.17-blocknote-canonical` (last pre-pivot commit), PRD bumped to v0.18 "Markdown epoch," and a GitHub Release.
**Context:** A long Brandon↔Tyler conversation (notes processed 2026-06-13) reframed the foundation while it's still cheap to change. Three things converged: (1) Brandon wants to write sermons with colors *and* keep papers/songs in a portable, multi-output format; (2) Tyler is joining as a co-builder whose modules (Papers, Songs, Sermons, Discipleship) are markdown/ChordPro-native and whose Savor app already proves the tiptap→markdown pattern in production; (3) the v0.17 decision made **BlockNote JSON canonical** precisely because plain markdown can't hold sermon colors — but an *extended* markdown can (inline HTML for colors, Pandoc footnotes/superscripts/citations for papers, ChordPro for songs). The realization: the color objection that drove BlockNote-canonical dissolves once "markdown" means "extended markdown," and one canonical format then serves everyone, making Tyler's PR-#1 "multiple canonical formats per type" question moot.
**Decision:**
1. **Markdown is the canonical body format.** `items.body` stores `{format, text}` (still jsonb, no column-type migration): `format: "markdown"` by default (an extended dialect — CommonMark/GFM + Pandoc features + inline HTML `<mark>`/`<span>` for colors/highlights), with markdown-family formats like `chordpro` allowed per type. The markdown `text` is the source of truth; the Word/`.docx` (pandoc), chord chart, slides, and Save-Offline print/PDF all **render from** it — never a second stored source. `body_text` for FTS becomes a light markdown-syntax strip rather than a JSON walk.
2. **The editor is a markdown-native WYSIWYG surface** (renders rich, not raw, with a likely source/preview toggle). Library is TBD (tiptap / Milkdown / Lexical with markdown serialization; BlockNote demoted from canonical-definer to a mere candidate). The polished "Notion feel" (slash menu, block drag) is wanted but **not a v1 requirement** — the accepted cost of a durable, greppable, multi-output base. Revisit later, or adopt an existing lib.
3. **Bespoke-first, one catch-all** (supersedes Principle 8 "Notion-default"). Each content type is designed with the features it needs; most are Tier-3 (PRD §3.7). Tier 2 collapses toward a **single customizable catch-all** for the temporary tail; a catch-all use that recurs is **promoted** to a permanent bespoke type via Claude Code.
4. **A content type may declare its own canvas** (PRD §4.13, revised). Songs get a chord editor, papers a workspace with a quote-bank sidebar; a type without one gets the default markdown canvas. The "no item dead-ends in a bare row" promise holds.
5. **Contributed workflow modules, per-instance.** A module = a type + its canvas + exporters + optional integration, packaged to **register onto** core rather than reach into it. Build module boundaries clean now so per-user enable/disable is a later config flip (**module-ready, not a marketplace** — the analog of "multi-user-ready, not multi-user").
6. **Two-builder model + a core-change contract.** Ledgr is now built by Brandon and Tyler on one shared codebase, each deploying their own single-tenant instance. Changes to **core** (data model, the body-format contract, the type/canvas model, the module boundary, the provider interfaces, the cross-cutting invariants, the MCP/API contract, the nine principles) need both-agree + an ADR; everything else moves fast solo. `COLLAB.md` holds rotating availability/plan notes (defined in CLAUDE.md). *(This first pivot was Brandon-directed and committed straight to main; the both-agree-via-PR process is the going-forward norm for subsequent core changes.)*
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep BlockNote-canonical* (status quo): rejected — makes papers/songs second-class and forces Tyler's "two canonical formats" complexity. *Per-type canonical format* (Tyler's PR-#1 proposal — BlockNote for some types, markdown for others): rejected as more complex than needed once extended-markdown proves rich enough for sermons; one base format with per-type editors/canvases is cleaner. *Do it later:* rejected — this reverses a shipped decision and touches the serializer, FTS extraction, print renderer, and email-in; foundation phase is the cheap moment, after more types build on it is expensive. The real cost accepted: losing BlockNote's turnkey Notion-like block UX until it's rebuilt or a library is adopted.
**Affects (docs, this pass):** CLAUDE.md (Principle 6, editor/body line, new "Building together" + core definition), `ledgr-prd.md` (v0.18 banner + §1, §3.1, §3.7, §4.1, §4.13, §6.1, §10, §12), `schema.md` (`body`/`body_text`/revisions/FTS), `README.md`, `roadmap.md`, `next_steps.md`, `explorations/block-linked-action-items.md`, `explorations/local-first-split.md`, new `COLLAB.md`. **Code impact (next, not yet done):** `src/lib/markdown.ts` (invert: parse/serialize markdown as source), `body` read/write to `{format, text}`, `body_text` extraction, the editor component, the print/export renderers fed from markdown. To be scoped as its own slice.

## ADR-038: Markdown-native editor — adopt Tiptap with the first-party `@tiptap/markdown` extension
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** **accepted** (2026-06-13) — CORE decision, **both-agree satisfied: Brandon recommended, Tyler agreed** (CLAUDE.md "Building together"). M2 (stand-up + round-trip proof) is now unblocked.
**Context:** Roadmap Phase M, slice **M1 — editor selection**. ADR-037 made Markdown the canonical body format and left the editor library TBD (Tiptap / Milkdown / Lexical), with a stated lean toward Tiptap. M1's job is to pick one against concrete criteria and record why; the actual stand-up + round-trip proof is M2. The editor must preserve what the v0.17 BlockNote path already does and the markdown serializer (`src/lib/markdown.ts`) already emits:
- **Lossless markdown round-trip** (type → markdown → reload → identical), because markdown is now the source of truth, not a derived export.
- **Color/highlight marks** that serialize to the pinned inline-HTML encoding in `src/lib/colors.ts` — `<span style="color:…">` for text color and `<mark class="hl-<name>" style="background-color:…">` for highlight (9 Notion-palette colors). This inline-HTML-in-markdown choice is *why* sermon colors survived the pivot (ADR-037); the editor must reproduce it exactly.
- **`@`-mention** as the markdown link the serializer already produces: `[@Title](ledgr://item/<uuid>)`. The mention carries `{itemId, title}`; `src/lib/mentions.ts` diffs these out of the saved body into `relations` rows (role `mention`) on every save, so the editor's mention node must expose a stable item id.
- **Lazy-load + bundle discipline** (Principle 8 / PRD §6.4): the editor already loads only through `LazyEditor` (code-split, client-only) and must keep doing so.
- **A credible path to the later "Notion feel"** (slash menu, block drag — wanted, explicitly *not* a v1 requirement per ADR-037) and to Obsidian-style `^block-id` anchors (a Phase-3 feature, `explorations/block-linked-action-items.md`; M1 only keeps the door open).
**Decision:** Adopt **Tiptap** (ProseMirror under a maintained React API) with its **first-party `@tiptap/markdown` extension** as the markdown-native canvas, replacing BlockNote when M2–M4 land. Rationale on each criterion:
1. **Round-trip:** `@tiptap/markdown` is *bidirectional* and round-trip-tested (parse markdown → Tiptap JSON → serialize back), driven via `setContent(md, {contentType:'markdown'})` / `editor.getMarkdown()`. It is now first-party (not the older community `tiptap-markdown`), which is the Principle-5 maintenance answer.
2. **Color marks:** custom marks define a `renderMarkdown(node, helpers)` hook that returns an arbitrary string, so a `textColor`/`highlight` mark emits our exact `colors.ts` inline-HTML verbatim, with a matching `parseMarkdown` handler for the reverse. **This is the one genuinely bespoke piece** — round-trip of custom marks needs the matching parse handler or it's lossy. Bounded and known; proven in M2.
3. **Mentions:** Tiptap ships an official `Mention` extension (the `@`-suggestion UX is off-the-shelf); we give it an `itemId` attribute and a `renderMarkdown` that emits `[@Title](ledgr://item/<id>)`, so `mentions.ts` keeps working unchanged.
4. **Bundle:** headless + tree-shakeable extensions, stays behind `LazyEditor`.
5. **Notion-feel + block anchors:** Tiptap has *official* slash-command (suggestion), drag-handle, and node-id extensions — the clearest off-the-shelf path to the deferred polish, and node ids are the natural seat for `^block-id` later.
6. **Team fit (decisive):** Tiptap is **Savor-proven in Tyler's production app** for the exact Tiptap→markdown pattern, so the largest unknown (custom-mark round-trip) is already walked by a co-builder, and it's the stack he brings to the Papers/Songs modules.
**Why / alternatives:** **Milkdown** — *technically the purest fit*: it's markdown-native by construction (a remark AST *is* its document model), so lossless round-trip is inherent rather than an add-on. Rejected as the pick, not on capability but on ecosystem and fit: bare-bones React integration (hand-built UI for menus/handles), a smaller ecosystem to lean on (Principle 5), and no in-house production proof — against Tiptap's larger ecosystem, off-the-shelf slash/drag/mention extensions, and Tyler's Savor track record. Kept as the documented runner-up: if Tiptap's custom-mark round-trip proves uglier than expected in M2, Milkdown's native-markdown model is the fallback. **Lexical** (Meta) — fastest/lightest and great for huge docs, but markdown is an import/export transform layer, *not* the canonical model, so it's the weakest fit for "markdown is the source of truth," and its lower-level API means more code for the same result with no offsetting team familiarity. Rejected.
**Verification:** None yet — this is a recommendation, deliberately code-free (M1 is "spike + ADR"; the lean was already Tiptap and Savor is the de-facto spike). The proof is **M2**: stand the editor up on a scratch route reading/writing `{format:"markdown", text}` and verify type → markdown → reload → identical with colors and mentions intact, the same bar `verify-print` (23/23) holds for the render side. **This ADR does not flip to `accepted` until Tyler agrees** (core-change contract).
**Affects:** none yet (no code). When accepted and built (M2–M4): adds `@tiptap/*` + `@tiptap/markdown` deps, replaces `src/components/editor/` (`Editor.tsx`, `schema.tsx`, mention node), retires `@blocknote/*`; `src/lib/markdown.ts` inverts into the M4 migration tool; `src/lib/colors.ts` and `src/lib/mentions.ts` are preserved contracts the new marks/mention node must honor.

## ADR-039: Alpha/build-phase posture — no production data, so the markdown cutover goes direct (M3+M4 collapse), not staged
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed build-pacing call). Not a change to the core body-format/type contract (ADR-037 stands), so it doesn't itself need both-agree; it does re-scope shared roadmap Phase M, so Tyler is flagged in `COLLAB.md`.
**Context:** The Phase M slices (M1–M6) were ordered so "the app keeps working after each one," and M4 carried a careful data migration (dry-run on a DB copy, eyeball sermon colors before flipping, keep the BlockNote read path alive in parallel until then). Brandon clarified the premise that drove that caution is false right now: **Ledgr is pre-production (alpha / build phase) — not in real Sunday/daily use, no real user data.** The careful-migration machinery protects a running tool and real content that don't exist yet. The stated goal is to get fully onto the new (Tiptap/markdown) stack and keep building features cleanly and efficiently.
**Decision:**
1. **Declare an explicit project status: ALPHA / build phase, pre-production.** No production data; data-loss, careful-migration, and backward-compatibility concerns are **suspended** until a tracked flip to **v1.0 production**. Recorded as a status callout at the top of CLAUDE.md. The flip is the *same gate* as the existing "no Saturday deploys once Ledgr is in real Sunday use" rule — when it happens, record it in this log, update the CLAUDE.md line, and migration caution applies from then on.
2. **The markdown cutover goes direct.** Drop the "keep the app working in parallel / no BlockNote removal until a careful migration" constraint. **Collapse M3 + M4 into one cutover slice (new M3):** repoint the renderers (print `src/lib/print-html.ts`, OneDrive export, FTS `body_text`) to markdown; wire the Tiptap editor (built in M2) into the real `ItemEditor`/`ItemCanvas`, replacing BlockNote; switch `items.body` read/write to the `{format:"markdown", text}` contract; rework `src/lib/mentions.ts` to extract `ledgr://item/<id>` from markdown instead of walking JSON; update email-in to write markdown (trivial, already plain text); **convert existing dev bodies best-effort via the proven `src/lib/markdown.ts` serializer, or just reseed — no DB-copy dry run, no eyeball gate**; uninstall `@blocknote/*` and delete `src/components/editor/`. After this slice BlockNote is gone and markdown is the only path. **M5** (per-type canvas seam) and **M6** (module registration boundary) are unchanged.
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep the staged, data-safe plan* — rejected as premature ceremony: it spends effort guarding data and a parallel BlockNote path that don't matter pre-production, against Brandon's explicit "build cleanly and efficiently." *Wipe and reseed instead of converting* — allowed and equivalent under this posture; convert-via-serializer is kept as the default only because it's already written and free, not because the data is precious.
**Affects:** CLAUDE.md (new status callout), `roadmap.md` (Phase M intro + M3/M4 → one cutover slice), `next_steps.md` (turning-point + queue rescope), `COLLAB.md` (Tyler heads-up). No source changes in this ADR; the cutover itself is the next build slice.

## ADR-040: M3 executed — Markdown is the only body path; markdown-it for server render; dev data wiped, not migrated; BlockNote fully removed
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted. Implements the already-agreed core decisions (ADR-037 body format, ADR-038 Tiptap, ADR-039 direct cutover), so it is execution, not a new core decision. The one genuinely new piece — a server-side markdown-rendering dependency (markdown-it) — is a non-core renderer/Principle-5 call (the roadmap pre-authorized "one vetted markdown lib"); **flagged to Tyler in COLLAB** because it sets the core markdown→HTML path the modules will share.
**Context:** Roadmap **Phase M slice M3** (the merged M3+M4 cutover, ADR-039). M2 stood the Tiptap editor up in isolation; M3 makes markdown the only path: repoint every renderer/reader/writer off BlockNote JSON and onto the `{format,text}` markdown body, then delete BlockNote.
**Decision:**
1. **Body contract → `{format,text}`.** New `src/lib/body.ts` owns the shape: `makeMarkdownBody(text)`, `isItemBody(x)`, and the tolerant `bodyMarkdown(x)` (extracts `.text`, degrades null/foreign to `""`). `items.body` / `revisions.body` stay **jsonb** — no column migration, the shape just changed inside. Every reader/writer goes through `body.ts`.
2. **Server render via markdown-it** (new `src/lib/markdown-render.ts`). One `markdown-it` instance, `html:true` (passes the editor's `<span style>`/`<mark class>` color HTML through), with one token-rewrite core rule that (a) shifts body headings down one level so the document title keeps `<h1>`, and (b) renders `ledgr://item/<id>` links as `<span class="mention">` (a `ledgr://` URI is meaningless on paper/a public link). Exports `markdownToHtml` (print/share) and `markdownToText` (render-then-strip for the FTS `body_text`). **Server-only** — never imported by a client component, so the editor bundle never pays for it. markdown-it is the **one vetted markdown dependency** (Principle 5): single synchronous package, battle-tested; chosen over remark (multi-package, async) for simplicity.
3. **Readers switched:** `print-html.ts` keeps the self-contained document shell + CSS (added `th`) and now renders the body via `markdownToHtml(bodyMarkdown(body))` (the BlockNote JSON walker is gone); `export/engine.ts` emits `bodyMarkdown(item.body)` directly (the body *is* the markdown); `body-text.ts` → `markdownToText(bodyMarkdown(body))`; `mentions.ts` → `collectMentionIdsFromMarkdown` (regex for the `ledgr://item/<id>` href) instead of walking JSON.
4. **Writers switched:** `parseItemPayload` accepts a `{format,text}` object (or null) and rejects the old block array; `ItemEditor` moved to `src/components/markdown-editor/` and wired to `LazyMarkdownEditor` (reads `bodyMarkdown(item.body)`, writes `makeMarkdownBody(markdown)`); email-in emits markdown (`emailToMarkdown`, light inline-escaping).
5. **Data: wiped, not migrated (Brandon's in-session call).** ADR-039 pre-authorized "wipe or convert"; I first converted, Brandon directed **wipe and start fresh** (alpha, nothing to protect). All 30 dev items deleted (cascades cleared relations/revisions/attachments/share_tokens); users + types kept. Because there is no data to migrate, the BlockNote→markdown serializer (`src/lib/markdown.ts`) and the migration script were **deleted, not kept as a tool** — removing the last BlockNote vestige.
6. **BlockNote retired:** `@blocknote/core|mantine|react` uninstalled; `src/components/editor/` deleted; the stale `.bn-root`/`.ledgr-mention` rules dropped from `globals.css` (the editor carries its own CSS).
7. **Security note recorded:** `html:true` is safe under Ledgr's single-trusted-author model (Save Offline is owner-only; a share link publishes the owner's own content; no other user's data exists on an instance). Revisit with a sanitizer only if Ledgr ever renders content authored by someone other than the viewer's owner.
**Side fix (pre-existing, surfaced here):** the OneDrive export engine stamped `exportedAt: new Date()` while the schema's `updatedAt.$onUpdate` set a *second* `new Date()` microseconds later in the same UPDATE, so `needsExportWhere`'s `updatedAt > exportedAt` was true on a millisecond boundary → a spurious re-export on the next run (flaky, ~40% in `verify-export`). Confirmed flaky on pre-M3 code too. Fixed by pinning both stamps to one instant (`set({ exportedAt: now, updatedAt: now, … })`); `verify-export` now 5/5 green.
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep `markdown.ts` as a migration tool* — rejected once Brandon chose wipe: with no data to migrate it is dead BlockNote code, against "start from scratch." *remark instead of markdown-it* — markdown-it is the simpler single synchronous package for a string→string server render. *Sanitize the HTML* — deferred under the single-author model (Principle 5; the editor only ever emits the safe color HTML).
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; full `next build` clean (all routes, incl. `/items/[id]`, `/items/[id]/print`, `/share/[token]`). **24/24 verify scripts green** — rewrote `verify-print` (markdown→HTML), added `verify-body-contract` (the `{format,text}` contract + FTS strip + markdown mention scan), and updated the BlockNote-body fixtures in `verify-editor`/`verify-email-in`/`verify-lists-search`/`verify-items`/`verify-relations`/`verify-share`/`verify-export` to markdown. **In-browser (dev stand-in):** the share render shows the heading shift, color span, `<mark>` highlight, mention-as-flat-name (no `ledgr://` leak), code block, and GFM table with no console errors; the real canvas mounts the Tiptap editor over a `{format,text}` body (toolbar, colors, highlight, mention chip), and a live browser edit autosaved back as `{format,text}` markdown with `body_text` reindexed — heading syntax and color HTML intact through the round-trip.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/body.ts`, `src/lib/markdown-render.ts`; rewritten `src/lib/print-html.ts`, `src/lib/body-text.ts`, `src/lib/mentions.ts`, `src/lib/email/html.ts`; edited `src/lib/api.ts`, `src/lib/export/engine.ts`, `src/lib/email/sync.ts`, `src/db/schema.ts` (comments), `src/app/globals.css`, `src/lib/editor/mention-markdown.ts` (+`collectMentionIdsFromMarkdown`); moved `ItemEditor.tsx` into `src/components/markdown-editor/` + `ItemCanvas.tsx` import; **deleted** `src/components/editor/`, `src/lib/markdown.ts`; `package.json` (−`@blocknote/*`, +`markdown-it`/`@types/markdown-it`); verify scripts as above.

## ADR-041: M5 — the per-type canvas seam (a type may declare its own canvas; shell/canvas split, default = markdown)
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted. **Implements the per-type-canvas pivot ADR-037 already decided with both-agree** ("bespoke-first with per-type canvases"), so the *capability* isn't a new core decision — this ADR records its concrete, minimal shape. Tyler's PR #1 (`ty-additions/FOR-BRANDON-approach-diff.md`, decision #2) names "a system type may declare its own canvas component" as the single most important thing to agree on; ADR-037 said yes. The **registration API** is deliberately *not* finalized here — that's M6, co-designed with the first real module (Papers). Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md` since the seam's shape is shared core.
**Context:** Roadmap **Phase M slice M5**, the platform hook the Songs/Papers modules need. Before this, `ItemCanvas` was one server component that loaded the item *and* hardcoded the whole rendering, branching inline per type (`task` → Subtasks, `meeting` → MeetingPrep, `entity` → EmbeddedView) — so the only way a module could get a chord grid or a paper workspace was to edit that shared file. The seam has to let a type render through its *own* canvas while everything without one keeps the markdown canvas unchanged (PRD §4.13 / ADR-037: "types without a canvas get the default markdown canvas"). Scope per the roadmap: ship **default-only plus one trivial proof**, not the full module API.
**Decision:**
1. **Shell / canvas split.** `src/components/canvas/ItemCanvas.tsx` is now a thin **shell**: it owns the universal frame — owner check, item load, trash/`notFound` guards, and the ancestor breadcrumb — then resolves the type's canvas and renders `<Canvas item ownerId variant />`. Everything type-specific moved out.
2. **The default canvas.** `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` is the markdown canvas (the markdown editor + the type's standard panels + the backlinks panel + Save Offline + Share + the collapsed Fields section) — a near-verbatim extraction of the old `ItemCanvas` body. Every type without a registered canvas renders through it, so the default experience is unchanged.
3. **Policy split from wiring (for testability).** `src/lib/canvas-registry.ts` is the **pure policy** half — `canvasIdForType(type)` returns a canvas id, defaulting to `"markdown"`; it imports no components (only `import type`), so it resolves identically on the server and in a plain-node verify script. The **wiring** half (canvas id → React component) is a small `Record` in the shell, with a `?? MarkdownCanvas` fallback so a policy/wiring drift can't crash the page. This mirrors how a module will later *declare* `{type → canvas}` (policy) and *provide* the component (wiring) — so the split is M6-shaped, not throwaway.
4. **The one trivial proof: `link`.** `src/components/canvas/LinkCanvas.tsx` registers for the `link` type — it foregrounds the URL as a click-through chip, then composes `<MarkdownCanvas/>` underneath. It exercises the seam (a non-default canvas renders for one type) and demonstrates the exact pattern a real module canvas follows: add a bespoke surface, reuse the standard canvas. Removing the `link` entry from the registry drops links straight back to the default — nothing else depends on it.
5. **Footer-fields extracted + pinned.** The collapsed Fields section's logic moved from `ItemCanvas` into a pure `footerFieldsFor(item)` in `src/lib/canvas-fields.ts` (beside `topStripFields`), so the extraction is one testable place and the ADR-018 "due/urgency are task-only, even on legacy rows" invariant is asserted by a test, not just prose.
**Why / alternatives:** *Thin shell (canvas owns everything visual incl. Related/Share/Fields)* — rejected for M5: maximum module freedom, but every custom canvas would re-implement or forget the cross-cutting chrome. *Thick shell (canvas = only the body editor)* — too restrictive; a chord grid needs to replace more than the editor. The chosen middle — **the canvas is the whole type-specific surface; the shell is load + guards + breadcrumb; shared chrome is composed, not duplicated** — matches Tyler's "canvas = the type's editing UI" and keeps the default DRY (LinkCanvas just wraps the default). *One combined registry returning components* — rejected because importing it would drag the editor bundle into the verify script; the policy/wiring split keeps the policy pure and testable. *Finalize the module-registration API now* — deferred to M6 by the roadmap ("build it to fit the path actually walked," with Papers), so M5 stays a minimal, reversible seam.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; full `next build` clean (all routes compile, incl. `/items/[id]`). New `scripts/verify-canvas-seam.mts` **16/16** — `canvasIdForType` (`link` → its own canvas; `note`/`task`/`meeting`/`entity`/unknown/empty → default) and `footerFieldsFor` (bare note = Type/Created/Updated only; a note with legacy due/urgency still hides them — ADR-018; task/link/entity keep their distinguishing field in the strip, not the footer). No existing verify script imports the touched modules, so no regression surface. **In-browser (dev stand-in, auth-stub):** the `link` item renders the URL chip above the title with the full default canvas beneath it (editor toolbar, URL field strip, Related, Save Offline, Share, Fields), and a `note` renders through the unchanged default canvas (no chip, markdown headings/lists/rules intact) — zero console errors on both.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/canvas-registry.ts`, `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx`, `src/components/canvas/LinkCanvas.tsx`, `scripts/verify-canvas-seam.mts`; edited `src/lib/canvas-fields.ts` (+`footerFieldsFor`/`FooterField`), `src/components/canvas/ItemCanvas.tsx` (slimmed to the shell + canvas wiring); `.claude/launch.json` (`autoPort: true` on the dev config, so the preview server coexists with a manual dev server). No schema/DB change, no new dependency. **Next: M6 — the module-registration boundary**, built with the Papers module, which turns the hardcoded wiring `Record` into a module contributing its `{type, canvas, exporters, integration}`.

## ADR-042: The foundational build delivers the module *capability*, not the modules themselves
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed scope clarification). Reaffirms Principles 6–7 and the "module internals are not core — move fast, solo" line in CLAUDE.md "Building together," so it sets no new core contract; it sharpens the existing one. Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md` since he owns the modules.
**Context:** Phase M (the foundation rework) ends with M5 (the per-type canvas seam, done — ADR-041) and M6 (the module-registration boundary). M6 was framed in the roadmap as "build alongside the first real module (Papers)," which risked reading as "ship Papers as part of the foundation." Brandon clarified the intent while clicking through the app: **adding modules (Papers, Songs, Sermons/Lessons, Discipleship, …) is NOT part of the foundational/core build.** The foundation's job is to make the architecture such that modules can be added later and fit cleanly.
**Decision:** The foundational/core build (Phase M) delivers the **capability** for modules to plug in — the per-type canvas seam (M5) and the module-registration boundary (M6: a module contributes its `{type, canvas, exporters, integration}` onto core, per-user enable a later flip). It does **not** include building the modules themselves. M6 is *informed by* the real module specs (Tyler's PR #1, esp. Papers) and proven with a minimal reference registration so the seam is exercised, but Papers/Songs/etc. are **post-foundation, non-core work** built on top of the finished capability (mostly Tyler's lane; "module internals — move fast, solo"). **Phase M is "done" when the slots exist and are proven, not when any module ships.** This preserves the "fit the path actually walked" wisdom (ADR-037) by *designing M6 against* a real spec, not by *shipping* a module inside the foundation.
**Why / alternatives:** *Couple M6 completion to shipping Papers* — rejected as scope creep into a module during foundation, and it would stall the core on a specific module's readiness. *Design M6 purely speculatively (no real spec)* — rejected too; designing against Tyler's actual Papers/Songs requirements is what keeps the boundary from being a guess. The middle — capability as deliverable, real specs as the design input, a thin proof as the gate — is the call.
**Affects:** docs only — `roadmap.md` (Phase M scope callout + M6 line + out-of-scope note), `next_steps.md` (M6 framing). No code.

## ADR-043: M6 — the module-registration boundary (a module contributes `{type, canvas, exporters, integration}`; core is the first module). Phase M complete.
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted. The **module-system boundary is core** (CLAUDE.md "Building together" → both-agree + ADR). **Brandon directed shipping this solo without waiting on Tyler's sign-off** ("finish off Phase M, push live, no confirmation needed from Tyler on this one"), so the both-agree gate is **explicitly waived by the owner for this merge**; it is designed against Tyler's PR #1 specs and flagged to him in `COLLAB.md` so he can still react. Implements roadmap **M6** and the capability-not-modules scope of ADR-042; the per-type-canvas pivot it builds on was already both-agreed (ADR-037).
**Context:** Phase M's last slice. M5 (ADR-041) split `ItemCanvas` into a shell + the default `MarkdownCanvas` and added the per-type canvas seam as two deliberately-minimal halves: a **pure policy** (`canvasIdForType` in `canvas-registry.ts`, no component imports → node-testable) and a **hardcoded wiring `Record`** (`CANVAS_COMPONENTS` in the shell). M5 explicitly deferred the registration *API* to M6, "built to fit the path actually walked." M6 turns that hardcoded wiring into a real boundary: a *module* (Tyler PR #1 §1 — a workflow packaged as a unit: system type(s) + canonical body format + canvas + exporters + optional integration) contributes its bundle *onto* core rather than editing shared files, with per-user enable as a later config flip.
**Decision:**
1. **`src/lib/modules.ts` — the pure policy/contract half.** Defines the contract: `ModuleManifest = { id, label, enabledByDefault, types: ModuleTypeDef[], exporters: ExporterDef[], integration?: IntegrationDef }`; `ModuleTypeDef = { key, label, canonicalFormat, canvasId, icon? }`; `ExporterDef = { id, label, forType, fileExtension, render }`; `IntegrationDef = { id, label, direction }`. Holds the registry (`registerModule`, `allModules`, the `isModuleEnabled` enable seam) and the resolvers core dispatches through: `canvasIdForType`, `canonicalFormatForType`, `exportersForType`, `moduleForType`, `typeDefFor`, `registeredTypeKeys`. **Kept pure** — imports only `react` types + `@/lib/body` (`MARKDOWN_FORMAT`) + `import type` getItem — so it resolves identically on the server and in a plain-node verify script (the discipline M5 set). The canvas-contract types (`CanvasItem`/`CanvasProps`/`CanvasComponent`) moved here from `canvas-registry.ts`, which is **deleted** (folded in).
2. **Core is the first module (`coreModule`).** The five system types (task/meeting/note/link/entity) are a built-in manifest — all markdown-canonical, only `link` declaring a bespoke `canvasId`. So the **whole app now resolves type behavior through this one boundary**; the default markdown experience is byte-for-byte unchanged. This is the strongest proof the boundary is real, and the exact shape Papers/Songs follow.
3. **`src/lib/module-wiring.tsx` — the impure wiring half.** The one thing that can't be pure: `canvasId → React component` (`markdown`→`MarkdownCanvas`, `link`→`LinkCanvas`) + `canvasComponentFor(id)` with a `?? MarkdownCanvas` fallback. Linked to the policy by the `canvasId` string. So a verify script (or any pure import of the registry) never drags the editor bundle in. `ItemCanvas` now does `canvasComponentFor(canvasIdForType(item.type, owner.id))` — owner-aware so the per-user enable flip routes a disabled module's type back to the default without touching the call site.
4. **Exporters are deterministic code on the def.** `ExporterDef.render` is plain code (Principle 7, no model). A real module with a heavy renderer (pandoc→docx) keeps that in its own module file, which core's pure registry never imports, so core stays node-pure. (The OneDrive export *engine* is core infrastructure, not one of these per-type module exporters.)
5. **Canonical-body-format-per-type is now a real platform capability** (answers Tyler PR #1 decision #1 in code): `canonicalFormatForType(type)` resolves the owning type's declared format (markdown by default; a type may declare `chordpro` etc.). No renderer/editor rewiring yet — everything is still markdown — but the slot Songs/Papers read from exists and resolves.
6. **Per-user enable seam (the "later flip").** `isModuleEnabled(moduleId, ownerId?)` returns the manifest default today and ignores `ownerId`; per-user enablement becomes a lookup against a settings table right here, no call-site change. A disabled module's type resolves to the default canvas, contributes no exporters, and reports no format override.
7. **Proof = a reference registration, not a module (ADR-042).** `referenceModule` is exported from `modules.ts` as executable documentation touching all four slots (a type with its own format + canvas, an exporter whose `render` runs, a pull integration); it is **not** in the built-in list, so the live app ships core-only and no DB `types` row exists for it. The M6 verify script registers it (plus a ChordPro-format fixture and a disabled fixture) to prove resolution; core's live `link`→`LinkCanvas` proves the enabled canvas-wiring path end-to-end.
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep the M5 split (policy pure, wiring impure), generalized to all four slots, linked by string ids* — chosen; it preserves node-testability and matches what M5 called "M6-shaped, not throwaway." *One combined registry returning components* — rejected: importing it drags the editor bundle into the verify script (the exact thing M5 avoided). *Make core a special case outside the registry* — rejected: registering core as the first module means one boundary the whole app flows through, the honest dogfood. *Ship a live reference module/type* — rejected per ADR-042 (foundation ships the capability, not modules); the reference registration lives as exported documentation + a verify fixture, zero live footprint. *Build the per-user enable storage now* — rejected as out of scope; the seam (owner-threaded resolvers, `isModuleEnabled`) is in place so it's a later table lookup, not a refactor. *Move label/icon authority into the registry* — rejected: the DB `types` table stays the runtime source for label/icon enumeration (it's per-owner data); the registry owns the type's *code behavior* (canvas/format/exporters), and a module's manifest *declares* label/icon only for its future install/seed step.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; full `next build` clean (✓ compiled, all routes incl. `/items/[id]`, `/items/[id]/print`, `/share/[token]`; ran with the dev stand-in's set-but-empty Clerk keys). New **`scripts/verify-module-registry.mts` 38/38** — core dogfooding (5 types resolve, `link` keeps its canvas, no core exporters, all type keys enumerated), a workflow module slotting in (register `referenceModule` → its canvas/format/exporter[run deterministically]/integration all resolve; unknown before registration), format-per-type (a ChordPro fixture resolves `chordpro` + its chord canvas), the enable seam (a disabled fixture's type → default canvas, no exporters, no format override, not enumerated), and duplicate-id rejection. **`scripts/verify-canvas-seam.mts` still 16/16** (repointed to `modules.ts`; the M5 invariants + the ADR-018 footer-fields invariant unchanged). **In-browser (dev stand-in, auth-stub):** the `link` item renders the URL chip above the title with the full default canvas beneath (toolbar, URL strip, Related, Save Offline, Share, Fields) — core's bespoke canvas resolved through the boundary; a `note` renders the unchanged default markdown canvas (no chip, headings/emphasis/rule intact) — zero console warnings/errors, zero server errors. No schema/DB change, no new dependency.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/modules.ts`, `src/lib/module-wiring.tsx`, `scripts/verify-module-registry.mts`; edited `src/components/canvas/ItemCanvas.tsx` (resolve via the boundary, owner-aware), `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` + `LinkCanvas.tsx` (`CanvasProps` import → `@/lib/modules`), `scripts/verify-canvas-seam.mts` (import → `@/lib/modules`); **deleted** `src/lib/canvas-registry.ts`. **Phase M (the Markdown-epoch foundation rework) is complete** — M1–M3 (ADR-038/040), M5 (ADR-041), M6 (this). The modules themselves (Papers, Songs, …) are post-foundation, non-core work on top of the capability (ADR-042; mostly Tyler's lane).

## ADR-044: Slice 33 — the Build surface + the custom type & property builder (Phase 3, Tier 1)
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted. Touches **core** (the data model — a `types` column — and the type model / custom-type identity, both both-agree areas per CLAUDE.md "Building together"). **Brandon directed shipping it solo without waiting on Tyler's sign-off** (same waiver as ADR-043, "build the full shell and full type/property builder and then merge; we do not need to run this by Tyler yet"); flagged to him in `COLLAB.md` so he can react. Opens roadmap **Phase 3, Tier 1** (the Build surface UX), the priority after Phase M.
**Context:** Phase M delivered the module *capability*; Phase 3 Tier 1 builds the **Build surface** (PRD §4.10): the configuration side of Ledgr, switched from Work, where custom types/properties and views are made and later wired into Work. The dormant `types.property_schema` column (Phase 1) finally gets a writer, and the parked type/kind authoring UX (`explorations/type-and-kind-ux.md`, §1–3) lands with it. The switch UX was Brandon's call: a single floating button, separate from the nav, that turns build mode on/off.
**Decision:**
1. **The Work/Build switch is a floating button** (`src/components/build/BuildModeButton.tsx`), top-right, separate from the nav bar (Brandon's design over a nav toggle / a "Build" slot / a top menu). Its on/off state is **derived from the path** (`/build*`), not a stored flag, so it can never disagree with where you are: click from Work → `/build`; click from Build → `/`. Mounted in `NavShell` (so it's signed-in-gated, since `Nav` returns null when signed out) and shows "Building" (amber, active) vs "Build" (neutral).
2. **`/build` home** (`src/app/build/page.tsx`): the building-block menu — Types & properties, Views (the existing surface), and clearly-labeled "soon" placeholders for Templates/Workflows and Work-surface wiring (the §4.10 building-block contract). New users already start with structure (the five system types + system views), so this is a menu over a pre-loaded core, not a blank slate.
3. **`src/lib/types.ts` — the type registry store** (mirrors `views.ts` discipline: hand-rolled validation, one parse path, row→definition coercion). `property_schema` is an **ordered `PropertyDef[]`** (`{key, label, kind, options?}`), kinds `text|number|date|checkbox|url|select|multi_select` (`relation` deliberately omitted — the @-mention + Related panel already covers item-to-item links). CRUD + `parseTypeInput`/`parsePropertySchema`. **Types are instance-global, not owner-scoped** (the table has no `owner_id`; one user per deploy) — mutations still run behind `requireOwner`, and the `items.type → types.key` FK plus a counted pre-check guard an in-use delete. A **type key is immutable** (PK + FK target); **system types are extendable but not deletable**.
4. **New `show_in_quick_capture` column on `types`** (migration **0008**, `not null default true`): quick capture becomes **data-driven and opt-in** (type-and-kind-ux §2). Default true keeps the five core types capturable; the builder toggles it so a "data only" custom type stays out of the curated dropdown. (Defaulted opt-*out* for least surprise — a one-line flip if Brandon prefers opt-in.)
5. **`TypeBuilder.tsx` + `/build/types{,/new,/[key]/edit}`**: the builder form (label, create-only auto-slugged key, icon, the quick-capture toggle, and a property editor with kind + comma-separated select options + reorder/remove). Client component; imports only erased `import type` from `types.ts`, so the DB layer never enters the bundle (same pattern as `ViewBuilder`).
6. **Custom properties on the canvas** (`src/components/build/CustomProperties.tsx`): `MarkdownCanvas` is now async, loads the type's schema via `getType`, and renders an editable field per `PropertyDef` over `items.properties`, PATCHing on change (the FieldStrip optimistic-with-revert pattern). It holds the **full** properties object in state and overlays the edited key, so a PATCH can't wipe the namespaced system keys (`email`/`todoist`/`calendar`/`match`/`notify`) the schema doesn't know about. This makes the builder end-to-end real.
7. **Type/kind authoring UX** (the parked exploration, now built): §1 the entity **Kind** field is a dropdown of existing kinds + "New kind…" (`distinctEntityKinds` merges the built-in vocabulary with the owner's used kinds) in both `FieldStrip` and capture; §2 above; §3 the capture relate-picker is renamed **"Relate to…"** (killing the double "Entity" meaning) and an **inline kind picker** shows when capturing an entity, so entities no longer land kind-less.
8. **User types need no `modules.ts` change.** A user type is just a `types` row; the registry resolvers fall back to the default markdown canvas + markdown format for any unregistered type (ADR-043), so a custom type opens to the full default canvas (proven: a `hiring_candidate` item rendered the editor + its `Stage` select). The **DB owns label/icon/property_schema/enumeration; the registry owns code behavior** — the split holds.
9. **Open Q6 (custom-type identity), working resolution:** *types* are first-class and creatable here; *entity kinds* stay a reused property-style vocabulary, **not** auto-graduated to types — promotion to a bespoke type is the explicit "create a type" action (and, for real modules, the registry + a seed row per ADR-043). The kind registry and the type registry stay distinct mechanisms.
**Why / alternatives:** *Work/Build toggle inside the nav bar* / *a "Build" nav slot* / *a top menu* — all rejected for Brandon's standalone floating button (one affordance, unmistakably a mode switch, no nav real-estate cost). *Stored build-mode flag* — rejected for path-derived state (can't desync). *Owner-scope the `types` table* — rejected: no `owner_id` exists and v1 is single-user-per-deploy; multi-user type scoping would be its own core schema change. *Editable type key* — rejected (renaming the PK orphans every item). *Delete a type with items* — blocked (the FK would reject it anyway; the counted pre-check just gives a better message). *`property_schema` as an object map* — rejected for an array (display order matters; insertion order on objects is fragile). *Include `relation` as a property kind* — deferred (duplicates the relations surface). *An icon picker* — deferred (icon is a plain text field for now; no icon-set dependency, rule 5). *Wipe-clean vs example data* — the verification's `hiring_candidate` type + item were removed so the registry returns to the five system types.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; full `next build` clean (all routes, incl. `/build`, `/build/types`, `/build/types/[key]/edit`, `/build/types/new`, `/api/types`, `/api/types/[key]`; ran with the dev stand-in's set-but-empty Clerk keys). New **`scripts/verify-types.mts` 37/37** against Neon under throwaway owners — parse/validate (key slug rules, kinds, select-needs-options, duplicate keys, option dedupe/trim, order preserved, quick-capture default), CRUD, duplicate-key rejection, system-type protection, the in-use delete guard, and the owner-scoped entity-kind vocabulary. Regression smoke green: `verify-canvas-seam` 16/16, `verify-module-registry` 38/38, `verify-items` pass (none import the touched modules). **In-browser (dev stand-in):** the Build toggle shows "Building" on `/build` and "Build" on Work routes; `/build` renders the four cards; `/build/types` lists the five system types; **creating "Hiring Candidate" with a `Stage` select through the real form** landed it in the list (1 field); an item of that type opened through the default markdown canvas with an editable `Stage` select (—/Applied/Interview/Offer) whose edit **persisted** (`properties.stage = "Interview"`); quick capture's dropdown was data-driven (showed Hiring Candidate); selecting Entity revealed the kind picker (built-ins + used kinds + "New kind…") with the relate picker reading "Relate to…" — zero console errors throughout. (Screenshots flaked on a headless-renderer timeout this session; the accessibility-tree snapshots are the structural proof.)
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (+`types.show_in_quick_capture`), `drizzle/0008_*`; new `src/lib/types.ts`, `scripts/verify-types.mts`, `src/app/api/types/route.ts` + `[key]/route.ts`, `src/components/build/BuildModeButton.tsx` + `TypeBuilder.tsx` + `CustomProperties.tsx`, `src/app/build/page.tsx` + `types/page.tsx` + `types/new/page.tsx` + `types/[key]/edit/page.tsx`; edited `src/components/nav/Nav.tsx` (data-driven `typeOptions` + `entityKinds`), `src/components/nav/NavShell.tsx` (mount the toggle, thread `entityKinds`), `src/components/capture/CaptureModal.tsx` (kind picker + relate rename), `src/components/canvas/FieldStrip.tsx` (kind dropdown), `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (async; load schema + kinds, render `CustomProperties`). No new dependency.

### ADR-044 addendum — round-2 fixes from Brandon's first use (2026-06-13)
Six issues surfaced clicking through the shipped slice; all fixed, same slice/posture (non-core UX + one editor capability):
1. **Custom types now appear in the per-type list tabs.** `ListTabs` became an async server component that fetches the registry and appends a tab per custom type, linking to a new generic focused list at **`/list/[type]`** (the five system types keep their bespoke `/tasks` etc.). `ListPage.tab` widened to `string`.
2. **The boolean field is clearer.** The `checkbox` kind already existed but read as "Checkbox"; relabeled **"Checkbox (yes/no)"** in the builder. Verified it renders + persists on the canvas (`properties.resolved = true`).
3. **The view builder's type dropdown is data-driven.** Was hardcoded to the five system types; `ViewBuilder` now takes a `types` prop fed by `listTypes()` from the new/edit view pages, so a view can filter to a custom type.
4. **The markdown editor has checkboxes / task lists.** Added `TaskList` + `TaskItem` (from **`@tiptap/extension-list`**, promoted from transitive to a direct dep — same vendor/version already resolved) + a "☑ Tasks" toolbar button + CSS. `@tiptap/markdown` round-trips `- [ ]`/`- [x]` natively (no bespoke serializer, unlike the color marks). `markdown-render.ts` gained a compact hand-rolled markdown-it rule (no plugin dep) so the same task markdown renders as real checkboxes on the print/share document and the export. Verified the full round-trip in-browser (markdown → checkboxes → toggle → `- [x]` back) and in `verify-print` (4 new task-list checks).
5. **The Build toggle moved** from top-right to the right edge **~1/3 up from the bottom** (thumb-reachable on a phone, measured 33% up / 31px in), clear of the centered bottom bar.
6. **Views reads as part of Build.** The toggle's "in Build" state now covers `/build*` **and `/views*`** (a `BUILD_PREFIXES` list), so opening Views from the Build home keeps the indicator on "Building" instead of flipping to "Build".

`tsc` + `next build` clean (`/list/[type]` compiles); `verify-print` (now incl. task lists), `verify-share`, `verify-export`, `verify-body-contract` green; in-browser confirmed all six against the dev stand-in, zero console errors. New dep: `@tiptap/extension-list@^3.26.1`. **Affects (round 2):** `src/components/build/BuildModeButton.tsx`, `src/components/lists/ListTabs.tsx` (async + custom tabs) + `ListPage.tsx` (tab: string), new `src/app/list/[type]/page.tsx`, `src/components/views/ViewBuilder.tsx` + `src/app/views/new/page.tsx` + `views/[id]/edit/page.tsx` (data-driven types), `src/components/build/TypeBuilder.tsx` (relabel), `src/components/markdown-editor/MarkdownEditor.tsx` + `markdown-editor.css` (task list), `src/lib/markdown-render.ts` + `src/lib/print-html.ts` (server task-list render), `scripts/verify-print.mts`, `package.json`.

## ADR-045: Slice 34 — per-type item templates (Phase 3, Tier 2a)
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted. Touches **core** (a new `templates` table — the data model is a both-agree area per CLAUDE.md "Building together"). **Brandon directed shipping Tier 2 solo** (same waiver as ADR-043/044 — "do whatever is logical and safe, then commit"); flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`. First half of roadmap **Phase 3, Tier 2 — templates** (the workflow/wiki structure generator is ADR-046, the other half).
**Context:** Tier 1 (ADR-044) gave types a `property_schema`; Tier 2 makes *starting from a preset* cheap. Per-type item templates store property defaults + starter body content (roadmap Phase 3, Brandon 2026-06-12). The Phase-2 meeting-prep agenda (`src/lib/meetings/prep.ts`, `DEFAULT_AGENDA`) is the named forerunner: a hardcoded starter body for one type; this generalizes it so any type carries named, editable starting points, authored in the same editor items use.
**Decision:**
1. **New `templates` table** (migration **0009**): `{id, owner_id → users, type → types.key (ON DELETE cascade), name, body jsonb, property_defaults jsonb, created_at}`, indexed `(owner_id, type)`. **Owner-scoped** (a template is personal config, like a `views` row — not shared structure), unlike the instance-global `types` registry. A table, **not** `items` (rule 2 covers user *content*; a template is config, the same call `views`/`matchers` made) and **not** a column on `types` (templates are many-per-type, owner-scoped, and a starter body on the hot `getType` read — called on every canvas mount — would fatten it; a side table keeps type reads lean). The cascade drops a type's templates if the type itself is deleted (`deleteType` already blocks while *items* use it).
2. **`src/lib/templates.ts` store** (mirrors `views.ts`/`types.ts`: hand-rolled validation, one parse path, row→definition coercion). `body` accepts a raw markdown string (wrapped to `{format,text}`) or an already-shaped body; an empty body stores null. `parseDefaults` drops null/empty values so a default never writes an empty key. `type` is set on create and **immutable on patch** (the defaults are keyed to that type's schema; re-pointing would orphan them). CRUD + `createItemFromTemplate` + `templateCountsByType`.
3. **`createItemFromTemplate` = `createItem` with the body + defaults filled in**, `inbox: false` (deliberate creation, like "+ New" — *not* an Inbox arrival, ADR-010) and a blank title (the user names it). So a template rides the whole existing item-create path (revisions, mention-sync, body-text/FTS) for free.
4. **API:** `GET/POST /api/templates` (+ `?type=` filter), `GET/PATCH/DELETE /api/templates/[id]`, and `POST /api/templates/[id]/apply` — a distinct endpoint so "create from template" is explicit and the store owns the seeding (rather than overloading `POST /api/items`).
5. **Builder UI** (`/build/templates{,/new,/[id]/edit}` + `TemplateBuilder.tsx`): name, type select (immutable when editing), a **controlled property-defaults editor** keyed off the selected type's `property_schema` (the mirror of `CustomProperties`, which edits a live item), and the **starter body in the same Tiptap editor items use** — reused in *controlled* mode (`LazyMarkdownEditor` with a stable `initialMarkdown` + `onChange`, no item to autosave against; `itemId` is optional, only for @-mention self-exclusion). `/build` home gains a real "Item templates" card.
6. **Template-aware "+ New"** (`NewItemButton`): self-fetches `/api/templates?type=` on mount and, when the type has templates, becomes a menu — "Blank" + each template. Done in the *one* component, so every list page that already renders `<NewItemButton type=…/>` (the five system lists + `/list/[type]`) gets the menu with **zero page changes**.
7. **The meeting-prep forerunner is now an expressible instance** (not rewired): `DEFAULT_AGENDA` could be saved as a `meeting` template; prep still synthesizes its panel live (ADR-025). Generalizing prep onto templates is a later, optional step.
