**Why / alternatives:** *Templates as `items`* — rejected (would pollute every owner-scoped list/search/FTS/export unless excluded everywhere; config belongs in a side table). *Templates as a `types` column* — rejected (many-per-type + owner-scoped + bloats the hot `getType`). *Mutable template type* — rejected (orphans the defaults). *Seed hot fields like due/urgency into templates* — deferred; the contract is type-uniform (`body` + `propertyDefaults`) for now, and a relative-due offset is the more useful future shape than an absolute date. *Title default* — deferred (blank, like "+ New"). *Overload `POST /api/items` for apply* — rejected for the explicit `/apply` endpoint.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; full `next build` clean (new routes `/api/templates{,/[id],/[id]/apply}`, `/build/templates{,/new,/[id]/edit}`, ran with the dev stand-in's empty Clerk keys). New **`scripts/verify-templates.mts` 27/27** against Neon under throwaway owners — parse/validate (name/type required, body string→wrapped, empty→null, defaults drop empties, array rejected), CRUD, owner-scoping (foreign get/update/delete are not-found), apply (seeds body + defaults, `inbox` false, blank title), and the type cascade. **In-browser (dev stand-in):** built an "Interview candidate" template for a custom type through the real form (the markdown editor mounted in controlled mode, the property-defaults section rendered the type's fields, a URL default set); it landed on the `/build/templates` index grouped by type with a "1 field" badge; the type's list showed **"+ New ▾"** with `["Blank","Interview candidate"]`; applying it created an item carrying `{website_link: …}` with `inbox:false` and a blank title — zero console errors. Verification template + item were cleaned up.
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (+`templates`), `drizzle/0009_*`; new `src/lib/templates.ts`, `scripts/verify-templates.mts`, `src/app/api/templates/route.ts` + `[id]/route.ts` + `[id]/apply/route.ts`, `src/components/build/TemplateBuilder.tsx`, `src/app/build/templates/page.tsx` + `new/page.tsx` + `[id]/edit/page.tsx`; edited `src/components/home/NewItemButton.tsx` (template menu) and `src/app/build/page.tsx` (Item templates card). No new dependency.

## ADR-046: Slice 35 — workflow & wiki structure templates + board grouping by a custom property (Phase 3, Tier 2b)
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted. The view-definition shape widens (a board can group by a property) — **views are explicitly NOT core** ("view definitions and dashboard widgets — move fast, solo", CLAUDE.md), so this half adds no new core surface beyond what ADR-045 already flagged. **Shipped solo per Brandon's Tier 2 direction**; noted to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`. Completes roadmap **Phase 3, Tier 2 — templates** (ADR-045 was item templates).
**Context:** PRD §4.14 — the Build surface leads with "New Workflow" / "New Wiki": guided creation that auto-generates a type + properties + starter views via the §3.6 machinery, then surfaces the result on Work and retires it without data loss. The two `/build` "soon" cards were the placeholders. A workflow is fundamentally *records moving through stages on a board*, so the canonical output view is a **board grouped by a custom "Stage" select** — which the slice-27 view engine couldn't do (it grouped only by built-in fields). So this slice has two parts: the view-engine capability, then the generator on top.
**Decision:**
1. **A workflow/wiki template is a *generator*, not a stored entity.** Its output is ordinary `types` + `views` rows. So "surface it / retire it" is just pin/unpin (slice 29), there's nothing new to archive, and "the data stays put" falls out for free. No new table.
2. **Board grouping by a custom select property.** `ViewGrouping` widens from `{field}` to `{field: GroupField} | {propertyKey: string} | null`; `parseGrouping` accepts a `propertyKey`. The pure grouping logic (`groupValueFor`/`orderedGroups`/`dueBucket`) is **extracted from `ViewRenderer` into `src/lib/view-grouping.ts`** (import-light, node-testable — the M5/M6 pure-policy discipline). A property grouping reads `items.properties[key]` (already selected by `listColumns`); columns order by the property's **option list** (resolved by the view page from the type's schema and passed as `groupOrder`), then present-but-unlisted values alphabetically, `none` last — so a workflow board reads Applied → Interview → Offer, not alphabetically. `ViewBuilder` offers the type's select/multi_select properties as group-by options and **preserves a property grouping on edit** (a generated board re-saved through the builder keeps its grouping instead of resetting to status).
3. **`src/lib/structure-templates.ts`** — pure `planStructure` (→ `planWorkflow`/`planWiki`) maps the guided answers to a `TypeCreateInput` + `ViewInput[]` reusing `parseTypeInput`/`parseViewInput` (one validation home, deterministic, no model — Principle 3); impure `applyStructurePlan` persists over `createType`/`createView`/`pinView`. A **workflow** prepends a `stage` select (options = the steps) and makes a board-grouped-by-stage + a table; a **wiki** makes a title-sorted table (relations via @-mentions, light on status — no stage/board). Named **presets** (Hiring/Content pipelines, Trip/Reading wikis) are plain data the form prefills ("the small set of big, obvious buttons").
4. **`POST /api/build/structures`** plans + applies + optionally pins, returning `{typeKey, primaryViewId}` so the client opens the new board.
5. **UI:** `/build/new` is one query-driven page — chooser (preset cards + blank "New Workflow"/"New Wiki") with no `kind`, the guided `StructureBuilder` (stages editor with reorder = column order, fields editor, "add to dashboard" toggle) with `kind` set. `/build/surface` is the **Work-surface wiring** page: pin/unpin views as dashboard widgets (reuses `PinButton`/`/api/dashboard`), nav slots shown read-only. The two `/build` "soon" cards became real links.
6. **"Wire into Work" = the dashboard-widget path** (pin the generated board), which already exists end-to-end (slice 29) and is offered inline in the flow. **Nav-slot wiring is deferred**: the nav is still the hardcoded `NAV_SLOTS` stand-in, and making it data-driven (locked home, badges, reorder, thumb-reach) deserves its own slice. PRD §4.14's "widget and/or nav slot" is satisfied by the widget path.
**Why / alternatives:** *A `workflows` table / a stored "structure" record* — rejected; a workflow *is* a type + views, and not storing it is what makes retire-without-loss trivial. *Group the board by the built-in `status` enum* — rejected; workflow stages are arbitrary and per-type, not open/done/archived. *Make `TableLayout` show custom-property columns instead of a board* — deferred; the board-by-stage is the canonical workflow view and the table layout's fixed columns are a separate enhancement. *Store the column order in the view's grouping* — rejected for resolving it live from the type's options (no staleness when stages change). *Build nav-slot configuration now* — deferred (its own slice). *Full preset catalog / Claude-generated structures (§4.14)* — the deterministic generator is in; the MCP "Hey Claude, make a workflow for X" path rides Tier 3 over this same endpoint.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; full `next build` clean (new routes `/build/new`, `/build/surface`, `/api/build/structures`; empty Clerk keys). New **`scripts/verify-structures.mts` 38/38** against Neon — pure planning (stage select + options order, board grouping, ≥2-stage guard, wiki has no stage, bad name/kind), all four presets plan cleanly, the pure grouping helpers (property read, none-group, array-join, option-order vs alpha, due buckets), and `applyStructurePlan` (type + two views created, primary pinned, duplicate-key rejected) with cleanup. **`verify-views.mts` extended + green** (parses field *and* property grouping, rejects a blank propertyKey). **In-browser (dev stand-in):** the `/build/new` chooser showed both sections with presets; generating a "VTest Pipeline" workflow created the type + board + table, pinned the board, and the board rendered **APPLIED** and **OFFER** columns in stage-option order (Interview correctly absent — no items) with the items in their stages; zero console errors. Verification type/items/views were cleaned up.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/view-grouping.ts`, `src/lib/structure-templates.ts`, `src/app/api/build/structures/route.ts`, `src/components/build/StructureBuilder.tsx`, `src/app/build/new/page.tsx` + `surface/page.tsx`, `scripts/verify-structures.mts`; edited `src/lib/views.ts` (`ViewGrouping` + `parseGrouping`), `src/components/views/ViewRenderer.tsx` (pure helpers + `groupOrder` + `properties` on `ViewItem`), `src/app/views/[id]/page.tsx` (resolve `groupOrder`), `src/components/views/ViewBuilder.tsx` + `src/app/views/new/page.tsx` + `views/[id]/edit/page.tsx` (property group-by + pass `propertySchema`), `src/app/build/page.tsx` (two cards real), `scripts/verify-views.mts`. No new dependency.

## ADR-047: Slice 36 — the MCP server (Phase 3, Tier 3): a hand-rolled Streamable-HTTP endpoint over the existing item libs
**Date:** 2026-06-13
**Status:** accepted. **CORE** — the machine/MCP API contract is on the both-agree+ADR list (CLAUDE.md "Building together"). **Shipped solo per Brandon's standing Tier-direction** ("build the next tier"), same waiver as M6 / slices 33–35; flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`. Opens roadmap **Phase 3, Tier 3 — the Claude layer** (the MCP server; scheduled Claude tasks + Notion migration follow).
**Context:** PRD §5.5 + Principle 4 ("Claude is a first-class client"): a thin MCP server exposing search/read/create/update items + list-by-entity/date, auth via a personal API token, enabling "what's open with Roger," "file this as a task due Friday," "prep tomorrow's 1:1" from Claude desktop/web/mobile. The two judgment calls were *how to speak MCP* (SDK vs hand-roll, and where it's hosted) and *how the token resolves to an owner* (the token scheme stores no owner).
**Decision:**
1. **Hand-rolled MCP over the Streamable HTTP transport, no SDK.** For request/response tools the protocol is a small, stable JSON-RPC surface (`initialize`, `tools/list`, `tools/call`, `ping`), so we implement it directly rather than take `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk` — the same dependency call ADR-034 made for Web Push (Principle 5). The protocol layer is verified against the **2025-06-18 spec** (lifecycle + transports): a POST carrying a JSON-RPC *request* gets one `application/json` response; a POST carrying only a *notification* (e.g. `notifications/initialized`) gets **202, no body**; GET/DELETE → **405** (we offer no server-initiated SSE stream and keep no session). Version negotiation echoes the client's version when supported (we accept 2024-11-05 / 2025-03-26 / 2025-06-18), else returns our latest.
2. **In-app endpoint at `POST /api/mcp`, stateless.** No separate process to host or keep warm (Principle 4 $0, Sunday-proof) — it's a Next route. **Stateless** (no `Mcp-Session-Id`): every call re-authenticates and re-resolves the owner, so there's no per-connection state, which suits a serverless function and a single user. Added to the `proxy.ts` public set (Clerk never runs on it); the machine token is the only credential, which also makes the spec's DNS-rebinding `Origin` check moot (a forged origin can't forge the bearer).
3. **Auth = the existing machine-token scheme (ADR-004) with a new `mcp` scope.** No change to the token format; `verifyMachineToken(authz, "mcp")` gates the route. Owner resolution mirrors the other machine jobs: `resolveMcpOwner()` reads `LEDGR_MCP_OWNER_UPN || ONEDRIVE_EXPORT_UPN || GRAPH_MAILBOX_UPN || DEV_USER_EMAIL` → the `users` row (single-user v1; a multi-user build would map each token to its own owner).
4. **Six tools, each a thin wrapper over the libs the REST API already uses** (search.ts / views.ts / items.ts / relations.ts / types.ts), so the MCP surface can't drift from the app's own contract or skip owner-scoping: `search_items` (FTS), `list_items` (by type/status/kind/due-window/entity — the "list by entity/date"), `get_item` (fields + markdown body + relations), `create_item` (body as markdown, `relateTo` links to existing items, defaults `inbox:false`), `update_item`, and `list_types` (so the model learns the type/property vocabulary). `create_item`/`update_item` **reuse `parseItemPayload`**, so an MCP write validates exactly like an `/api/items` write.
5. **Pure/impure split, the M5/M6 discipline.** `src/lib/mcp/protocol.ts` (envelope, version negotiation, message classification — pure, node-testable), `server.ts` (the method dispatcher), `tools.ts` (the registry + `callTool`), `owner.ts` (resolution); the route is a thin transport shell. **`parseItemPayload`/`asUuid` were extracted from `api.ts` into a new pure `src/lib/item-input.ts`** (api.ts re-exports them, so the 17 route call sites are untouched) — `api.ts` imports `next/server` + the Clerk owner chain, which a node verify script can't load, so the parsing had to move to stay reusable.
6. **`/health` `checks.mcp`** canary (`hasScopedToken("mcp")` + `resolveMcpOwner()`), like `checks.graph` — never changes overall status. Tool errors surface as MCP `isError` results (the session survives); unexpected errors are `captureError`-ed (source `mcp`) with a correlation id.
**Why / alternatives:** *Take `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk`* — rejected for Principle 5: the SDK is built around Node http/Express and would need stateless-per-request adaptation in a Next route, for a protocol surface we can hand-roll in ~120 lines and pin to the spec ourselves; documented here so a future maintainer knows it's the off-ramp if MCP grows features we want (sampling, elicitation, resources). *A separately hosted MCP server* — rejected; an in-app route is $0 and rides the same deploy. *Stateful sessions (`Mcp-Session-Id`)* — unnecessary for request/response tools and worse for serverless. *Put the owner in the token entry* — rejected; it'd change the ADR-004 format that cron tokens (which act across owners) share, and single-user resolves fine by UPN. *Expose a `delete_item` tool* — deferred; create/update/relate cover the named use cases, and a model-driven delete is higher-risk (Trash/restore stays a human gesture for now). *Structured tool output (`structuredContent`/`outputSchema`)* — skipped for pretty-JSON text content (universally supported); a clean later enhancement.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; full `next build` clean (`/api/mcp` compiles as a dynamic route). **`scripts/verify-mcp.mts` 50/50** against live Neon — pure protocol (version negotiation, message classification incl. no-batching, envelope builders), the dispatcher (initialize negotiates + advertises tools + serverInfo + instructions; tools/list returns all six with object inputSchemas and correct read-only annotations; ping → `{}`; unknown → -32601; notification → null; invalid → -32600), and all six tools end-to-end (create entity + task with body/due/`relateTo` → get_item shows the confirmed relation + verbatim body → search_items FTS + type filter → list_items by entity and by due-window (week includes / overdue excludes a +2d task) → update_item to done drops it from the open list → list_types has the five system types), plus validation (bad/missing type, bad UUID, missing item, unknown tool, empty patch all return `isError`) and **owner scoping** (owner2 can't read owner1's item), with two temp owners cleaned up. **In-browser HTTP smoke (dev stand-in, real route):** GET → 405, POST no-token → 401, `initialize` → 200 (serverName "ledgr", negotiated 2025-06-18, instructions present), `notifications/initialized` → 202, `tools/list` → the six tools, `create_item` then `get_item` round-tripped the body over the wire, a bad `MCP-Protocol-Version` → 400, unknown method → JSON-RPC -32601; the smoke item was deleted and the temporary dev token removed from `.env.local`.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/mcp/{protocol,server,tools,owner}.ts`, `src/lib/item-input.ts`, `src/app/api/mcp/route.ts`, `scripts/verify-mcp.mts`; edited `src/lib/api.ts` (re-export the moved parsers), `src/lib/auth/machine.ts` (`hasScopedToken`), `src/proxy.ts` (public route), `src/app/health/route.ts` (`checks.mcp`), `.env.example` (`LEDGR_MCP_OWNER_UPN` + `mcp` scope), `runbook.md` (§1f, env table, §2 canary). No new dependency.
## ADR-048: Papers module — tabbed canvas, scaffold-in-properties, docx-via-route
**Date:** 2026-06-14
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** The second workflow module in Tyler's lane (after Songs), built on the M5/M6 foundation (ADR-042/043). A `paper` is a seminary-paper workspace replacing the hand-run "HTML outline viewer + MSM Word doc" flow (`ty-docs/Paper_Outline_Viewer_Build_Spec.md`). Three parts the writer builds in order: a **quote bank** (sources gathered before drafting), an **outline** (sections/paragraphs with notes), and the **final paper**. A working MSM `.docx` renderer already existed as a CLI (`ty-docs/msm-render.js`). Module internals are "not core / move fast solo" per CLAUDE.md; the one core-adjacent temptation (a binary exporter) was deliberately avoided.
**Decision:**
1. **One `paper` item, tabbed canvas — Quote Bank · Outline · Draft** (`PaperCanvas` → `PaperCanvasClient`, wired as canvas id `paper`). The **Draft** is the canonical markdown `body` (the deliverable; gets revisions + FTS; exports to docx). The **Outline** (markdown) and **Quote Bank** (structured) are the *scaffold* that sits beside it. (Tyler's model: outline its own markdown surface, quote bank alongside it, both together and separate from the final draft.)
2. **Scaffold lives in `items.properties`** — `properties.outline` (markdown string) + `properties.quoteBank` (`QuoteEntry[]`) + title-page meta keys. No schema migration: the existing `PATCH /api/items/:id` already replaces `properties` wholesale. **`PaperCanvasClient` is the single writer of a paper's properties** (it preserves unknown/system keys and overrides only the keys it owns), so `PaperCanvas` does **not** render the generic `CustomProperties` panel — two whole-object properties writers would race. The title-page meta form (`PaperMeta`) lives inside the Draft tab.
3. **Deterministic MSM citation engine** (`src/lib/papers/citation.ts`, pure): structured source (book | video) + page → the three MSM 4th-ed footnote forms (Full / Short / Ibid.), transcribed from the build spec. The quote bank shows all three per entry; **Cite** mints a unique `[^id]` marker, splices it at the Draft caret, and appends the matching `[^id]: …` definition — the markdown-canonical footnote mechanism the renderer consumes. Each insertion gets a fresh marker so a first reference and a later shortened one are distinct numbered notes.
4. **MSM `.docx` ships via a dedicated route, not the module exporter slot.** `ExporterDef.render` returns a `string`; a `.docx` is a binary buffer. Rather than widen that contract (a **core** change needing Brandon + ADR), the renderer is ported to `src/lib/papers/msm-docx.ts` and served by `GET /api/items/[id]/render-docx` (owner-scoped, `paper`-only). `paperModule.exporters` is empty. The positional `FootnoteReferenceRun` approach makes the CLI's old duplicate-id unpack/pack fix unnecessary.
5. **Draft + Outline use a bespoke raw-markdown textarea** (`PaperMarkdownArea`), not the shared Tiptap WYSIWYG. Papers are footnote-heavy academic prose; `[^id]` footnotes are a raw-markdown feature Tiptap neither renders nor exposes an insertion handle for. The textarea makes footnotes first-class and click-to-cite trivial, and keeps Papers self-contained (no edit to the shared editor). CodeMirror is a future upgrade (the scoped plan's "textarea → CodeMirror later").
6. **Type seeded with a `property_schema`** (title-page meta as text fields + `stage` select) via `scripts/seed-papers.mjs` (idempotent, `is_system=false`). The schema is the data-model declaration; the canvas reads/writes these keys directly. `PAPER_STAGES` source of truth is `src/lib/papers/types.ts`.
**Why / alternatives:** *Outline-generates-the-markdown-skeleton* — rejected (lossy round-trip; notes leak into the deliverable). *Outline/quote bank as separate child items* — deferred (heavier cross-item orchestration; the caveat below is the upgrade path if `properties` bloats). *Widen `ExporterDef` for binary* — rejected (core change for one module's need; a route is cleaner). *Reuse the Tiptap editor for the Draft* — rejected (no footnote node, no external insertion handle; would require editing a shared core component). *pandoc for docx* — rejected (system binary, not Vercel-friendly; the JS `docx` package is proven in `ty-docs`).
**Caveat (logged):** `items.properties` is selected on normal item reads, so a very large outline/quote bank bloats those payloads (Principle 8). Acceptable for v1 (single user, modest paper counts); promote the outline to a child `note` item if it grows (gets its own revisions/FTS).
**New dependency:** `docx` (runtime) — the only realistic MSM-compliant Word output; pandoc needs a binary. Single new runtime dep.
**Shared-file touches (flag for Brandon):** `src/lib/modules/register.ts` (+`paperModule`) and `src/lib/module-wiring.tsx` (+`paper` canvas) — both additive; the five core types are unchanged.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-papers.mts` **16/16** (registration/resolvers, citation engine book+video Full/Short/Ibid, a real `renderMsmDocx` → 10KB buffer with 3 positionally-allocated footnotes). Regression green: `verify-module-registry` 38, `verify-canvas-seam` 16, `verify-songs` all pass. `tsc` + `next build` clean (`/api/items/[id]/render-docx` registered); eslint clean; `paper` type seeded to the dev DB. (In-browser canvas walkthrough left for Tyler's morning check.)
**Affects:** new `src/lib/papers/{types,citation,msm-docx}.ts`, `src/lib/modules/papers.ts`, `src/components/canvas/PaperCanvas.tsx`, `src/components/paper-editor/{PaperCanvasClient,PaperMarkdownArea,QuoteBank,PaperMeta}.tsx`, `src/app/api/items/[id]/render-docx/route.ts`, `scripts/{seed-papers.mjs,verify-papers.mts}`, `explorations/song-import.md`; edited `src/lib/modules/register.ts`, `src/lib/module-wiring.tsx`, `package.json` (+`docx`).
**Renumbered on merge:** Tyler authored this as ADR-045; that number was already taken on `main` by per-type item templates, so it became ADR-048 when his Songs + Papers branch merged in (2026-06-14).

## ADR-049: Per-view configurable columns
**Date:** 2026-06-14
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Brandon's first-use feedback: "the items list only shows the created date on most items — let me pick what shows in a view." The list/table layouts (`ViewRenderer`) had a fixed column set; the row data (`ViewItem`, incl. `properties`) was already present, so what was missing was a per-view column choice. Views are **non-core** config, so this needed no ADR-by-agreement; logged because it extends the View Definition contract (like ADR-046's board-by-property).
**Decision:**
1. **`columns` jsonb on `views`** (migration 0010), an ordered `ViewColumn[]` where a column is either `{source:"field", key}` (a built-in field: type/status/urgency/kind/dueDate/meetingAt/createdAt/updatedAt/url) or `{source:"property", key}` (one of the type's custom `property_schema` keys). **null = the layout's default columns**, so every pre-existing view is byte-for-byte unchanged.
2. **Tolerant parse (`parseColumns`, the views.ts discipline):** malformed entries dropped not rejected, deduped on source:key, order preserved, all-invalid collapses to null. Same coercion on read (`rowToDefinition`) so a hand-edited row reads cleanly.
3. **Honored by the row-based layouts only** (list, table, agenda); board/calendar keep their card shapes. The table expresses its own default four columns as field columns so one render path serves both. In the list, status/urgency keep their chips; other columns render as labelled text, blank values omitted.
4. **Property-column labels resolved server-side.** The view page loads the type once (it already did for board grouping) and passes a `key→label` map to `ViewRenderer`, so a property column reads "Stage", not "stage". `ViewBuilder` offers field columns (filtered to the type, mirroring the date/sort selects) + the type's properties as checkboxes; check order = column order.
**Why / alternatives:** *A separate `view_columns` table* — rejected (rule 5; one jsonb column on the row that owns it, like filter/sort/grouping). *Make the plain list pages (/list, /inbox) column-configurable too* — deferred; those aren't View Definitions yet (they become system views later), and the view surface is where "pick what shows" belongs. *Per-column width/sort/reorder UI* — deferred; checkboxes in canonical order cover the ask.
**Verification:** `verify-views.mts` extended (parse keep/drop/dedupe/order/collapse + a create→getView columns round-trip), all green against Neon; `tsc` + `next build` clean. **In-browser (dev stand-in):** built a table view with columns `[type, createdAt, url]` through the real API and it rendered exactly `Title | Type | Created | URL` with the Created dates populated and URL blank for tasks; the builder's Columns fieldset renders the type-appropriate field checkboxes.
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (+`views.columns`), migration `0010`, `src/lib/views.ts` (`ViewColumn`/`COLUMN_FIELDS`/`parseColumns` + input/definition/store), `src/components/views/ViewRenderer.tsx` (column helpers + list/table/agenda honor columns + `propertyLabels`), `src/components/views/ViewBuilder.tsx` (Columns picker), `src/app/views/[id]/page.tsx` (resolve `propertyLabels`), `scripts/verify-views.mts`. No new dependency.

## ADR-050: Templates can preset relations (people/attendees), not just properties
**Date:** 2026-06-14
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Brandon's first-use feedback: a "pastors meeting" template should pre-select the people who normally attend, so a new meeting from it starts with them related. ADR-045 templates preset a type's **custom properties**, but the people on a meeting are **relation edges** (the `relations` table), not properties — and core types ship with no custom properties, so a meeting template looked empty. There is no `relation` property kind (deliberately deferred, `types.ts`). This brushes core (the relation concept), so per CLAUDE.md it gets an ADR + a COLLAB heads-up to Tyler; Brandon waived the wait (Tyler isn't on core yet). The broader "`relation` as a first-class property kind" stays parked in `explorations/entity-vs-custom-type.md`; this is the targeted slice (`explorations/template-property-defaults.md` option A).
**Decision:**
1. **`relation_defaults` jsonb on `templates`** (migration 0010) — an array of `{ targetId, role }` edges. Tolerant parse (`parseRelationDefaults`): drop non-UUID/malformed entries, default role to `"related"`, dedupe on (targetId, role). Kept off the core property model entirely — relations stay in the relations table where they belong.
2. **`createItemFromTemplate` writes the edges on apply**, after the item is created, via the existing `relateItems` path (so they're owner-validated, live-checked, and land as confirmed edges — the same gesture as a manual relate). **Resilient:** a target deleted/trashed since the template was saved is skipped (caught `ItemError`), never aborting the create — the item already exists and one stale attendee shouldn't lose it.
3. **`TemplateBuilder` gains a "Related items" picker** (entity options passed from the new/edit pages via `listEntityOptions`): add-from-dropdown + removable chips. The input type's `relationDefaults` is optional (parse always sets it; the store normalizes to `[]`) so existing hand-built callers are unchanged.
**Why / alternatives:** *Add a `relation` property kind* — rejected here (a core data-model change tied to the entity-vs-custom-type question; folds into that exploration, not this slice). *Pre-relate via the matcher engine* — rejected (reactive, calendar-driven; doesn't serve "+ New from template"). *Store edges in `properties`* — rejected (relations are a first-class table; `properties` can't carry an edge with owner-scoping/confirm semantics). *Let templates preset core structured fields too (urgency, due-offset)* — deferred (noted in the exploration; a later whitelist alongside this).
**Verification:** `verify-templates.mts` extended (parse dedupe/drop/default-role/non-array reject; create+getView round-trip; apply writes an edge per live target, **skips a stale target while still creating the item**, and won't relate a target owned by someone else), all green against Neon; `tsc` + `next build` clean. **In-browser (dev stand-in):** created a meeting template with two preset people, applied it, and the new meeting opened with its starter agenda body **and** the Meeting Prep panel showing "With Roger Martinez, Tom Bradley" — the preset edges landed as confirmed relations. Test artifacts cleaned up.
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (+`templates.relation_defaults`), migration `0010`, `src/lib/templates.ts` (`RelationDefault`/`parseRelationDefaults` + input/definition/store + apply-writes-edges), `src/components/build/TemplateBuilder.tsx` (Related-items picker), `src/app/build/templates/{new,[id]/edit}/page.tsx` (pass entities), `scripts/verify-templates.mts`. No new dependency.

## ADR-051: Bespoke-tool catalog — attach a module capability to a user-named type (Tyler's spike, promoted)
**Date:** 2026-06-14
**Status:** accepted. Touches **core** (the type + module model — a both-agree area per CLAUDE.md "Building together"). Authored by Tyler as the `spike/bespoke-tool-catalog` branch and flagged "NOT MERGED, ADR-pending Brandon's review"; **Brandon reviewed and approved merging it (2026-06-14)** — this ADR is that sign-off. Realizes the "bespoke-tool catalog" idea captured in `next_steps.md` (a Build-surface browser of module behaviors).
**Context:** the module system (ADR-042, M6) binds a module's behavior — canvas, canonical format, exporters — to a fixed *type key* (`song`, `paper`). Bespoke-first (Principle 6) wants the reverse too: a user creates a type under *their own* name ("Worship Set", "Sermon Notes") and attaches an existing bespoke tool (Chord Chart, Paper Workspace) underneath, so behavior is decoupled from the key. This is the catalog: browse the registered module capabilities and pin one to a custom type.
**Decision:**
1. **`ModuleCapability` + `capabilities[]` on a `ModuleManifest`** (`src/lib/modules.ts`): a capability is an attachable behavior bundle (canvas id + canonical format + exporters) a module exposes for use under an arbitrary type. `attachableCapabilities()` enumerates them; `capabilityById(id)` resolves one. Songs declares `chord-chart`, Papers declares `paper-workspace`.
2. **Capability-aware resolvers.** `canvasIdForType` / `canonicalFormatForType` / `exportersForType` take an optional capability id. Resolution order: a registered module **type** still wins (unchanged for `song`/`paper`), **else** the attached capability, **else** the default markdown canvas. So core behavior is untouched; the capability only fills the gap for a plain custom type.
3. **`types.capability` column** (`text`, nullable; migration **0011** — see renumber note). Threaded through `src/lib/types.ts` (`TypeInput.capability`, `parseCapability` validates the id against the *live registry* so a type can't store a capability no enabled module offers), the type API, and `TypeBuilder`. `null` = a plain custom type (default canvas), so every existing type is unchanged.
4. **Build surface:** a 6th `/build` card + a `/build/tools` catalog page; a capability banner in `TypeBuilder`. `ItemCanvas` / the modal item route pass the type's capability into the resolvers.
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep behavior keyed only to the type key* — rejected (forces every bespoke use through a developer-named type; the catalog lets the tail of named workflows reuse a tool without new module code). *A join table for type→capability* — rejected (rule 5; one nullable column on the row that owns it). *Make `capability` optional in `TypeInput`* — rejected (kept it required so every create/patch path states it explicitly; `null` is the plain case, and `tsc` enforces no caller forgets it).
**Renumbered on merge:** Tyler authored the migration as `0010_bespoke_capability`; `0010` was already taken on `main` by ADR-049/050 (`0010_quick_impossible_man`: `views.columns` + `templates.relation_defaults`), and the spike never committed a `0010` snapshot. On merge the spike's `0010` SQL was dropped and the column **regenerated via `drizzle-kit` as `0011_bespoke_capability`** off main's schema, so the snapshot/journal are clean. Applied to Neon before pushing (additive nullable column — the then-deployed code ignored it, no 500 window).
**Verification:** `verify-bespoke-capability.mts` **18/18**; regression green — `verify-module-registry`, `verify-canvas-seam`, `verify-types`, `verify-songs`, `verify-papers`, `verify-templates` all pass against Neon; `tsc --noEmit` clean (no `createType` caller broke on the new required field). `next build` skipped locally (dev server up — the `.next/dev/types` clash); Vercel production build is the gate.
**Affects:** `src/lib/modules.ts` (`ModuleCapability`/`capabilities[]`/`attachableCapabilities`/`capabilityById` + capability-aware resolvers), `src/lib/types.ts` (`capability` on input/definition + `parseCapability`), `src/db/schema.ts` (+`types.capability`), migration **0011**, `src/lib/modules/{songs,papers}.ts` (declare capabilities), `src/app/build/page.tsx` (+ card) + `src/app/build/tools/page.tsx` (catalog), `src/app/build/types/{new,[key]/edit}/page.tsx`, `src/components/build/TypeBuilder.tsx` (banner), `src/components/canvas/ItemCanvas.tsx` + `src/app/@modal/(.)items/[id]/page.tsx` (pass capability), `scripts/verify-bespoke-capability.mts`, `scripts/verify-templates.mts`. No new dependency.

## ADR-052: Slice 37 — the weekly health check (Phase 3, Tier 3b): a deterministic scheduled self-monitor
**Date:** 2026-06-14
**Status:** accepted. **Not core** — a scheduled cron over existing canaries + the existing Web Push sender, no data-model, body-format, or MCP-contract change, so it's "move fast, solo." Shipped solo per Brandon's standing Tier direction ("build the next tier"); flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`. Advances roadmap **Phase 3, Tier 3 — the Claude layer** (the second of its three items: MCP server done in ADR-047, this is "scheduled Claude tasks," the selective Notion migration remains). **Renumbered on merge:** authored on the `claude/next-tier-slices-opeeao` branch as ADR-048; that number was taken on `main` by the Papers module (and 049/050/051 followed), so it became ADR-052 when the branch merged in (2026-06-14).
**Context:** PRD §5.5 lists "scheduled Claude tasks (morning briefing, weekly health check)" and §6.2 spells the health one out: "a weekly scheduled Claude task hits `/health` and emails Brandon on failure." The morning-briefing half already exists in its deterministic form — the daily agenda push (slice 30, ADR-034) is a count summary of the day. This slice builds the missing sibling, the weekly health check: the "no silent failures" guard (Principle 9) and specifically the §12 failure mode where GitHub Actions auto-disables after 60 days of repo inactivity and a sync stalls unnoticed.
**The Principle-3 tension, resolved deterministically.** Principle 3 says "AI lives only in the deliberate, human-in-the-loop Claude/MCP layer, **never in a cron job**." A literal "scheduled *Claude* task" that calls the Anthropic API on a timer to author prose would violate that — and amending a principle is a both-agree+ADR core decision, not a solo call. So this job is **plain code, no model**: it reads canaries and applies fixed rules. The richer AI-authored briefing the PRD imagines stays human-in-the-loop (ask Claude over the MCP server, ADR-047, which can already read everything). If Brandon later wants model-authored scheduled output, that's a separate, principle-amending decision (and a line on the $0 cost target) — noted, not taken here.
**Decision:**
1. **`gatherHealth()` extracted to `src/lib/health.ts`.** The `/health` route's snapshot logic (DB check, every job canary, MCP/Graph, captured errors) moved into one function returning a typed `HealthReport`; the route is now a thin wrapper. So the self-monitor reads the **exact same canaries** in-process rather than self-calling its HTTP endpoint — cleaner than §6.2's "hits `/health`" phrasing, and it still works when routing itself is the problem. The JSON shape is unchanged (additive: a new `checks.healthCheck`).
2. **A pure `evaluateHealth(report, recentErrorCount, now)` → `HealthAlert[]`** (in `src/lib/health-check.ts`, node-testable, the M5/M6 discipline). Fixed, deterministic rules: **DB down** → critical; **captured errors** over a 7-day window → warn; a **configured-and-failing Graph grant** → warn (the secret-expiry alarm); a **stalled scheduled job** → warn. Alerts sort critical-first so the push leads with what matters.
3. **"Stalled, not merely unconfigured."** A freshness rule fires only when a job *ran before* (its `…RunAt` canary is set) but its last clean success is older than a per-job budget (export 48h, calendar/todoist 24h, email 12h, agenda 48h). A job that never ran is a Brandon-step, not a fault, and stays silent — the alpha posture and Sunday-proofing both say don't cry wolf.
4. **`runHealthCheck(ownerId, sender, opts)`** gathers (or takes an injected report, for tests), evaluates, and on a non-empty alert list **pushes once** via the existing `PushSender`/`sendToOwner` (slice 30) and stamps `job_state` `health:check` with `lastAlertAt` + the alerts; on a clean run it stamps `lastSuccessAt` and stays **silent** (PRD §6.2 is failure-only). The sender may be **null** (VAPID unset): the job still evaluates and records — the value is the self-monitoring, not only the notification. **Findings are written to `job_state`, never `error_log`**, so rule-2 can't feed back on itself.
5. **Delivery is Web Push, not email.** §6.2 says "emails Brandon," but `email-out` isn't built (parked, §5.4) and push is the channel Ledgr already has. `checks.healthCheck` in `/health` is the durable record either way.
6. **`GET /api/machine/health-check`** (cron-scoped machine token) + **`.github/workflows/health-check.yml`** (weekly Mon 13:00 UTC). Weekly rides the GitHub Actions scheduler seam like notify-prep — the same `LEDGR_CRON_TOKEN`, swappable for a local cron in Phase 4. A non-200 fails the workflow loudly (GitHub emails) — a second, transport-level signal independent of the app.
**Why / alternatives:** *Call `/health` over HTTP from the job* (§6.2's literal phrasing) — rejected for an in-process `gatherHealth()` (no self-HTTP/token juggling; works when routing is the fault). *Write alerts to `error_log`* — rejected (it'd feed the "captured errors" rule a week later, a false-alarm loop); `job_state` + the canary instead. *Send a weekly "all green" push* — rejected (notification spam; failure-only per §6.2). *Alert on any unconfigured integration* — rejected (everything is Brandon-step-blocked in alpha; only a *previously-working, now-stalled* job alerts). *Model-authored briefing* — deferred; would amend Principle 3 (core, both-agree) and the cost target.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` clean (re-run after merge into current `main`). The pure evaluator proven 15/15 against synthetic snapshots (green→no alerts; DB-down→critical; errors→warn with window naming; Graph configured-failing alerts while unconfigured stays quiet; stalled-vs-never-ran-vs-fresh; per-budget; critical-sorts-first). `scripts/verify-health-check.mts` carries the DB-backed half (an unhealthy injected report pushes + stamps `lastAlertAt`; a healthy one is silent + stamps `lastSuccessAt`; a null sender still records). `next build` is the Vercel production gate (dev server up locally). **Brandon-step to light it up:** none new — the weekly workflow uses the existing `LEDGR_CRON_TOKEN`, and delivery uses the existing VAPID keys (§1e); until VAPID is set the check still runs and records to `/health`, it just can't push.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/health.ts` (extracted `gatherHealth` + `HealthReport`), `src/lib/health-check.ts`, `src/app/api/machine/health-check/route.ts`, `.github/workflows/health-check.yml`, `scripts/verify-health-check.mts`; edited `src/app/health/route.ts` (thin wrapper + the `healthCheck` canary), `runbook.md` (§2 canary, §2a job table). No new dependency, no schema/DB change.

## ADR-053: Per-owner UI settings store + highlight-color theming (v5 UI batch)
**Date:** 2026-06-14
**Status:** accepted (Brandon agreed to the core schema touch; this ADR is the "both-agree + ADR" record). **Core-adjacent** — adds a `users.settings jsonb` column (migration 0012), the first per-owner preferences store. Shipped on `v5-ui-changes` with the 15 UI feedback items and merged to main after Brandon's nod.
**Context:** Several v5 feedback items needed a place to persist a per-owner preference: a highlight-accent color, the Trash retention window, and the nav position. Three one-off columns (or tables) would be three migrations and three core touches; a single jsonb blob is one.
**Decision:**
1. **`users.settings jsonb`** (nullable). Shape parsed + defaulted in `src/lib/settings.ts` (`UserSettings` = `{highlightColor, trashRetentionDays, navPosition}`, `parseSettings` validates against the palette/ranges so a partial/hand-edited blob is always safe). `getSettings`/`updateSettings` are owner-scoped. `GET`/`PATCH /api/settings`; `/settings` page.
2. **Highlight color is themed via a CSS variable.** The root layout reads the owner's setting and sets `--accent` inline on `<body>`; `:root` carries the default. Accent buttons/badges use `var(--accent)`. The live picker writes `--accent` on `<body>` (not `<html>`) so the change is instant.
3. **nav position drives both the nav chrome and the layout body padding** (top/bottom/left/right; left/right = a desktop side rail, mobile stays the bottom bar). Trash retention feeds the Trash purge/UI.
**Why a blob, not columns:** preferences are read together (layout + nav), rarely queried individually, and grow over time; a jsonb avoids a migration per preference. Validated-on-read keeps it honest.
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (users.settings), migration 0012, `src/lib/settings.ts`, `src/app/api/settings/route.ts`, `src/app/settings/page.tsx`, `src/components/settings/SettingsForm.tsx`, `src/app/layout.tsx` (--accent + body padding), `src/app/globals.css` (--accent default), nav (`Nav.tsx`/`NavShell.tsx`), Trash (`/trash`), and the accent-using components. **Coordination:** other instances must run `npm run db:migrate` after pulling (adds 0012). `BuildModeButton.tsx` is now unused (Build moved into the nav kebab).

---

## ADR-054: Changelog + shared collab notes — GitHub as the cross-deploy shared medium
**Date:** 2026-06-14
**Status:** accepted. **Not core** — a new non-core page + a per-instance integration (like Todoist/Graph), no schema, body-format, type/canvas, module-boundary, or MCP-contract change. Tyler's slice, shipped solo and flagged to Brandon in `COLLAB.md`.
**Context:** Tyler wanted, in the kebab "More" menu, a Changelog (a 3/4-canvas list of "roughly how many things changed in a push + a quick summary") next to a 1/4 markdown notes panel where he and Brandon leave each other notes and clear them once read. The wrinkle: Brandon and Tyler run **separate single-tenant deploys** (separate Vercel + Neon), so a DB-backed page would only ever show one person's data on their own instance — defeating "see what each other did." The shared data has to live somewhere both deploys reach. (Decided with Tyler: shared data via **git-committed files**, and the changelog **derived live from commits**, not manually authored.)
**Decision:**
1. **GitHub is the shared medium** (git already is for `COLLAB.md`/`decisions.md`). The **Changelog reads the repo's commit history live** via the GitHub REST API; the **collab notes live in a committed file** (`COLLAB_NOTES.md`) read and written via the Contents API. Both deploys point at the same repo, so each sees the other's pushes and notes. **One PAT, plain `fetch`, no Octokit** (Principle 5; the Graph/Todoist hand-roll precedent).
2. **`src/lib/github/client.ts`** — config (`getGithubConfig`, null = "not configured", the storage/Graph posture), `getChangelog` (one cached list call + per-commit immutable detail for the file/line counts = "roughly how much changed"), `readNotes`/`writeNotes` (Contents API; `writeNotes` passes the prior blob sha so a stale Save returns 409 instead of clobbering a concurrent edit; `ensureNotesBranch` auto-creates a non-deploy notes branch when configured), `checkGithub` health canary. Pure parse seams (`toChangelogEntry`, `decodeContent`) are node-testable.
3. **`/changelog` page** (server component): 3/4 commit list grouped by day with author/time/stats/sha; 1/4 `CollabNotes` client panel (reuses `LazyMarkdownEditor` in controlled mode; explicit Save/Clear; 409 → "reload" prompt). **`GET`/`PUT /api/collab/notes`**, owner-guarded. Kebab "More" gained a Changelog link. `checks.github` added to `gatherHealth`.
**Why live-from-commits, not a manual changelog file:** the source of truth for "what was pushed" *is* git; deriving from commits means zero authoring step and it's always current. Notes are the one thing that needs runtime read/write, so they're the committed file (cleared = a commit of empty content).
**Trade-off (documented):** a notes Save commits to the repo, and a commit on the deploy branch triggers a Vercel build. `GITHUB_NOTES_BRANCH` (e.g. `collab-notes`, auto-created, not deployed) opts out of that churn; default leaves notes on the deploy branch (fine during alpha, where pushes deploy constantly anyway).
**Affects:** new `src/lib/github/client.ts`, `src/app/changelog/page.tsx`, `src/components/changelog/CollabNotes.tsx`, `src/app/api/collab/notes/route.ts`, `scripts/verify-changelog.mts` (21/21); edits to `src/components/nav/NavShell.tsx` (kebab link), `src/lib/health.ts` (+ `github` canary; `verify-health-check.mts` synthetic updated), `.env.example`/`runbook.md` (§1g + env table + `checks.github`); new `COLLAB_NOTES.md` seed. **Brandon-step (to use it live):** set `GITHUB_TOKEN` per runbook §1g; until then both surfaces show a clean "not connected" state.

---

## ADR-055: Retire the `entity` meta-type → bespoke `person`; drop the `kind` column; universalize the interactive related list
**Date:** 2026-06-14
**Status:** accepted (Brandon + Tyler agreed; **CORE** — touches the data model, the type model, and the relation substrate, so it took the "both-agree + ADR" path). Supersedes the entity half of ADR-003 (the `kind` column) and resolves exploration `entity-vs-custom-type.md`.
**Context:** Since the Build surface (slice 33, ADR-044) lets any type carry its own properties and relate to anything, the dedicated `entity` type was doing two separable jobs: (a) the universal "thing everything links to" *and* (b) the bespoke people/orgs type the calendar matchers need. Job (a) is now generic (the `relations` table has no type restriction; any item links to any item). What was left was a single `entity` type fanned out by a `kind` column (person/org/project/topic/campus, ADR-003) — i.e. one meta-type re-implementing "types" via a column, which predates and is obsoleted by the real type registry. Confusing, not architectural.
**Decision:**
1. **`entity` → a single bespoke `person` system type.** Brandon uses only the person anchor; org/project/topic/campus are not seeded (create them as their own types if ever wanted). Migration 0013 inserts `person`, repoints `items`/`templates` rows from `entity`, drops the `entity` row.
2. **The `items.kind` column is dropped entirely** (migration 0013), and removed from the generated FTS tsvector (rebuilt without it; the `items_search_gin` index recreated). Sub-classifying a person (staff/volunteer) is a `select` *property* on the type, not a built-in column. `DEFAULT_ENTITY_KINDS`/`distinctEntityKinds` and all kind UI (capture, field strip, view filter/group/column, MCP `kind` param) are gone.
3. **The interactive related list is now universal.** The entity-only `EmbeddedView` (inline check-off / create-inherits / remove-as-unrelate) was folded into `RelatedPanel` so **every** item's detail page gets it: related tasks check off and edit their due date in place (`RelatedRow`, `NewRelatedTask`). The canvas (markdown editor) stays pure; the panel lives at the bottom of the item, which is what Brandon wanted. `EmbeddedView.tsx` deleted; the `itemType !== "entity"` empty-state special-case removed.
4. **The `entityId` filter was renamed `relatedTo`** across `views.ts`/`search.ts`/`/api/items/query`/MCP — it was always "items related to this id, either direction, confirmed only," never entity-specific. Calendar/meeting machinery repointed from `e.type='entity'` to `'person'` (`getMeetingPeople`, export `listPersonTitles`, export frontmatter key `entities:` → `people:`); the matcher *engine* needed no change (it was already type-agnostic). `listEntityOptions` → `listPersonOptions`; `/entities` route deleted (People rides the generic `/list/person`).
**Why / alternatives:** Considered (a) keeping `entity` and just generalizing the affordances — rejected as leaving the confusing meta-type in place; (b) promoting all five kinds to seeded types — rejected because Brandon doesn't use org/project/topic/campus and seeding unused types is its own clutter. **The `relation` property kind stays deferred:** it is NOT required to remove `entity` (the relations table already links any item to any item, and the universal interactive panel covers the critical "check off a person's tasks" need). It remains a future enhancement for *typed* relation fields (a Meeting's "Attendees") and `@`-relate-at-capture.
**Deliberate scope line:** the matcher internals keep their `entityId`/`entityIds` naming (`matchers.action.entityIds` is a persisted jsonb key; the engine attaches item ids of any type and never filters `type='entity'`). Renaming it would need a data migration for a purely cosmetic gain, so it's left as-is. Flagged here so it's a known, intentional exception, not an oversight.
**Affects:** migration `drizzle/0013_dizzy_arclight.sql` (+ snapshot/journal); `src/db/schema.ts` (kind column + FTS); `scripts/seed.mjs`, `src/lib/modules.ts`, `src/lib/type-order.ts` (person system type); item CRUD (`items.ts`, `item-input.ts`, `api/items/route.ts`, `subtasks.ts`); views (`views.ts`, `view-grouping.ts`, `ViewRenderer.tsx`, `ViewBuilder.tsx`); canvas (`MarkdownCanvas.tsx`, `FieldStrip.tsx`, `canvas-fields.ts`); relations (`RelatedPanel.tsx` + new `RelatedRow.tsx`/`NewRelatedTask.tsx`, `EmbeddedView.tsx` deleted); meetings (`prep.ts`, `promote.ts`, `MeetingPrep.tsx`, `push/notify.ts`); export (`engine.ts`); MCP (`tools.ts`, `server.ts`); capture (`CaptureModal.tsx`, `Nav.tsx`, `NavShell.tsx`); search/tasks/templates pages + `SearchClient.tsx`/`TemplateBuilder.tsx`; list routing (`ListTabs.tsx`, `/entities` deleted → `/list/person`); `schema.md`; the affected verify scripts. **Coordination:** other instances must run `npm run db:migrate` then `npm run db:seed` after pulling (migration 0013 drops `kind` and swaps the type; any stored view filtering `type:'entity'` or grouping/filtering by `kind` must be re-saved — alpha, reseed freely).

## ADR-056: Configurable nav slots — the middle nav is owner config, not a hardcoded table
**Date:** 2026-06-15
**Status:** accepted (Tyler solo — **not core**; nav/chrome is per-instance UI, the same lane as the v6 nav redesign and the `railSize`/`navDensity` settings. Flagged to Brandon in `COLLAB.md`.) Closes the deferral noted in ADR-046 / roadmap (the old read-only "Navigation slots" panel on `/build/surface` carried a "later slice" comment; this is that slice). Builds on the build spec `nav-customization-spec.md`.
**Context:** The nav's middle slots were a hardcoded `NAV_SLOTS` array (`src/lib/nav.ts`): not reorderable, not removable, and seeded with developer/admin destinations (Views, Items) that don't belong in daily nav. The `/build/surface` page showed them read-only.
**Decision:**
1. **The middle slots are owner config** in the existing `users.settings` jsonb (no migration — same pattern as the v5/v6 settings). New `navSlots: NavSlotConfig[]` (max 5) + `mobileNavSlots: NavSlotConfig[] | null` (null = mirror desktop; max 4 — the bottom bar is tighter). A slot is either a `destination` (one route: a `builtin` page, a saved `view`, or a `type` list) or a `tools` group (a button that opens a popover of child destinations, max 8, no nesting). Home is always slot 1 and New/More always trail — all three are locked and never stored (prepended/appended at render).
2. **`parseSettings` is the tolerant gate:** unknown icon → the `items` fallback, malformed slot dropped, a slot pointing at Home (`/`) stripped, a nested tools-child flattened to a plain destination, counts capped. A hand-edited or partial blob always yields a safe list.
3. **The icon set is a shared library** (`src/lib/nav-icons.ts`, ~45 hand-rolled SVG glyphs + `navIconPaths`/`isNavIcon`) replacing the `switch(slot)` NavShell carried — no icon-library dependency (Principle 5). `NavGlyph` is the one presentational renderer (server + client).
4. **The Build surface is a live editor** (`NavSlotsEditor` + `NavSlotEditor` + `NavIconPicker`): a live preview bar, native HTML5 drag-reorder (no DnD library), a destination/tools-group form with a searchable icon picker, and the Desktop/Mobile split (mobile mirrors desktop until set custom). It persists the whole array to `PATCH /api/settings` on each change (no partial updates, no new API route).
**Why / alternatives:** Kept the existing `ShellSlot` render path (Nav.tsx resolves config → render-ready slots, counts filled server-side) so the four v6 layouts (bottom pill / top bar / left+right rails) were untouched apart from the icon lookup and a new tools-popover path. A `destination` at `/search` still opens the command palette (parity with the old Search slot). Archive was dropped from the built-in options (no `/archive` route — offering it would dead-link); `/views`/`/items` stay available but are off the default set.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/nav-icons.ts`, `src/lib/nav-slot-options.ts`, `src/components/nav/NavGlyph.tsx`, `src/components/build/NavIconPicker.tsx`/`NavSlotEditor.tsx`/`NavSlotsEditor.tsx`; rewrote `src/components/nav/NavShell.tsx` (icon lookup + tools popovers) + `Nav.tsx` (read config) + `src/app/build/surface/page.tsx` (live editor); `src/lib/settings.ts` (+`NavSlotConfig`, `navSlots`/`mobileNavSlots`, parse); **deleted `src/lib/nav.ts`** (`NAV_SLOTS` gone — `DEFAULT_NAV_SLOTS` now lives in settings). `scripts/verify-nav-and-deletes.mts` covers the pure logic.

## ADR-057: In-context delete confirmation as the standard; type-delete can take its items
**Date:** 2026-06-15
**Status:** accepted (Tyler's call). The confirmation-UI half is **not core** (presentation). The **type-delete cascade touches core** (item-deletion semantics over the `items`/`types` data model) — shipped solo at Tyler's direction under the same waiver pattern as the M6/slice-33 core work, but flagged to Brandon in `COLLAB.md` as a core-touch to ratify. **The hard-delete in decision point 2 below is superseded by ADR-058** (type-delete now soft-deletes to Trash); the in-context-confirm half (point 1) stands.
**Context:** Five destructive actions used the browser `window.confirm()` popup (type/view/template delete, collab-notes clear). And deleting a type that's in use was a dead end — the FK `items.type → types.key` blocks it and the only guidance was "reassign or trash them first," with no way to act on it from the dialog.
**Decision:**
1. **`ConfirmButton` (`src/components/ui/ConfirmButton.tsx`) is the new standard** for any confirm-before-delete: a trigger that opens an in-context popover (title/description, optional extra body, Confirm/Cancel) anchored to itself, closing on outside-click/Esc. `onConfirm` may throw to surface an API error inside the popover. Replaced all five `confirm()` sites (TypeBuilder, ViewBuilder, TemplateBuilder, CollabNotes, plus the new nav-slot remove). No `window.confirm` remains in the app.
2. **A type's delete confirmation can take its items too.** When a type is in use, the popover offers "Also delete the N items using this type." Checked, it calls `DELETE /api/types/[key]?withItems=1` → `deleteTypeWithItems` (`src/lib/types.ts`), which **hard-deletes** the owner's items of that type plus their descendants (recursive on `parent_id`) in one statement, then drops the type. Relations/revisions/attachments cascade (existing FK `ON DELETE cascade`); the type's templates cascade with the type row.
**Why / alternatives:** Hard-delete (not soft-delete to Trash) because a trashed row still carries `type = key` and would keep the FK blocking the type delete — and deleting a type is itself a permanent Build action, so the items go with it. Owner-scoped (the owner-scope-every-query invariant; one user per deploy), with a global re-check before dropping the type row so a cross-owner reference surfaces a clear message rather than a raw FK error. `parent_id` is `NO ACTION` (not `RESTRICT`), so a single statement removing a whole subtree is safe. The UI is explicit that the items are removed permanently, not trashed.
**Affects:** new `src/components/ui/ConfirmButton.tsx`; `src/lib/types.ts` (+`countItemsOfType`, `deleteTypeWithItems`); `src/app/api/types/[key]/route.ts` (`?withItems=1`); `src/app/build/types/[key]/edit/page.tsx` (+`itemCount`); `TypeBuilder.tsx`/`ViewBuilder.tsx`/`TemplateBuilder.tsx`/`CollabNotes.tsx` (confirm → `ConfirmButton`). `scripts/verify-nav-and-deletes.mts` covers the cascade against Neon.

## ADR-058: Types are soft-deleted to Trash (recoverable), not hard-deleted — supersedes ADR-057's hard-delete
**Date:** 2026-06-15
**Status:** accepted (Tyler's call, the same session). **Core-touch** (extends the soft-delete model to the `types` table) — flagged to Brandon in `COLLAB.md` to ratify, like ADR-057. Supersedes decision point 2 of ADR-057.
**Context:** ADR-057 hard-deleted a type's items when deleting the type. That quietly broke the standing **"Soft-delete only. Deletes move to Trash (30-day purge)"** convention (CLAUDE.md) — deleting a type was the one destructive action with no undo. The fix is to bring types into the same Trash model.
**Decision:**
1. **`types` gains a `deleted_at` column** (migration `0014_nice_fantastic_four.sql`). A soft-deleted type stays as a row (so its trashed items keep a valid `items.type → types.key` FK) but drops out of `listTypes()` (registry, pickers, Build list, quick-capture). `getType` still resolves it so labels render for trashed items; `assertTypeExists` excludes it so you can't create/retype an item into a trashed type.
2. **Deleting a type soft-deletes it.** Empty type → `deleteType` stamps `deleted_at`. In-use type via `?withItems=1` → `softDeleteTypeWithItems` stamps the type and its live items (+ descendants, recursive on `parent_id`) with **one shared `now()`** so they form a restorable unit. Items go to Trash, not hard-deleted; relations/revisions/attachments are left intact for a clean restore.
3. **Restore.** `restoreType` (`POST /api/types/[key]/restore`) revives the type and the items that share its `deleted_at`. Restoring a single item from Trash (`restoreItem`) auto-revives its type if that type is soft-deleted — an active item never references a hidden type. The Trash page gained a "Types" section (`listDeletedTypes` + `TypeRestoreButton`) listing soft-deleted types with their trashed-item count.
4. **Purge.** `purgeExpiredTrash` hard-deletes soft-deleted types past the retention window after it purges items (the FK is clear by then; the type's templates cascade with the row).
**Why / alternatives:** Soft-deleting only the type while leaving its items live was rejected — it would orphan live items under a hidden type. Surfacing types as first-class Trash entries (vs. only implicit recovery by restoring an item) was chosen because the user explicitly wanted "the type and the things associated with it" both recoverable. The Trash "N items" label counts the type's own trashed items; restore also brings back their descendants (a deliberate, documented small mismatch).
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` + migration `0014`; `src/lib/types.ts` (`deletedAt` on `TypeDefinition`, `listTypes` filter, `deleteType` soft, `softDeleteTypeWithItems` (was `deleteTypeWithItems`), `restoreType`, `listDeletedTypes`, `countLiveItemsOfType`); `src/lib/items.ts` (`assertTypeExists` excludes deleted, `restoreItem` revives type, `purgeExpiredTrash` purges types); `src/app/api/types/[key]/route.ts` + new `restore/route.ts`; `src/app/trash/page.tsx` + new `src/components/trash/TypeRestoreButton.tsx`; `TypeBuilder.tsx` copy. `scripts/verify-nav-and-deletes.mts` 38/38 (soft-delete, hide-from-registry, restore, auto-revive, create-blocked). **Coordination:** other instances run `npm run db:migrate` after pulling (additive nullable column, safe).

## ADR-059: Hide a type from everyday surfaces (turn off built-ins you don't use)
**Date:** 2026-06-15
**Status:** accepted (Tyler's call). **Core-touch** (a `types` column + a registry-visibility rule) — flagged to Brandon in `COLLAB.md`.
**Context:** The five built-in types (Task, Meeting, Note, Link, Person) are seeded and can't be deleted, but a user may simply not want one (Link is the obvious candidate — see the open question below). They needed a way to turn a built-in off without deleting it or its data.
**Decision:**
1. **`types` gains a `hidden` boolean** (migration `0015`, default false). A hidden type still exists and its items still work, but it drops out of the everyday surfaces: quick capture, the +New menus, the list-tab strip, and the nav-slot destination options. It is **not** blocked from item creation (unlike a soft-deleted type) — hidden is a UI-surfacing flag, not a lifecycle state.
2. **One lever:** `listTypes()` excludes hidden (and deleted) by default; `listTypes({ includeHidden: true })` is used only on the Build → Types page, where you manage visibility. Quick capture (Nav.tsx) and the list tabs (ListTabs) add `hidden = false` to their own queries; ListTabs keeps the active tab even if its type was just hidden, so you're never stranded.
3. **The toggle** is an eye on each Build → Types row (`TypeVisibilityToggle` → `POST /api/types/[key]/hidden` → `setTypeHidden`, then `router.refresh()`); hidden rows are dimmed and labeled. Works for system and user types alike. Editing a type through the builder never touches the column, so the hidden state survives edits.
4. **Types-page polish (same slice):** the page reads as a small table — a **"Quick Capture" column** (a circular checkbox per row that flips `show_in_quick_capture` via `setTypeQuickCapture` → `POST /api/types/[key]/quick-capture`, the same column the builder's checkbox writes) next to the **"Show" (visibility eye)** column; a subtle dashed "Create new type" affordance at the foot of the list (quiet until hover); and a card pointing to the bespoke-tool catalog ("Check our bespoke data types") that names a few live capabilities (Chord Chart, Paper Workspace) so someone building a plain type knows richer pre-built behavior exists to borrow.
**Why / alternatives:** Distinct from `show_in_quick_capture` (capture-only) and `deleted_at` (in Trash, blocks creation): `hidden` is "out of the way everywhere, but still fully usable if you navigate to it." A dedicated lightweight `/hidden` endpoint (vs. routing through the full-definition PATCH) keeps the toggle from having to resend the whole type.
**Open question (for Brandon):** Tyler's view is that **Link shouldn't be a built-in at all** — it should be a bespoke capability a user adds if they want it, leaving the built-ins as Meeting, Note, Person, Task. That's a change to `coreModule`/seed (core, both-agree) — parked in `COLLAB.md` for discussion; the `hidden` flag is the pragmatic interim (hide Link if you don't want it).
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` + migration `0015`; `src/lib/types.ts` (`hidden` on `TypeDefinition`, `listTypes({includeHidden})`, `setTypeHidden`, `setTypeQuickCapture`); `src/components/nav/Nav.tsx` + `src/components/lists/ListTabs.tsx` (filter hidden); new `src/app/api/types/[key]/hidden/route.ts` + `quick-capture/route.ts` + `src/components/build/TypeVisibilityToggle.tsx` + `TypeQuickCaptureToggle.tsx`; `src/app/build/types/page.tsx` (Quick Capture + Show columns, create affordance, catalog card). `scripts/verify-nav-and-deletes.mts` covers both flags. **Coordination:** `npm run db:migrate` after pulling (additive non-null-with-default column, safe).

---

## ADR-060: Pre-built Bible/passage relational database — verse is the atomic unit
**Date:** 2026-06-14 (Brandon + Tyler build meeting; logged 2026-06-15)
**Status:** accepted. **Core** — a data-model/relational decision (the `passage` relational hub, how references resolve into the relation graph). Both agreed in the 6.14 session. Adopts and closes `explorations/scripture-passages-as-entities.md`. The module *build* (the table seed, the auto-tagger) is non-core module work and lives in the build queue, not the foundational rework. *(Numbered 060 because the same-evening entity→person retirement and the nav/type batch took 055–059.)*
**Context:** A long debate over how scripture references should connect to content. Tyler argued for **pre-shipping** the whole Bible as a relational structure so every reference auto-connects; Brandon initially argued free-typed tags (Notion-style "type a tag, press Enter to create") already covered it. The resolution went to pre-built: a free-typed tag does not guarantee correct *shape* and only tags *one side* of the relation, so you'd still have to visit every other item to tag it consistently ("did I tag it with generosity or giving?"). A pre-built relational table removes the two-sided tagging burden entirely and makes "show me everything I have on Hebrews 11:1" a graph query, not a tag-hygiene exercise.
**Decision:**
1. **Ship the Bible as a pre-built relational structure: book → chapter → verse, with the verse as the atomic unit.** A chapter is the container of its verses; a single-verse reference and a multi-verse passage (e.g. Luke 11:35-36) both resolve through the same structure, with a **passage range linking each individual verse in the range**. Sub-verse granularity (11:35a/b) is explicitly **rejected** as too far.
2. **A deterministic, RefTagger-style auto-tagger** recognizes reference patterns in many surface forms ("Luke 11:35", "LK 11.35", "Luke 1135") and wires the relation automatically. **It is plain code / a cron job, no model in the loop** (Principle 3). Any remaining representation edge cases get resolved with Claude's help during the build, not at runtime.
3. **Modeled as a bespoke `passage` type, related to via the existing `relations` table** — not as a `kind` of a generic "entity." Note (ADR-055): the `entity` meta-type was retired and the `kind` column dropped, so the original "passage as an `entity.kind`" framing in the exploration is superseded; a passage is its own system/bespoke type, a verse is an item, and any other item relates to it through `relations`. This does **not** need the deferred `relation` property kind (item-to-item relations already exist) — the same finding that let ADR-055 drop `entity`.
**Why pre-built over tag-on-demand:** the relational table does the work once for everyone; content connects without retroactive tagging of existing items, and there is no tag-inconsistency drift. Storage cost is negligible (Markdown + relations).
**Affects:** `schema.md` (a `passage` type + its book/chapter/verse rows + relations; forthcoming), the relations engine, a new bespoke Bible/passage module + auto-tagger (build queue). Feeds future passage-organized inputs (Quiet Time Journal API, Logos).

---

## ADR-061: Notes are a module attachable to every type; relations are the primary organizing principle
**Date:** 2026-06-14 (Brandon + Tyler build meeting; logged 2026-06-15)
**Status:** accepted. **Core** — touches the type/module model and how content is organized (part of `explorations/storage-organization.md`). Both agreed in the 6.14 session.
**Context:** Brandon's prior sermon-prep workflow used nested notes (a parent note plus ~3 children: messy brain-dump, quotes/references, a staging/draft). Examining it showed it largely duplicates the Papers module shape. The broader question: are notes organized as **files/folders** or as **notes-inside-notes**, and how does either map to Ledgr's relation graph?
**Decision:**
1. **Notes are a built-in module that can attach to every type** (e.g. notes on a sermon, notes on a meeting), not a standalone silo. This is the same bespoke-module-attaches-to-any-item pattern the rest of the system already uses.
2. **Relational databases (tags, categories, relations) are the primary organizing principle** for how content is organized in Ledgr — chosen over a files/folders model. Even "folder" is reframed relationally ("a child of that folder"). This dovetails with ADR-055 (relations, not a meta-type column, are how things connect). It settles the organize-in-app half of `storage-organization.md`; the export-to-MD-file-tree mapping (one primary parent → folder path, the rest → wiki-links) remains the open part of that exploration.
3. **A "project" is not a functional type** — it is a relational connection across tasks/meetings/notes. Confirmed against live test data: nothing functionally changes about a task when it gains subtasks or a parent project; it just needs relations. Confirms `explorations/project-items.md`.
**Affects:** the notes module design, the type/canvas model docs, `explorations/storage-organization.md` and `project-items.md` (org half resolved here).

---

## ADR-062: Share/Print renders the canvas; a per-property "include in share" flag decides what's exposed
**Date:** 2026-06-14 (Brandon + Tyler build meeting; logged 2026-06-15)
**Status:** accepted. **Core-adjacent** — extends the property schema and the export/share contract (renders-from-Markdown is unchanged; ADR-019/028 lineage). Both agreed in the 6.14 session.
**Context:** Reviewing Share and Print: a meeting's share showed only the canvas, omitting attendees/date/topics, which raised "what exactly should a share include, and who decides?" A Papers Print failed where preview worked, because Print/Share pull from the **canvas**, and that note type's canvas differed from what was expected.
**Decision:**
1. **Share and Print always render the item's canvas/draft — the final product.** This reaffirms the canonical principle: every output renders *from* Markdown, the canvas is the rendered artifact, nothing is stored as a second source.
2. **Each content type decides which fields/properties appear in a share, via a per-property "include in share?" toggle** set when a property is added — mirroring the existing "show in Quick Capture" toggle. The per-type field choices themselves are answered type by type as modules are built (open, not blocking).
**Open (tracked, not blocking):** whether multiple share links per item is intentional (the "new share link" UI implies more than one) — to investigate. The default per-type field sets are unresolved and decided per module.
**Affects:** the property schema (a per-property share flag), the Share/Print render path, `schema.md` (note the flag).

---

## ADR-063: Build mode gets a fixed left sidebar; Work/Build is "two modes, one rule"; universal command palette
**Date:** 2026-06-15
**Status:** accepted (Tyler's lane — UI/chrome). **Mostly non-core** (nav chrome, new Build pages, a search component). One Work-nav-config touch (the destination picker's "Build tools" category) is additive over ADR-056. Flagged to Brandon in `COLLAB.md`: the `/build/views` producer/consumer split (he built the original `/build` "Views" card → `/views`) and the User-Settings-housed-in-both resolution. From `build-mode-restructure-spec.md`.
**Context:** The Work/Build switch (ADR-044) opened a Build *home* that was a card grid duplicating navigation, and `/views` straddled "use a view" and "build a view." Build needed a real, scannable home for its growing set of tools, and the use/build line needed stating as a principle.
**Decision:**
1. **Two modes, one rule** (written into CLAUDE.md): *Work is for using the system; Build is for building and maintaining it.* The separation is the **default, not a wall** — any route is a valid nav destination, and a power user can pull a Build tool into their Work nav. Opt-in, invisible by default.
2. **Build mode gets a fixed, hardcoded left sidebar** (`BuildSidebar.tsx`), replacing the Work bottom bar/rail in Build (`/build*`). Three groups under three verbs — **DATA** (Types & Properties, Templates, Workflows & Wikis, Bespoke Tools), **INTERFACE** (Views, Work Surface), **MAINTAIN** (Model Overview, Data Hygiene, Import & Migration, Claude & MCP, User Settings). Dropdowns sparingly (the Vercel discipline): only **Types & Properties** expands this phase (lists the user's actual types for a quick edit-jump). Desktop-first; mobile collapses to a hamburger drawer (explicitly not a focus this phase). Structure lives in **`src/lib/build-nav.ts`** — the single source of truth for the sidebar *and* the destination picker's "Build tools" category.
3. **`/build` home becomes the System Overview (= Model Overview)** — the card grid is retired (the sidebar navigates now). v1 is informational: type/item/view/template counts, which views are on Work, and a "Needs attention" seed (types with zero items → the seed of Data Hygiene).
4. **Producer/consumer split for views:** `/views` stays on the Work side (browse/open/run — the consumer); new **`/build/views`** is the builder/manager (the producer, the INTERFACE → Views entry). The builder routes (`/views/new`, `/views/[id]/edit`) stay put for now; the manager links into them. *(Brandon to confirm.)*
5. **Universal command palette (⌘K), `CommandPalette.tsx`** — one surface in both modes searching everything: items (FTS API), built-in pages, views, types, Build/Maintain sections, named settings. Grouped, context-aware ranking (content-first in Work, structure-first in Build) via the pure `src/lib/command-index.ts`. Result model is a **`destination | action` union** from the start (only destinations produced this phase — the populate-later seam). Supersedes the old `SearchModal`.
6. **"Build tools" category in the Work-nav destination picker** (ADR-056) — every Build entry offered as a slot destination, so the cross-the-line capability is discoverable.
7. **Chrome:** in Build the wordmark is **"Build Mode"** with a slow accent glow (`.build-wordmark`, a breathing `@keyframes`, reduced-motion respected); the Work More-menu door is destination-named **"Build"**, the sidebar's way out is **"Back to Work."** **User Settings** is the one deliberate both-places entry (Work kebab + Build sidebar); `/settings` keeps the Work nav and its H1 is now "User Settings" (never bare "Settings"). `/views` no longer reads as Build (`isBuildPath` = `/build*` only).
8. **Stubs:** `/build/hygiene`, `/build/import`, `/build/claude` are real routes with a title + a one-paragraph plan-note (`BuildStub.tsx`), so the sidebar never dead-links; the tools themselves are later phases.
**Why / alternatives:** A hardcoded sidebar (not a configurable slot bar) is the clean paradigm break from Work — Build is a system surface, not user-shaped, so no DB row. Keeping the builder routes under `/views` for now (vs. moving them under `/build/views`) minimizes Brandon coordination while still drawing the producer/consumer line. The action-result union is built in even though unused so adding commands later isn't a refactor.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/build-nav.ts`, `src/lib/command-index.ts`, `src/components/nav/BuildSidebar.tsx`, `src/components/search/CommandPalette.tsx`, `src/components/build/BuildStub.tsx`, `src/app/build/views/page.tsx`, `src/app/build/{hygiene,import,claude}/page.tsx`, `src/app/api/command-index/route.ts`; rewrote `src/app/build/page.tsx` (System Overview); `src/components/nav/NavShell.tsx` (Build-mode swap, padding, palette, `isBuildPath`) + `Nav.tsx` (`buildTypes`); `src/lib/nav-layout.ts` (`BUILD_SIDEBAR_PX`), `src/lib/items.ts` (`itemCountsByType`), `src/lib/nav-slot-options.ts` + `NavSlotEditor.tsx` ("Build tools"), `src/app/views/page.tsx` (consumer copy), `src/app/settings/page.tsx` ("User Settings"), `globals.css` (`.build-wordmark`), CLAUDE.md ("Two modes, one rule"). Deleted the dead `BuildModeButton.tsx` and the superseded `SearchModal.tsx`. No DB migration. `scripts/verify-build-mode.mts` covers the pure pieces.

---

## ADR-064: Customizable dashboards — multiple named dashboards, widgets as jsonb, dashboard-level focus
**Date:** 2026-06-15
**Status:** accepted (Tyler's lane — views/dashboards are explicitly non-core per CLAUDE.md). A new `dashboards` table is an additive schema change, not a touch to core `items`/`types`/`relations`. From the approved plan `~/.claude/plans/ok-let-s-quick-build-crispy-neumann.md` (interview with Brandon). Supersedes the single-dashboard model of ADR-031.
**Context:** ADR-031's dashboard was one per owner: pinned views rendered as uniform 8-item list previews, ordered by a single `views.dashboard_order` integer — no per-widget settings, no layout-faithful rendering, no multiple dashboards. Brandon wanted multiple named dashboards (Home, Today, a project-focused one), each a freely resizable/draggable grid of widgets, where a widget is a "chunk" of a view with its own gear settings, plus a dashboard-level "focus" that scopes every widget to one project at once.
**Decision (Slice 1 — the data/API foundation):**
1. **New `dashboards` table** (migration 0016), one row per dashboard, with the full widget array inline as a `widgets` jsonb column — matching how `views`/`templates` store config as jsonb and keeping a dashboard read to one row + a batched per-widget fan-out (no normalized `dashboard_widgets` table, no join, atomic layout saves). Columns: `name`, `position`, `focus_item_id` (FK items, **ON DELETE SET NULL** so deleting the focus clears it without dropping the dashboard), `widgets`.
2. **Three widget kinds:** `view` (renders a chunk of a saved view), `stat` (a count from a view's filter), `action` (non-data: quick-capture / new-from-template / link). `view`/`stat` require a real `viewId`; `action` has none. **Every data widget is backed by a real saved View** (Brandon's call — no hidden/ad-hoc views).
3. **Widget settings are display-only overrides** (itemLimit, sortOverride, renderStyle compact|faithful, titleOverride for view; label for stat; action config) applied in-memory at render/query time — they **never mutate the backing view** (asserted in the verify script).
4. **Dashboard-level focus** is a pure filter-merge: `applyFocus(filter, focusItemId)` injects `relatedTo=focusItemId` when focus is set and the widget doesn't already pin its own relation. `viewWhere` already restricts `relatedTo` to confirmed edges, so there's no new query logic.
5. **Home/Today assignment** rides `users.settings` (no schema change): nullable `homeDashboardId`/`todayDashboardId`, tolerant-parsed back to null if the id is malformed/removed, so a deleted dashboard silently falls back to the fixed built-in layout. (The `/` and Today route resolution lands in Slice 7.)
