**Affects:** new `src/lib/tasks/provider.ts`, `scripts/verify-tasks-seam.mts`; edited `src/app/api/machine/todoist-sync/route.ts` + `src/app/api/todoist/sync/route.ts` + `src/app/api/todoist/webhook/route.ts` (adapter skip), `src/lib/health.ts` (+`checks.tasksAdapter`), `scripts/verify-health-check.mts` (fixture), `.env.example`, `runbook.md` (§1d), `ledgr-prd.md` (§4.5/§5.2 reversal notes). No new dependency, no migration. **Completes the Native Tasks chunk (ADR-073): tasks are fully native on Brandon's instance.**

## ADR-082: Configurable, category-backed statuses — per-type status schemas + a done-checkbox that keys off a fixed category
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler greenlit the whole Tasks Polish chunk** up front). S2 of the Tasks Polish chunk (finishing touches on Native Tasks). **CORE** — it changes the `items.status` shape and the machine/MCP status contract. **Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`.**
**Decision:**
1. **Status splits into a user-defined *key* + a fixed *category*.** `items.status` becomes **text** (a slug from the type's schema; `open`/`done`/`archived` are preserved verbatim, so no existing row is rewritten). A new **`items.status_category`** enum — `not_started | in_progress | done | archived` — is denormalized alongside and **every hot path keys off it, never the label**: Today, the default task filter, the subtask-progress rollup, the done-checkbox, recurrence-complete, the meeting/push/ICS/export queries. "Active" = `not_started ∪ in_progress` (`ACTIVE_CATEGORIES`), exactly what `status='open'` meant before.
2. **Statuses are defined per type** (`types.status_schema` jsonb: an ordered `{key,label,category,color,isDefault}[]`; null = **inherit the system default** — To Do / Done / Archived, the original three recategorized). The **In Progress category ships empty**: the plumbing is ready, so adding one status to it works system-wide with no new wiring (Brandon's explicit ask). The pure engine + helpers live in client-safe **`src/lib/status.ts`** (`parseStatusSchema`/`resolveStatusSchema`/`categoryOfStatus`/`defaultStatusKey`/`validateStatusSchema`); the DB-touching resolver is `src/lib/status-schema.ts` (`statusSchemaForType`, a separate module to avoid an items.ts↔types.ts cycle).
3. **The done-checkbox is a category, not a literal.** A new **`POST /api/items/[id]/complete`** (`toggleItemDone`) resolves the item type's default **done**/**not-started** status server-side and flips between them — so every client checkbox (`SubtaskCheckbox`, `RelatedRow`, widget rows) needs no status schema, and it routes through `updateItem` so a recurring task still advances. The canvas status dropdown weaves a ✓ into done-category options and shows the current status's color dot.
4. **Custom statuses render everywhere, with their colors.** The kanban (`ViewRenderer`/`BoardDnd`) shows **a column for every status in the type's schema, in order, with its color** (not the four bare categories — Brandon's #2). Row chips (`/tasks`, the Related panel, list/agenda) show the label + color; the `/tasks` Status filter offers `active` (default) + each of the type's statuses; the canvas dropdown shows labels + colors + the done-glyph.
5. **A focused Build editor** (`StatusSchemaEditor` on the type edit page → **`PATCH /api/types/[key]/statuses`** → `setTypeStatusSchema`): inherit-vs-custom, add/label/color/default per category. Saving **re-syncs every item's `status_category`** against the new schema (a recategorized status re-buckets existing rows), so the denormalized column never goes stale.
6. **`ViewFilter` gains `statusCategory`** (`active` | the four buckets) for bucket filtering; `status` stays the exact-key filter (it now accepts any slug — an unknown key simply matches nothing). The daily surfaces filter by category; the generic view builder filters by category.
**Why / alternatives:** *A flat status list with no categories* rejected — every existing query, the checkbox, and recurrence need to know "is this active/done/closed" without enumerating labels; the fixed category is that anchor (and answers Brandon's "does the plumbing still work?" — yes, it keys off the category). *Computing category on read (a join to the type schema)* rejected for the hot queries (Today/filter would need a per-row schema lookup); **denormalizing `status_category` onto the item** keeps them an indexed-enum scan (Principle 8), at the cost of a re-sync when the schema recategorizes (bounded, owner-scoped). *Keeping the old `item_status` pgEnum* — retained defined-but-unused so the migration diff stayed additive (dropping it makes drizzle-kit prompt to disambiguate a rename); the Postgres type lingers harmlessly. *A custom popover status dropdown* (fully colored per-option, like ClickUp's) deferred — a native `<select>` with a current-value color dot + a ✓ on done labels delivers the same information with no dependency (Principle 5); revisit as polish. *An owner-global editable default status set* deferred — "inherit" means the system default for now; a type customizes directly (covers Brandon's "add statuses to tasks" need).
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-statuses.mts` — 26 pure checks (parse tolerance, resolve, category lookup, default-per-category, the active set, strict save validation: rejects empty/no-done/no-active/bad-slug/missing-color, normalizes one default per category) ALL PASS. **In-browser against live Neon:** the editor route persisted a custom task schema (To Do/In Progress/Research/Done/Archived) and re-synced categories; a task set to "Research" read category `in_progress`; the done-checkbox toggled a non-recurring task Research→Done→To Do (categories tracking) and **advanced** a recurring task instead of completing it; the `/tasks` filter listed the custom statuses + showed a colored "Research" chip; a status board rendered the custom columns with their colors; the canvas dropdown showed the labels, the `Done ✓` glyph, and the current color dot. Regression: `verify-views` (updated — status accepts any key now; statusCategory is validated), `verify-structures`, `verify-recurrence` green. `tsc` + full `next build` + eslint clean; migration 0022 applied to Neon (status→text, status_category backfilled from status, types.status_schema added).
**Affects:** new `src/lib/status.ts`, `src/lib/status-schema.ts`, `src/components/build/StatusSchemaEditor.tsx`, `src/app/api/items/[id]/complete/route.ts`, `src/app/api/types/[key]/statuses/route.ts`, `scripts/verify-statuses.mts`, migration `drizzle/0022_*`; edited `src/db/schema.ts` (status→text + `status_category` enum/column/index + `types.status_schema`), `src/lib/item-enums.ts` (ItemStatus = string), `src/lib/items.ts` (createItem/updateItem set category, `toggleItemDone`, listColumns), `src/lib/item-input.ts` (status = slug), `src/lib/types.ts` (statusSchema on the definition + `setTypeStatusSchema` + re-sync), `src/lib/recurrence-service.ts` (default done/not-started keys + category), `src/lib/views.ts` (`statusCategory` filter), `src/lib/today.ts`/`scheduling.ts`/`ics-data.ts`/`push/notify.ts`/`export/engine.ts`/`starter-widgets.ts`/`meetings/{prep,promote}.ts`/`clone.ts` (category semantics), `src/lib/subtasks.ts` (carry category), and the render surfaces (`FieldStrip`, `MarkdownCanvas`, `ViewRenderer`, `BoardDnd`, `view-grouping.ts`, `ViewBuilder`, `RelatedRow`/`RelatedPanel`, `SubtaskCheckbox`, `Subtasks`, `WidgetBody`, `DashboardView`, `/tasks`, `/items`, `/views/[id]`, today `page.tsx`). Migration 0022; no new dependency.

## ADR-083: Recurrence completions calendar + the inverted occurrence edit (carve-out)
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler greenlit the whole Tasks Polish chunk** up front). S3 of the Tasks Polish chunk. **Not core** — it adds app-level operations over the *existing* recurrence model (ADR-076): no schema change, no change to the `properties.recurrence` shape, no change to the machine/MCP contract or the `tasks` seam. Builds directly on ADR-076 (the per-date completion log) and replaces ADR-076 §9's deferred "this and future" RRULE-split with a cleaner carve-out. **Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`** as a heads-up (it's in the recurrence area; his module-type tasks inherit the calendar for free).
**Context:** ADR-076 shipped the recurrence engine: a virtual series carries an RRULE + a per-date completion log, and the done-checkbox advances `scheduled` to the next uncompleted occurrence. Two gaps remained for daily use: (1) you could only complete *the current* occurrence (the checkbox), never tick a specific past/future date or fix a mistake out of order; (2) ADR-076 §9 cut "edit this occurrence" to a v1 scope-out. S3 closes both, exactly as Brandon settled 2026-06-18.
**Decision:**
1. **Completions = a month-calendar on the recurring task** (TaskNotes "Completions" style). A `RecurrenceCalendar` renders the RRULE projection for the viewed month (occurrence days are buttons, non-occurrence days inert); **every occurrence date is individually checkable in any order**, toggling its entry in the per-date completion log (`properties.recurrence.completeInstances`). The "up next" occurrence is highlighted, completed days filled with a ✓, carved/skipped days struck through.
2. **A toggle is a direct log edit, NOT the checkbox gesture.** New pure helpers in `recurrence.ts` (`isOccurrence`, `toggleCompleteInstance`, `addSkippedInstance`, `instanceState`) mutate only the log — they compute no next date. The service (`toggleOccurrenceCompletion` in `recurrence-service.ts`) applies the toggle then **recomputes `scheduled` = the next uncompleted occurrence on/after *today*** (forward-looking — `nextUncompletedOnOrAfter(rule, today)`), with status following (done + scheduled cleared when nothing remains forward, else not-started). So missed *past* dates stay absent from the log and never resurrect as `scheduled` (ADR-076 §1/§8), but ticking today's occurrence advances and un-ticking it returns. Distinct from `completeOccurrence`/`skipOccurrence`, which branch on the anchor mode for the "I just did the current one" gesture.
3. **The inverted occurrence edit (replaces "this and future").** Editing a recurring task edits the **series** by default. To shape one date differently, **carve it out**: `carveOccurrence` deep-clones the series PROTOTYPE (the shared `cloneItemSubtree`, ADR-076 §6 — fresh unchecked subtasks, fresh body, carried relations, **no** recurrence) into a fresh **DETACHED** one-off scheduled on that date, the series adds the date to `skippedInstances` and advances past it, and the user lands on the new item to edit it. **The carve is NOT linked by the `occurrence` role** (so the materialized create-next-after-completion machinery never fires on it) — completing the carved one-off leaves the series untouched. "Edits never touch the parent," verified.
4. **Virtual-series only.** A materialized series' occurrences are already their own items with their own checkboxes; editing the series log there would desync. The canvas shows the calendar only for `occurrenceMode === "virtual"`, and `toggleOccurrenceCompletion`/`carveOccurrence` guard it (bad_request otherwise).
5. **One endpoint, two actions:** `POST /api/items/[id]/occurrence` with `{action:"toggle"|"carve", date}` (the date must be a valid occurrence; the route validates the YMD). Both recompute the series' scheduled + status server-side, so the client only edits the log. The calendar is a new card (`recurrenceCalendar`, label "Completions") in the field-level canvas vocabulary (ADR-069), placed right after the Repeat control; it's `null` for a non-recurring (or materialized) task, which `ItemRglInner`'s `visibleIds` filter already drops cleanly.
**Why / alternatives:** *A "this and future" RRULE split* (ADR-076 §9) rejected for the carve — splitting a series into two rules is fiddly and rarely what's meant; carving one date into a detached copy is simpler and matches the mental model ("just this one is different"). *Linking the carve by the `occurrence` role* (like a materialized occurrence) rejected — it would trip create-next-after-completion and re-couple the one-off to the series, the opposite of "detached." *Anchoring the scheduled recompute at `dtstart`* (earliest uncompleted ever) rejected — a long-running daily series would resurrect months of untouched past dates as `scheduled`; today-anchored keeps misses absent (ADR-076 §1). *Editing the log via the generic `propertyPatch` from the client* rejected — the server must recompute `scheduled`/status atomically from the edited log, so a dedicated endpoint owns the rule. *Carving on a materialized series* rejected — its occurrences are already separate items. *`window.confirm` for the carve* — banned (ADR-057); an inline confirm bar in the calendar (one UI, two triggers: the per-cell ✎ and the "Edit next occurrence" button) is the in-context standard.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-recurrence-calendar.mts` — pure (`isOccurrence` incl. COUNT/UNTIL bounds, `toggleCompleteInstance` add/remove/sort/dedupe + clears-skipped, `addSkippedInstance`, `instanceState`) + live-Neon service (toggle future = logged + scheduled unchanged; toggle today = scheduled skips to next uncompleted; untoggle returns scheduled; non-occurrence rejected; counted series → done + scheduled cleared; carve = detached one-off scheduled on the date with no recurrence + no occurrence edge + a fresh subtask, series skips + advances, completing the one-off leaves the series put; materialized/non-recurring/owner-scope guards) — **ALL PASS (39 checks)**. Regression: `verify-recurrence` green; `verify-canvas-layout` updated (vocab + completions card) and green. **In-browser against live Neon:** built a weekly-Wed series, the calendar rendered its Wednesdays; ticking Jun 17 marked it ✓ and advanced `scheduled` to Jun 24 (persisted across reload); "Edit next occurrence (Jun 24)" → confirm → carved a detached one-off (scheduled Jun 24, no recurrence, fresh "Prep agenda" subtask) and the series skipped Jun 24 + advanced to Jul 1, navigating to the new item. `tsc` + full `next build` + eslint clean. No migration.
**Affects:** new `src/components/canvas/RecurrenceCalendar.tsx`, `src/app/api/items/[id]/occurrence/route.ts`, `scripts/verify-recurrence-calendar.mts`; edited `src/lib/recurrence.ts` (+`isOccurrence`/`toggleCompleteInstance`/`addSkippedInstance`/`instanceState`/`InstanceState`), `src/lib/recurrence-service.ts` (+`toggleOccurrenceCompletion`/`carveOccurrence`/`writeSeriesLogState`), `src/lib/canvas-layout.ts` (+`recurrenceCalendar` card kind/spec/vocab/label), `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (parse the rule once; mount the calendar in both canvas paths, virtual-only), `scripts/verify-canvas-layout.mts` (vocab assertion). No migration, no new dependency.

## ADR-084: Natural-language quick-add — parse date/recurrence/urgency out of a task title
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler greenlit the whole Tasks Polish chunk** up front). S4 of the Tasks Polish chunk. **Not core** — a pure title parser + capture-UI wiring over the existing item create path; no schema, no MCP/seam change. Extends the hand-rolled NL date parser (ADR-077) and produces a stored RRULE via the recurrence engine (ADR-076).
**Context:** Native tasks own capture now (ADR-080), but creating a task still meant typing a title then setting scheduled/repeat/urgency by hand. Todoist's quick-add ("Call Bob tomorrow p1 every week") is the muscle-memory Brandon wanted: type one line, the date/recurrence/urgency are pulled out, the title left clean.
**Decision:**
1. **A pure title parser** `parseTaskTitle(title, todayYmd)` in `src/lib/nl-date.ts` (the ADR-077 module, extended). Returns `{ title (cleaned), scheduledDate, dueDate, recurrence, urgency, detections[] }`. Reuses `parseNaturalDate` for dates, `makeRecurrence`/`nextOccurrenceOnOrAfter` for the rule. Pure + client-safe (caller passes today), the same constrained-grammar discipline as the rest (Principle 3 — explicit tokens, never an NLP guess).
2. **The grammar** (explicit tokens, scanned anywhere in the title, recurrence stripped first so "every monday" isn't also read as a weekday date):
   - **Date → scheduled** (the plan, ADR-077): `today`/`tomorrow`/`tonight`/`yesterday`/`tmrw`, `in N days|weeks|months`, `next week|month|weekend`, `weekend`, full weekday names, `jun 20`/`20 jun`(+year), `m/d[/yy]`, ISO. **`by <date>` → the due deadline** (the one date that means a hard deadline, not a plan).
   - **Recurrence → RRULE**: `every day|week|month|year`, `daily|weekly|monthly|yearly|annually`, `every N days|weeks|months|years`, `every <weekday>`, `every weekday`/`weekdays`. dtstart = the parsed scheduled date, else today; with no explicit date the first occurrence becomes the scheduled date.
   - **Urgency**: `p1..p4` (Todoist) and `!1..!4` → critical/high/normal/low.
3. **Strip-and-confirm, on save + a manual trigger.** In the global **CaptureModal**, when type = task: a **live "Detected" preview row** shows the chips (📅/⏰/🔁/❗) + the cleaned title as you type (confirm-by-visibility, an explicit token can't surprise you); a **✨ Apply** button (the manual trigger) strips the tokens into the title and commits the fields (scheduled + recurrence as removable chips, due + urgency into the existing controls); and **Create parses again** (parse-on-save) so a title typed and submitted without Apply still resolves. Committed fields win over a re-parse.
4. **Bare dates map to `scheduled`, not `due`.** In Ledgr's model scheduled = the plan (the Todoist-"due" analog: it surfaces the task on Today), due = the hard deadline. So a quick-add date is the plan; only `by <date>` sets the deadline — consistent with ADR-077 and the chunk's scheduled-first direction.
**Why / alternatives:** *A date/NLP dependency (chrono-node)* rejected — Principle 5; the same hand-roll as ADR-076/077, and the confirm step covers ambiguity. *Bare 3-letter weekday abbreviations (mon/tue/…)* excluded from the scanner — they collide with ordinary words ("sat", "wed", "sun") and parse-on-save can't ask; full names + explicit forms are unambiguous (a `\b` also protects `p3` inside "mp3", etc.). *Word-based urgency ("urgent"/"important")* excluded — too collision-prone for silent parse-on-save; `pN`/`!N` are intentional markers. *Auto-switching the capture type to task on a detected token* rejected — capture defaults to the catch-all `unmarked` by design (ADR-067); the user picks Task, then parsing engages (predictable, Principle 3). *Live strip (rewriting the input as you type)* rejected — it fights the cursor; the non-destructive preview + an explicit Apply is calmer.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-nl-task.mts` — 36 pure checks (every date/recurrence/urgency shape, `by <date>` → due, recurrence dtstart + first-occurrence scheduling, combined titles, detection ordering, and the no-false-positive cases: "wedding" not Wednesday, "mp3" not p3, plain titles untouched) — **ALL PASS**. Regression: `verify-scheduling` (the existing nl-date grammar) green. **In-browser against live Neon:** typed "Call Bob tomorrow p1 every week" with type=Task → the Detected row showed 🔁 Weekly · 📅 Jun 19 · ❗ Critical → "Call Bob"; ✨ Apply stripped the title and committed the chips + urgency; Create produced a task (title "Call Bob", scheduled Jun 19, urgency critical, recurrence FREQ=WEEKLY, inbox:true). Parse-on-save also confirmed ("Water plants every 3 days" created without Apply → daily/3, scheduled today). `tsc` + full `next build` + eslint clean. No migration.
**Affects:** new `scripts/verify-nl-task.mts`; edited `src/lib/nl-date.ts` (+`parseTaskTitle`/`ParsedTaskTitle`/`TaskTitleDetection` + recurrence/urgency matchers), `src/components/capture/CaptureModal.tsx` (controlled title, live detection preview + ✨ Apply, scheduled/recurrence chips, parse-on-save in `capture()`). No migration, no new dependency.

## ADR-085: Relative subtask scheduling — a stored offset from the parent's scheduled date, set by calendar-pick
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler greenlit the whole Tasks Polish chunk** up front). S5 of the Tasks Polish chunk. **Not core** — a scheduling behavior over existing data (a new `properties.relativeSchedule` shape, no column/migration), plus additive hooks in two core primitives (`updateItem`, `cloneItemSubtree`). **Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`** (it touches clone.ts + updateItem, which his materialized occurrences + templates ride). This is the "short ADR (subtask date semantics)" S5 called for.
**Context:** A recurring/scheduled task's subtasks usually want to land *relative* to the parent — "send invites 2 days after the event date," "prep the day before." Hard-coding each subtask's absolute date breaks the moment the parent moves or a recurring occurrence lands on a new date. Brandon's call (2026-06-18): store an offset, set it by picking a date (Ledgr back-calculates the offset), recompute per occurrence.
**Decision:**
1. **The offset is the source of truth; `scheduled_date` is derived.** A subtask carries `properties.relativeSchedule = { offsetDays: N }` (jsonb, no column — light owner data like `properties.recurrence`/`focus`). Its `scheduled_date` **column** holds the concrete derived day (parent's scheduled + N), so every existing scheduled query/sort/Today/ICS/overdue-roll keeps working unchanged. N may be negative ("2 days before"). Pure helpers in client-safe **`src/lib/relative-subtask.ts`** (`parseRelativeSchedule`/`relativeOffsetOf`/`offsetBetween`/`applyOffset`/`describeOffset`); calendar-day UTC math (ADR-008).
2. **Set by calendar-pick; Ledgr back-calculates.** The `SubtaskSchedule` control on each task subtask row: pick a date → if the parent has a scheduled date, store `offsetDays = picked − parentScheduled` (relative); with no parent date, store a plain absolute date (no offset). The row shows the date + a `+Nd`/`−Nd` chip.
3. **Recompute triggers (deterministic, no model):** (a) **parent scheduled-date change** — `updateItem` calls `recomputeRelativeChildren` (`src/lib/relative-subtask-service.ts`) whenever a task's `scheduledDate` changes, re-deriving every relative child and **chaining down** (a relative child's own relative children re-derive against the child's new date); (b) the **recurrence advance / S3 calendar toggle/carve** paths (`advanceSeriesRow`/`writeSeriesLogState`) call it too, since they set `scheduled_date` outside `updateItem`; (c) **occurrence materialize** — `cloneItemSubtree` derives a relative child's date from the new clone's scheduled day + the carried offset (the offset isn't stripped), so a materialized occurrence's subtasks land N days out. **Offsets are relative to the IMMEDIATE parent** (they chain), matching "the parent's scheduled date."
4. **No anchor ⇒ cleared, not stale.** If the parent loses its scheduled date, a relative child's derived date clears (the offset stays, so it re-derives when the parent is re-dated). An **absolute** (non-relative) subtask is never touched by a parent move.
**Why / alternatives:** *A `scheduled_offset` column* rejected — it's light owner data and only relative subtasks have it (Principle 2/8: jsonb like recurrence/focus); the hot column stays the concrete `scheduled_date`. *Storing only the offset and computing the date on read* rejected — every scheduled query would need a per-row parent lookup; deriving the concrete date on write keeps reads an indexed scan. *Offset relative to the series root (not the immediate parent)* rejected — "the parent's scheduled date" means the immediate parent, and chaining composes naturally. *Recomputing through `updateItem` (re-entrant)* rejected — `recomputeRelativeChildren` writes children directly and recurses with a depth cap, avoiding the recurrence/mention/category side-effects of a full update. *An absolute-vs-relative toggle in the UI* deferred — picking a date with a dated parent is relative by default (the feature); a future toggle can add a "pin to an absolute date" escape hatch.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-relative-subtasks.mts` — pure (parse tolerance, `offsetBetween`/`applyOffset` incl. negative + month-cross, `describeOffset`) + live-Neon (relative child shifts with the parent, absolute child untouched, clears when the parent loses its date + re-derives when re-dated with the offset preserved, offsets chain parent→child→grandchild, and the clone/materialize path derives a relative child's date while a plain child stays undated) — **ALL PASS (26 checks)**. Regression: `verify-recurrence`/`verify-recurrence-calendar`/`verify-subtasks` green. **In-browser against live Neon:** on a parent scheduled Jun 25, the subtask's "＋ when" → picking Jun 27 stored `relativeSchedule {offsetDays:2}` + scheduled Jun 27; rescheduling the parent to Jul 2 shifted the subtask to Jul 4 (offset preserved); the row chip read "Jul 4 +2d". `tsc` + full `next build` + eslint clean. No migration.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/relative-subtask.ts` (pure), `src/lib/relative-subtask-service.ts` (recompute), `src/components/subtasks/SubtaskSchedule.tsx`, `scripts/verify-relative-subtasks.mts`; edited `src/lib/items.ts` (recompute on scheduled change), `src/lib/recurrence-service.ts` (recompute after advance / calendar log write), `src/lib/clone.ts` (derive relative child dates on clone), `src/lib/subtasks.ts` (+`relativeOffset` on `SubtaskNode`, select `properties`), `src/components/subtasks/Subtasks.tsx` (thread `parentScheduled`, render the control), `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (pass `parentScheduled`). No migration, no new dependency.

## ADR-086: Tasks Polish S6 loose ends — ICS EXDATE, a reminder picker, a focus star on the canvas, a "planned" marker, and the Top-3 focus widget
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler greenlit the whole Tasks Polish chunk** up front). S6 — the final slice of the Tasks Polish chunk, closing named follow-ups from ADR-077/078/079. **Not core** (UI + a non-core `ViewFilter` extension + additive pure ICS fields; no schema/MCP/seam change). **Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`.**
**Context:** ADR-078 (focus), ADR-079 (ICS reminders), and ADR-077 (planned/deferred) each left explicit follow-ups: the focus star only lived on Today, the reminder lead-time the feed honored had no picker, completed occurrences kept reminding, there was no focus dashboard widget, and the "planned" marker was Today-only. S6 closes the high-value, well-bounded ones.
**Decision:**
1. **ICS EXDATE for completed/skipped occurrences.** A recurring task's feed VEVENT now emits `EXDATE;VALUE=DATE:…` for its `completeInstances ∪ skippedInstances` (pure `ics.ts` + `ics-data.ts`), so a subscribing calendar drops days already done or carved out — no stale reminder. EXDATE is emitted only alongside an RRULE.
2. **A per-task reminder picker** (`ReminderControl` on the task canvas): a small dropdown writing `properties.reminder.minutesBefore` (the value the feed already honored, ADR-079) — Default (9 AM) / Midnight / 1 day / 2 days / 1 week before, via the atomic `propertyPatch`.
3. **A focus-today star on the item canvas** — the existing `FocusStar` (ADR-078) mounted on the task canvas (with the current focus state + app-today), so you can star the task you're looking at, not just from Today.
4. **A "planned" marker on the Tasks list** — in the due dimension, a task with a scheduled date but no deadline shows `planned <date>` (mirrors the Today marker, ADR-077), so an empty due column doesn't read as "no date at all."
5. **A Top-3 focus dashboard widget** — a new `ViewFilter.focusedToday` flag (resolved at query time to `properties @> {focus:{date: <today>}}`, index-backed, since the marker auto-clears overnight so "today" can't be stored) + a **"Today's Focus" starter widget**. The dashboards engine (ADR-064/065) runs it through the same `queryViewItems`, so the widget is the verified engine, not new rendering.
**Deferred (documented, lower-value / higher-churn):** the focus star on every list/board *row* (the canvas + Today zone cover the primary surfaces); drag-reorder of the Today focus zone (the `order` field exists); the fully-colored custom status-dropdown popover (ADR-082's optional polish — the native `<select>` with a color dot + ✓ already conveys it). The canvas focus star + reminder picker are **classic-path only** (the default canvas); a custom grid layout can add cards later.
**Why / alternatives:** *VTODO with a status instead of EXDATE* rejected — the feed is VEVENT (ADR-079, universally rendered); EXDATE is the standard way to drop occurrences. *A reminder time-of-day picker* deferred — all-day tasks make "minutes before midnight" the natural lever, and presets cover the real cases without a time widget. *A bespoke "focus" widget kind* rejected — extending `ViewFilter` keeps "every widget is a view" (ADR-064) and reuses the engine + the `properties @>` index (the ADR-072 propertyFilters precedent). *Storing "today" in the focus widget's filter* rejected — the marker auto-clears overnight (ADR-078), so the date must resolve at query time.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-ics.mts` extended (pure: EXDATE emitted for completed/skipped, none without an RRULE; live-Neon: a recurring task's `exdates` = completed ∪ skipped, sorted) and `scripts/verify-views.mts` extended (live-Neon: `focusedToday` returns today's focus + excludes other days; parses) — both **ALL PASS**. Regression: `verify-focus` green. **In-browser against live Neon:** the task canvas showed the focus star + reminder dropdown; starring set `properties.focus={date:today,…}` and the reminder set `properties.reminder.minutesBefore=1440`; a future-scheduled, deadline-less task showed "planned Jun 30" on the Tasks list. `tsc` + full `next build` + eslint clean. No migration.
**Affects:** new `src/components/canvas/ReminderControl.tsx`; edited `src/lib/ics.ts` (+`exdates` + EXDATE emission), `src/lib/ics-data.ts` (set `exdates` from the log), `src/lib/views.ts` (`focusedToday` filter + parse), `src/lib/starter-widgets.ts` (+"Today's Focus"), `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (focus star + reminder on the task canvas), `src/app/tasks/page.tsx` ("planned" badge), `scripts/verify-ics.mts` + `scripts/verify-views.mts`. No migration, no new dependency. **Completes the Tasks Polish chunk (S1–S6).**

## ADR-087: Meeting recording v1a — the `transcript` child type, the Transcript panel + awaiting-minutes view, and the Principle-3 reading for a Claude-over-MCP minutes automation
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler pre-approved the feature and all three core touches** 2026-06-18, see `explorations/meeting-recording.md` "Core flags" + the COLLAB approval). This is **v1a** of the meeting-recording chunk (paste-first; no audio pipeline yet — that's v1b). The data/UI pieces (the `transcript` type, the panel, the view) are **non-core**; **the Principle-3 interpretation in point 5 is the CORE element this ADR ratifies.** **Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`.**
**Context:** Meeting recording → transcription → AI minutes is a committed 1.0 item. The converged design (`explorations/meeting-recording.md`, 2026-06-18) made the **transcript the pivot** (audio is disposable, deferred to v1b), upload/paste-only, privacy not a blocker, and — the key move — **processing is a Claude-over-MCP workflow, not an in-app LLM call.** v1a proves the valuable part (transcript → minutes + tasks) with almost no new infrastructure: no outbound LLM call, no transcription service, no storage concern.
**Decision:**
1. **A transcript is its own item, not a region of the meeting body.** A new `transcript` system type (migration 0023 + `seed.mjs`; `is_system`, visible, `show_in_quick_capture=false`). Rationale: a 20k–35k-word transcript would swamp the meeting body editor and the human-facing doc; a separate item also lets a meeting carry several transcripts. It is **not** added to `coreModule` — an unregistered seeded type falls back to the default markdown canvas (the same path `paper`/`song` would take if unregistered), so no core module edit.
2. **A transcript is tied to its meeting two ways, deliberately.** `parent_id = the meeting` (containment — the subtask soft-delete cascade carries it to Trash) **and** a confirmed `relations` edge `meeting→transcript`, role `transcript` (association). The edge is what makes the connection first-class to the MCP graph: `get_item(meeting)` lists its transcripts in `related`, and `list_items(type=transcript, relatedTo=<meeting>)` finds them — so "look at recent meetings, pull their transcripts, explore" is one hop, not a fragile title search (Brandon's explicit concern). `createTranscript` (`src/lib/meetings/transcripts.ts`) writes both in one place so a transcript can't exist invisible to the automation.
3. **The "needs minutes" signal is a `select` property on the transcript** (`minutes`: `none`/`draft`/`done`), seeded in the type's `property_schema`; new transcripts are stamped `minutes=none` at create so the index-backed `properties @>` filter matches. A saved view **"Transcripts awaiting minutes"** (`type=transcript`, `propertyFilters:[{minutes:none}]`, seeded per owner by `scripts/seed-meeting-views.mts`) is the automation's work queue. `none` → processed → `draft` → reviewed → `done`; only `none` is "awaiting," so the automation never double-processes.
4. **Minutes land in the meeting body; suggested tasks land in the Inbox related to the meeting** (Brandon's leanings). Tasks are real `task` items (`inbox=true`, `relateTo` the meeting), not `unmarked` — they're unambiguously action items, so forcing a retype would be friction. (Trivially changed; it's a line in the prompt.)
5. **CORE — the Principle-3 reading (this ADR amends how Principle 3 is applied).** Principle 3 says "AI lives only in the deliberate Claude/MCP layer, never in a cron job." A *scheduled* Claude-over-MCP automation brushes against the "never in a cron" clause. The ratified reading: **the principle keeps Ledgr's own backend model-free and deterministic** (no Anthropic key in the app, no model in a Ledgr cron, no summary seam) — and an **external** Claude automation hitting the public MCP/API and producing **staged** outputs (minutes as a draft you edit, tasks in the Inbox for triage, the transcript left `draft` not `done`) **honors that intent**. The safeguard that keeps it clean is that **nothing auto-commits**; the human-in-the-loop staging is load-bearing, not incidental. The processing prompt is documented (`docs/meeting-minutes-automation.md`) and surfaced on Build → AI & MCP; it satisfies "tweak the prompt" for free (it's text Brandon edits) and generalizes as the blueprint for every future "AI on purpose" feature. If Brandon ever wants it fully hands-off (auto-commit), that's a further decision.
**Why / alternatives:** *Transcript as a `## Transcript` region in the meeting body* rejected — swamps the editor + the doc, and forecloses multiple transcripts. *minutes-state on the meeting* rejected in favor of the transcript — "Transcripts awaiting minutes" is then a clean single-type view, and the transcript is the unit the automation processes. *An in-app `generate_minutes` MCP tool / outbound LLM call* deferred (v1b "Deferred" list) — the existing 12 tools (ADR-047/071) already express the whole flow (`run_view`→`get_item`→`update_item`→`create_item`→`update_item` with `propertyPatch`), so v1a needs no new tool and no first outbound LLM call. *A typed `relation` property "Transcripts" on the meeting type* (ADR-067) rejected for the surface — the bespoke Transcript panel is the richer surface; a plain role-`transcript` edge gives the graph/Related-panel discoverability without a redundant field box.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-meeting-transcripts.mts` **16/16 on live Neon** — create writes the child + the confirmed `transcript` edge + `minutes=none`; the MCP-discovery path (`get_item(meeting).related` and `list_items(relatedTo)` both surface the transcript); word counts; the awaiting-minutes filter (none in, draft/done out); guards (parent must be the owner's live meeting). `scripts/verify-canvas-layout.mts` still green (new `meetingTranscripts` card in the meeting vocabulary). `tsc` + full `next build` + eslint clean. **In-browser on live Neon:** opened a meeting → Transcript panel; pasted a transcript → appeared as "No minutes yet · N words"; opened the transcript → full editor + the Minutes dropdown (none/draft/done); the awaiting view listed it; setting `minutes=done` via the canvas (the `propertyPatch` write the automation uses) dropped it from the view. Test data cleaned up.
**Affects:** migration `drizzle/0023_meeting_transcript_type.sql` (+ journal/snapshot) + `scripts/seed.mjs` (the `transcript` type); new `src/lib/meetings/transcripts.ts`, `src/app/api/meetings/[id]/transcripts/route.ts`, `src/components/meetings/MeetingTranscripts.tsx` + `AddTranscript.tsx`; edited `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (the panel, classic + grid card) and `src/lib/canvas-layout.ts` (the `meetingTranscripts` card); new `scripts/seed-meeting-views.mts` (the awaiting view), `scripts/verify-meeting-transcripts.mts`, `docs/meeting-minutes-automation.md`; edited `src/app/build/claude/page.tsx` (the Automations section). **v1b (the `transcription` provider seam + AssemblyAI adapter, audio upload, the `attachments.purge_after` retention column + purge) is deferred to its own ADRs (the other two pre-approved core touches).**

## ADR-088: The `transcription` provider seam + an AssemblyAI adapter (meeting recording v1b)
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler pre-approved — the `transcription` seam is one of the three pre-approved core touches**, `explorations/meeting-recording.md` "Core flags"). **CORE** (provider interfaces are core), additive, mirrors the existing seams. **Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`.** This is **V1b-1** of the meeting-recording chunk; audio upload/auto-transcribe (V1b-2) and audio retention (V1b-3, ADR-089) build on it.
**Context:** v1a (ADR-087) made the transcript the pivot and shipped the paste path. v1b adds *convenience* transcription: upload audio, Ledgr transcribes it into a transcript. Per CLAUDE.md provider-interface discipline (storage/auth/scheduler/calendar/mail/push/tasks), the transcription API must sit behind a thin seam so the adapter can be swapped and a future local build is a packaging exercise. Transcription is a deterministic, user-triggered API call — fine under Principle 3 (the model here is a speech-to-text service, not a reasoning step; only the *minutes* are "AI on purpose," and those stay in the Claude-over-MCP layer, ADR-087).
**Decision:**
1. **A `transcription` provider seam** (`src/lib/transcription/{types,provider,assemblyai}.ts`), env-selected, **null-safe** (returns `null` when unconfigured, exactly like `getStorage()`), so the paste path and the whole app work without it — audio transcription is simply not offered. The interface is a **submit + poll job model** (`submit(audioUrl, opts) → {jobId}`, `poll(jobId) → TranscriptionResult`), because long meetings transcribe over minutes and a serverless request can't block that long; the caller submits on upload and polls from a status check/cron. `TranscriptionResult` carries `status` (queued/processing/completed/error), `text`, diarized `segments` (`{speaker, start, end, text}`), and `error`. A pure `transcriptToMarkdown` renders a finished transcript (diarized → "**Speaker A:** …" paragraphs; plain otherwise).
2. **AssemblyAI is the first adapter** (Brandon's lean) — real bundled speaker diarization, takes long files by URL with no chunking, clean REST. **No SDK dependency** (Principle 5): two `fetch` calls (POST `/v2/transcript` with `audio_url` + `speaker_labels`, GET `/v2/transcript/{id}`), and the response→result mapping is a **pure `mapTranscriptResponse`** (tolerant: unknown status → "processing" so polling continues), node-testable with fixtures and no live key.
3. **Enabled by the presence of `ASSEMBLYAI_API_KEY`** (the deliberate opt-in, like the R2 vars enabling storage); `TRANSCRIPTION_ADAPTER` selects the adapter (default "assemblyai") and can be set to "none" to disable even with a key. `transcriptionAdapter()` is the pure id (mirrors `tasksAdapter()`), surfaced as **`/health` `checks.transcription`**.
**Why / alternatives:** *A blocking `transcribe()` that submits + waits* rejected — a 3-hour file exceeds any serverless timeout; the job model is the only shape that fits. *OpenAI gpt-4o-transcribe* rejected (the spec's cost table) — a hard 25MB/25-min cap forces chunking on long meetings; AssemblyAI/Deepgram/Gemini take long files directly. *Gemini one-call transcribe+summarize* deferred — weaker prompt-based diarization, and it would fold the summary back into the API instead of the Claude-over-MCP layer; the seam keeps it swappable if that changes. *An SDK* rejected (Principle 5) — two signed-less REST calls don't earn a dependency.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-transcription.mts` (pure, no DB/key) **ALL PASS** — `mapTranscriptResponse` over queued/processing/completed-with-diarization/error/unknown-status fixtures; `transcriptToMarkdown` diarized vs plain; the null-safe env-selected selection (unconfigured → none/null; key → assemblyai; explicit none disables). `verify-health-check`/`verify-provider-seams` green (the new `checks.transcription` canary). `tsc` + eslint clean. **Live submit/poll against AssemblyAI is gated on a configured key + a real audio URL — pending (the graph-auth integration-gated posture); it gets its in-browser eyeball when V1b-2 lands the upload path with a key set.**
**Affects:** new `src/lib/transcription/types.ts`, `assemblyai.ts`, `provider.ts`; edited `src/lib/health.ts` (`checks.transcription`); new `scripts/verify-transcription.mts`; edited `scripts/verify-health-check.mts` (fixture) + `.env.example` (`TRANSCRIPTION_ADAPTER`/`ASSEMBLYAI_API_KEY`). No migration, no new dependency. **V1b-2 (audio upload → submit on completion → poll → fill the transcript) and V1b-3/ADR-089 (the `attachments.purge_after` retention column + purge) build on this seam.**

## ADR-089: Audio upload → auto-transcribe pipeline + the audio-retention column/purge (meeting recording v1b)
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler pre-approved — the audio-retention schema touch is one of the three pre-approved core touches**, `explorations/meeting-recording.md` "Core flags"). The **`attachments.purge_after` column is CORE** (schema.md); the upload/auto-transcribe/poll pipeline over the ADR-088 seam is **non-core** plumbing. **Flagged to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`.** This is **V1b-2 + V1b-3**, completing the meeting-recording chunk's v1 (in-app recording stays deferred).
**Context:** ADR-088 stood up the transcription seam. This adds the actual audio path — upload audio to a meeting, auto-transcribe it into a transcript — and the storage discipline that keeps audio from eating the ~10GB quota: audio is transient, the transcript is the artifact Ledgr keeps. Two open points were settled with Brandon at build (the AskUserQuestion this session): **compression deferred**, and **client-poll + cron backstop** for completion delivery.
**Decision:**
1. **Audio upload reuses the presign flow** (`/api/attachments` → R2 PUT, bytes never proxy the app server), with `audio/*`+`video/*` allowed and a **2GB per-file cap** for AV (`maxFileBytesFor`; R2 single PUT supports 5GB). The upload **is** the intent — `AudioUpload` does presign → PUT → `POST /api/meetings/[id]/transcribe`, no separate button.
2. **Auto-transcribe on upload completion** (deterministic plumbing, Principle 3 — the model is a speech-to-text service, not reasoning). `startAudioTranscription` (`transcription-service.ts`) creates the transcript child (visible immediately as "Transcribing…", written with the same meeting→transcript edge as a pasted one, ADR-087) and submits the audio URL; a submit failure marks the transcript errored rather than throwing. `advanceTranscription` polls once and, on completion, fills the transcript body with diarized markdown (`transcriptToMarkdown`) and leaves `minutes=none` so it **enters the awaiting-minutes view** — the audio path rejoins the v1a minutes flow exactly. The provider is injected (default `getTranscription()`), so the orchestration is node-testable with a fake — no live key.
3. **Completion delivery = client-poll + cron backstop** (Brandon's pick). The panel mounts `TranscriptionPoller` while a transcript is in-flight, hitting `GET /api/transcription/[id]/status` (which advances the job server-side) every 4s and refreshing on completion; `.github/workflows/transcription-poll.yml` (every 15 min → `GET /api/machine/transcription-poll`) finishes jobs the user navigated away from. No dependency on AssemblyAI reaching us (Sunday-proof), works on localhost + prod.
4. **Compression deferred** (Brandon's pick). The spec's Opus-mono-16kHz compress-on-ingest implies server-side ffmpeg, which Vercel serverless doesn't ship; AssemblyAI takes 5GB/10hr files by URL with no chunking, so compression isn't needed to transcribe — only to save storage, which the purge already bounds. It becomes a documented knob behind the seam, added only if storage bites. (Honors Principle 5 — no ffmpeg.wasm dependency.)
5. **CORE — audio retention** (`attachments.purge_after`, migration 0024). Audio is transient: when a transcript is **produced from** the audio (transcription completes), `advanceTranscription` stamps the audio attachment `purge_after = now() + 30 days` (Brandon's window — a buffer to catch a bad transcription before the source is gone). The daily purge cron (`/api/machine/purge`) now also runs `purgeExpiredAudio` (R2 bytes then row, per-item so one failure can't strand the rest), reusing the purge machinery. A `deleteAttachment` lib + `DELETE /api/attachments/[id]` give the "delete now" override. **Retention starts when the transcript exists, not on an explicit "confirm" gesture** — "a transcript exists" is enough signal that the audio did its job, and the 30-day buffer + delete-now cover the edge cases without a new ceremony.
**Why / alternatives:** *Compress in-app* rejected (point 4 — no ffmpeg on Vercel, and unnecessary given URL-based transcription). *Webhook delivery* rejected for v1 — needs public reachability (no localhost), couples us to AssemblyAI's callback; the client-poll + cron is more robust and Sunday-proof. *Cron-only delivery* rejected — minutes-to-hours of lag kills "instant minutes right after the meeting." *An explicit "confirm transcript" gesture to start retention* rejected — extra ceremony; transcript-exists + the 30-day buffer + delete-now is simpler and safe. *Hard-deleting audio the instant a transcript lands* rejected — no buffer to catch a bad transcription.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-transcription-flow.mts` **20/20 on Neon** (fake provider: start writes child + edge + processing state + jobId; submit-failure → error; advance processing no-op / completed fills diarized body + stays awaiting / terminal no-op; `listPendingTranscriptions`; guards — no provider / wrong meeting / non-audio / missing). `scripts/verify-audio-retention.mts` **10/10 on Neon** (spy storage: `markAudioForPurge` stamps ~30d; `purgeExpiredAudio` purges past + deletes bytes, keeps future/null; `deleteAttachment` row+bytes + not_found + cross-owner guards; the completed-transcription→stamp tie-in). `tsc` + full `next build` (all new routes registered) + eslint clean. **In-browser on Neon:** the meeting panel renders and the upload control is correctly **hidden** without a key (paste-only), `/health` shows `transcription: "none"`. **The live audio→transcript eyeball is gated on a configured `ASSEMBLYAI_API_KEY` + a real recording — pending (the integration-gated posture); the whole pipeline is proven against a fake provider + fixtures.**
**Affects:** migration `drizzle/0024_tranquil_landau.sql` + `src/db/schema.ts` (`attachments.purge_after`); `src/lib/attachments.ts` (`maxFileBytesFor` AV cap, `markAudioForPurge`/`purgeExpiredAudio`/`deleteAttachment`, `AUDIO_RETENTION_DAYS`); new `src/lib/meetings/transcription-service.ts`; edited `src/lib/meetings/transcripts.ts` (the `transcription` sub-state in the summary); new routes `POST /api/meetings/[id]/transcribe`, `GET /api/transcription/[id]/status`, `GET /api/machine/transcription-poll`, `DELETE /api/attachments/[id]`; edited `/api/machine/purge` (audio purge); new `src/components/meetings/AudioUpload.tsx` + `TranscriptionPoller.tsx`, edited `MeetingTranscripts.tsx`; new `.github/workflows/transcription-poll.yml`; new `scripts/verify-transcription-flow.mts` + `scripts/verify-audio-retention.mts`. New dependency: none. **Completes the meeting-recording chunk's v1 (v1a paste + v1b audio); in-app recording remains deferred.**

## ADR-090: Block anchors (Obsidian-style `^id`) + action-item → task promotion from the canvas
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon; **Tyler agreed** — the canonical-body-format touch is CORE and was agreed this session before build). Pulls the parked Phase-3 feature `explorations/block-linked-action-items.md` forward. **CORE** (it extends the canonical body-format contract); the promote UX on top is non-core. **Flag to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`.**
**Context:** Reviewing the meeting canvas, Brandon wanted to write action items inline (a checkbox line), then promote a specific line to a task that links back to *that line*. He believed the `^block-id` anchor for this already existed; it did not — ADR-038/M1 only kept the door open (Tiptap chosen partly for it), the feature sat unchecked in `roadmap.md`/`next_steps.md`, and the editor had no anchor code. ADR-037 had flagged the real constraint: markdown has no native stable block ids the way BlockNote JSON did, so the exploration resolved on **Obsidian's approach** (a trailing `^id` marker in the source). Before building, the exploration's one load-bearing risk was spiked: `marked` (the parser `@tiptap/markdown` uses) preserves a trailing `^a1b2c3` verbatim on plain and task lines, and no superscript extension is enabled to collide with the caret — so the mechanism is sound.
**Decision:**
1. **The anchor is a trailing `^id` marker in the body markdown** (6 chars `[a-z0-9]`), riding as **plain text** — no schema change, no new body-format token to parse. Pure helpers (`src/lib/editor/block-anchor.ts`) generate/detect/strip/locate it and are dependency-free so both the server render and the client editor share them. *Rejected:* a Tiptap node-id global attribute serialized to `^id` — more robust but heavier (re-implements block serialization); deferred as a hardening option if the literal-text marker proves fiddly.
2. **The marker never reaches the human-facing render** (the clean-share acceptance criterion, exploration 2026-06-15): `markdownToHtml` + `markdownToText` (`src/lib/markdown-render.ts`) strip trailing `^id` (fence-aware), so share/print/export/FTS read as clean prose. In the editor it's **dimmed**, not hidden (Obsidian's reading-view feel). Verified live: the print render of a promoted line shows the text, not the caret.
3. **The action-item marker is the GFM task checkbox** (`- [ ]`, Brandon's pick) — nothing new to learn. On desktop a checkbox line shows a hover **"→ task"** widget (a ProseMirror widget decoration firing a `ledgr-promote-line` DOM event, so the generic editor stays decoupled — the event only fires when a meeting wired the promote path). The popup pre-fills the **title** from the line text (marker + `^id` stripped) and the **details** from the line's **de-indented sub-bullets** (`extractPromotable`, deterministic — Principle 3), both editable. Mobile keeps the prep panel's input.
4. **Promotion reuses `promoteActionItem`** (ADR-025) + the relations write path: the task is `inbox:false`, related to the meeting and its people (so it lands in next time's prep), carries the pulled sub-bullets as its body, and stores **`properties.source = { type:"meeting", itemId, blockRef }`** — the back-reference to the exact line, no schema change. Before the POST the editor flushes the body save (`onRequestSave`) so the freshly-inserted anchor is persisted, then refreshes.
5. **`ensureAnchorAtPos`/`ensureAnchorAtSelection` + `scrollToBlockId`** are the editor primitives (append an anchor if absent, unique within the doc; jump+flash a line by id). The in-app `#^id` deep link and the **read-side "→ task" badge on a promoted line** (which would also guard against re-promoting the same line) are **follow-ups** — the back-reference is stored now; surfacing it both ways is the next slice.
**Why / alternatives:** *Toolbar/selection trigger instead of per-line hover* — simpler, but Brandon specifically wanted the in-flow hover affordance; the widget delivers it (the primitives also support a toolbar path later). *AI/MCP extraction of action items* — rejected for this path; promotion is deterministic and precise-by-construction (born from the exact line), the human-in-the-loop counterpart to the Claude-over-MCP minutes (ADR-087). *Storing the anchor in a new column* — rejected; it rides `properties`, like every other source link.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-block-anchor.mts` **32/32** (generate/detect/strip incl. fence-skip + footnote non-collision; `extractPromotable` title + de-indented sub-bullets; the `marked` round-trip on plain + task lines). `scripts/verify-meeting-prep.mts` **11/11 on live Neon** (added: block-linked promotion stores `source.itemId`+`blockRef` and carries the sub-bullet body; **also fixed a pre-existing harness bug** — the raw-insert `mk()` set `status:"done"` but not `status_category`, which defaults to `not_started` post-ADR-082, so a "done" fixture read as active). `tsc` clean. **In-browser on live Neon:** appended a checkbox action item with sub-bullets to a meeting → hovered the line → "→ task" → popup pre-filled (title from the line, details from the de-indented sub-bullets) → created the task → the meeting body gained ` ^4301gk` (dimmed in the editor, **stripped from the print render**), the task carried `source.blockRef:"4301gk"` + the sub-bullet body + `inbox:false`, and appeared in the prep panel.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/editor/block-anchor.ts`, `src/components/markdown-editor/block-anchor-extension.ts`, `src/components/markdown-editor/PromoteLinePopup.tsx`, `scripts/verify-block-anchor.mts`; edited `src/lib/markdown-render.ts` (strip), `src/lib/meetings/promote.ts` + `src/app/api/items/[id]/promote-task/route.ts` (body + blockRef → `properties.source`), `src/components/markdown-editor/MarkdownEditor.tsx` + `ItemEditor.tsx` + `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (the promote prop chain), `markdown-editor.css`, `scripts/verify-meeting-prep.mts`. No migration, no new dependency. **Follow-ups (DONE same session, 2026-06-18):** the read-side **"✓ task" badge** on a promoted line (links to the task; replaces the promote button so a line can't be double-promoted — promoted-ref map server-queried via `promotedBlockRefs` and pushed into plugin state); the **`#^id` deep link** (scroll + a *plugin-managed* flash decoration — a manual class is wiped by the next PM re-render); a **"Copy link to this line"** toolbar button (anchors the cursor's line, copies an absolute `/items/<id>#^<id>` URL; works on any line/type); and a **task → source-line back-link** ("↳ from <meeting>") on the task canvas, completing the round-trip. **Still open:** extending the deep link to **public share** URLs (`/share/<token>#^id`). Verified in-browser on live Neon (badge swap + re-promote suppression, badge→task SPA nav, source back-link, hash → scroll + flash; the copy button's clipboard write is blocked only by the headless test context — the anchor + URL build correctly). **Shipped alongside (non-core meeting-canvas polish, same session):** removed the vestigial fixed "Agenda" frame, relabeled "Meeting prep" → "People", and added heading icons via a shared `SectionHeading` (reusing the nav-icon library).

## ADR-091: Scheduled time + duration on tasks (time-blocking Stage A), timed ICS blocks
**Date:** 2026-06-18
**Status:** accepted (Brandon: "yep do stage a"). **Non-core**: `properties`-first, the direction Brandon pre-agreed in `explorations/calendar-time-blocking.md` (2026-06-15); no schema/seam/body-format touch, so no Tyler-agree required. The eventual **column promotion** and **Stage B** (multi-session blocks as event items + the event-model reframe) remain the core, both-agree conversations still ahead. Builds on the native-tasks dual-date model (ADR-076/077) and the published ICS feed (ADR-079).
**Context:** Brandon's read on the task model: "Scheduled" should have an optional *time* (start, ideally start/end) so a task can be a block of time that syncs to his calendar with a notification; "Due" does not need a time. That is exactly the deadline-vs-scheduled distinction already written down in the time-blocking exploration, and its **Stage A** (a single scheduled block on the task itself). The payoff path already exists: the ICS feed (ADR-079) publishes dated tasks to his calendar, today as all-day events; giving a task a time turns that into a real timed block.
**Decision:**
1. **The time is an optional refinement of the scheduled CALENDAR DAY, not a change to `scheduled_date`.** `scheduled_date` stays a UTC-midnight, zone-free calendar day (ADR-008), so everything built on that invariant (Today's partition, the recurrence math, the overdue auto-roll, relative subtasks, the focus layer) is untouched. A task with no time behaves exactly as before.
2. **Stored in `properties.scheduledTime = { start: "HH:MM", durationMinutes }`** (`properties`-first, no migration, not core). Promoting to real columns (`scheduled_at` / `scheduled_minutes`) once the shape proves out is the later **ADR step**, per the exploration's plan; rides `properties` like `reminder`/`recurrence`/`focus`/`relativeSchedule` today.
3. **Floating local wall-clock time (no zone).** The VEVENT emits `DTSTART:<date>T<HHMM>00` with no `Z`/`TZID`: a single-user *plan* ("I'll work 2:00–3:30") that renders at that clock time wherever the calendar shows it. This is the one genuinely new thing a time introduces over the zoneless all-day model; floating is correct for one user in one timezone. *Rejected:* storing a UTC instant the way `meeting_at` does — wrong for a recurring plan and forces a timezone Ledgr otherwise never needs.
4. **Due stays date-only** (Brandon's call): a deadline has no time, mirroring Todoist's deadline vs due-time split.
5. **Input is start time + a duration dropdown** (15m…4h), which *is* the storage, with the computed range shown as a hint ("2:00 PM – 3:30 PM") to answer the start/end framing Brandon asked for. *Rejected:* an end-time picker as the input — equivalent to start+duration but invites end-before-start and cross-midnight validation; duration is cleaner and the range hint still gives the start→end view.
6. **The ICS feed is where it pays off.** A timed task emits a timed VEVENT (floating `DTSTART` + `DTEND` = start + duration, default 60m, with past-midnight day rollover) instead of an all-day one; the default VALARM becomes **at-start** (`PT0M`) vs the all-day **9am** (`PT9H`), and a set reminder lead is minutes-before-start. A **timed recurring** series keeps the stored RRULE verbatim and emits **EXDATE as DATE-TIME** (matching the timed `DTSTART`, RFC 5545) so completed/skipped occurrences still drop. The time attaches **only when the event sits on the scheduled day or the recurrence anchor**, never a due-only event (the time refines the *scheduled* day).
7. **The control lives in the task canvas extras row** (classic path) next to Focus/Reminder, gated on `hasSchedule` (a scheduled date or a recurrence anchor): a time with no day to sit on shows a "set a scheduled date" hint instead of inputs. Optimistic `propertyPatch` (the ReminderControl pattern); clearing the start writes `scheduledTime: null` and the task reverts to all-day.
**Why / alternatives:** `properties`-first proves the UX with zero migration and stays solo-movable, exactly the path the exploration settled. **Stage B** (several blocks per task, the "40 hours of sermon prep across two weeks" case, modeled as event items linked to the task) needs the event-model reframe and is a both-agree + ADR conversation; it is not required for the single-block case Brandon described, so it is deliberately out of scope here. Floating vs UTC-instant covered above.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-scheduled-time.mts` **35/35** (pure helper: parse/validate/default-duration/format incl. cross-midnight; pure ICS builder: timed `DTSTART`/`DTEND`, floating no-`Z`, at-start vs 9am alarm, reminder override, default 60m, day rollover, timed-recurring RRULE + DATE-TIME EXDATE; live-Neon: time attaches on a scheduled day, is ignored on a due-only event). `scripts/verify-ics.mts` **26/26** (no regression, all-day path intact). `tsc` + `eslint` + `next build` clean. **In-browser on live Neon:** opened a scheduled task → "Time" control with start + duration → set 2:00 PM / 1.5 hr → DB `properties.scheduledTime = {start:"14:00",durationMinutes:90}`, feed emitted `DTSTART:20260619T140000` / `DTEND:20260619T153000` + at-start alarm; live duration change re-rendered the range; cleared the start → `scheduledTime:null`, feed reverted to all-day `DTSTART;VALUE=DATE` + 9am alarm (seed task left clean).
**Affects:** new `src/lib/scheduled-time.ts` (pure parse/format helper), `src/components/canvas/ScheduledTimeControl.tsx`, `scripts/verify-scheduled-time.mts`; edited `src/lib/ics.ts` (timed VEVENT/alarm/EXDATE branch), `src/lib/ics-data.ts` (attach the time on the scheduled day), `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (render the control in the task extras row). No migration, no new dependency. **Follow-ups:** surface the time on Today + the Tasks list rows (today they show the day only); the grid-canvas path (classic-path only for now, like Focus/Reminder); the **column promotion** (the core ADR step); **Stage B** (multi-session event-model blocks).

## ADR-092: Email-in attachments — link, don't copy (+ R2 server-PUT Content-Length fix)
**Date:** 2026-06-19
**Status:** accepted (Brandon, this session: "Link, don't copy"). **Non-core** — email-in is an integration adapter (Brandon's lane); no schema, seam, or body-format change. Reverses the email-in slice of **PRD §5.3 / slice 26** ("attachments stored to object storage"); the general attachment model (§3.4, browser-presigned uploads, the `attachments` table) is untouched.
**Context:** A real email-in run failed with `R2 put failed: 411`. Two findings came out of it. (1) **The bug:** `R2Provider.putObject` signed a PUT with a buffered body but no `Content-Length`; local Node's undici infers it, but Vercel's Node runtime hands `fetch` a streamed body and R2 rejects it (`411 MissingContentLength`). (2) **The design question Brandon raised:** copying every email attachment into R2 grows storage with mostly *noise* — inline signature images/logos on every message — for files that already live in his M365 mailbox. He preferred linking back over copying.
**Decision:**
1. **R2 `putObject` sets `Content-Length` explicitly** (signed in, so the SigV4 signature still matches). Proven against live R2: a streamed PUT without the header 411s; with it, 200 — on both code paths aws4fetch can take. (Shipped as PR #32 ahead of this ADR; the only `putObject` caller was email-in, so blast radius was contained. Browser presigned PUTs were unaffected — the browser sets the length.)
2. **Email-in links to attachments instead of copying them.** No bytes to R2, no `attachments` rows. The note body gets a footer: **From** (sender), an **Open original email in Outlook** link, and the attachment **names + sizes**. The bytes stay in the original mail.
3. **Inline attachments are skipped** (`isInline`), and the attachment list is fetched **metadata-only** (`$select` drops `contentBytes`, so we never download bytes). Signature/embedded images were the bulk of the churn.
4. **`internetMessageId` is the stable handle, replacing the volatile Graph `id`.** Verified live: a message's Graph `id` (and its `webLink`) **change when it moves folders** — the stored pre-move id 404s after the import move. So the dedup guard switched from `properties.email.messageId` to `internetMessageId` (RFC822 Message-ID, stable across moves; falls back to `messageId` when absent), and the open-link re-resolves through it.
5. **Open-in-Outlook is an owner-gated redirect** (`GET /api/email/open?mid=<internetMessageId>`) that resolves the *current* `webLink` on each click. A `webLink` captured at import is pre-move and goes stale; re-resolving keeps the link working after the import move and any later re-filing. *Rejected:* storing a post-move webLink (still breaks on re-file, needs a create→move reorder or a second write).
6. **"Save to Ledgr" (on-demand byte copy)** — a per-file button that resolves the message by `internetMessageId`, fetches that one attachment, and `putObject`s it — is a **documented follow-up, not built.** The §1 Content-Length fix is what makes that path correct when it lands. (`properties.email.attachments` already stores the names/sizes/types it needs.)
**Why / alternatives:** Leaning on M365 (the mailbox holds the bytes) keeps R2 near-empty — "cheap on the back end" with zero new dependency. Two other Brandon ideas were weighed and **deferred**: *doc→Markdown conversion* (PDF/Word/Excel/PPT) needs heavy parsers and is lossy without OCR/AI — its right home is a future on-demand Claude-over-MCP action (Principle 3), not auto-conversion in a cron; *image compression* needs `sharp` (painful on Vercel) and was already deferred for meeting audio — filtering inline images beats compressing them. *OneDrive re-upload* was rejected as more plumbing for a copy the mailbox already holds.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-email-in.mts` — pure footer (sender/link/sizes, empty cases) + Neon engine (note/task routing, HTML→markdown, the body footer, `internetMessageId` dedup with no double-import, delta-token persistence, errored-run-doesn't-advance) — all pass. Live `resolveWebLink` against the real mailbox returns the current webLink for the known `internetMessageId` and `null` for an unknown one. `scripts/verify-storage-r2.mts` round-trips `putObject` (put → signed GET → exact-length read-back → delete) for empty/small/3 MB. `tsc` + eslint clean. **Pending:** the in-prod end-to-end eyeball (a real attachment email → note with footer + working Outlook link, nothing in R2).
**Affects:** `src/lib/storage/r2.ts` (Content-Length); `src/lib/email/{types,html,graph-source,sync}.ts` (metadata-only fetch, inline skip, `internetMessageId`, footer, dedup); new `src/app/api/email/open/route.ts` (redirect); new `scripts/verify-storage-r2.mts`; rewritten `scripts/verify-email-in.mts`. No migration, no new dependency. **Follow-ups:** build "Save to Ledgr"; optionally surface the attachment list/Outlook link as a canvas panel (today it's in the body); the orphaned pre-change "New Proposal" note can be deleted (alpha test artifact).

## ADR-093: Templates redesign — templates become prototype items (clone-to-apply), with children, dynamic variables, and apply-to-existing
**Date:** 2026-06-20
**Status:** accepted; **TPL1–TPL5 shipped 2026-06-20 — chunk complete** (TPL1: data model + exclusion + apply-rewire, migrations 0025/0026; TPL2: real-canvas authoring + Save-as-template + duplicate + delete; TPL3a: the pure variable resolver `src/lib/template-vars.ts` — date/`{{title}}`/`{{ask:Label}}` tokens — resolved over the cloned tree + the apply-time prompt form; TPL3b: structured due/scheduled date rules (none|offset-from-apply|fixed) in the registry `apply_config`, authored from the banner, applied to the cloned root with relative-subtask cascade; TPL4a: per-type default applied by "+ New" + a chooser (Blank + all, default ★, preview) via `listTemplatesForPicker`; TPL4b: `applyTemplateToExisting` merges a template onto a started item — fill-blanks ("change only the unchanged") or overwrite, adding (never deleting) subtasks/relations, with token/date-rule resolution; TPL5: MCP parity (`list_templates` now reports `askLabels`/`isDefault`/`applyConfig`; `apply_template` gained `targetId`+`mode` for apply-to-existing) + the `new-from-template` dashboard action widget made addable + configurable with a real template picker. TPL2/TPL3/TPL4/TPL5 non-core/additive — TPL5's MCP-contract touch is additive parity with the already-shipped lib + the ADR-071 tool set, covered by this ADR's ratified scope, not a new core decision). **CORE** — reverses ADR-045's "templates are a config table, not items," so it needs both-agree + this ADR per CLAUDE.md "Building together." **Tyler ratified the direction (logged in `COLLAB.md`).** Decisions captured from a design session with Brandon (the four forks below).
**Context:** ADR-045/050 shipped templates as an owner-scoped `templates` config row (`{body, property_defaults, relation_defaults}`) applied by `createItemFromTemplate` = one `createItem`. Brandon's asks now exceed that shape: a template must carry *everything an item can* (title, full body, all core fields, properties, relations) including **child items** (a task's subtasks, a meeting's tasks, a paper's sections), support **variable/relative content** (set a date to today, put today's date in the title), be **easily duplicated/deleted**, offer a **template-chooser UX** when creating from a type's area, and optionally **apply to an already-started item, changing only the unchanged fields.** The config-blob shape can't express children or full fidelity without re-implementing a mini item-tree plus a second editor that would drift from the real one. Meanwhile `cloneItemSubtree` (ADR-076, `src/lib/clone.ts`) already deep-clones an item + subtree with reset, and its header names "the subtree-aware template apply" as a planned caller; recurrence already treats a task as a prototype it stamps copies from; relative subtasks (ADR-085) already do "N days from the parent." The pieces for "a template is a prototype item" are built.
**The four decisions (design session, 2026-06-20):**
1. **Authoring model = templates are real items.** A template's content lives as a normal `items` row + subtree, authored/edited in the **same canvas** as any item (real subtasks, body, properties, relations: no second editor, no drift). Reverses ADR-045's "templates as items — rejected." The pollution ADR-045 feared (lists/search/FTS/export) is handled by a single `is_template` exclusion, the same discipline as `deletedAt`/`inbox`/hidden `is_system` types.
2. **Variables = dates + ask-on-apply prompts + computed (the full tier).** Text tokens in title/body (`{{today}}`, `{{today+7d}}`, `{{now}}`, `{{nextSunday}}`, `{{title}}` echo, format variants), each **fixed-or-dynamic** (Notion's "date when duplicated" toggle); structured **relative date offsets** for due/scheduled (fixed | offset-from-apply | none; relative subtasks already do offset-from-parent); and **`{{ask:Label}}` prompts** collected into a small form on apply. Resolved by a pure resolver over the cloned tree; reuse `nl-date.ts`.
3. **Apply-to-existing = fill-blanks (default) + overwrite (explicit).** Beyond stamping new items, a template can apply to an item already started: **fill-blanks** sets only empty scalars, adds missing subtasks, leaves typed text alone (Brandon's "change only the unchanged"); an explicit **overwrite-from-template** mode resets fields. (ClickUp's merge-on-apply precedent.)
4. **Create UX = per-type default + chooser.** Each type may have a **default template** that "+ New" uses automatically; a **chooser** (picker with a small preview) lists the rest + Blank. (ClickUp's per-list default precedent.) Generalizes today's "+ New ▾" menu.
**Storage shape (planned, TPL1):** add `items.is_template boolean default false` (excluded from every owner-scoped surface). Evolve the `templates` table into a thin **registry/metadata** row: `{id, owner_id, type, name, prototype_item_id → items.id, is_default boolean, apply_config jsonb (date-field rules / var defaults), created_at}`; the old `body`/`property_defaults`/`relation_defaults` content moves onto the prototype item. Alpha posture: convert existing rows or reseed freely (ADR-039 — no data to protect). **Apply = `cloneItemSubtree(prototype)` + the variable-resolution pass + (new-item | merge-into-existing).**
**Why / alternatives:** *Extend the config table with a children-jsonb + core-field defaults + a nested builder* — rejected as the primary path (a second editor to maintain forever, lower fidelity, drifts as the item model grows; the explicit alternative Brandon weighed and declined). *Drop the registry table entirely, templates = `items WHERE is_template`* — viable; kept the thin registry to preserve `/api/templates`, the "+ New" menu, MCP `list_templates`/`apply_template`, and the Build index with minimal churn, and to hang `is_default`/`apply_config`. *Keep new-items-only* — rejected; Brandon wants apply-to-existing. *Dates-only variables* — rejected; he chose the full tier.
**Verification (TPL1):** `verify-templates.mts` rewritten for the new model — **46/46 on Neon**: parse/validate, registry CRUD + default uniqueness, the `is_template` subtree-inheritance invariant, the EXCLUSION net (prototype + subtree absent from list/search/view/Today/Build-counts/related, present by id for authoring), apply = `cloneItemSubtree` producing real items that carry body/properties/subtasks/relations, soft-delete + prototype-cascade, and the `deleteType` FK guard counting prototypes. Regression: `verify-mcp` (updated for the new template shape) / `verify-views` / `verify-recurrence` green; `tsc` + `next build` + eslint clean. Migrations **0025** (drop body/property_defaults/relation_defaults + add `items.is_template`) and **0026** (registry cols + reseed `DELETE FROM templates` before the NOT NULL + partial unique `(owner_id,type) WHERE is_default`) applied. The two-migration split avoids drizzle-kit's interactive rename prompt (no table has simultaneous add+drop). **Remaining:** TPL2–TPL5 (each with its own `verify-*`); an in-browser eyeball of the Templates UI loop (folded into TPL2's authoring-canvas eyeball).
**TPL1 affects (done):** `src/db/schema.ts` (+`items.is_template`, `templates` reshape + unique index), `drizzle/0025_*`+`0026_*`; `src/lib/items.ts` (`isTemplate` on ItemInput + the createItem inheritance invariant + getItem column + the three exclusions); the exclusion sweep across `src/lib/{views,today,search,relations,mentions,scheduling,ics-data,export/engine,push/notify,todoist/sync}.ts`; `src/lib/templates.ts` (full registry rewrite + clone-apply); `src/lib/mcp/tools.ts` (list/apply_template shape); `src/app/api/templates/[id]/route.ts` (comment); new `src/components/build/{NewTemplateForm,DeleteTemplateButton}.tsx`, rewritten `src/app/build/templates/{page,new/page}.tsx`; deleted `src/components/build/TemplateBuilder.tsx` + `src/app/build/templates/[id]/edit/page.tsx`; `scripts/verify-templates.mts` (rewrite) + `scripts/verify-mcp.mts` (template block). No new dependency.
**Verification (TPL2):** `verify-templates.mts` extended to **64/64 on Neon** — the additive `cloneItemSubtree({isTemplate})` marking root+subtree, `createTemplateFromItem` (clone an item's subtree into a template carrying body/subtasks/relations; source stays real and listed; prototype excluded; guards reject a template/trashed/foreign source), `duplicateTemplate` ("Copy of …", non-default, fresh subtree), `getTemplateByPrototype` (root yes / real-item no / subtask no / owner-scoped). Regression `verify-mcp`/`verify-recurrence` green (clone change backward-compatible); tsc/eslint/`next build` clean. **In-browser on Neon (dev-auth):** the amber "Template" banner renders on the prototype canvas with rename/set-default/duplicate/delete (and correctly suppresses "← All items"/"Save as template"); "Save as template" on a real item runs end-to-end → a new prototype with its banner; the index lists templates by type with set-default (uniqueness live)/duplicate/delete; no console errors. **TPL1's deferred UI eyeball is thereby closed.**
**TPL2 affects (done):** `src/lib/clone.ts` (+`CloneOverrides.isTemplate`, root-only); `src/lib/templates.ts` (`getTemplateByPrototype`/`createTemplateFromItem`/`duplicateTemplate`); new `src/app/api/templates/from-item/route.ts` + `src/app/api/templates/[id]/duplicate/route.ts`; new `src/components/canvas/{TemplateBanner,SaveAsTemplateButton}.tsx` + `src/components/build/TemplateRowActions.tsx`; edited `src/components/canvas/{ItemCanvas,Modal}.tsx`, `src/app/@modal/(.)items/[id]/page.tsx`, `src/app/build/templates/page.tsx`; deleted `src/components/build/DeleteTemplateButton.tsx`; `scripts/verify-templates.mts` (TPL2 block). Non-core (the clone option is additive); no new dependency, no migration.
**Verification (TPL5):** the MCP + dashboard parity slice. **`list_templates`** now returns each template's `askLabels` (via `templateAskLabels`, so a client knows which `answers` to pass), `isDefault`, `prototypeItemId`, and `applyConfig` (when non-empty). **`apply_template`** gained `targetId` + `mode` → routes to `applyTemplateToExisting` (fill | overwrite) when a `targetId` is given, else `createItemFromTemplate` — mirroring `POST /api/templates/[id]/apply` (the lib already supported both; the tool only needed the args). The **`new-from-template` dashboard widget** (its `ActionWidgetSettings`/parser/`ActionWidgetBody` render existed since the dashboards slices but were unreachable): a new **"Actions"** section in `AddWidgetMenu` + `handleAddAction` in `DashboardClient` make it addable; the settings popover's raw text keys became **dropdowns** — a **template `<select>`** from `/api/templates` (new-from-template; also carries the template's type into `targetType`) and a **type `<select>`** from `/api/types` (quick-capture) — which closes Tyler's dashboards follow-up "richer action-widget pickers (type/template dropdowns vs text keys)" (COLLAB heads-up); an unconfigured new-from-template widget shows a "Pick a template in settings" guard instead of creating a blank item. Also fixed a latent `verify-templates` leak (its `vtmpl_other_*` type-mismatch fixture was never cleaned up). `verify-mcp` **71/71** (askLabels/isDefault reported, apply-to-existing fill carries the property + body + returns the same item, owner-scope), `verify-dashboards` **21/21** (a valid `templateId` UUID round-trips, an invalid one drops to null), `verify-templates` **105/105**; tsc/eslint/`next build` clean. **In-browser on Neon (dev-auth):** add widget → guard → gear template dropdown → pick → one click applied the template and opened the new item (resolved body + cloned subtask), no console errors. The MCP-contract touch is **additive parity** (new optional args, new output fields; the original tools unchanged) within this ADR's ratified scope + ADR-071's tool set — no new core decision.
**TPL5 affects (done):** `src/lib/mcp/tools.ts` (`list_templates` enrichment, `apply_template` targetId/mode + `applyTemplateToExisting`/`templateAskLabels` imports); `src/components/dashboards/{AddWidgetMenu,DashboardClient,WidgetSettingsPopover,ActionWidgetBody}.tsx` (Actions section, handleAddAction, template + type dropdowns, the guard); `scripts/verify-mcp.mts` + `scripts/verify-dashboards.mts` (TPL5 blocks) + `scripts/verify-templates.mts` (the `typeKeyOther` cleanup fix). No schema/migration, no new dependency, no protocol change.
