(Historical: the earlier "Affects (planned)" list — `items.is_template`, the registry reshape, `template-vars.ts`, the exclusion sweep, the chooser, etc. — all shipped across TPL1–TPL5.)

## ADR-094: Calendar events — rename meeting→event, pull-on-add calendar list, tags as an ordinary type, and a configurable event task-pull rule
**Date:** 2026-06-20
**Status:** accepted (design settled with Brandon this session; **Tyler OK'd the core changes**). Shipped in four slices, each with its own `verify-*`: **E1** (rename meeting→event, migration 0027), **E2** (tag type + tags field, migration 0028), **E3** (calendar feed + click-to-add, migration 0029), **E4** (configurable task-pull rule, no migration). **🎉 Chunk COMPLETE 2026-06-20 (PRs #51–#54, all live on Vercel).** **CORE** (renames a system type, seeds a new one, reverses ADR-023's calendar auto-create, touches the MCP example contract), so both-agree + this ADR per CLAUDE.md "Building together."
**Context:** Three pains with the calendar/meetings model. (1) Calendar sync auto-materializes **every** polled event as a `meeting` item (`src/lib/calendar/sync.ts`, ADR-023), so the whole calendar is a firehose into Meetings; Brandon wants to *pull in* the events he cares about, not receive all of them. (2) "meeting" is too narrow: a conference session he takes notes at, a time-block, a dated note are all events with a time, not meetings. (3) Meeting prep shows the **union of every task related to every confirmed person** on the meeting (`src/lib/meetings/prep.ts`): fine for a 1:1, noise for a group ("All Pastors" should pull Pastors-tagged tasks, not all 8 attendees' lists). No tag/label concept exists (only a long-flagged proposal). The event-model generalization was already a queued Brandon↔Tyler sync topic (`COLLAB.md`).
**The four decisions:**
1. **Rename `meeting` → `event` (E1).** One umbrella type; "meeting-ness" (the prep panel + people) shows when an event has people related to it. A conference is an event with no people and a body of notes. User-facing surfaces renamed (type key + label, the `/events` route + tab, the MCP tool examples, push text, starter widget); deliberately-kept **internal** names (no user value, high churn): the `meeting_at` column, `src/lib/meetings/`, the `MeetingPrep`/`MeetingTranscripts` components, the `/api/meetings/*` API paths, the `transcript` relation role, the `meetingPrep`/`meetingTranscripts` canvas-card ids.
2. **Calendar = a list you pull from, not a firehose (E3).** Sync caches event metadata (a lightweight side table, not `items`); **matched** events (a matcher recognizes the series/attendee, ADR-024) **auto-promote** to real `event` items, everything else waits in the calendar list as **one-click adds**. Reverses ADR-023's "every event → item." Keeps standing meetings automatic without re-adding them weekly, and keeps the noise out.
3. **Tags as an ordinary, non-privileged type (E2).** Seed a lightweight `tag` type (like the base types) but special-case it **nowhere** in code; tagging a task/event is a `relations` edge (the schema already frames "tagging a task with a person is an edge"), so a tag is the same edge pointed at a tag item. People stay their own type because `person` is **load-bearing for calendar matching** (attendee email → person item); a tag has no identity/email. So: keep person rich, add tag as its lightweight sibling, unify them only at the query layer. Resolves the cross-cutting-labels question (Tyler) toward tag-items-via-relations. Brandon's instinct drove this: if the pull query is user-configurable, `tag` needn't be privileged, it is just one of several types you might pull by (project, ministry area, …).
4. **A configurable event task-pull rule (E4, the real new mechanism).** Each event carries `properties.taskPull`: a small query, `{ groups: [{ match: "any"|"all", seeds: [...] }], statusScope }`, the groups OR'd together. Default with no config = "active tasks related to the **people on this event**," union, so a calendar 1:1 reproduces today's behavior with zero setup. v1 UI renders exactly **one flat group**: a seed-chip set (people / tags / any item, typeahead) plus an **Any/All** toggle (Any = union, All = intersection). The compiler OR's N groups from day one, so nested `(A AND B) OR (C AND D)` is an additive "+ group" button later, no migration. Authored on the event and on its **template** (recurring series inherit it via the matcher applying the template). Rides the existing view / embedded-query engine (`relatedTo` + `statusCategory`). No NOT/exclude in v1.
**Why / alternatives:** *Collapse everything into tags* (Brandon weighed it): rejected, a tag has no email so the calendar can't auto-link a 1:1 to a person, which rebuilds the `entity` type ADR-055 retired. *Hardcode pull-by-person + pull-by-tag*: rejected, it privileges `tag` and bakes the facets into code; the configurable rule generalizes to any type. *Full nested boolean builder now*: rejected, fiddly UX rarely needed for meeting prep; the group-shaped storage keeps the door open additively. *Flat-only storage*: rejected, adding tiers later would need a shape migration. *Keep auto-creating all events*: rejected, the firehose Brandon named. *Pure click-add everything*: rejected, re-adds standing meetings each occurrence. *Rename the `meeting_at` column / the internal dirs*: deferred as internal tidy (low value, high churn). *A `meeting` vs `event` two-type split*: rejected, one type whose behavior adapts to its relations is simpler and matches bespoke-first.
**Verification (E1):** migration **0027** renames the type via insert-new / repoint / delete-old (the `items.type → types.key` FK has no `ON UPDATE CASCADE`), repointing `items`, `templates`, and `views.filter` jsonb; idempotent and a no-op on a fresh DB. Applied to Neon: the type is now `event` (is_system), **28 existing items repointed**. Code swept across ~18 `src` files + the route dir move `/meetings`→`/events` + ~14 verify scripts; the misses a quoted grep wouldn't catch were fixed (`canvas-fields.ts` unquoted `meeting:` TOP_STRIP key, `mcp/tools.ts` example type-keys, push display text). `tsc` + `eslint` + `next build` clean; **15/15 affected verify scripts pass** (calendar-sync, meeting-prep, meeting-transcripts, today-inbox, views, module-registry, mcp, push, matchers, canvas-seam, canvas-layout, lists-search, relations, transcription-flow, audio-retention). In-browser eyeball deferred to the chunk.
**Affects (E1 done):** `drizzle/0027_rename_meeting_to_event.sql`; `scripts/seed.mjs`; `src/lib/{modules,type-order,canvas-layout,canvas-fields,views,starter-widgets,today,push/notify,calendar/sync,mcp/tools}.ts`, `src/lib/meetings/{prep,promote,transcripts}.ts`; `src/components/lists/ListTabs.tsx`, `src/components/views/ViewBuilder.tsx`, `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx`; `src/app/meetings` → `src/app/events`; ~14 `scripts/verify-*.mts` fixtures; `src/lib/v1-goals.ts` (Brandon's 1.0 bar). No new dependency. **E3–E4 affects recorded as they ship.**
**Verification (E2):** migration **0028** seeds the `tag` type (is_system=false, show_in_quick_capture=false, hidden=false) and appends a built-in `tags` relation field (`{kind:"relation", targetType:"tag", cardinality:"many"}`) to `task`/`event`/`note`, merge-safe + idempotent (`COALESCE(property_schema,'[]') || …` only `WHERE NOT (… @> '[{"key":"tags"}]')`); seed.mjs mirrors both for fresh DBs. **No app code changed:** tagging rides the existing ADR-067 typed-relation machinery (RelationProperties/RelationField render the field; create-on-miss makes a `tag`), and "everything tagged X" is the tag's universal related panel. Applied to Neon. `verify-tags.mts` **15/15** (ordinary type; the field on all three types; a 2-tag round-trip read back via `outgoingRelationsByRole`; the tag gathering a task + an event; owner-scoping); `tsc`/eslint clean; regressions green (`verify-types`, `verify-relations`, `verify-relations-typed`, `verify-canvas-layout`). In-browser eyeball deferred to the chunk.
**Affects (E2 done):** `drizzle/0028_tag_type_and_tags_field.sql`; `scripts/seed.mjs` (tag insert + tags-field append); new `scripts/verify-tags.mts`. No app-code change, no new dependency.
**Verification (E3):** migration **0029** adds the `calendar_events` cache table (owner-scoped; `(owner_id, ms_event_id)` unique; `(owner_id, start_at)` feed index; `promoted_item_id` FK → items ON DELETE SET NULL). `runCalendarSync` rewritten: upsert every polled event into the cache, AUTO-PROMOTE only events a matcher recognizes (injected `shouldPromote`/`onPromoted` keep the engine matcher-agnostic + node-testable), reconcile a pre-existing/promoted item exactly as before, leave the rest in the feed; result counts are now `promoted`/`cached` (was `created`). New `src/lib/calendar/feed.ts`: `listCalendarFeed` (upcoming, un-promoted, non-cancelled, by start) + idempotent `promoteCalendarEvent` (creates the item, sets `promoted_item_id`, runs the matchers best-effort). `POST /api/calendar/events/[id]/add`; a "From your calendar" section + `AddEventButton` (router.refresh) on `/events`. Both sync routes (machine + "sync now") wire `shouldPromote = matchEvent(...).matchedMatcherIds.length > 0` + `onPromoted = applyMatchersToMeeting`. Applied to Neon. `verify-calendar-feed.mts` **14/14** (auto-promote gating, the 4 cached, feed excludes matched/cancelled/past/pre-existing, manual promote idempotent, owner-scoping) + `verify-calendar-sync.mts` updated (shouldPromote=true keeps the reconcile-path coverage; `promoted`/`cached` counts; cache cleanup) green; `tsc`/eslint/`next build` clean. In-browser eyeball deferred to the chunk.
**Affects (E3 done):** `src/db/schema.ts` (+`calendarEvents`), `drizzle/0029_calendar_events_cache.sql`; rewrote `src/lib/calendar/sync.ts`; new `src/lib/calendar/feed.ts`; `src/app/api/machine/calendar-sync/route.ts` + `src/app/api/calendar/sync/route.ts` (shouldPromote/onPromoted wiring); new `src/app/api/calendar/events/[id]/add/route.ts`; new `src/components/calendar/AddEventButton.tsx`; `src/app/events/page.tsx` (feed section); new `scripts/verify-calendar-feed.mts` + updated `scripts/verify-calendar-sync.mts`. No new dependency.
**Verification (E4):** the configurable task-pull. Pure `src/lib/events/task-pull.ts` (`parseTaskPull`/`effectiveTaskPull`/`expandSeeds`/`combineTaskIds`; `properties.taskPull = { groups:[{ match:"any"|"all", seeds }], statusScope }`, default = one ANY group of `["@people"]`). `src/lib/events/task-pull-service.ts` queries the active tasks `relatedTo` each expanded seed (any-role confirmed edges both directions, so a `tags` edge counts) and combines them (ANY=union, ALL=intersection, groups OR'd). `getMeetingPrep` resolves open tasks through it + returns the rule + seed labels; `TaskPullControl` (chips + Any/All toggle + items typeahead) edits the rule via `propertyPatch { taskPull }` (null = reset to default). The prep panel now always shows Open tasks (a tag rule pulls without people). Templates carry the rule in `properties` (cloned on apply); a matcher applying a template to a series propagates it. `verify-task-pull.mts` **16/16** (pure parse/expand/combine + live default/tag/ALL-intersection/mixed/statusScope/owner-scoping) + `verify-meeting-prep` regression green; `tsc`/eslint/`next build` clean. In-browser eyeball deferred to the chunk.
**Affects (E4 done):** new `src/lib/events/task-pull.ts` + `src/lib/events/task-pull-service.ts`; `src/lib/meetings/prep.ts` (resolve open tasks via the rule, return rule+seeds); `src/components/meetings/MeetingPrep.tsx` (render the control, Open tasks always shown); new `src/components/events/TaskPullControl.tsx`; new `scripts/verify-task-pull.mts`. No migration, no new dependency.

## ADR-095: Canvas tabs — split one item's body into named tabs (sections of the same markdown)
**Date:** 2026-06-20
**Status:** accepted (Tyler proposed + built; Brandon agreed before build). **Core-adjacent** — touches the canonical body format (a section-delimiter convention every reader sees), the type/canvas model (the default canvas gains a tab mode; auto-on for the `note` core type), and the module boundary (a new `tabs` capability on `coreModule`). Built on branch `canvas-tabs`. **No migration.**
**Context:** A Google-Docs-style "tabs" ask (Tyler, 2026-06-20): along the top of the canvas, add tabs that split the item into sections. His case: a song's note holds 5–6 lyric versions plus notes and ideas, each its own tab. Wanted auto-on for notes and attachable to any other type.
**Decision:**
1. **Tabs are named sections within the ONE markdown body, not separate items or a new column.** A tab is delimited by an invisible HTML-comment marker `<!-- tab: Title -->`; a body is "tabbed" iff it contains ≥1 marker. The canonical `{format:"markdown", text}` body is unchanged (ADR-037/040), so every reader (render, FTS, share, print, clone, MCP) sees the whole document; only the canvas knows about tabs. Content before the first marker becomes a leading untitled tab so nothing is hidden.
2. **Encoding = invisible marker, NOT `# H1`-as-tab.** Chosen so a stray heading in pasted content can't accidentally create a tab and so in-content headings are unconstrained. "Split on `# H1`" is reserved as a future *import* path (an uploaded `.md` → tabs), decoupling durable storage from the upload nicety.
3. **Human-facing readers flatten markers to `## Title` headings** (`flattenTabs` in `markdown-render.ts`, applied in `markdownToHtml` + `markdownToText`), so a shared/printed/exported/searched multi-tab note reads as titled sections — the `stripBlockAnchors` precedent (ADR-090). Clone/MCP keep the raw body (tabs preserved).
4. **The canvas is the only behavioral change.** A client `TabbedBody` wraps the existing markdown editor: a tab strip + "+ Add tab" across the top, an inline title for the active tab, click-to-switch, rename, delete (deleting the last tab reverts to a plain untabbed body). Tab content lives in `useState`; the editor is remounted per tab (`key`) on a switch and re-fed its own emitted markdown on each keystroke (MarkdownEditor's `getMarkdown() === initialMarkdown` guard makes that a no-op, so the cursor is never disturbed). The strip only appears once a body is tabbed; an untabbed item shows just a subtle "+ Add tab" and is otherwise unchanged.
5. **Availability via the capability seam (ADR-051).** Auto-on for `note` (`MarkdownCanvas` enables tabs when `item.type === "note"`); opt-in for any other type by attaching the new `tabs` `ModuleCapability` (on `coreModule`) from the Build bespoke-tool catalog (`MarkdownCanvas` also enables tabs when `typeDef.capability === "tabs"`). The capability's `canvasId` stays the default markdown canvas — tabs are a sub-behavior of it, not a separate canvas.
6. **No schema change.** Tabs live in the body; tab order = document order; titles = the markers. Active tab is UI-ephemeral (defaults to the first). So no migration, which keeps the blast radius small.
**Why / alternatives:** *Tabs as separate child items / a new column* — rejected; would split the body and break "every reader sees the whole doc." *`# H1` = tab* — rejected for storage (collision with content headings); kept as an import path. *A separate `markdown-tabs` canvas component* — rejected; duplicating the large `MarkdownCanvas` is worse than a gated wrapper around the shared editor. *Bespoke module canvases (Chord/Paper) tab-able now* — deferred (default canvas only first, like Feature B).
**Verification:** pure codec `scripts/verify-canvas-tabs.mts` **19/19** (parse/serialize round-trip, untabbed pass-through, preamble→leading tab, flatten→`##` headings + marker strip, title sanitization keeps a marker single-line); `tsc` + eslint clean on all touched files; the Test note page renders 200 (server compiles MarkdownCanvas → ItemEditor → TabbedBody). **Remaining:** an in-browser eyeball of the tab interactions (add/switch/rename/delete + save round-trip) — synthetic checks can't cover the live editor.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/editor/canvas-tabs.ts` (pure codec), `src/components/markdown-editor/TabbedBody.tsx`, `scripts/verify-canvas-tabs.mts`; edited `src/components/markdown-editor/ItemEditor.tsx` (+`tabsEnabled`), `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (compute `tabsEnabled`, thread to the body editors), `src/lib/markdown-render.ts` (flatten in both render fns), `src/lib/modules.ts` (`tabs` capability on `coreModule`). No migration, no new dependency.

---

## ADR-096: Task priority P1–P6 (replaces the 4-level `urgency` enum)
**Date:** 2026-06-21
**Status:** accepted (Tyler), **CORE — pending Brandon's nod before merge to main.** Part of the Todoist-style Tasks redesign (`explorations/tasks-redesign.md`). Building on branch `tasks-build`; **flagged in COLLAB.** Alpha posture (ADR-039): convert/reseed dev data freely.
**Context:** Tasks carried a 4-level `urgency` pgEnum (`low/normal/high/critical`). Tyler wants Todoist-style **P1–P6** (1 highest … 6 lowest), color-coded (P1 red · P2 gold · P3 purple · P4 blue · P5 green · P6 none), driving the colored checkbox, the capture-card chip, the row metadata, the Today grouping, the board, and NL quick-add from one vocab.
**Decision:**
1. **One shared vocab `src/lib/priority.ts`** — `PRIORITIES = [1..6]`, `Priority` type, `priorityStyle` (Tailwind classes per number; P6 neutral/no-accent), `priorityLabel`/`prioritySortKey` (null = unset, sorts last as P6), `toPriority` (coerce `3`/`"p3"`/null), `fromLegacyUrgency` (critical→1, high→2, normal→4, low→6), and `autoPriorityOnFirstSubtask` (a task gaining its FIRST subtask auto-bumps to **P5** only if it had no explicit priority — Tyler, 2026-06-21).
2. **Field shape:** the `items.urgency` pgEnum becomes a **`smallint` 1–6** (null = unset). **The column keeps the name `urgency` internally** to avoid a ~30-file rename; it is surfaced **everywhere user-facing as "Priority" / P1–P6**. (A later cosmetic column rename is optional, not required.) `Urgency`/`URGENCIES` in `item-enums.ts` become the numeric `Priority`/`PRIORITIES` (re-exported through `items.ts`).
3. **Migration:** `ALTER COLUMN urgency TYPE smallint USING (CASE 'critical'→1, 'high'→2, 'normal'→4, 'low'→6 END)`, then drop the old `urgency` enum type. Alpha, so existing dev tasks remap by that table; no data to protect.
4. **NL quick-add (ADR-084):** extend the `p1..p4` parse to **`p1..p6`** (and `!1..!6`).
5. **Auto-P5-on-subtask** wires into the subtask-create path (`createItem` with a parent task / the subtasks API): set the parent to P5 if it was unset.
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep the enum, add values* — rejected; an enum can't be cleanly numeric/ordered for 1–6. *Smallint, rename column → `priority`* — cleaner name but ~30-file churn + a riskier migration; deferred to an optional cosmetic follow-up. *A separate priority field alongside urgency* — rejected (two overlapping concepts).
**Affects (building):** new `src/lib/priority.ts`; `src/db/schema.ts` (enum→smallint) + a migration; `src/lib/item-enums.ts` (Priority/PRIORITIES), `item-input.ts` (validate 1–6), `items.ts`, `nl-date.ts` (p1–p6 + numeric levels), `view-grouping.ts` (P-label groups), `canvas-fields.ts`/`FieldStrip.tsx` (a colored priority picker), and the display/sort spots (`ViewRenderer`, `BoardDnd`, dashboards, triage, mcp tools, matchers, todoist/calendar sync that set urgency). **Pending: build + `verify-priority` + Brandon ratify before merge.**

## ADR-097: Item lock toggle + the canvas "⋯" actions menu
**Date:** 2026-06-21
**Status:** accepted (Brandon, requested). Non-core: no schema change, no provider-seam change.
**Context:** The item canvas chrome scattered its actions — "Trash" / "Save as template" / "Apply template…" in the header, "Customize layout" loose in the canvas body. Brandon wanted them gathered behind one 3-dot menu top-right (so they collapse on mobile) and a new **lock** toggle that makes an item read-only.
**Decision:**
1. **A single `ItemActionsMenu` ("⋯")** at the top-right of both surfaces — the modal header (`Modal.tsx`) and the full-page chrome (`ItemCanvas.tsx`). It gathers **Lock/Unlock · Customize layout · Save as template · Apply template…** (the existing `SaveAsTemplateButton`/`ApplyTemplateButton` render as menu rows; their own popover/modal still drive the input). "Customize layout" moved out of `MarkdownCanvas` into the menu. **Trash stays** in the modal header (it wasn't in the consolidation request).
2. **Lock state lives in `items.properties.locked`** (a boolean), toggled with the existing **`propertyPatch`** per-key merge — *not* a new column. Rationale: lock is read only when an item is opened (the canvas already loads `properties`), never in a list/hot query, so a column isn't earned; `properties` is the designed home for non-hot per-item flags, and this sidesteps a core `schema.md` change (both-agree + ADR) for a per-instance UX feature. It doesn't leak into FTS (boolean, not a string) or `CustomProperties` (renders from the type's schema only).
3. **Locked = read-only on the four things Brandon named:** title (`readOnly` + `pointer-events-none`), body (Tiptap `setEditable(false)` drops contenteditable so the cursor can't enter; the formatting toolbar hides), the field strip, and custom properties (both wrapped in a `disabled <fieldset>` so every control disables at once). Subtasks/relations/recurrence are deliberately left interactive (out of the stated scope).
**Why / alternatives:** *An `items.is_locked` column* — rejected for now (core schema change requiring Tyler's agreement, for a flag no query needs to be hot). *Per-field disabling by hand* — rejected; a `disabled` fieldset with `display:contents` locks a whole panel in one wrapper without disturbing layout.
**Affects:** new `src/components/canvas/ItemActionsMenu.tsx`; `Modal.tsx` (+`locked` prop, menu in the right cluster), `@modal/(.)items/[id]/page.tsx` (reads `properties.locked`), `ItemCanvas.tsx` (menu replaces the loose template buttons), `MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (computes `locked`, threads it down, drops the two "Customize layout" links), `ItemEditor.tsx`/`MarkdownEditor.tsx`/`TabbedBody.tsx` (`editable`/`locked`), `FieldStrip.tsx` + `CustomProperties.tsx` (`locked` fieldset), `SaveAsTemplateButton.tsx` (wrapper made full-width for the menu row).

## ADR-098: Favorites — a star toggle + a nav flyout for instant access to key items
**Date:** 2026-06-21
**Status:** accepted (Brandon, requested). Non-core: no schema change, no provider-seam change.
**Context:** Brandon wanted instant access to a small, curated set of key items — a built-in nav entry that "flows out" into a simple list, reorderable by drag on mobile and desktop, with a star toggle living alongside the lock/template actions on the item canvas, easily toggled on/off.
**Decision:**
1. **Favorites are an owner-curated, ordered list of item ids in `users.settings`** (`settings.favorites: string[]`), *not* a new column or a tag/relation. Rationale: it's a per-user preference list exactly like `navSlots` (ADR-056) — order is the array order, membership is presence — so it rides the existing jsonb settings blob (no migration, owner-scoped) and stays out of the core `schema.md` (which would need both-agree + ADR). A `tag` would conflate "instant-access bookmark" with "categorization"; an `items` column would put non-hot state on the hot table and be a core change. Validated/deduped/uuid-checked/capped (100) in `parseSettings`.
2. **The Favorites nav slot opens a flyout, it doesn't navigate** (Brandon's call: flyout over a dedicated page). `NavShell` special-cases a destination whose href is `FAVORITES_HREF` (`/favorites`) into a popover (`FavoritesFlyout`) — the same pattern as the `/search` slot opening the command palette, reusing the tools-popover open-state + outside-click closer. There is deliberately **no `/favorites` route**; the slot is the only entry point.
3. **The flyout fetches on open, links each row to its canvas, and reorders by drag** via pointer events (mouse + touch unified, no DnD dependency — Principle 5), committing the order to `PATCH /api/favorites`. Rows can be unstarred in place. Added to `DEFAULT_NAV_SLOTS` and the destination picker (`nav-slot-options.ts`) so it's present out of the box and addable/removable.
4. **The star toggle lives in the canvas `ItemActionsMenu`** (ADR-097's "⋯" menu, beside Lock), optimistic, writing `POST /api/favorites {itemId, favorite}`. Page + modal chrome resolve current membership via `isItemFavorited` (one settings read, page/non-template only).
**Why / alternatives:** *Favorite as a `tag`* — rejected; favorites is access, not classification, and needs explicit order. *An `items.favorite`/`favorite_rank` column* — rejected; core schema change for non-hot state, where the settings list is the established non-core home. *A dedicated `/favorites` page* — Brandon picked the flyout; a page can be added later if "see all" is wanted (the lib/API already back it).
**Affects:** `src/lib/settings.ts` (+`favorites`, `FAVORITES_HREF`, `FAVORITES_HARD_CAP`, parse + default slot); new `src/lib/favorites.ts` (pure list ops + DB-backed store) and `src/app/api/favorites/route.ts` (GET/POST/PATCH); new `src/components/nav/FavoritesFlyout.tsx`; `NavShell.tsx` (flyout slot); `nav-slot-options.ts` (picker entry); `ItemActionsMenu.tsx` (+star), `ItemCanvas.tsx`/`Modal.tsx`/`@modal/(.)items/[id]/page.tsx` (thread `favorited`); `scripts/verify-nav-and-deletes.mts` (favorites pure checks).

## ADR-099: Recurrence engine — monthly ordinal weekdays + day-of-month (amends ADR-076's RRULE subset)
**Date:** 2026-06-21
**Status:** accepted. **CORE** (extends the shared native recurrence engine + the stored RRULE shape the ICS feed emits — amends ADR-076 point 4). **Brandon gave permission for this change** (Tyler asked; Brandon agreed to extend the subset). Alpha posture (ADR-039): additive, back-compat, no migration. Pulls forward the monthly-positional part of `next_steps.md`'s NL-recurrence item.
**Context:** Tyler's real Todoist workflow includes monthly-positional repeats the engine couldn't express: "first/third Sunday of the month," "the third Thursday," "first and second Thursday," "3rd of the month." ADR-076 deliberately shipped a *constrained* RFC-5545 subset (`FREQ`, `INTERVAL`, weekly `BYDAY`, `COUNT`, `UNTIL`) with the `rrule` package as the documented off-ramp. These cases need ordinal `BYDAY` (`1SU`, `3TH`, `1TH,2TH`, `-1FR`) and `BYMONTHDAY` (`3`, `-1`) — still well within a hand-rolled subset, so we extend rather than take the dep.
**Decision:**
1. **`RRuleParts` gains two optional MONTHLY-only fields:** `byDayOrdinal?: {ordinal, weekday}[]` (ordinal 1..5 or -1 = last) and `byMonthDay?: number[]` (1..31 or -1 = last day). Weekly `byDay` is unchanged (plain weekdays); ordinals are parsed/emitted only for `FREQ=MONTHLY`.
2. **Parse/format** (`parseRRule`/`formatRRule`): a `BYDAY` token is now `(-?\d{1,2})?(WEEKDAY)` — plain → `byDay`, ordinal → `byDayOrdinal`; `BYMONTHDAY` parsed to `byMonthDay`. Emitted in `FREQ;INTERVAL;BYDAY;BYMONTHDAY;COUNT;UNTIL` order. **The stored string stays standards-shaped RFC-5545**, so the ICS feed (T4) still emits it **verbatim** — `src/lib/ics.ts`/`ics-data.ts` unchanged.
3. **`enumerateOccurrences`** gains a monthly-positional branch: step whole months by `INTERVAL` from `dtstart`'s month; within each month emit every matching date (nth-weekday via `nthWeekdayOfMonth`, day-of-month via `monthDayOf`), sorted/deduped, `>= dtstart`. Months that lack a date (a 5th Friday, day 31 in a 30-day month) are simply skipped. `nextOccurrenceOnOrAfter`/`nextUncompletedOnOrAfter`/`isOccurrence` ride it for free (all go through `enumerateOccurrences`).
4. **`describeRule`** renders the new cases: "Monthly on the first Sunday", "Monthly on the first & second Thursday", "Monthly on the 3rd", "Monthly on the last day".
5. **NL quick-add (`nl-date.ts`)** adds the grammar: `[the] <ordinal>[ and <ordinal>…] <weekday> [of the month]` → ordinal `BYDAY`; `[the] <Nth> of the month` → `BYMONTHDAY`. Also added **`every other …`** → `INTERVAL=2` (incl. `every other <weekday>`) — that one needed no engine change. The recognized phrase is stripped from the title and shown as a chip (the strip-and-confirm discipline, ADR-084).
6. **`RecurrenceControl` (the canvas editor) has no UI for these yet but must not destroy them:** `rebuild()` now carries `byDayOrdinal`/`byMonthDay` through unchanged whenever the preset stays monthly (parsed via `parseRRule`), dropping them only when the user deliberately switches the frequency away from monthly. A dedicated editor UI (an ordinal/day picker under the Monthly preset) is a follow-up.
**Why / alternatives:** *Adopt the `rrule` npm package now* — rejected; still a small, deterministic addition (~60 lines + two month helpers), and the off-ramp stays documented if the subset keeps growing. *Reuse weekly `byDay: Weekday[]` and store ordinals elsewhere* — rejected; ordinals belong in `BYDAY` per RFC-5545, so a typed `byDayOrdinal` keeps the stored string standards-shaped and the ICS feed verbatim. *Emit the parser grammar before the engine could enumerate it* — rejected as a silent-broken-rule trap; engine first, then parser.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-recurrence.mts` +19 (parse/format round-trip for ordinal `BYDAY` incl. multi + last, `BYMONTHDAY` incl. -1; enumeration: first Sunday, 1st & 2nd Thursday, last Friday, `BYMONTHDAY=31` skips short months, `BYMONTHDAY=-1` = each month's last day, 5th-Friday skip; four `describeRule` cases) — **ALL PASS** (incl. the live-Neon service section). `scripts/verify-nl-task.mts` +14 (`every other` week/weekday/month; first-sunday/third-thursday/first-and-second/3rd-of-month/last-of-month parse, schedule, label, title-strip) — **ALL PASS**. `verify-recurrence-calendar`/`verify-ics` regressions green. `tsc`/eslint clean.
**Affects:** `src/lib/recurrence.ts` (types, parse/format, enumerate branch + `nthWeekdayOfMonth`/`monthDayOf`, `describeRule`, `makeRecurrence`), `src/lib/nl-date.ts` (`every other` + monthly-positional grammar, `RecMatch` fields), `src/components/canvas/RecurrenceControl.tsx` (preserve monthly extras on rebuild), `scripts/verify-recurrence.mts` + `scripts/verify-nl-task.mts`. No migration, no dependency, no MCP/API shape change. Amends ADR-076 point 4 (the RRULE subset is now: `FREQ`, `INTERVAL`, weekly `BYDAY`, monthly ordinal `BYDAY` + `BYMONTHDAY`, `COUNT`, `UNTIL`).

## ADR-100: Web clipper — bookmarklet + share-target capture of readable page content (no images)
**Date:** 2026-06-21
**Status:** accepted (Brandon, requested). Non-core: no schema change, no provider-seam change — rides the existing machine-token API contract, the `link` type, and the `{format, text}` body. New dependencies justified below (Principle 5). Builds `explorations/web-clipper.md` (parked/post-1.0; Brandon pulled it forward this session).
**Context:** Brandon wanted an Evernote-style clipper: save a page's readable content as Markdown into the Inbox, from desktop Chrome and from mobile. On images (2026-06-21): **strip them for now** — "if I want to do something different later I can build it then." The size worry is mostly moot (markdown stores image *references*, a few hundred bytes, never the bytes; the only real bloat path, base64-inlining, would also multiply through the `revisions` snapshots), so text-only is both the simplest and the lightest choice, with an "archive images → resize/WebP → R2" option left as a clean future layer.
**Decision:**
1. **One extraction module** (`src/lib/clip/extract.ts`), deterministic (Principle 3, no model): **Mozilla Readability** finds the article, **Turndown** serializes to Markdown. **Images stripped** (an `addRule` returning "" for `img/picture/svg/video/audio/iframe/noscript` — turndown's built-in image rule beats `remove()`, so a removal rule is required). Relative links **absolutized** against the page URL. Two entries: `extractArticle(html, url)` (DOM the client already has) and `fetchAndExtract(url)` (server fetch, bounded 8s/3MB/http(s)+html, best-effort → null).
2. **`POST /api/machine/capture`** — same `api`-scoped machine token as `/api/machine/items` (the token IS the credential), so **CORS is open (`*`)**: a bookmarklet runs on whatever origin the user is reading and there are no cookies to protect; an `OPTIONS` preflight is served. Accepts `{url, html?, title?}`, creates a `link` item (`inbox: true`) with the markdown body; extraction failure still lands a URL-only item (never silently drops). Covered by the existing `/api/machine(.*)` Clerk bypass — no `proxy.ts` change.
3. **Desktop = bookmarklet** (over a Chrome extension first; the exploration doc's recommendation). A Build → AI & MCP generator (`ClipperSetup.tsx`) takes a pasted api token and assembles the draggable `javascript:` link client-side (the server never holds the raw token; href set via a ref to bypass React's `javascript:`-URL sanitization). It reads the live DOM (`document.documentElement.outerHTML`) — **reading the DOM is never CSP-blocked** (only *script injection* is), so auth'd/SPA pages work — and POSTs to the capture endpoint.
4. **Mobile = the existing PWA share target** (`/capture/share`, ADR-016) extended: a shared URL now runs `fetchAndExtract` to fill the body, degrading to URL + title on a paywall/non-article page.
**Why / alternatives:** *Chrome/Firefox extension first* — deferred; the bookmarklet has no store-approval/install flow and covers the common case, and reading the DOM sidesteps the CSP limitation the doc feared. *Client-side extraction in the bookmarklet* — rejected; would need to inject Readability (CSP-blocked on many pages) or bundle it (huge `javascript:` URL); sending the DOM to one server module keeps desktop + mobile on identical extraction logic (no drift). *Base64-inline images / rehost to R2* — declined for now (Brandon); inlining bloats body + every revision snapshot, rehosting spends the ~10GB quota — left as a future opt-in behind this same contract. *Promote a content-bearing clip to `note`* — kept as `link` with a body; triage decides. *New deps* (`@mozilla/readability`, `linkedom`, `turndown`) — justified: these are the canonical extraction combo the doc already names, and reimplementing Readability is far more maintenance than three well-worn libs; Turndown runs server-side on its bundled DOM, linkedom is the lightweight serverless-friendly DOM for Readability's input.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/clip/extract.ts`, `src/app/api/machine/capture/route.ts`, `src/components/build/ClipperSetup.tsx`, `scripts/verify-clip-extract.mts` (12/12); edited `src/app/capture/share/page.tsx` (body via `fetchAndExtract`), `src/app/build/claude/page.tsx` (+Web clipper section). New deps: `@mozilla/readability`, `linkedom`, `turndown` (+ `@types/turndown`). No migration.

## ADR-101: Repo moved to the `strategicli` GitHub org and made public (to keep Vercel deploys free)
**Date:** 2026-06-22
**Status:** accepted (Brandon). Infra / collaboration decision, **not** a change to anything in CLAUDE.md's core list (no data model, body format, type/canvas, module boundary, provider seam, MCP/API, or principle touched). Supersedes the original "personal private repo" hosting.
**Context:** To let Tyler push to `main` and run his own deployed instance off the shared codebase, the repo needed a home where a second person can both push *and* connect their own Vercel project. A personal repo blocks the second half: Vercel only lets the repo **owner** connect a personally-owned repo (a collaborator cannot), so Tyler could never wire his own Vercel to `brandonscollins/ledgr`. The repo was therefore transferred to a new GitHub org, **`strategicli`**, with both of us as org **Members** (members, not outside collaborators, since Vercel rejects outside collaborators on org repos too). That move then tripped a second rule: **Vercel's free Hobby plan refuses to deploy a *private* repo owned by an *org*** (a private *personal* repo is fine; a private *org* repo needs Vercel Pro, ~$20/user/mo). So the org migration unblocked Tyler's Git connection but broke the free deploy for both of us.
**Decision:**
1. The repo lives at **`github.com/strategicli/ledgr`** (org-owned); both of us are Members with write access, so either can push to `main`.
2. **The repo is public.** Chosen to preserve Vercel's native Git integration (auto-deploy on push, preview URLs, instant rollback) at **$0** on Hobby for both instances.
3. **Each person deploys their own Vercel project** from the one repo with their own env vars (Neon, Clerk, R2, Graph, Todoist, MCP). A push to `main` redeploys both instances independently. No shared/paid Vercel team.
4. **Secrets verified clean before going public:** no `.env` was ever committed (only `.env.example`), and a full-history gitleaks scan across all refs (including merge diffs) returned zero findings. Real credentials live only in Vercel env settings and local `.env.local` (gitignored), so "public" exposes code + docs, not keys, and nothing needed rotating.
5. **GitHub Secret Scanning + Push Protection enabled** (free on public repos) as the guard against a future accidental secret commit.
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep a personal private repo*: rejected, because a collaborator can't connect it to their own Vercel, so Tyler couldn't run his instance (push access, the one thing a personal repo grants a collaborator, wasn't the whole goal). *Vercel Pro (~$20/mo each)*: rejected, it breaks the ~$0 cost target (Principle 8) for an alpha tool. *GitHub Actions + Vercel CLI deploy* (free, keeps the repo private by building in CI and uploading prebuilt output so Vercel never connects to the repo): viable, and the documented fallback if the repo must go private again, but rejected now for the CI plumbing plus loss of native preview comments, since public gets the same free result with zero setup. *Mirror org→personal repo*: rejected, extra repos plus sync lag for no gain over public. **Trade-off accepted:** the source and planning docs (the PRD names the church and Brandon's role) are now publicly visible; reversible by going private and adopting the Actions route or Pro.
**Affects:** repo hosting (`github.com/strategicli/ledgr`), the Vercel Git connection for both instances, and each clone's `origin` remote (`git remote set-url origin https://github.com/strategicli/ledgr.git`). No code, schema, or provider-seam change.

---

## ADR-102: AI shapes the workspace over MCP — config-write tools + an orientation resource
**Date:** 2026-06-23
**Status:** accepted. **Core** (the machine/MCP API contract, on CLAUDE.md's frozen core list — it adds tools *and* a `resources` capability). **Additive only** — the twelve ADR-047/071 tools are unchanged and the original transport/method set still works. **Tyler pre-approved this direction** (the `explorations/ai-workspace-shaping-over-mcp.md` carry-forward + the ADR-047 "later extensions to `tools.ts` are not new core" blessing); built solo at Brandon's direction with the four design calls below, flagged in `COLLAB.md` to ratify.
**Context:** ADR-071 brought the MCP server to 12 tools, but every *write* tool was item-level; the three config tools (`list_types`/`list_views`/`list_templates`) only read, and dashboards/nav had no MCP surface at all. So the model could file and read items, but not *shape* the workspace. Brandon's aim — "the AI is FOR them": a user speaks naturally ("set up my main toolbar", "make me a place to track sermons") and the model makes Ledgr-correct moves, instead of the user learning the Build screens. The foundations were already there: the validated `parse*`+`create*`/`update*` libs the Build REST routes use (`types.ts`/`views.ts`/`dashboards.ts`/`settings.ts`), the `build-nav.ts` source of truth, and the rich multi-sentence tool-description style. Resolves the **write/shape half** of `explorations/ai-workspace-shaping-over-mcp.md` (ADR-071 was the read/apply half).
**Decision:**
1. **Eight new tools, each a thin wrapper over an already-owner-scoped lib** (the ADR-047/071 discipline — the surface can't drift from the app contract or skip owner-scoping; **safety lives in the parsers**, so the model literally can't persist an illegal config): **`describe_workspace`** (the read-before-write snapshot), **`create_type`**/**`update_type`** (`parseTypeInput`+`createType`/`updateType`), **`create_view`**/**`update_view`** (`parseViewInput`+`createView`/`updateView`), **`create_dashboard`**/**`add_widget`** (`parseDashboardInput`/`parseWidget`+`createDashboard`/`addWidget`), and **`update_nav`** (`updateSettings` scoped to the nav fields). Tools go **12 → 20.** **No config delete tool** — these shape by create/update only; destruction stays in the Build UI (tightens the safety story, like ADR-071 deferring authoring).
2. **The orientation guide is served as an MCP *resource*** (Brandon's call over a fatter `INSTRUCTIONS` string). `server.ts` gains a `resources` capability + `resources/list`/`resources/read` (+ an empty `resources/templates/list` so probing clients don't error); the one stable guide doc lives in the new pure `src/lib/mcp/guide.ts` (`ledgr://guide/workspace-shaping`, `text/markdown`). The guide is the unchanging "how a Ledgr workspace works" (Work/Build, the type/property model, views, dashboards/widgets, nav slots, the read-before-write rule, a worked toolbar example) — the complement to `describe_workspace`'s live, per-owner "what you have." `INSTRUCTIONS` gained a short paragraph pointing at both.
3. **`describe_workspace` returns summaries + drill-down** (Brandon's call over one fat snapshot): a compact cross-surface read — types (key/label/propertyCount), views (id/name/layout), dashboards (id/name + a short widget list), the nav (layout knobs + slots + assigned home/today dashboards), and the Build-tool catalog. Full detail stays in the existing `list_types`/`list_views` (the model pulls it for the one thing it's changing). Index-backed, **no `body`** (Principle 8) — ≈1–2k tokens and roughly flat, vs. a fat snapshot's 5–15k that grows with the workspace. It also closes a read-gap: dashboards and nav had no MCP read before.
4. **Config-write safety = conversational confirm + soft-delete + legibility** (Brandon's call over building a confirm/undo step). Config writes have no revision history (Track-changes/TC1 covers content, not a new type or nav rearrange), so the guarantee is: the model confirms the concrete change in chat before calling; types soft-delete to Trash and are re-editable; `describe_workspace` keeps state legible; and there is no delete tool. No new infra.
5. **Principle 3 reading (deterministic by default, AI on purpose):** the tools are deterministic primitives; the *model deciding to call them* is the deliberate, human-in-the-loop AI layer. Nothing here auto-commits in a cron — consistent with the same reading ADR-087 §5 set for the Claude-over-MCP minutes automation.
**Why / alternatives:** *Pre-encoded intent enums* (a fixed menu of shapes) — rejected; clarify-and-suggest *falls out* of the guide + live state (the model reads the nav has a rail and a floating bar, reads the current slots, and asks "which toolbar?"), so it needn't be hand-scripted. *Fatter `INSTRUCTIONS` string instead of a resource* — rejected (Brandon); a resource is structured, cache-friendly, and pulled on demand. *One fat `describe_workspace` snapshot* — rejected (Brandon) on cost; shaping is occasional and even small edits need detail on one thing, not all. *A confirm/undo step for config writes* — rejected for v1; conversational confirm + soft-delete + no-delete-tool suffice, and a confirm flag fits stateless MCP poorly. *Config delete tools* — deferred; destruction stays in the Build UI. *Per-tool ownerId on type writes* — n/a; types are instance-global (no `owner_id`) but gated by the authenticated machine token, exactly as the Build REST routes are gated by `requireOwner`. **No new dependency** (Principle 5) — the libs, the hand-rolled JSON-RPC server, the resource shape, and the description style all already existed.
**Affects:** `src/lib/mcp/tools.ts` (+8 tools; imports from `types`/`views`/`dashboards`/`settings`/`build-nav`; new config-summary helpers `typeView`/`viewView`/`dashView`/`navView`). `src/lib/mcp/server.ts` (`resources` capability; `resources/list`/`resources/read`/`resources/templates/list`; `INSTRUCTIONS` paragraph). New pure `src/lib/mcp/guide.ts`. `scripts/verify-mcp.mts` extended (20-tool list + annotations, the resources methods + unknown-uri error, and the shaping tools end-to-end on Neon: `create_type`→`describe_workspace`→`update_type`, `create_view`→`update_view`, `create_dashboard`→`add_widget`, `update_nav`, plus owner-scoping + parser-validation errors) — **101/101 on live Neon.** Also verified via a live HTTP round-trip through `POST /api/mcp` on Neon (both capabilities advertised, 20 tools, the guide resource reads, `describe_workspace` returns the real workspace). `tsc`/eslint/`next build` clean. **No schema/migration, no protocol *version* change, no new dependency.** Resolves the write/shape half of `explorations/ai-workspace-shaping-over-mcp.md`.

---

## ADR-103: Weekly DB backup goes to OneDrive only, not a public-repo GitHub artifact
**Date:** 2026-06-24
**Status:** accepted (Brandon). Security follow-on to ADR-101 (the public-repo flip); ops/infra, **not** a change to anything on CLAUDE.md's core list. Flagged in `COLLAB.md` for Tyler (the workflow is shared).
**Context:** ADR-101 made `strategicli/ledgr` public to keep Vercel deploys free. The weekly `backup` workflow (`.github/workflows/backup.yml`, runbook §4) stored its full `pg_dump` as a GitHub Actions artifact (`ledgr-backup-YYYY-MM-DD`, 60-day retention) — a design written when the repo was private. **GitHub Actions artifacts on a public repo are downloadable by any signed-in GitHub user** (and relayable anonymously, e.g. nightly.link), so a complete production database dump was effectively public. The OneDrive leg meant to be the private destination had never run: the four Graph secrets (`GRAPH_TENANT_ID`/`GRAPH_CLIENT_ID`/`GRAPH_CLIENT_SECRET`/`ONEDRIVE_EXPORT_UPN`) existed in Vercel env but were never added to the **separate** GitHub Actions secret store, so the upload step hit its warn-and-skip guard every run. ADR-101's pre-flip secret scan checked committed code, not Actions artifacts, so this vector was missed. Real exposure was small (alpha, ~44 KB of seed data, ADR-039 "no production data to protect"), but it is structural and had to close before real pastoral data lands.
**Decision:**
1. **OneDrive `/Ledgr/Backups/` is the sole backup destination.** The `upload-artifact` step is removed from the `backup` job — no plaintext DB dump is stored on the public repo.
2. **A missing Graph secret now FAILS the run** (was warn-and-skip, `exit 0`). With no artifact fallback, a backup that can't reach OneDrive must fail loudly (GitHub emails on failure) rather than silently produce nothing.
3. **The four Graph secrets were added to the repo's Actions secret store** (the same values already in Vercel env / `.env.local`), so the scheduled job uploads to OneDrive.
4. **The two existing exposed artifacts were deleted** (`ledgr-backup-2026-06-19`, `…-2026-06-12`); the live DB is unaffected (each dump is a copy of it).
5. **The restore procedure (runbook §4) now reads from OneDrive** `/Ledgr/Backups/` instead of the Actions artifact.
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep the artifact but encrypt it* (gpg symmetric, preinstalled on the runner, no new dep) — rejected for v1: it adds a passphrase secret and a decrypt step in restore for no gain over a private OneDrive copy that the restore-test already validates. *Make the repo private again* — rejected; ADR-101 chose public deliberately for free Vercel deploys and that trade still holds. *Leave it* — rejected; the exposure is structural and grows with real data. **No new dependency** (Principle 5); deterministic plumbing (Principle 3).
**Affects:** `.github/workflows/backup.yml` (artifact step removed; OneDrive step now required/hard-fail; header comment), `runbook.md` §4 (restore reads from OneDrive; the four Graph secrets are required repo Actions secrets), the repo's Actions secrets (four Graph secrets added), and the two deleted artifacts. No code, schema, or provider-seam change. The `restore-test` job is unchanged (it never uploaded an artifact).

---

## ADR-104: Viewing an item must not bump its edit date (a body PATCH is a no-op when the text is unchanged)
**Date:** 2026-06-24
**Status:** accepted (Brandon, bug fix). Touches a core cross-cutting invariant (soft-delete + revisions, and `updated_at` semantics) on the shared `updateItem` path, so flagged in `COLLAB.md` for Tyler. Behavioral refinement only: no schema, no migration, no MCP-contract shape change (`verify-mcp` 101/101 unchanged).
**Context:** Opening an item (no typing, no clicks) bumped its `updated_at` (the "edit date") about 1.5s later and snapshotted a redundant revision. Reproduced on a real item: opening it moved `updated_at` from 2026-06-22 to today, with the body byte-identical before and after. Root cause: the Tiptap body editor fires one programmatic `onUpdate` shortly after it mounts (a normalize pass, not a user edit) carrying the loaded markdown verbatim; `ItemEditor`'s debounced autosave PATCHed `{ body }`; and `updateItem` wrote `body`/`body_text` whenever `patch.body !== undefined`. Because `items.updated_at` is Drizzle `$onUpdate(() => new Date())`, any UPDATE moves it. Net: every view cost one no-op write, one edit-date bump, and one junk revision (eroding the ~50-per-item revision cap).
**Decision:** Two guards, with the data layer as the guarantee.
1. **API no-op guard (`updateItem`).** The pre-update select now reads the existing `body`; `writeBody = patch.body !== undefined && (the text differs, or the format differs when both sides are well-formed `{format,text}`)`. When false, the body is not written, no revision is snapshotted, and mentions are not re-synced. If the patch carried only a no-op body, the item is returned untouched (200, no UPDATE, no bump) rather than erroring; a patch with no recognized fields at all still errors as before. This covers every caller (editor, MCP `update_item`, REST) and stops the redundant revisions.
2. **Host source guard (`ItemEditor.onBodyChange`).** A `savedBodyText` ref seeded from the loaded body; an emitted body equal to it is skipped (the ref advances on each real change). This stops the phantom at the source, so opening an item fires no PATCH and does not flash the save-status indicator. A real edit always differs, so it still saves.
**Why / alternatives:** An editor-side guard keyed on the editor's own `onCreate` serialization was tried and rejected: at that lifecycle point `getMarkdown()` did not equal the stored text, so it missed the phantom. The stored body (which the phantom provably re-emits) is the stable baseline, and the host already holds it. The host guard alone is not the guarantee (it cannot cover MCP/REST, and a tabbed body may not round-trip the reassembled markdown exactly); the API guard alone fixes the edit-date and revision spam but still lets the wasted PATCH fire and flash "Saved" on open. Both together are correct for all callers and clean in the common path. Suppressing the editor's mount `onUpdate` outright was rejected as fragile across Tiptap internals; comparing serialized output is robust. No new dependency (Principle 5), deterministic (Principle 3), and it serves "fast for the user, cheap on the back end" (Principle 8) while keeping revisions meaningful.
**Affects:** `src/lib/items.ts` (`updateItem`: `body` added to the pre-update select; the `writeBody` gate over the body write, the revision snapshot, and the mention re-sync; the no-op-body early return; `isItemBody` import). `src/components/markdown-editor/ItemEditor.tsx` (`savedBodyText` ref + the `onBodyChange` skip). Verified on Neon (dev-auth): the bug reproduced, then after the fix opening items no longer bumps `updated_at` and fires no PATCH, a real edit still bumps + writes + snapshots, and an explicit identical-body PATCH returns 200 with no bump. `verify-items`, `verify-revisions`, `verify-body-contract`, `verify-mcp` all green; tsc/eslint clean. No schema, no migration, no MCP-contract shape change, no new dependency.

## ADR-105: Per-type list tabs ("list lenses") — default sort tabs + customizable, with widget/view tabs
**Date:** 2026-06-24
**Status:** accepted (Brandon). Non-core (per-instance UI config in `users.settings`, the navSlots/favorites posture — ADR-056/098); no migration, no dependency. The one shared-file touch is an additive sort-mode extension to the view query builder (`src/lib/views.ts`); the public `ViewSort`/`parseSort` and the MCP `create_view` contract are unchanged, so it's flagged in `COLLAB.md` for Tyler but needs no both-agree gate.
**Context:** Only `/tasks` had a horizontal tab strip; every other type list showed one fixed ordering (`updatedAt desc`). Brandon wanted that strip on every type by default: a few built-in orderings always present, each reversible, plus tabs based on the type's own properties, with the customization tucked into Build. He also asked that a tab be able to be "a widget" (a saved view), bringing the dashboard-widget flexibility to this surface (the convergence `explorations/flexible-surfaces.md` §2 anticipated).
**Decision:** A type's list page renders a tab strip of "lenses." A lens is either a **sort** (orders the plain list) or a **view** (renders a saved view via the existing `ViewRenderer` — the dashboard "view widget" reused as a tab).
1. **Four virtual sort defaults**, computed not seeded, so every type has them free: Recent (`updatedAt desc`), Newest (`createdAt desc`), A→Z (`title asc`), Most linked (confirmed-relation count desc). The active sort tab carries a direction toggle that flips `?rev`, so each default inverts in place (Brandon chose this over duplicate per-direction tabs). URL-driven (`?lens=&rev=`), server-rendered, no client JS, like `/tasks`.
2. **Customization in Build > Types > edit** (`ListTabsEditor`): reorder/rename/remove/add/reset. Add offers a built-in field, one of the type's own properties (text/number/date/select), or a saved view. Stored per type in **`users.settings.listTabs`** (absent key = defaults; full-list replace, the navSlots model). A focused `PATCH /api/types/[key]/list-tabs` writes it; `null`/empty resets.
3. **Engine (additive, internal):** `queryViewItems` accepts a `ListSort` superset adding `mostLinked` (a correlated `count(*)` over confirmed `relations`, served by `relations_source_idx`/`target_idx`) and a property sort (`properties->>key`, with a guarded numeric cast so non-numbers sort last). The stored `ViewSort`/`parseSort`/MCP shape are untouched.
4. **View-lens render** reuses the `DashboardView` orchestration (`getView` → scope → `queryViewItems` + `countViewItems` + grouping → `ViewRenderer`) in a self-contained `src/lib/view-render.ts` (`resolveViewLens` + `applyTypeScope`, mirroring `applyFocus`), so no dashboard code is touched. A missing/deleted view falls back to the default sorted list. View authoring stays in `ViewBuilder`; a lens only references a view.
5. **Scope:** the generic `/list/[type]` plus the bespoke Notes and Links lists. Events and Tasks keep their richer bespoke tabs (Brandon's call).
**Why / alternatives:** *Storing lenses on the type definition* (a `types.list_tabs` column) was rejected: it's display config, not data model, and would pull a non-core feature through the core both-agree gate and a migration; `users.settings` matches the navSlots/favorites precedent and keeps it per-instance. *Modeling a lens as a full saved view* (seeding ~4 views per type) was rejected as heavier and polluting the views manager; virtual defaults cost nothing and need no rows. *Exposing `mostLinked`/property sort through the public `ViewSort` + MCP `create_view`* was deliberately deferred to keep the core surface small; the lens feature uses the internal superset. *Duplicate per-direction tabs* for reverse was rejected by Brandon in favor of the in-place toggle. Deterministic (Principle 3), no new dependency (Principle 5), body-free + owner-scoped + capped (Principle 8), defer-by-hiding (the lens generalizes the older `types.default_view_id`, left untouched).
**Affects:** new `src/lib/list-lenses.ts` (Lens types, `defaultLenses`/`lensesForType`/`resolveLensSort`/`selectLens`/`parseLenses`/`parseListTabs`/`lensPropertyOptions`), `src/lib/view-render.ts` (`resolveViewLens`/`applyTypeScope`), `src/components/lists/ListLenses.tsx` + `ViewLensBody.tsx`, `src/components/build/ListTabsEditor.tsx`, `src/app/api/types/[key]/list-tabs/route.ts`. Modified `src/lib/views.ts` (`ListSort` + `listOrderExpr`), `src/lib/settings.ts` (`listTabs`), `src/app/list/[type]/page.tsx`, `src/app/notes/page.tsx`, `src/app/links/page.tsx`, `src/app/build/types/[key]/edit/page.tsx`. `scripts/verify-list-lenses.mts` (30+ checks: defaults, reverse, mostLinked both directions, property text vs numeric guard, view-lens scope + fallback, owner-scoping, body-free SQL, settings round-trip) green on Neon; tsc/eslint/`next build` clean; in-browser eyeball on Neon (strip + reverse + most-linked on Notes and `/list/person`, the Build panel with real saved-view widget options, no console errors).

## ADR-106: Per-type status DISPLAY MODE — none / done-checkbox / custom-statuses (presentation over the ADR-082 category plumbing)
**Date:** 2026-06-24
**Status:** accepted (Brandon + Tyler agreed; Tyler greenlit slice 1 up front). **CORE** — it adds a `types` column and changes how the canonical `task` type and the view builder present status, so it's flagged in `COLLAB.md`. **Additive**: no change to `items.status`/`status_category`, the machine/MCP status contract, or any existing query.
**Context:** Brandon + Tyler decided tasks should default to a simple **done/undone checkbox**, not a multi-status `select`, with multiple statuses an opt-in per type ("if a user wants status, they create that; the plumbing that decides 'is it complete' runs through a simple yes/no"). Brandon separately flagged that the **view builder always offered a Status filter even for types that don't use status** (a Person has no "complete"). The key realization: **ADR-082 already made the plumbing category-backed** — `status_category === 'done'` is the yes/no, decoupled from the label, and a done-checkbox + the recurrence-aware `toggleItemDone` already exist. So the ask is a thin **presentation layer over that model**, not a data-model change. (A boolean redesign was considered and rejected — see Why.)
**Decision:** A per-type **display mode** — `'none' | 'checkbox' | 'select'` — in a new nullable **`types.status_mode`** (text, not an enum, matching `items.status`; adding a mode never needs a migration). Resolved (never null) by `resolveStatusMode` in `src/lib/status.ts`.
1. **The mode is presentation only.** The fixed category plumbing (`status_category`) is untouched and stays the source of truth for "is it done". `none` hides every status affordance (canvas control, view-builder Status filter/group/column, list chip/checkbox); `checkbox` shows a binary done/not-done checkbox (completing via the existing `POST /api/items/[id]/complete` → `toggleItemDone`, so it stays recurrence-aware and needs no schema); `select` is today's multi-status dropdown + colored kanban.
2. **Resolution + defaults (status is opt-in).** Unset/unknown → `none`, UNLESS the type defines a custom `status_schema` → `select` (a multi-status type never hides its own statuses). Migration 0032 + `seed.mjs` backfill explicitly: **`task` → checkbox** (the new binary default), **any type with a custom `status_schema` (project + user types) → select**, **everything else → none**. So person/note/link/event and freshly-created user types show no status until the user enables it. **`event` is `none`** (events use the shared default canvas, which by ADR-018 has no status field; `none` preserves that exactly — checkbox would require wiring a status control into the default canvas, deferred).
3. **The Build control** (`StatusSchemaEditor`, "Completion tracking"): three radios; the existing inherit/define status-schema editor shows only under "Custom statuses". Saves via the focused `PATCH /api/types/[key]/statuses` (now `{ mode, statuses }`) → `setTypeStatusConfig`.
4. **The task canvas** (`TaskCanvas`) renders a done-checkbox section (reusing `SubtaskCheckbox` → the complete endpoint) in checkbox mode, the status `select` (in `FieldStrip`) in select mode, and nothing in none mode.
5. **The view builder** (`ViewBuilder`) gates the Status filter, the status group-by option, and the status column on the selected type's mode — the same "offer a field only if the type has it" rule already applied to dates/urgency. "Any type" keeps status.
6. **Defer-by-hiding.** Switching a type to checkbox/none **never rewrites its stored `status_schema`** (the setter writes the schema only in select mode), so flipping back to select restores the user's statuses verbatim.
**Why / alternatives — and DO NOT collapse this back to a boolean (Brandon's explicit ask that the rationale survive):** *A real boolean `items.done` column* (the first option weighed) was rejected: the done/undone the user sees in checkbox mode **is already** the category plumbing (`status_category === 'done'`). Collapsing status to a boolean would delete the category abstraction that (a) lets a recurring task **advance** instead of "completing" (ADR-076), (b) backs the `in_progress`/`archived` buckets and the **planned archive axis** (its own forthcoming ADR), (c) lets `project` and any type keep genuine multi-status, and (d) keeps the **machine/MCP status contract** (a text key + a category) stable. The mode is the cheap, reversible *presentation* choice; the category is the load-bearing *model*. A future builder (or Tyler's AI) tempted to "simplify" the two-field status into one boolean should stop here: the simplification is already done — in the category, not the column. *Restricting everyone to two statuses* was rejected (it's the noise Brandon wanted gone and contradicts the opt-in choice). *Deriving the mode from the schema shape* (no stored column) was rejected: `none` is not derivable (every type inherits a default schema), and Brandon wanted an explicit user-set toggle (the legibility convention). *Defaulting unset types to `select`* (today's behavior) was rejected in favor of opt-in `none`, which matches bespoke-first and removes the view-builder noise for new types; existing inherited-status user types (e.g. `hiring_candidate`) therefore default to `none` and re-enable status with one click (flagged in `COLLAB.md`).
**Scope / deferred (noted, not built here):** the list **renderer** still shows the default status column for a `none`-type **table** view (the common list/agenda/calendar surfaces are already clean — `ItemRow` shows a checkbox only for tasks and `StatusChip` hides the resting "open"); a `none`-type board defaults to grouping by status. Threading `status_mode` through `ViewRenderer` + its render hosts is a small fast-follow. Also deferred: a status control on the **default canvas** for non-task checkbox/select types (so a custom type's mode shows on its item page), and exposing `status_mode` through the MCP `list_types`/shaping tools. The **archive axis** (a cross-cutting `items.archived_at` "hide-but-recoverable" flag, orthogonal to done/undone) is its own next slice + ADR; this ADR leaves the `archived` status category in place for it to reconcile.
**Affects:** new mode engine in `src/lib/status.ts` (`STATUS_MODES`/`StatusMode`/`isStatusMode`/`resolveStatusMode`); `src/db/schema.ts` (`types.status_mode`); migration `drizzle/0032_nice_azazel.sql` (additive column + backfill) + `scripts/seed.mjs` (project mode + idempotent backfill); `src/lib/types.ts` (`TypeDefinition.statusMode`, `rowToDefinition` resolve, `setTypeStatusSchema` → `setTypeStatusConfig(key, mode, schema)`); `src/app/api/types/[key]/statuses/route.ts` (`{ mode, statuses }`); `src/components/build/StatusSchemaEditor.tsx` (three-way "Completion tracking"); `src/app/build/types/[key]/edit/page.tsx` (pass `initialMode`); `src/components/canvas/TaskCanvas.tsx` (checkbox section + mode-gated strip); `src/components/views/ViewBuilder.tsx` (`usesStatus`/`fieldColumnsForView` gating) + `src/app/views/new/page.tsx` + `src/app/views/[id]/edit/page.tsx` (pass `statusMode`); `scripts/verify-statuses.mts` (+10 mode checks).
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-statuses.mts` 35/35 (incl. the new mode parse/resolve/opt-in-default checks); `verify-types` + `verify-views` green (no regression); tsc + `next build` + eslint clean; migration 0032 applied to Neon and the backfill confirmed (`task`=checkbox, `project`=select, the rest=none). In-browser on Neon (dev-auth): the Build "Completion tracking" control shows three modes with Person resolving to None (schema editor hidden); the view builder's Status filter is present for any/task/project and **absent** for person/note; the task canvas shows a done-checkbox (no status `select`) labeled with the current status, and clicking it completed a non-recurring task (open→done→open via the endpoint) while the recurring task advanced its occurrence; the `PATCH …/statuses` route round-tripped person→checkbox→none (schema preserved as null) and rejected an invalid mode. No change to `items`, the FTS column, or the MCP contract; no new dependency.

## ADR-107: Interface density, a whole-UI scale knob (per surface), driven from the root font-size
**Date:** 2026-06-24
**Status:** accepted. **NOT core**: pure UI personalization stored on `users.settings` (the navSlots/favorites/textSize posture), no schema change, no migration. **Additive** and opt-in: the new `default` level (1.0) leaves the app pixel-identical to before, so Tyler's instance is untouched until he picks a level. Built solo (UI/UX polish + per-instance config, the "move fast" side of the COLLAB split).
**Context:** Brandon wanted to scale the *whole* interface (nav, menus, titles, buttons, toggles, spacing), not just the markdown reading canvas that `textSize` already sizes, and to set it separately for desktop and mobile. The requirement that fixed the mechanism: it has to "stay relative as we change the UI," meaning a screen built later should inherit the scaling without being enumerated.
**Decision:** One knob, **`--ui-scale`**, drives the **root font-size**: `html { font-size: calc(100% * var(--ui-scale)) }` (globals.css). Because the app is built from rem-based Tailwind utilities, scaling the root rem scales every rem-based dimension at once (type, spacing, the nav chrome, the prose canvas), and any UI added later inherits it for free, with nothing listed by hand.
1. **Levels.** `compact` / `default` / `comfortable` / `roomy` map to `UI_SCALE` = 0.9 / 1.0 / 1.1 / 1.2 (`src/lib/settings.ts`). The factors stay modest so the layout never breaks, and `default` is exactly 1.0 (a no-op).
2. **Per surface.** `uiDensity` (desktop) plus `mobileUiDensity` (null mirrors desktop, else overrides on phones below the `sm` breakpoint). The layout resolves both and emits a **server-rendered `<style>`**: `:root{--ui-scale:<desktop>}@media (max-width:639.98px){:root{--ui-scale:<mobile>}}`. The var must sit on `:root` (custom properties inherit down, not up, and the `html` font-size rule reads it), and a media query cannot live in an inline `style` attribute, hence the `<style>` block. The 639.98px ceiling complements the nav's 640px (`sm`) desktop breakpoint, so chrome and density switch surfaces together. Values are fixed numbers from `UI_SCALE`, so there is nothing to escape.
3. **Nav geometry moved px to rem.** `RAIL_W` / `TOP_BAR_H` / `BUILD_SIDEBAR_W` (formerly `RAIL_PX` / `TOP_BAR_PX` / `BUILD_SIDEBAR_PX`, `src/lib/nav-layout.ts`) are now rem strings (14rem/4rem/1.5rem, 3.5rem, 15rem, equal to the old px at the 1.0 scale). The same constants feed both the rendered nav width and the body clearance, so the frame and its clearance scale together and stay locked at any density. `NavShell`/`BuildSidebar` consume the rem values.
4. **Coexists with `textSize`.** `textSize` still sizes only the prose canvas via `--prose-font-size`; `--ui-scale` is the orthogonal whole-UI knob. The settings form gains a "Display density" section (separate Desktop and Mobile rows, Mobile offering "Same as desktop"), saved through the existing `PATCH /api/settings` and validated in `parseSettings`.
**Why / alternatives:** A *spacing-only design token* (or a per-component enumeration of every size) was rejected: it would not satisfy "stays relative as we change the UI," since each new component would have to opt in. Scaling the rem unit at the root is the one place that catches everything, present and future, for free. Emitting the var *inline on `<html>`* was rejected: an inline style would beat the media query, so the mobile override could never win, which is why the var comes from a `<style>` rule on `:root`. Two things deliberately do **not** move: px borders stay crisp (1px hairlines don't blur), and rem-based media-query **breakpoints** don't shift, because a media query evaluates rem against the initial 16px rather than the overridden root, so the responsive layout and the mobile/desktop split stay put at any density.
**Affects:** `src/lib/settings.ts` (`UI_DENSITIES`/`UiDensity`/`UI_SCALE`, the `uiDensity`/`mobileUiDensity` fields, defaults, and `parseSettings` validation); `src/app/globals.css` (the `--ui-scale` token + the `html` font-size rule); `src/app/layout.tsx` (resolve both scales, emit the per-surface `<style>`); `src/lib/nav-layout.ts` (rem constants `RAIL_W`/`TOP_BAR_H`/`BUILD_SIDEBAR_W` + the `navPadVars` switch); `src/components/nav/NavShell.tsx` and `src/components/nav/BuildSidebar.tsx` (consume the rem constants); `src/components/settings/SettingsForm.tsx` (the "Display density" section). No schema, no migration, no new dependency.
**Verification:** built and verified in the originating cloud session; re-confirmed here with `tsc --noEmit`, eslint, and `next build` clean. The `default`/`default` pair is pixel-identical to the prior UI (1.0 scale; the rem nav constants equal the former px), so the opt-in is safe; non-default levels scale nav, menus, titles, buttons, and spacing together from the root font-size, with px borders and the responsive breakpoints intentionally unmoved. Coexists with the prose `textSize`; no change to any query, the FTS column, or the MCP contract.

## ADR-108: Task canvas right rail — compact rows + a single Schedule popover (Todoist-style), and a reusable `Popover` primitive
**Date:** 2026-06-24
**Status:** accepted. **NOT core** — UI/UX polish of the `task` canvas only (the "move fast, solo" side of the COLLAB split); no schema, no migration, no change to the data model, the canvas seam, or the MCP contract. The underlying scheduled-date/time/repeat/reminder writes and their endpoints are untouched.
**Context:** Brandon flagged the task canvas right rail as cluttered: ~7 always-expanded sections (Status, Scheduled w/ chips + NL box, Due, Urgency, Relations, the full Repeat editor, and Reminders & Focus) stacked down the rail, with the recurrence editor's four controls always on screen even when set to a simple "Daily". He asked for Todoist's pattern (he supplied screenshots): a resting list of one-line property rows, each showing its value or an "add" affordance, that open a popover with the full editor — and specifically for repeat (plus time and reminder) to live *inside* the date popover rather than as their own sections.
**Decision:** The rail becomes a divided list of compact rows; the heavy scheduling editors collapse behind one **Schedule** row.
1. **One Schedule row, one popover.** A `SchedulePopover` row summarizes the lot ("Thu, Jun 25 · 8:18 PM · ↻ Daily") and opens a popover holding, top to bottom: the date (a reusable `DayField` = native date input + Today/Tomorrow/+1wk/Clear chips + natural-language box), then **Time** (`ScheduledTimeControl`), **Repeat** (`RecurrenceControl`, incl. Next date / Stored as + the virtual-mode `RecurrenceCalendar`), and **Reminder** (`ReminderControl`). Those four controls are **reused verbatim in `bare` mode** — this relocates them, it does not reimplement them. The date is optimistic in the row; each sub-control keeps its own optimistic + `router.refresh()` write, which re-feeds the row's summary props.
2. **Due / Priority / Status as rows.** `DueRow` opens a small date popover (same `DayField`); `PriorityRow` opens a None + P1–P6 swatch menu (replacing the bare `<select>`); `StatusRow` (select-mode types only) opens a swatch menu of the resolved statuses. Checkbox-mode status stays the inline done-checkbox (ADR-106); `none` shows nothing. Relations and custom scalar properties stay their existing editors, wrapped in the same row rhythm.
3. **Focus today stays visible.** The one-tap focus star is a labeled row at the bottom, deliberately **not** tucked behind a popover (frequent daily action; legibility convention).
4. **A reusable `Popover` primitive** (`src/components/ui/Popover.tsx`): a trigger button + a floating panel, closing on outside-click or Esc, with a render-prop `close()` for editors that dismiss on commit. Built in-house (no Radix/Floating-UI — Principle 5), generalizing the open/outside-click/Esc logic ConfirmButton pioneered for content-bearing popovers.
5. **Completion moves to the title (Todoist-style), the rail Status row goes away (checkbox mode).** Brandon's follow-up: put the "mark complete" control where Todoist does — a circle next to the title, **colored by the task's priority** (P1 red … P5 green, P6/none neutral; `priorityStyle`), and strike through + dim the title when done. New `TaskTitle` (`src/components/canvas/TaskTitle.tsx`) renders the circle + the title editor and owns one optimistic `done` state so the circle fills and the title strikes **instantly** on click (then `/complete` lands — recurrence-aware via the existing `toggleItemDone` — and refresh re-syncs). The strike/dim must live **on the title `<textarea>` itself** (a new `done` prop on `ItemEditor`), because `text-decoration` doesn't cross a textarea boundary from a parent. The redundant rail **Status row is dropped in checkbox mode** (one completion control, by the title); `select` types keep `StatusRow` (a circle can't carry multiple statuses) and `none` shows neither — the title still strikes when its category is done in any mode.
**Why / two load-bearing choices:** *(a) The panel portals to `<body>` with fixed positioning, not in-flow `absolute`.* The item Modal panel is `overflow-hidden` around an inner `overflow-y-auto` scroll area, so a tall in-flow popover (the Schedule editor especially) would clip against it. Fixed + portal floats above the modal and never clips; it flips above the trigger and caps its height when space below is tight, and re-measures on scroll/resize (capture-phase scroll, to catch the modal's inner scroll) so it stays glued to its row. *(b) Esc is claimed in the CAPTURE phase.* The Modal closes on Esc unless `e.defaultPrevented` is already set, but its `document` keydown listener is registered first (bubble phase), so a bubble-phase `preventDefault()` in the popover ran too late and Esc closed the whole modal. Listening in capture runs the popover first; it marks the Esc handled, then the modal's bubble handler stands down — Esc now closes only the popover. (The shared `ConfirmButton` has the same latent bubble-phase bug; flagged as a fast-follow, not fixed here.) *Alternatives rejected:* a CSS-only/absolute popover (clips in the modal); a popover library (dependency weight); converting relations/custom props to popovers too (they're already inline field editors — out of scope).
**Scope / deferred:** the **classic `MarkdownCanvas`** (non-task types: event/note/link) keeps its existing expanded `FieldStrip`/recurrence layout — the same row pattern can adopt it later. `ConfirmButton`'s capture-phase Esc fix. `FieldStrip`'s rail mode is now unused (task was its only rail consumer) but left in place.
**Affects:** new `src/components/ui/Popover.tsx`; new `src/lib/format-date.ts` (`formatDayLabel`); new `src/components/canvas/rail/` (`styles.ts`, `row-ui.tsx`, `DayField.tsx`, `SchedulePopover.tsx`, `DueRow.tsx`, `PriorityRow.tsx`, `StatusRow.tsx`); new `src/components/canvas/TaskTitle.tsx` (priority-colored completion circle + struck-through title); `src/components/markdown-editor/ItemEditor.tsx` (a `done` prop strikes/dims the title `<textarea>`); `src/components/canvas/TaskCanvas.tsx` (rail recomposed as rows; title via `TaskTitle`; dropped the `FieldStrip`/`section`/strip scaffolding, the four direct control imports, and the checkbox-mode rail Status row). No schema, no migration, no new dependency.
**Verification:** `tsc --noEmit` + eslint clean. In-browser on Neon (dev-auth, the "Review Kingdom Come outline with Tom" task): the rail renders as compact rows (To Do · Schedule · Due · Priority · Tags/Project · Focus today); the Schedule row summarizes "Thu, Jun 25 · 8:18 PM · ↻ Daily"; its popover opens (not clipped) with Date/Time/Repeat/Reminder all reflecting the stored values (date 2026-06-25, 8:18 PM for 2 hr, Daily, On schedule, Separate note each time, 9 AM default); the Priority menu picks (P2→P1) PATCH `→ 200` and update optimistically (restored to P2 after); **Esc closes the popover while the modal stays open** (the capture-phase fix). The title completion circle renders in the priority color (amber for P2); clicking it fills the circle (white check) and strikes through + dims the title instantly, hits `/complete → 200`, and un-done reverts — confirmed the `<textarea>` strike-through renders in Chromium. No console errors; no change to any query, the FTS column, or the MCP contract.

## ADR-109: Tasks default to the effective plan date (scheduled ?? due); the task canvas regains its arrangeable grid
**Date:** 2026-06-24
**Status:** accepted (Brandon). **Part A (the plan-date default) is CORE** — it adds a `plan` value to the `list_items` `dateField` and `create_view` date enums and changes the default date field, both part of the **machine/MCP API contract**. It is **additive** (a new allowed value, nothing removed) and shipped solo on Brandon's standing instance-direction waiver, **flagged to Tyler in COLLAB.md**. **Part B (task canvas arrange) is NOT core** (UI wiring of the task canvas, the "move fast, solo" side); no schema, no migration, no dependency.
**Context:** Brandon's tasks live on a *scheduled* (planned) date; he does not use the *due* (deadline) date and may never. The canonical surfaces already keyed "overdue / on the plate" off the effective plan date (scheduled if set, else due): Today, the overdue auto-roll (ADR-077), and the ICS feed. Two stragglers disagreed: the `/tasks` list computed red/placement from the *earliest* of due/scheduled (`min`), and the generic view/widget/MCP date filter defaulted to `dueDate` alone, so the "Overdue Tasks" / "Tasks Due Today" starter widgets and any plain task view came up empty for a scheduled-only user. Separately, "Customize layout" (the per-type arrangeable grid, ADR-069 Feature B) silently did nothing on tasks: ADR-108 moved the task type onto the bespoke `TaskCanvas` rail, which never consumed the `arrange` flag or a saved `canvas_layout`, so the grid path (which lives in the default `MarkdownCanvas`) was bypassed.
**Decision — Part A (effective plan date is the task default).**
1.
