A first-class **`plan`** date option, the effective plan date `COALESCE(scheduled_date, due_date)`, added to the view engine's `DATE_PROPERTIES` (filter window + calendar/agenda placement), `SORT_FIELDS`, `GROUP_FIELDS`, and `COLUMN_FIELDS` (`src/lib/views.ts`). It is a single `PLAN_DATE` SQL expression reused across the window predicate, the order-by, and the board bucket. Because it is a COALESCE of the two UTC-midnight calendar-day columns, it is treated as a calendar-day field (same UTC day boundaries as due/scheduled, ADR-008), and a task with no due date never breaks: COALESCE falls through to NULL, which reads as "no date" exactly like an undated task.
2. **`plan` is the default** wherever a date window or task placement is computed: the filter window defaults to `plan` when no `dateField` is named (was `dueDate`), and a non-event calendar/agenda defaults placement to `plan` (was `dueDate`). The builder offers `plan` first for task/any types (`dateFieldsFor`), so a new task view picks it by default; events still default to `meetingAt`.
3. **The stragglers now agree.** `/tasks` computes its row date and overdue from `scheduled ?? due` (was `min`) and sorts by `plan`; the three task starter widgets filter and sort by `plan` (relabeled: "Tasks Today" = planned-or-due today, "Overdue Tasks" = past the planned date, "Upcoming Tasks" = planned-or-due in 7 days). The MCP `list_items` `dateField` documents the new `plan` default. The whole app now reads "scheduled primarily, due secondarily," and a missing due date is invisible.
4. **A both-dates user is still served:** naming `dateField: dueDate` (or `scheduledDate`) still filters/sorts on that single column, so a deadline-keeper can build a pure-deadline view. The change is to the *default*, not to the columns.
**Decision — Part B (task canvas regains the arrangeable grid).** `TaskCanvas` now mirrors `MarkdownCanvas`'s dispatch: when `arrange` (entering `?arrange=1`) or a saved `types.canvas_layout` exists, it **delegates to `MarkdownCanvas`** (the same wrap `LinkCanvas` uses), which renders the field-level `react-grid-layout` cards; otherwise it renders the ADR-108 compact rail unchanged. So the bespoke rail stays the **default** (Tyler's current setup), the DnD editor works again on tasks (it had regressed), and "Reset layout" (layout → null) returns to the rail. No new grid code: tasks reuse the proven `ItemLayoutGrid` + card vocabulary.
**Why / alternatives:** *Part A as a computed pseudo-field, not a stored column:* there is nothing to store, the plan date is derived from two existing columns, so a COALESCE expression is correct and migration-free (Principle 2/8). *Changing the default rather than adding an opt-in:* Brandon asked for the whole app to behave scheduled-primary by default, and a both-dates user opts back to a single column by naming it (the rarer case). *Overloading the existing `dueDate` default* was rejected: it silently hid scheduled-only tasks from widgets, the exact bug. For Part B, *reimplementing the grid inside `TaskCanvas`* was rejected (a duplicate of `MarkdownCanvas`'s card factory), and *a separate capability flag* was rejected (the arrange/saved-layout dispatch already expresses "default vs customized" with no config). **Known limitation (pre-existing, deferred):** the grid card vocabulary has no focus-star / scheduled-time / reminder card, so a task arranged into the grid loses those rail-only controls until cards are added; this matched the pre-ADR-108 grid and is noted for a later vocabulary addition.
**Affects:** `src/lib/views.ts` (`plan` in the four field enums + `PLAN_DATE` + window/sort defaults), `src/components/views/ViewRenderer.tsx` (`dateOf`/`usesUtc`/column value/labels/default date column), `src/components/views/ViewBuilder.tsx` (`dateFieldsFor`/`groupFieldsFor` offer `plan` first + labels), `src/lib/view-grouping.ts` (`plan` board bucket), `src/app/tasks/page.tsx` (`effDate` = scheduled ?? due, sort by `plan`), `src/lib/starter-widgets.ts` (three task widgets → `plan`), `src/lib/mcp/tools.ts` (`dateField` default doc), `src/components/canvas/TaskCanvas.tsx` (delegate to `MarkdownCanvas` when arranging / saved layout); corrected a stale assertion in `scripts/verify-canvas-seam.mts` (task has its own canvas, not the default). No schema, no migration, no new dependency.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-views.mts` extended and green on live Neon (new: `plan` accepted as dateField/sort/grouping; default window with no `dateField` is `plan`; a scheduled-past task is overdue; a future-scheduled past-due task is NOT overdue, scheduled wins; due-only-today and scheduled-today both land "today"; `dateField: dueDate` still flags the past-due task; sort-by-plan orders by the effective date; the window SQL is a `coalesce`). `verify-canvas-seam` (task resolves to its own canvas) + `verify-canvas-layout` green. `tsc --noEmit` + eslint + `next build` clean. Server-rendered HTML confirmed (dev-auth on Neon): a task's default route renders the compact rail (Schedule/Due/Priority/Focus rows, no grid), `?arrange=1` renders the grid + arrange UI, `/tasks` lists with the plan sort, and the view builder offers "plan date (scheduled, else due)" as the task default. (The live preview browser's Suspense fallback did not resolve under dev streaming, a harness quirk; the server returned 200 and the fetched HTML carries the correct output.)

## ADR-110: Note "date taken" — an editable `items.note_date` column
**Date:** 2026-06-24 (merged 2026-06-25)
**Status:** accepted. **CORE** (adds a column to the shared `items` table). **Brandon approved** (Tyler asked; Brandon agreed, 2026-06-25). Alpha posture (ADR-039): additive nullable column + a one-time backfill of existing notes; back-compat. **Renumbered from a provisional ADR-100 → ADR-110 on merge** (ADR-100 had been taken by the Web clipper); the migration likewise renumbered `0032 → 0033` (it collided with ADR-106's `status_mode` migration `0032_nice_azazel`).
**Context:** A note's displayed date was `updated_at` (last edit). Tyler wanted a distinct, user-editable date for *when the note was actually taken*, defaulting to the creation day, with `created_at`/`updated_at` left intact. The choice was property-vs-column (the two-person fork): a `properties.note_date` JSONB key would have been non-core and shippable solo, but isn't natively sortable/groupable. "When I took this note" is the natural sort/group key for notes (and the basis for future "notes from last week" views), so it earns hot-field status — a real column — which makes it a core change.
**Decision:**
1. **New column `items.note_date timestamptz` (nullable), indexed `items_note_date_idx`** (migration 0033). A calendar day stored **UTC-midnight**, exactly mirroring `due_date`/`scheduled_date` (ADR-008) — `FieldStrip` slices the ISO (no local-format) so the picked day stays put. Physically on `items` (like the other type-specific date columns), note-scoped in behavior.
2. **Default on create:** `createItem` sets `note_date` to the **creation calendar day in the app timezone** (`appTodayYmd()` → UTC-midnight) for `type === "note"` only; every other type leaves it null. User-editable afterward; an explicit `noteDate` on create is respected.
3. **The note type gains its one baked-in field** (amends ADR-018's "notes surface nothing"): `TOP_STRIP.note = ["noteDate"]`, label **"Date taken"**, a plain `<input type="date">` in `FieldStrip` (no NL chips). Renders on both the classic and grid canvas (vocabulary + `sys:noteDate` label added to `canvas-layout.ts`).
4. **Save path:** `ItemInput`/`ItemPatch` gain `noteDate?: Date | null`; `parseItemPayload` coerces it via `asNullableDate`; `updateItem` sets it; `listColumns` carries it (so lists/`getItem`/views all see it, body-free rule intact). The notes list shows `note_date` (formatted in **UTC**, since it's a calendar day) and falls back to `updated_at` for any null.
5. **Backfill** (migration 0033, alpha): existing notes get `note_date = date_trunc('day', created_at AT TIME ZONE 'UTC') AT TIME ZONE 'UTC'`.
**Why / alternatives:** *Store as a `properties.note_date` JSONB property* — rejected for the durable model (not sortable/groupable without GIN gymnastics, no first-class field), though it would have been non-core/solo; the column is the right long-term shape and worth the both-agree gate. *Reuse `created_at`* — rejected; `created_at` is the immutable row-birth instant, not an editable calendar day. *A Postgres `date` type* — rejected for consistency; the codebase's calendar-day convention is UTC-midnight `timestamptz` (ADR-008).
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-note-date.mts` (new) 11/11 on Neon — parse coercion, note default = today UTC-midnight, task stays null, explicit-on-create respected, PATCH update + clear, `getItem` carries the column. `verify-canvas-layout` updated (note vocabulary is now exactly `sys:noteDate`) — ALL PASS. `next build` + eslint clean. **Merge note:** brought onto `main` after Brandon's ADR-102–109 batch; auto-merged `schema.ts`/`items.ts`, took Brandon's `TaskCanvas` (its ADR-108 rewrite dropped the `StripValues` block my one-liner targeted), and grafted the notes-list date display into his ADR-105 list-lenses page.
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (`note_date` column + index), `drizzle/0033_parallel_toad.sql` (column + index + backfill), `src/lib/items.ts` (`ItemInput`/`ItemPatch`, `listColumns`, `createItem` default, `updateItem` set, `appTodayYmd` import), `src/lib/item-input.ts` (parse), `src/lib/canvas-fields.ts` (`CanvasField` + `TOP_STRIP.note`), `src/components/canvas/FieldStrip.tsx` (`StripValues` + `noteDate` control + label), `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (strip value), `src/lib/canvas-layout.ts` (`sys:noteDate` label), `src/app/notes/page.tsx` (list display), `scripts/verify-note-date.mts` + `scripts/verify-canvas-layout.mts`. **For modules:** the `note_date` column is note-scoped, so a module type ignoring it sees null.

---

## ADR-111: Dashboard canvas — full-bleed backgrounds, per-widget appearance, any-item embed widgets, and tab/section containers
**Date:** 2026-06-25
**Status:** accepted (Brandon). **NOT core** — the Work-surface dashboard, the "views/dashboard widgets, move fast solo" side of the collab line (ADR-064/065 were built the same way). The only schema touch is **one additive column** (`dashboards.appearance` jsonb); everything else rides the existing `dashboards.widgets` jsonb or reuses shipped machinery (react-grid-layout, the autosaving item editor, R2). Courtesy COLLAB note to Tyler when the migration lands; no both-agree gate. Full build plan: `explorations/dashboard-canvas.md`.
**Context:** ADR-064/065 made dashboards real (multiple named, resizable/draggable grids of `view`/`stat`/`action`/`text` widgets, dashboard-level focus, Set-as-Home/Today). Brandon wants the dashboard to become a genuine *canvas*, not a uniform card grid: a customizable background (color/gradient/image, and a moving video), per-widget control over chrome (show/hide the title and the border, set a background color/accent, collapse), an embedded item he can type into like a sticky note, widgets that collapse, and a tabbed grouping of widgets. The base already points the way: the `text` widget renders chrome-free (proving per-widget chrome is feasible), and the per-widget `settings` + per-breakpoint `layout` + the single PATCH save path + tolerant parsers are in place.
**Decision — three customization layers + an embed widget.**
1. **The stage (dashboard-level appearance).** A new nullable **`dashboards.appearance` jsonb** (one additive migration) holds the background (`{kind: none|color|gradient|image|video, value, scrim, blur}`), `showTitle`, `density`, and an optional `accent`. The grid floats over a full-bleed background with an adjustable dark **scrim** + blur so any photo stays legible (the trick Notion sidesteps by limiting backgrounds to a header strip). Image/video bytes go to **R2** (existing provider, presigned URLs). `null` = today's plain dashboard, untouched (never forced, the `canvas_layout` precedent).
2. **Per-widget appearance (cross-cutting).** A new **`appearance` object on `DashboardWidget`** (rides the existing `widgets` jsonb, **no migration**), available to every kind: `{showHeader, showBorder, background, accent, collapsible, collapsed}`. Generalizes the chrome-free `text`-widget path to all kinds: a stat with header+border off becomes a floating number; a solid background makes a colored tile; **collapse** is a view-mode chevron (not edit-gated) that folds a widget to a one-line bar and remembers its expanded height. The gear popover (`WidgetSettingsPopover`) gains an Appearance section.
3. **Item-embed widget (`embed`).** A new kind that embeds **any item** (not just notes) by a new **`itemId`** (sibling to `viewId`), rendering the item's title (toggleable via `showHeader`) + body through the **existing autosaving editor** so it edits in place. The "sticky note" is an `embed` with a colored background and the header hidden. The lightweight `text` widget **stays** for pure labels/headings (a header costs no item). Honors "everything is an item" (Principle 2): the content is searchable, exportable, openable full-screen, relatable. *(Brandon: any item, not only notes.)*
4. **Tab/section container (`container`).** A new kind holding child widgets in its `settings` with a display `mode` (`tabs` | `stack` | `section`) + `activeTab`. **One-level nesting only** (containers don't nest), so the server's per-widget data fan-out stays a single recursion. Whole-*page* tabs (a Sunday board, a review board) are already served by **multiple dashboards** + the switcher, so the tab *widget* is for tabs *within* a board.
**Deferred (future, more plumbing — Brandon).** A **journal / daily-note** mode: a "new page" affordance that creates an item titled by date (from a template) and surfaces today's entry, optionally listing recent ones. Builds on item templates (ADR-093) + a date-naming rule + the `embed` widget; spec'd in the plan, not in the first build.
**Why / alternatives:** *Item-embed over an inline-jsonb note* (Principle 2): a real item is searchable/exportable and reuses the autosaving editor, where an inline note would be a second, invisible content store; the `text` widget stays for labels so a header needs no item. Brandon widened it to any item, so the kind is a generic embed, not note-only. *Appearance as one cross-cutting object*, not per-kind `settings`: chrome (header/border/background/accent/collapse) is universal, so model it once and branch the frame on it, generalizing the existing chrome-free path rather than special-casing each kind. *Backgrounds/video are pure chrome* (Principle 4, Sunday-proof): the OneDrive export and print/share paths ignore `appearance`, so nothing preached depends on a background; **video is the one cost item** (Principle 8) and ships guarded — opt-in, muted/looped/`playsInline`, paused when the tab is hidden, disabled under `prefers-reduced-motion`, always a poster still so slow wifi / the offline fallback degrade to a static image. *One additive column + jsonb-resident widget fields*: matches the ADR-064 jsonb-per-dashboard discipline (one row read + a batched fan-out); the widget `appearance` and the new kinds need no migration because the parsers are already tolerant. *No new dependencies* (Principle 5): react-grid-layout, the markdown editor, and R2 are present; color choice is a swatch set, not a color-picker lib. *Container one-level nesting*: keeps the recursion and grid model simple; deeper nesting and whole-page tabs are out (the latter = multiple dashboards).
**Phasing (each slice independently shippable, cheapest-first):** (1) **Per-widget appearance + collapse** — no migration; biggest visible change; generalizes the `text` chrome path. (2) **Dashboard background** — the `appearance` column + Background panel (color/gradient/image, scrim/blur, title/density) + R2 upload reuse; **video** as a guarded opt-in sub-step. (3) **Item-embed widget (any item)** — new `embed` kind + `itemId`, reusing the autosaving editor; sticky-note = embed + color + no header. (4) **Tab/section container** — new `container` kind, child fan-out, drag-into. (5) **(Future) Journal / daily-note mode**.
**Affects (to come, per slice):** `src/lib/dashboard-widgets.ts` (+`appearance` shape + parser, +`embed`/`container` kinds, +`itemId`), `src/lib/dashboards.ts` (parsers, `appearance`-column parse, embed-item + container-child fan-out), `src/db/schema.ts` (+`dashboards.appearance`, one migration), `src/components/dashboards/*` (WidgetFrame appearance branch, WidgetSettingsPopover Appearance section, new `EmbedWidget` reusing the editor, `BackgroundPanel`, `ContainerWidget`, collapse), `src/app/dashboards/[id]/page.tsx` (fetch embed bodies + stage appearance), `globals.css` (background/scrim), R2 (existing) for uploads. New `scripts/verify-dashboard-canvas.mts`.
**Verification:** per slice as built (the `verify-dashboards.mts` pattern); in-browser eyeball each — background legibility with the scrim, chrome toggles, embed autosave + search/export, collapse persistence, tab swap.

---

## ADR-112: Machine-API write endpoints for relations + attachments (Notion migration load)
**Date:** 2026-06-25
**Status:** accepted (Brandon + Tyler agreed 2026-06-25). **Core**: the machine/MCP API contract is on the both-agree list (CLAUDE.md "Building together"); Tyler approved the addition.
**Context:** The one-time Notion → Ledgr migration (the sibling `~/code/notion-migration` tooling) loads items through `POST /api/machine/items`, but that endpoint only creates the item row; it ignores relations and attachments. Wiring the migration's thousands of relation edges (tag/person tagging, meeting attendees, note sub-page parent/child, email threading) and the ~3,900 image attachments needs token-gated batch endpoints, because the in-app relation/attachment routes are Clerk-gated and a machine-token script can't reach them. Brandon chose dedicated endpoints over the MCP `relate_items` tool (too slow and session-bound for thousands) and over a direct DB write (which bypasses owner-scoping and validation).
**Decision:** Add two endpoints under the existing `/api/machine/*` surface (ADR-066), `api`-scoped token, owner-scoped via `resolveMachineOwner`, each validating through the same lib the in-app routes use so the machine surface can't drift from the app contract:
- `POST /api/machine/relations`: batch-create edges, body `{ relations: [{ sourceId, targetId, role }] }` (max 100/call). Calls `relateItems` per edge; idempotent via the unique `(source_id, target_id, role)` constraint. Per-edge failures go in `errors[]` and never fail the batch (mirrors the items endpoint). The reserved `mention` role is rejected (body-owned, ADR-015).
- `POST /api/machine/attachments`: register an attachment row + return a presigned R2 PUT (the token-gated analog of the Clerk-gated `POST /api/attachments`). Only meaningful when R2 is configured; used by the migration's image pass.
**Why / alternatives:** keeps writes flowing through `relateItems` / the attachments lib (owner-scoping, validation, idempotency) instead of raw SQL, and scales to thousands where MCP would not. The endpoints are generic, not migration-specific, so they remain useful for any future machine integration.
**Affects:** `src/app/api/machine/relations/route.ts` (new), `src/app/api/machine/attachments/route.ts` (new); reuses `src/lib/relations.ts` (`relateItems`) and `src/lib/attachments.ts`. No schema change.

## ADR-113: Machine-API item-update (PATCH) endpoint (Notion migration load)
**Date:** 2026-06-26
**Status:** accepted (Brandon + Tyler agreed). **Core**: the machine/MCP API contract is on the both-agree list (CLAUDE.md "Building together"); Tyler approved the addition.
**Context:** Two of the migration's remaining passes update items that already exist rather than creating or relating them: the not-done task hierarchy re-pull (set `parent_id` on ~1,332 active tasks, dropped by the crawl) and the attachment pass (rewrite each item body's `_assets/…` refs to the served R2 `publicUrl` after upload). `POST /api/machine/items` only creates; `POST /api/machine/relations` (ADR-112) only relates. There was no token-gated way to update an existing item, and the in-app `PATCH /api/items/:id` is Clerk-gated. The considered alternative — a direct owner-scoped DB `UPDATE` — was rejected in favor of going through the same validated lib path as every other write (Brandon's call to keep the API the single door, even in alpha).
**Decision:** Add `PATCH /api/machine/items` (same route file as GET/POST, `api`-scoped token, owner-scoped via `resolveMachineOwner`). Batch shape mirrors POST: a bare `{ id, ...patch }` or `{ items: [{ id, ...patch }] }` (max 100/call), each entry naming its target by `id` and carrying the same fields POST accepts. Every entry is validated through the same `parseItemPayload(_, "patch")` and applied through the same `updateItem` the in-app PATCH uses — so it honors owner-scoping, the recurrence-complete and body-no-op guards, revision snapshots, and `assertValidParent` (parent_id changes stay cycle-safe). Per-entry failures go in `errors[]` and never fail the batch. Response `{ count, updated, errors }` (200 if anything updated, 400 if all failed).
**Why / alternatives:** keeps updates flowing through `updateItem` (validation, owner-scoping, parent-cycle check, revisions) instead of raw SQL, and batches to scale past the per-item round trips MCP would impose. Generic, not migration-specific, so it stays useful for any future machine integration that needs to write back to an item (the third verb after create/relate).
**Affects:** `src/app/api/machine/items/route.ts` (added `PATCH`); reuses `src/lib/items.ts` (`updateItem`) and `src/lib/item-input.ts` (`parseItemPayload`). No schema change.

## ADR-114: Floating table of contents (per-type, stored in users.settings)
**Date:** 2026-06-26
**Status:** accepted. **NOT core** — UI/UX + per-owner prefs (the "move fast, solo" side of the COLLAB split). No change to `items`/`types`/`relations`/`revisions`/properties, the body format, the canvas seam, the module boundary, or the machine/MCP contract; additive key on the existing owner-scoped `users.settings` blob, tolerant-parsed, so Tyler's instance is untouched until he changes it. Logged anyway, like ADR-053 (`users.settings`) and ADR-056 (`navSlots`), because the storage-location choice is worth recording.
**Context:** Brandon asked for a Notion-style floating outline — a thin right-edge rail of marks that expands on hover into a clickable, auto-built H1–Hn list and highlights the current section — built automatically from a document's headings, controllable per type (on/off + which levels), and synced across devices (server-side, not `localStorage`). He explicitly wanted mobile covered too, since scrolling long docs on a phone is a prime use case; the desktop rail doesn't translate to touch.
**Decision:** Store the per-type config in **`users.settings.tocByType: Record<typeKey, {enabled, levels}>`**, the same shape/posture as `listTabs` (a per-type override map): a tolerant `parseTocByType`, a `tocForType(settings, key)` resolver, and a focused per-type write route `PATCH /api/types/[key]/toc` (`{config}` saves, `{config:null}` resets — mirrors the list-tabs route, can't clobber a concurrent edit). **Default = auto-on, all levels (H1–H3)**, gated by the component to **≥2 headings**, so it just appears on long items and stays invisible on short ones (turned off per type in Build → Types via a new `TocSettingsEditor` panel modeled on `ListTabsEditor`). One client component, `FloatingToc`, mounts **once in `ItemCanvas`** (the universal seam — covers every canvas type without touching each) inside a `[data-toc-scope]` wrapper, and reads the live editor DOM (`.ledgr-prose`): a desktop **right-edge rail** (CSS `group-hover` expand) on `lg`+, and a **floating button → bottom sheet** on narrow/phone and in the (narrow, scroll-contained) intercept **modal**. It drives scroll + active-section tracking against `getScrollParent` (the window on the full page, the modal's own scroll div in the modal), never mutates ProseMirror's heading DOM (re-queries live by document order), and self-gates to nothing below the heading threshold.
**Why / alternatives:** a per-type **column on `types`** was rejected — `types` is the instance-global, **not** owner-scoped registry, so a personal reading preference belongs in owner-scoped settings (right under the multi-user-ready principle), and `users.settings` needs no migration (the sanctioned additive path, schema.md "Per-owner settings"). Reading the rendered DOM (vs. parsing markdown server-side) means the outline tracks edits live and reuses the headings the editor already renders. Per-item override (Notion's "This page" vs "New pages") and levels beyond H3 are deferred — type-level was the unit Brandon asked for, and the editor only exposes H1/H2.
**Affects:** `src/lib/settings.ts` (`TocConfig`, `DEFAULT_TOC`, `tocByType`, `tocForType`, `parseTocConfig`/`parseTocByType`), `src/app/api/types/[key]/toc/route.ts` (new), `src/components/build/TocSettingsEditor.tsx` (new), `src/components/canvas/FloatingToc.tsx` (new), `src/components/canvas/ItemCanvas.tsx` (mount + `data-toc-scope`), `src/app/build/types/[key]/edit/page.tsx` (panel). No schema/migration.

---

## ADR-115: Flip to v1.0 production (alpha posture ends, ADR-039 reversed)
**Date:** 2026-06-26 (Friday)
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed). This is the tracked flip ADR-039 named: from "alpha / build phase, pre-production" to **v1.0 production**. Not a change to any core contract (the data model, the canonical body format, the type/canvas model, the module boundary, the provider interfaces, the machine/MCP API, the nine principles), so it isn't a both-agree core change; it does reverse a shared-roadmap posture and re-arm migration caution on the shared schema, so Tyler is flagged in `COLLAB.md`. Per-instance: each builder runs a separate single-tenant deploy, so Tyler flips his own instance on his own date; this records Brandon's.
**Context:** ADR-039 (2026-06-13) declared an explicit ALPHA / build-phase posture: Ledgr held no production data and wasn't in real Sunday/daily use, so data-loss, careful-migration, and backward-compatibility concerns were suspended in favor of the cleanest, most direct path (convert-or-reseed dev data freely). ADR-039 named its own end condition, the same gate as the "no Saturday deploys once Ledgr is in real Sunday use" rule: "when it happens, record it in this log, update the CLAUDE.md line, and migration caution applies from then on." That condition is now met. The Notion → Ledgr migration load completed 2026-06-26 (machine-API endpoints in ledgr#84; the sibling `~/code/notion-migration` tooling), so Ledgr now holds Brandon's real meetings, tasks, notes, people, and roughly 3,900 attachments, and is in daily use.
**Decision:**
1. **Project status flips to v1.0 production.** The ALPHA callout atop CLAUDE.md is replaced with a production status line. The ADR-039 exemptions are **withdrawn**: data in Ledgr is production data and is handled as such.
2. **Migration caution applies from now on.** Schema changes get real migrations (additive, then backfill; no destructive reseed of live owner data); back-compat matters again. The safety net is the working invariants, not "there's nothing to lose": soft-delete + 30-day Trash, revision snapshots on save, and the weekly OneDrive backup (ADR-103).
3. **The "no deploys Saturday night" rule is now in force** (runbook §0; CLAUDE.md working conventions). Sunday is sermon delivery; don't ship into the weekend. Sunday-proof (Principle 4) is a live guarantee, not a future one.
4. **Scope is the shared core plus Brandon's instance.** Because the schema is shared, the re-armed migration caution covers anything touching the shared core (a destructive migration would hit Brandon's live data). Tyler's own production flip is on Tyler's timeline; flagged in `COLLAB.md`.
**Why / alternatives:** *Stay in alpha* is false now: there is real, hard-to-reproduce data (the Notion import) and the tool is in daily use, exactly the premise ADR-039 said would end the posture. *Flip silently, no ADR* was rejected; ADR-039 and CLAUDE.md both require the flip be recorded here so the reversal of migration caution is explicit and dated.
**Affects:** CLAUDE.md (status line flipped; the conditional "no Saturday deploys" convention now stated active), `roadmap.md` (the "alpha → v1.0 production flip" 1.0 item marked done), `next_steps.md` (top-of-queue production note), `runbook.md` (§0 status banner: production is live), `src/lib/v1-goals.ts` (the flip goal → done), `src/lib/health-check.ts` (drop the now-stale alpha-posture rationale; behavior unchanged), `package.json` (version 0.1.0 → 1.0.0), `COLLAB.md` (Tyler heads-up), this entry. Historical ADR-039-era notes elsewhere (the `roadmap.md` Phase M banners, the `next_steps.md` "alpha reseed" lines, ADR-039/110/111) stay as written: they record what was true under the alpha posture and remain accurate history.

## ADR-116: List paging past the 200-row cap (Load-more, true count, window growth)
**Date:** 2026-06-26
**Status:** accepted (Brandon, 2026-06-26). **Core-adjacent:** it touches the shared view-query engine (`src/lib/views.ts`), a cross-cutting concern on the both-agree list, but it is purely additive and preserves every list invariant (owner-scope, body-free, soft-delete). Tyler ack requested (COLLAB heads-up); a flag, not a blocker for Brandon's instance.
**Context:** Brandon's Notion import (ADR-115, same day) pushed several types past 200 live items. Every plain list (the sort-lens path) renders through `queryViewItems`, which defaulted to and hard-clamped at `VIEW_LIMIT = 200`, with no offset/cursor param and no UI to page. A type with 743 notes showed exactly 200, the subtitle read "200 notes" (it counted `rows.length`, the capped array, not the true total), and there was no next page. The cap had been invisible during the alpha because no type held more than 200.
**Decision:** Keep the one-page default and the body-free, owner-scoped query untouched; add paging by growing the render window rather than streaming offsets.
1. `VIEW_LIMIT` stays 200, now documented as the default page size and the Load-more increment. New `VIEW_MAX = 2000` is the hard ceiling; `viewItemsQuery` clamps to `[1, VIEW_MAX]` (was `[1, VIEW_LIMIT]`), so a caller can request a larger window while a backstop remains (rows are body-free, fine for a single user).
2. New pure `parseListWindow(?show=)` floors at one page and clamps to the ceiling.
3. New shared server component `LoadMore` renders "Showing X of Y" and a `scroll={false}` link that bumps `?show=` by one page, preserving the active lens/rev/property-filter params. It renders nothing once everything is shown, and at the ceiling shows a "narrow with a filter or search" note instead of a dead button (no client JS, Principle 5).
4. The four plain-list pages (`/notes`, `/links`, `/list/[type]`, `/events`) fetch a window plus the true `countViewItems` total in parallel, so the subtitle and footer report the real count, not the window.
**Why / alternatives:** *Just raise the cap* only moves the cliff and still gives no signal that more exist. *Client offset plus infinite scroll* is smoother but adds a fetch API, client state, and serialization the server-component lists don't otherwise need, so it was rejected for now (revisit if the window-grow reload feels slow). *Window growth* (re-fetch a bigger page on a server navigation) fits the existing server-rendered lists, keeps each page body-free and indexed, and needs no new endpoint. A **user-defined page size** (Brandon's second ask) is deferred to the view/lens surface where `listTabs` already lives; Load-more covers the immediate need.
**Affects:** `src/lib/views.ts` (`VIEW_MAX`, `parseListWindow`, clamp to `VIEW_MAX`), `src/components/lists/LoadMore.tsx` (new), the four list pages above (window + true count + footer), `scripts/verify-list-paging.mts` (new; ALL PASS on Neon: clamp, true count, 205-row window growth), plus `COLLAB.md`/`next_steps.md`/`roadmap.md`. **Same cap, not yet paged (follow-up):** `/items` (the all-items browse on the older `listItems` engine, grouped by type) and `/tasks` plus dashboard view widgets (date-windowed or preview-limited, less likely to hit 200). **Unaffected:** MCP (clamps its own input to 200); dashboard `itemLimit` now clamps to 2000 (an improvement, not a regression).

## ADR-117: OAuth shim for the MCP server (connect Ledgr's MCP from claude.ai and the Claude mobile apps)
**Date:** 2026-06-26
**Status:** accepted (Brandon, 2026-06-26; Tyler agreed 2026-06-26). **Core (both-agree + ADR):** this changes the machine/MCP API contract, which is on the frozen core list, so it took Tyler's agreement plus a `COLLAB.md` heads-up. The design deliberately keeps the change off the shared `schema.md` (no new tables, see Decision 7), so the core surface is the API contract only, not a migration on shared tables. Per-instance: the shim and `LEDGR_OAUTH_SECRET` are each builder's own deploy concern; this records Brandon's.
**Context:** Ledgr's MCP server (ADR-047) is a live, stateless Streamable-HTTP endpoint at `/api/mcp`, authenticated by a static Bearer token carrying the `mcp` scope (ADR-004: hashed in `LEDGR_API_TOKENS`, no DB row). Brandon wants to use the Ledgr MCP from anywhere, including his phone. The vehicle for that is Claude's account-level **custom connectors**: add the remote MCP server once and it is available across claude.ai web, Claude Desktop, and the iOS/Android apps. Research (2026-06-26, sources logged in session) confirmed the blocker: the **consumer connector UI (claude.ai web + mobile) is OAuth-only.** There is no field for a static bearer token or a custom `Authorization` header, and Anthropic marked that request "not planned" (anthropics/claude-ai-mcp#112). Claude Code and Desktop can pass a manual `--header "Authorization: Bearer …"` (the path the AI & MCP page already documents), but the consumer apps cannot. So bearer-only means no phone. A remote sandbox running an MCP client was rejected as redundant (the server is already hosted and reachable) and a "skill" cannot carry auth or a network connection at all.
**Decision:** Add a minimal, stateless OAuth 2.1 shim that **wraps, not replaces,** the static bearer model, dependency-free (node:crypto HMAC, mirroring ADR-004's hashed-token-in-env approach; no `jose`/`@node-oauth`, Principle 5).
1. **Discovery (RFC 9728 / RFC 8414).** New public routes `GET /.well-known/oauth-protected-resource` (advertises `/api/mcp` as the resource and Ledgr itself as the authorization server) and `GET /.well-known/oauth-authorization-server` (advertises the authorize/token/registration endpoints, `code` response type, `authorization_code` + `refresh_token` grants, PKCE S256 required).
2. **The 401 points the way.** `/api/mcp` on a missing or invalid token returns `WWW-Authenticate: Bearer resource_metadata="<origin>/.well-known/oauth-protected-resource"` (currently a flat 401), so a connector can discover the OAuth flow.
3. **Dynamic Client Registration (RFC 7591), stateless.** `POST /api/oauth/register` accepts Claude's registration and returns a `client_id` that is an HMAC-signed encoding of the submitted redirect_uri(s). No stored row: the signature is what is trusted at /authorize and /token. (Claude's connector flow uses DCR today; Client ID Metadata Documents are the newer "preferred" spec path and can be added later if Claude switches.)
4. **Authorize endpoint, owner-gated by Clerk.** `GET /api/oauth/authorize` stays Clerk-protected (it is NOT added to the `proxy.ts` public set), so only the signed-in owner reaches it. That Clerk login (Microsoft) is the entire access-control story for a single-user system: no separate consent screen. It validates the client_id signature, redirect_uri, and PKCE challenge, then issues a short-lived (~60s) authorization code that is itself an HMAC-signed token carrying the PKCE challenge, redirect_uri, and `mcp` scope.
5. **Token endpoint, stateless.** `POST /api/oauth/token` (public) verifies the code's signature and expiry, checks the PKCE verifier against the embedded S256 challenge, and issues an HMAC-signed **access token** (scope `mcp`, owner audience, ~1h expiry) plus a signed refresh token. Nothing is persisted; the signature plus expiry is the validation.
6. **`/api/mcp` accepts either credential.** The existing `verifyMachineToken` path (static `LEDGR_API_TOKENS` mcp token) is unchanged, so Claude Code, Desktop, and machine callers keep working with no migration. A second check accepts a valid signed OAuth access token bearing the `mcp` scope. Both resolve the same owner via `resolveMcpOwner`. The OAuth path is purely additive.
7. **No new state, no new dependency.** Zero DB tables (codes/tokens/clients are all signed, not stored) and zero packages. Signing uses a new `LEDGR_OAUTH_SECRET` env var via node:crypto HMAC-SHA256. This is what keeps the change off the shared schema.
8. **Revocation = rotate the secret.** Rotating `LEDGR_OAUTH_SECRET` (env edit + redeploy, runbook §3 style) invalidates every issued OAuth token at once. Per-token revocation is out of scope for single-user v1; secret rotation is the kill switch. Documented in the runbook.
**Why / alternatives:** *Stay bearer-only* makes phone access impossible by Anthropic's design (consumer connectors OAuth-only, #112 "not planned"). *Remote environment running a client* is a redundant, always-on, fragile box in front of an already-reachable server (against Principle 5). *A skill* cannot carry auth or open a connection. *DB-backed OAuth (client/code/token tables, or a library)* was rejected for v1: it pulls OAuth state onto the shared schema (a both-agree migration) and adds a dependency, when single-user lets us stay stateless with signed tokens; revisit if multi-user ever lands, where per-user token mapping and a revocation list would matter. *Client ID Metadata Documents instead of DCR* is the newer spec-preferred path but not what Claude's connector flow uses today; support DCR now, add CIMD if needed.
**Affects (planned, on acceptance):** new public routes `src/app/.well-known/oauth-protected-resource/route.ts` and `…/oauth-authorization-server/route.ts`; `src/app/api/oauth/{register,token}/route.ts` (public) and `src/app/api/oauth/authorize/route.ts` (Clerk-protected); `src/lib/auth/oauth.ts` (new: sign/verify codes + access/refresh tokens, PKCE S256, all node:crypto HMAC); `src/app/api/mcp/route.ts` (accept an OAuth access token; add the `WWW-Authenticate` header to the 401); `src/proxy.ts` (public set gains the two well-known routes + `/api/oauth/register` + `/api/oauth/token`; `/api/oauth/authorize` stays protected); `runbook.md` (`LEDGR_OAUTH_SECRET` issue/rotate as the OAuth kill switch); `src/app/build/claude/page.tsx` (document the claude.ai/mobile connector path); env (`LEDGR_OAUTH_SECRET`). `src/lib/mcp/owner.ts` unchanged. **Verification (planned):** a `scripts/verify-oauth-mcp.mts` walking discovery → register → authorize → token → an authenticated `/api/mcp` call, plus a real claude.ai mobile connect.

## ADR-118: Multi-select + bulk item operations (a reusable selection layer on every list)
**Date:** 2026-06-26
**Status:** accepted (Brandon, 2026-06-26). **Core-adjacent, additive:** it adds a new in-app HTTP surface (`/api/items/batch`) but introduces **no new item contract** — every bulk op validates through the same `parseItemPayload` and runs the same `updateItem` / `softDeleteItem` as the existing single-item routes and the machine batch route (ADR-113), so the data model, owner-scoping, soft-delete, revisions, and recurrence are all preserved unchanged. No `schema.md` change, no new dependency. Tyler heads-up posted (COLLAB); a flag, not a blocker, for Brandon's instance.
**Context:** Brandon asked to edit many items at once ("I want to edit 50 tasks at once and can't"). Every list rendered one independent row at a time (a single trash button per row, no selection), so any multi-item change meant opening items one by one. The plumbing for bulk already existed server-side — `updateItem` takes a full patch (status, dates, `parentId`, `propertyPatch`), `softDeleteItem` cascades to children, and the machine API already loops a batch PATCH — but there was no in-app endpoint under user auth and no UI to select rows.
**Decision:** Build it once as a reusable layer and make "every list surface includes multi-select" a working convention, not a per-page feature.
1. **Batch endpoint `/api/items/batch`** (user-auth via `requireOwner`): `PATCH { ids, patch }` applies one validated patch to each id via `updateItem`; `DELETE { ids }` soft-deletes each via `softDeleteItem`. Per-id errors are collected and returned (`{ count, errors }`), one bad id never failing the rest — the same discipline as the machine batch route. Capped at 200 ids/request (the list page window); the client chunks larger selections.
2. **A client selection layer** (`src/components/selection/`), kept thin so the pages stay server-rendered (the codebase norm): `SelectionProvider` (context holding the selected set + the in-view ordered ids, powering shift-click range + select-all), `SelectCheckbox` (a per-row island that renders nothing without a provider, so a shared row drops into a non-selectable surface unchanged), and `BulkActionBar` (the floating bar). `bulk-actions.ts` chunks the batch calls.
3. **Three actions** (Brandon's set): **Delete** (to Trash, behind the standard `ConfirmButton`, noting the child cascade), **Set…** a field + value applied to all (status, any select/multi_select property, or due/scheduled date — `propertyPatch` for the atomic per-key merge), and **Move…** (typeahead over the owner's items, mirroring `AddRelation`, sets `parentId`, with a "top level" escape). The action set is **config-driven** (`bulkConfigForType`): a status-less type (person/link/most notes) shows no status/date setter, and a mixed-type surface (Inbox) shows only Move + Delete.
4. **Archive is deliberately NOT built yet.** Brandon scoped it for the future archive feature; the `BulkActionBar` Set… field list is the documented seam where bulk Archive (set status to the type's `archived`-category default) slots in then.
5. **Wired onto every row-based surface:** `/tasks` (all four tabs), `/notes`, `/links`, `/events`, `/inbox`, the generic `/list/[type]` (which is also People and every custom type), and the shared `ViewRenderer` list/table/agenda layouts (so view lenses via `ViewLensBody` and the standalone `/views/[id]` page get it too).
**Why / alternatives:** *Per-page bulk wiring* was rejected — Brandon asked for it on every list "and all future," so a shared provider + checkbox + bar + a documented convention is the only thing that scales and keeps future surfaces consistent. *Client-side optimistic list mutation* was unnecessary: the lists are server-rendered, so a `router.refresh()` after the batch is the simplest correct path (selection clears on success, which is the desired outcome anyway). *One row-patch-per-id over the existing single-item endpoint in a client loop* would work but spams the pooled connection; a single batch request per 200 (server loops) respects the cheap-back-end rule. **Deferred (defer-by-hiding):** selection on the **board** and **calendar** layouts (visual grids where a checkbox is awkward), on **dashboard widgets** (read-only by design), and on **Trash** (restore/purge is a different action set). The renderer's `selectable` prop is off by default, so those surfaces simply don't show checkboxes.
**Affects:** `src/app/api/items/batch/route.ts` (new); `src/components/selection/{SelectionProvider,SelectCheckbox,BulkActionBar}.tsx` + `bulk-actions.ts` (new); `src/lib/bulk-config.ts` (new); `src/components/views/ViewRenderer.tsx` + `src/components/lists/ViewLensBody.tsx` (opt-in `selectable`); the list pages `/tasks`, `/notes`, `/links`, `/events`, `/inbox`, `/list/[type]`, `/views/[id]`; CLAUDE.md (new "every list includes multi-select" convention), `next_steps.md`, `roadmap.md`, `COLLAB.md` (Tyler heads-up), this entry. **Verification:** tsc + eslint clean; manual in-browser pass (select rows incl. shift-range, Set a property/status, Move, Delete) — see the session note.

## ADR-119: Production deploys reframed to "be deliberate," no fixed weekend/Saturday no-deploy window (supersedes ADR-028's rule; amends ADR-115 Decision 3)
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, 2026-06-27). **Non-core:** a working convention, not a core contract. "Sunday-proof" (Principle 4) is untouched, that is the offline-fallback guarantee, a different thing. Tyler heads-up posted in `COLLAB.md` because ADR-115 had told him the no-Saturday-deploys rule was in force for the shared codebase; this reframes it. A flag, not a gate.
**Context:** The "no deploys Saturday night / don't deploy into the weekend" rule (PRD §6.2, CLAUDE.md, runbook §0) was scoped by ADR-028 to activate once Ledgr was in real Sunday use, then switched on by ADR-115's v1.0 production flip (Decision 3). In practice the calendar ban is a poor fit: Brandon preaches only 2-3 times a year, so the overwhelming majority of weekends carry no sermon risk, and even a bad deploy is recoverable (git revert, plus soft-delete + revisions + the weekly backup). A blanket weekend/Saturday window was ceremony more than protection, and it kept surfacing as a warning that blocked ordinary work.
**Decision:** Replace the calendar rule with a production-mindfulness guideline.
1. **There is no fixed weekend/Saturday no-deploy window.** Ship when ready on any day.
2. **Be deliberate with production instead.** Ledgr is in daily use, so weigh changes that touch live data or production: prefer additive, reversible steps; lean on the safety net (soft-delete + 30-day Trash, revision snapshots, the weekly OneDrive backup, git revert); don't ship large, risky changes carelessly.
3. **Use judgment on the rare sermon-sensitive weekend.** If a specific deploy genuinely risks something Brandon is relying on for an imminent Sunday, hold it then, but that is a case-by-case call, not a standing rule.
4. **Principle 4 (Sunday-proof) is unchanged.** The offline OneDrive export + Save Offline PDF fallback remain a hard guarantee; this ADR is only about deploy *timing*, not the fallback paths.
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep the calendar rule* rejected as a bad cost/benefit at ~2-3 sermons/year. *Delete the rule with no replacement* rejected, the underlying intent (don't be reckless with a live app) is still right, so it's reframed, not dropped. *Rewrite the historical ADR-028/ADR-115 text* rejected: those are dated records of what was decided then; this ADR supersedes them going forward (the repo's standard "new ADR supersedes, history stays" pattern).
**Affects:** CLAUDE.md (status callout + the working-conventions bullet rewritten), `runbook.md` §0 (rule 1 rewritten), `ledgr-prd.md` §6.2 (the "Rule: no deploys Saturday night" line reframed), `next_steps.md` + `roadmap.md` (the live-queue/flip notes drop the no-Saturday-deploys clause), `COLLAB.md` (Tyler heads-up), this entry. **Left as history:** ADR-028 and ADR-115 (Decision 3) decision text, and the dated "Recently done" summaries that describe what was true then.

## ADR-120: Dashboard canvas built (ADR-111 DC1–DC4) + a new nested-list (parent + children) widget
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, 2026-06-27). **NOT core** — the Work-surface dashboard, the "views/dashboard widgets, move-fast-solo" side of the collab line (ADR-064/065/111 are all built this way). This is the build record for **ADR-111**'s plan (`explorations/dashboard-canvas.md`, DC1–DC4) plus one capability ADR-111 did not have: a **nested-list widget** Brandon added this session ("a widget that does items with subs/children — N projects, plus N child tasks for each"). The only schema touch is **one additive nullable column** (`dashboards.appearance` jsonb, migration 0034); everything else rides the existing `dashboards.widgets` jsonb (tolerant parsers) or reuses shipped machinery (react-grid-layout, the autosaving `ItemEditor`, the view engine, the relations read path). Courtesy `COLLAB.md` heads-up to Tyler; no both-agree gate. Built on one branch (`dashboard-canvas`) per Brandon's call, not slice-by-slice.
**Context:** ADR-111 decided the dashboard canvas (per-widget appearance, a full-bleed stage, an any-item embed, tab/section containers) but was unbuilt. Brandon asked to build it, and to add a nested-list widget. The session surfaced a data-model fact that shaped the nested widget: a task's **Project is a relation edge** (role `project`, ADR-067/`0031_project_type.sql`), while the `parent_id` tree is subtasks-under-a-task / sub-pages-under-a-note (the Notion import set `parent_id` on ~1,332 tasks as subtask nesting). Brandon first picked the `parent_id` hierarchy as the child source, then — once told project↔task is a relation — chose to **support both sources per widget** so his "projects + their tasks" example works via the relation role while subtask/sub-page hierarchies work via `parent_id`.
**Decision — four ADR-111 capabilities + a fifth widget kind, all on the existing jsonb except one stage column.**
1. **Per-widget appearance (DC1).** A new optional `appearance` object on `DashboardWidget` (rides `widgets` jsonb, **no migration**): `{showHeader, showBorder, background, accent, collapsible, collapsed}`. Absent = today's per-kind chrome via `defaultAppearance(kind)` (text stays chrome-free, every other kind a full card), so existing dashboards render identically; `effectiveAppearance(widget)` resolves the fallback. `WidgetFrame` now branches on it for ALL kinds (generalizing the old `if kind === "text"` chrome-free path): header off + border off + transparent = a floating number/sticky note; a color background = a colored tile; an accent = a tinted left edge. **Collapse** is a view-mode chevron (not edit-gated) that folds a widget to a one-line bar; the forced height-1 lives in `RglInner` **view-mode only**, so the stored expanded height is never clobbered (edit mode shows widgets expanded for resizing). Background/accent are a curated swatch set, not a color-picker lib (Principle 5).
2. **The stage / dashboard background (DC2).** A new nullable **`dashboards.appearance` jsonb** column (migration 0034): `{background: {kind: none|color|gradient|image|video, value, scrim, blur}, showTitle, density, accent}`. `null` = today's plain dark dashboard (never forced — the `canvas_layout` precedent). The grid floats over a full-bleed `StageBackground` with an adjustable dark **scrim** + blur so any photo stays legible. Curated color/gradient tokens map to CSS client-side; image is a **URL** (no bytes). **Video + raw byte-upload are deferred behind a guarded seam** — the parser accepts `video` and `StageBackground` renders a muted/looped/`playsInline` video, but the `BackgroundPanel` UI offers only none/color/gradient/image, since byte upload needs no-item R2 plumbing and video is the one cost/Sunday-proof watch item (ADR-111). Backgrounds are pure chrome: export/print/share never read `appearance` (Principle 4).
3. **Item-embed widget (DC3).** A new `embed` kind carrying **`itemId`** (sibling to `viewId`), rendering the item's body through the existing autosaving `ItemEditor` (`slot="body"`), so typing saves straight to the real item (revisions as usual) and the content stays searchable/exportable (Principle 2). The frame header shows the item title (toggled by `appearance.showHeader`); the **sticky note** is an embed with a colored background and the header off. The page fan-out fetches the embedded item's body — the one place a widget reads a `body`, acceptable since it IS the content. The lightweight `text` widget stays for pure labels.
4. **Tab/section container (DC4).** A new `container` kind holding child widgets in its `settings` (`{mode: tabs|stack|section, activeTab, title, children}`), **one-level nesting only** (the parser drops a nested container), so the server fan-out is a single recursion. Children render through the same `WidgetFrame` (drag handle suppressed) and are managed (add/remove/configure) from inside the container via the scoped `AddWidgetMenu`; child mutations flow up as a new `children` array through the dashboard's one PATCH path (which refetches so an added view child gets its data). Tab selection is local (ephemeral), so switching tabs never refetches. Whole-*page* tabs remain "multiple dashboards + the switcher."
5. **Nested-list widget (`tree`) — the new ask.** A view-backed kind: the backing view selects N **parent** items; under each parent its **children** are listed (rows with the compact-list treatment + a task check-off), capped at `childLimit` with a "+N more →" overflow, parents capped at `parentLimit`. **Two child sources, chosen per widget** (`childSource`): `children` = the `parent_id` hierarchy, or `relation` = a confirmed relation edge of a given `relationRole` (e.g. `project`, so a project lists its tasks). `hideCompletedChildren` defaults on (a dashboard shows live work); an optional `childType` filter narrows children to one type. Children are fetched batched + body-free + owner-scoped by a new `src/lib/dashboard-tree.ts` (`childrenByParentId` rides `items_parent_idx`; `childrenByRelation` mirrors `relatedSummaryFor`'s two-pass either-direction shape over confirmed edges) — one indexed query per source, never N+1.
6. **Machine/MCP contract held stable.** Adding kinds to `WIDGET_KINDS` would have auto-expanded the MCP `add_widget` enum (a frozen-core surface). Instead the tool's enum is **pinned to a local `MCP_WIDGET_KINDS = [view, stat, action, text]`**, so the canvas kinds (tree/embed/container) are UI-built and deliberately OFF the machine/MCP contract. No protocol or tool-shape change.
**Why / alternatives:** *Item-embed over an inline-jsonb note* (Principle 2) and *appearance as one cross-cutting object* are ADR-111's rationale, unchanged. *Both child sources per widget* (over Brandon's first pick of `parent_id` only): his motivating example ("projects + their tasks") is relation-backed in Ledgr, so a `parent_id`-only widget would have shown projects' sub-items, not their tasks — supporting both makes the example work while keeping the hierarchy case (subtasks/sub-pages) first-class; the marginal cost is one settings dropdown + an alternate batched query. *Pin the MCP enum* rather than extend the contract keeps ADR-111 genuinely non-core. *Collapse applied view-mode-only* avoids the react-grid-layout trap where forcing height-1 would persist and lose the expanded height. *Image-by-URL, video/upload deferred* keeps DC2 shippable without no-item R2 plumbing and honors the ADR-111 "video is the one guarded cost item" call (defer-by-hiding: the seam stays).
**Affects:** `src/lib/dashboard-widgets.ts` (the `appearance` shape + `defaultAppearance`/`effectiveAppearance`, the `tree`/`embed`/`container` kinds + their settings, `itemId` on the widget, the stage `DashboardAppearance` + curated tokens + `stageBackgroundCss`, widened `WidgetData`), `src/lib/dashboards.ts` (tolerant parsers for all the above + `appearance`-column parse + CRUD threading + `usedViewIds` reaching into containers), `src/lib/dashboard-tree.ts` (new), `src/lib/items.ts` (`ItemListRow` export), `src/db/schema.ts` + `drizzle/0034_*.sql` (the `dashboards.appearance` column), `src/components/dashboards/*` (`WidgetFrame` appearance/collapse branch, `WidgetBody` tree render, new `EmbedWidget`/`ContainerWidget`/`BackgroundPanel`/`StageBackground`, `WidgetSettingsPopover` Appearance section + tree/embed/container fields, `AddWidgetMenu` nested-kind + embed-picker + New-note + container, `DashboardClient` handlers + stage, `RglInner`/`DashboardGridLayout` collapse + sizing + `onAppearance`, the shared `widget-title.ts`/`widget-defaults.ts`/`appearance-styles.ts` leaves), `src/components/dashboards/DashboardView.tsx` (the per-kind fan-out incl. container recursion), `src/lib/mcp/tools.ts` (pinned `MCP_WIDGET_KINDS`). **Verification:** `scripts/verify-dashboard-canvas.mts` 28/28 on Neon (appearance parse/defaults, the new kinds + backing requirements, one-level container nesting, stage-appearance clamps/defaults, the batched tree child fetch from both sources with owner-scoping/body-free/hide-completed/type-filter, `usedViewIds` into a container, image parse + chrome-free default) + `verify-dashboards.mts` 19/19; tsc/eslint/`next build` clean. **Remaining:** in-browser eyeball at deploy (the dev-auth local preview doesn't hydrate the react-grid-layout edit-mode islands, the documented constraint). **Deferred:** ADR-111 DC5 (journal/daily-note mode), and DC2 video + raw byte-upload (guarded seam kept).
**Post-preview-review fixes (2026-06-27, same PR #93, after Brandon eyeballed the Vercel preview):** (a) **Relation role is a select, not a free-text box** — populated from the relation-kind property keys defined across types (the field key is the edge role, e.g. `project`); the earlier text box was unclear and glitchy. (b) **Settings persist+refetch is debounced** — `tree`/`view`/`container` settings live in `REFETCH_KINDS`, so a per-keystroke `router.refresh()` was racing the controlled input and blanking it / closing the popover; `handleSettings` now updates optimistically and debounces the persist + refresh (450ms), so typing/selecting never races a refetch. (c) **Popovers render in a portal** (`floating-menu.tsx`: `usePopoverPosition` measures the trigger on open, `FloatingMenu` portals to `document.body` with `position: fixed`) — the gear/add-widget/background popovers were `absolute` inside the `overflow-hidden` widget card, so a short widget clipped them; the portal floats above the canvas, flips left/right and up/down to stay in the viewport, and caps `maxHeight` to scroll internally. Replaced the interim `usePopoverAlign` hook. (d) **New `image` widget kind** (Brandon's "header image / quote pic" ask) — a chrome-free picture from a URL (`{url, alt, fit, link}`), like the stage background takes a URL (no upload plumbing; for an uploaded image, embed a note and paste, which uploads to R2). UI-only, kept off the MCP enum like the other canvas kinds.

## ADR-121: Multi-select is opt-in via a per-list "Select" toggle (refines ADR-118's always-reserved checkbox)
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, 2026-06-27). **NOT core** — a UI/UX refinement of the ADR-118 selection layer (the "move-fast-solo" side of the collab line); no change to the data model, the `/api/items/batch` contract, or the `bulk-config` shape. Brandon chose the toggle approach and its placement ("inline above the list, right-aligned").
**Context:** ADR-118 rendered `SelectCheckbox` on every selectable row at all times — hover-revealed on desktop (`opacity-0 group-hover:opacity-100`) and pinned visible on touch (`max-sm:opacity-100`). Two costs Brandon flagged: (1) even when invisible, the `h-4 w-4` box + the flex gap **reserve leading space**, bumping every row to the right on desktop; (2) on mobile the boxes are **always shown**, eating scarce width and reading as clutter.
**Decision — gate the whole selection layer behind an explicit select mode, off by default.**
1. **`SelectionProvider` gains `selectMode` state** (+ `setSelectMode`; leaving select mode clears the selection) and exposes `total` (the in-view id count).
2. **`SelectCheckbox` renders `null` unless select mode is on** — not an invisible box. A null flex child takes no gap, so an idle row is byte-for-byte the pre-ADR-118 layout: space reclaimed on desktop, nothing on touch. In select mode the box shows solid (the hover/`max-sm` opacity dance is gone).
3. **New `SelectModeToggle`** — a small right-aligned "Select" / "Done" button placed just above the list inside each provider; flips select mode, shows the live count ("Done · 3"), and hides itself when `total === 0`. It lives inside the provider, so it shares state with the checkboxes and the floating bar with no per-page plumbing.
4. **Table layout: new client cells `SelectHeaderCell` / `SelectBodyCell`** self-gate on select mode and return `null` when off, so the table's checkbox **column collapses** when idle. `ViewRenderer` is a server component and can't read the client mode, so the gating has to live in these client cells (the flex list/agenda rows need nothing — the null `SelectCheckbox` already collapses the gap).
5. **Wired into all eight ADR-118 surfaces** (`/tasks`, `/notes`, `/links`, `/events`, `/inbox`, `/list/[type]`, `/views/[id]`, `ViewLensBody`); the toggle is suppressed on **board/calendar** layouts, which remain the ADR-118 selection exceptions.
**Why / alternatives:** *Move the box into the left gutter (no reserved space, keep hover-reveal)* — rejected: with no reserved space the box overlaps the row's leading content (the type label / the task check-off circle), and touch has no hover, so mobile would still need a mode. An explicit toggle is the one mechanism that fixes **both** the desktop space and the mobile clutter and behaves the same on both. *Client context over a `?select=1` URL param* — context toggles instantly with no refetch and keeps the toggle co-located with the provider; the only wrinkle (the server-rendered table column) is handled by the two client cells. **Trade-off accepted:** desktop loses the one-hover quick-select; entering select mode is now one deliberate click (the universal pattern, and what makes mobile clean).
**Affects:** `src/components/selection/{SelectionProvider,SelectCheckbox}.tsx` (select-mode state + null-gating), `src/components/selection/{SelectModeToggle,SelectTableCell}.tsx` (new), `src/components/views/ViewRenderer.tsx` (table cells), `src/components/lists/ViewLensBody.tsx` + the seven list pages (drop the toggle in, layout-gated on the two view surfaces), `CLAUDE.md` (the multi-select convention bullet adds the toggle + the opt-in default), `next_steps.md`, this entry. **Verification:** tsc + eslint + `next build` clean; in-browser dev-auth pass on `/notes` (default = 0 selection checkboxes, title flush-left, "Select" present; toggle on → boxes appear, rows shift, "Done"; select rows → bulk bar "N selected"; "Done" → boxes gone, selection cleared, flush-left again) and `/tasks` (default 0 selection boxes, the task check-off circles intact, toggle present). Screenshots in the session.

## ADR-122: Web-clipper setup relocated to User Settings (discoverability over rebuild)
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, 2026-06-27). **NOT core** — UI/UX placement only; no change to the capture contract (`/api/machine/capture`), the extractor, the `link` type, or the machine-token auth. Brandon chose the destination (User Settings, over a dedicated Build nav entry).
**Context:** Brandon asked to "build a browser save feature that captures page content, working on mobile." It already exists: the web clipper shipped with ADR-100 (desktop bookmarklet reading the live DOM + mobile PWA share-target that re-fetches and extracts server-side, both landing a `link` item with readable markdown). The real problem surfaced mid-conversation: **Brandon didn't know it was there**, because the setup UI (`ClipperSetup`, the draggable bookmarklet) lived as the last section of **Build → AI & MCP**, below a divider next to MCP/HTTP-API tokens — the last place you'd look to "save a web page." So the work was discoverability, not capture. (Considered and declined this session: adding image capture — hotlink-by-default + an opt-in "archive to R2" pass — and a capture-time type picker. Brandon scoped both out: "I don't think we need to build ANYTHING new here.")
**Decision — give the clipper a findable home in User Settings.**
1. **New `src/components/settings/WebClipper.tsx`** ("Save from the web"): a plain-language blurb, a token breadcrumb (status dot + link to AI & MCP, where api tokens are generated), the existing `<ClipperSetup>` drag target under "On desktop", and a new **"On mobile"** numbered walkthrough (add Ledgr to the home screen → Share → Ledgr), which wasn't documented anywhere user-facing.
2. **`settings/page.tsx`** computes `origin` (from request headers, same derivation as the AI & MCP page) + `hasApiToken` (`hasScopedToken("api")`) and renders the section.
3. **AI & MCP page** keeps a short "Web clipper" paragraph (the endpoint is API-relevant) but its interactive drag UI is replaced by a pointer to *User Settings → Save from the web*; the now-unused `ClipperSetup` import is dropped.
**Why / alternatives:** *User Settings over a dedicated Build nav entry* (Brandon's pick) — the clipper is a **set-up-once** surface (drag the bookmarklet once, install the PWA once), so it doesn't earn a daily-nav slot; Settings is reached from both Work and Build, so it's discoverable without entering Build. (Because any route is a valid Work destination, Brandon can still pin Settings, or a future dedicated page, into his Work nav.) *Rebuild capture / add images* — declined; the feature works, and ADR-100's "hotlink + opt-in archive" image layer stays parked. *Keep it in AI & MCP too ("Both")* — declined to avoid a duplicated drag UI; a pointer is left instead (the defer-by-hiding analog: move, don't delete).
**Affects:** `src/components/settings/WebClipper.tsx` (new), `src/app/settings/page.tsx` (origin/token derivation + mount), `src/app/build/claude/page.tsx` (clipper section → pointer, dropped import), `src/components/build/ClipperSetup.tsx` (one-line copy fix: "generated above" → context-free), `next_steps.md`, this entry. No migration, no new dependency. **Verification:** tsc + eslint + `next build` clean; in-browser dev-auth eyeball of `/settings` (section renders, drag link activates on token paste, mobile steps read clearly).

## ADR-123: Auto-match events to people via a guessing layer + rules routed through templates
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, 2026-06-27). **CORE** (touches matching, `match_state` semantics, relations, and the `templates` schema) so it needs Tyler's ack + this ADR before any slice merges; COLLAB heads-up posted. Rolls out in four slices, EM1–EM4 (E1–E4 precedent), shipped behind this single design.
**Context:** Brandon's ask: events should arrive already knowing who they're about, so a meeting's tasks/notes/prayer connect to the right person. The slice-23 matcher engine could only attach people through hand-authored `attendeeEmail` rules, of which there are **0** in production, and nothing resolved an attendee email to a person who already stores that email, nor matched a title like "Roger/Brandon 1:1" to the Roger Knowlton person. Brandon explicitly reshaped the design in conversation: do not force a binary confirmed/suggested; instead **guess** who an event is about from several signals (email plus fuzzy title/details), let him **confirm**, and on confirm let him **pin** an ongoing rule. Crucially he wants the rule **routed through a template** ("a pinned match creates a template with that person pre-related"), so the template both selects which events it governs and carries recurring content (agenda, prayer). Verified data: the `person` type has an `email` text property (96/158 populated, unique, no collisions); the owner's own person carries the owner `users.email` (the self-match hazard and the clean self-exclusion key); 102/158 people are single-token names (the false-positive driver). Naive `word_similarity(name, title)` is unusable (it self-matches the owner and scores the real match below threshold); token-containment isolates the real candidate cleanly. `pg_trgm` is already installed.
**Decision — three layers, rule source moved onto templates.**
1. **Rule source = templates with a match rule (not the `matchers` table).** New nullable `templates.match_config` jsonb = `{ condition: MatcherCondition; autoApply: boolean }`, reusing the matcher engine's condition vocabulary (`attendeeEmail` / `seriesId` / `titleRegex` / `titleFuzzy`), `CONDITION_RANK` precedence, and `validateCondition` verbatim (one definition of "how a condition matches an event"). Only the SOURCE moves. The empty `matchers` table/store/engine are **deprecated dormant**, left in place (reversible, zero data migration). A matched template's preset people come from its prototype's real relation edges (ADR-050), applied as **confirmed** via the existing `applyTemplateToExisting`.
2. **Always-on deterministic person suggester** (`suggestPeopleForEvent`): attendee/organizer email → person by stored `email` (high confidence); **token containment** between the event title (and details) and person-name tokens, length floors (≥3 exact, ≥4 fuzzy `word_similarity ≥ 0.7`) plus a single-token-person cap (medium); a full-title fuzzy fallback (low). Owner person id + name tokens excluded. Ranked email > token > fuzzy, capped at 3. No model (Principle 3).
3. **Intake on add, three tiers** (`applyEventIntake`, one function for the manual Add path and any future path; create-only, so a rejected suggestion is never resurrected on re-sync): **A — recognized:** an `autoApply` template's condition matches → apply it (confirmed people + content); **B — unrecognized:** write the suggester's results as **suggested** person edges (reusing the existing ✓/✕ confirm-reject UX), nothing enters prep/task-pull until confirmed; **C — nothing:** no edges, an empty-state message + manual connect.
4. **Promotion stays MANUAL** (Brandon's Q2 call): events wait in the "From your calendar" feed until he clicks Add; the cron does not auto-promote. Adding a recognized event applies its locked-in template; adding an unrecognized one attaches suggestions. (Auto-promoting pinned events is a possible future toggle, default off, defer-by-hiding.)
5. **Pin-as-rule** (`pinEventAsTemplate`): from a promoted event with confirmed people, derive a default condition (attendee email → series id → title pattern), **create-or-update** an event template (template-explosion guard: reuse an existing rule that already matches) with the people pre-related and `autoApply: true`. This also closes the long-standing gap where a matched `templateName` was only displayed (`MeetingPrep`), never applied (re-keyed to `properties.match.{templateId,…}`, old shape still renders).
**Why / alternatives:** *Confirmed-immediately vs suggested-always* — both rejected for Brandon's guess-then-confirm-then-pin model: a curated email is strong but a fuzzy title is not, so suggestions confirm before they shape prep, while a pinned template applies confirmed (the owner already vouched once). *Keep the separate `matchers` table and link to a template by id* — rejected: with 0 rows there is no migration cost, and "a template that knows which events it governs" is the single concept Brandon described, with no second store to keep in sync. *Auto-promote events with a known person* — rejected as the default (re-creates the ADR-023 firehose the E3 feed deliberately replaced); left as a future opt-in. *AI for the ambiguous cases* — out of scope of the deterministic plumbing; stays in the on-demand Claude/MCP layer (PRD §5.5).
**Affects (EM1 shipped):** `src/db/schema.ts` (`templates.match_config` + `templates_match_idx`), migration `0035_eager_vanisher.sql`, `src/lib/templates/match-config.ts` (new), `src/lib/templates.ts` (`matchConfig` through CRUD), `src/lib/calendar/event-rules.ts` (new: `listEventRules`, `matchEventToTemplate`), `scripts/verify-event-rules.mts` (32/32 on Neon). **EM2–EM4 (planned):** `src/lib/calendar/suggest-people.ts`, `applyEventIntake` + `feed.ts`/`calendar-sync` wiring, `src/lib/templates/pin.ts` + `POST /api/events/[id]/pin-rule` + `MeetingPrep.tsx` UX. **Verification:** per-slice `verify-*.mts` + regressions (calendar-feed/sync, meeting-prep, task-pull, relations, templates); tsc + eslint + `next build` clean each slice.
**Addendum (2026-06-27, post-merge fix — supersedes decision point 3, tier B):** suggestions are now **computed LIVE on the event canvas** (`getMeetingPrep` runs `suggestPeopleForEvent` over the event item every render, minus confirmed people), **not pre-written as `suggested` edges at intake.** Why: the intake-write only surfaced people on events freshly Added through the calendar feed; opening an existing/imported/hand-made event showed nothing (Brandon hit this). Live-compute makes suggestions appear for **any** event and is the single, consistent surface (the People section), each with a **one-click "+ add"** (`SuggestedPeople.tsx` → `POST /api/items/[id]/relations`, a confirmed relate). `applyEventIntake` is now just **Tier A (apply a pinned template) or none**; the suggested-edge writing + `properties.match.suggestions` are removed (`addMatchEdge` no longer called from intake; it stays for the dormant matcher engine). `eventItemToCalendarEvent` (in `suggest-people.ts`) bridges item → the suggester. The owner-exclusion, signals, and pin-as-rule are unchanged. `verify-people-suggest` + `verify-event-template-apply` updated; `next build` clean.

## ADR-124: Standardized item-canvas sections (CanvasSection + 3 skins), and "Relations + Related" merged into "Properties" + "Linked here"
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, designed via before/build mockups; **Tyler acked** the relations/related re-presentation before merge). **CORE** for the relations/related presentation only (touches the universal related list, ADR-055, and typed relation fields, ADR-067); the section primitive + skins are UI/UX polish + a settings field (solo). One design, shipped together.
**Context:** The event view (and every item view) read as a flat wall of low-contrast gray: same muted uppercase headers, no containers, list rows melting together. Two distinct concepts also confused: **"Relations"** (`RelationProperties` — the type's *typed relation fields*, e.g. Attending/Tags, an edit surface) and **"Related"** (`RelatedPanel` — *everything linked here*, both directions, backlinks/@-mentions, which ALSO re-listed the typed fields at top). So a field value (Attending → Mike) appeared twice. Brandon's reframing: a relation field is a **property whose value points at other items**, so it belongs under **Properties**, marked; the connected web (backlinks, @-mentions, wiki-links) is a separate thing, **"Linked here."** He also asked the redesign generalize to all type views (not an event-only skin), and floated owner-selectable visual weight.
**Decision.**
1. **`CanvasSection` primitive** (`src/components/canvas/CanvasSection.tsx`): one panel shape for every item-view section — `icon · uppercase label · count pill · right-aligned action slot · body`. The section glyph uses `var(--accent)`. A `bare` prop drops the card chrome + centered column for when the per-type grid (ADR-069) already wraps it.
2. **Three skins, one body-level knob.** New per-owner setting `sectionStyle: heavy | light | unified` (settings.ts, the same jsonb rail as accent/textSize/uiDensity, no migration), emitted as `data-section-style` on `<body>` (layout.tsx). globals.css styles `.canvas-section` per skin: **heavy** = bordered raised card, **light** = a divider rule, **unified** = flat. **Default = light** (clean for a fresh instance / Tyler); the owner toggles it in User Settings (live, no reload). Nothing is enumerated, so a panel built later inherits the chosen weight for free.
3. **Relations → Properties.** The default canvas (MarkdownCanvas) now renders ONE **Properties** `CanvasSection` holding both scalar `CustomProperties` and typed `RelationProperties` (both `hideHeading bare`). Relational rows are marked with a blue `links` glyph (a property whose value points at other items). The separate "Relations" heading is gone.
4. **Related → "Linked here," de-duped.** `RelatedPanel` is now a `CanvasSection` titled **Linked here** (glyph `affiliate`). It **no longer renders the typed-relation-field sections** (they live under Properties); it still *claims* those items so they don't repeat in the type-grouped inbound list. Count = the non-field items; when none remain, it collapses to the quiet add affordances.
5. **Event prep, refined** (not core): `MeetingPrep` is three `CanvasSection`s (People / Open tasks / Recent meetings); suggested people render **inline** with confirmed people as dashed sparkle chips (hover = "Suggested · click to confirm"), not a separate row; **Open tasks reuse `RelatedRow`** so they check off + edit due/title in place (`manageable={false}` since they're rule-pulled, not host edges); confirmed people are avatar chips. `MeetingTranscripts` also moved onto `CanvasSection`.
6. **Long titles wrap** (Brandon's mobile note): `RelatedRow` defaults to `wrap` (title wraps instead of truncating, checkbox top-aligns to the first line); the fixed-width relation **chips** keep truncating (`InlineTitle wrap` opt-in, default off).
7. **Vestigial "+ Promote action item to task" button removed** (`PromoteTask.tsx` deleted). The current path is the inline **"→ task"** affordance on `[ ]` body lines (block anchors, ADR-090); the `/api/items/[id]/promote-task` route + `promoteActionItem` stay (that path still uses them).
**Why / alternatives:** *Keep two panels, just rename/tooltip* — rejected: the double-listing is the actual confusion; folding fields into Properties removes it. *Name them "Links"/"Connections"* — rejected (Brandon): a relation field is a property, not a separate "connection." *Card-per-section as the only style* — rejected: shipped as the owner-selectable `sectionStyle` (heavy is Brandon's pick; light is the safe default). *Fork a lighter task row for Open tasks* — rejected for reuse: `RelatedRow` already does optimistic check-off + inline due/title edit, so a `manageable` flag was enough.
**Affects:** new `src/components/canvas/CanvasSection.tsx`; `src/lib/settings.ts` (+`sectionStyle`), `src/app/layout.tsx` (body attr), `src/app/globals.css` (`.canvas-section*` skins + `.canvas-rows`), `src/components/settings/SettingsForm.tsx` (control), `src/lib/nav-icons.ts` (+`properties`,`affiliate` glyphs); `src/components/canvas/MarkdownCanvas.tsx` (merged Properties + Linked here), `src/components/relations/RelatedPanel.tsx` (Linked here + de-dup + `bare`), `RelationProperties.tsx` (link marker), `RelatedRow.tsx`/`InlineTitle.tsx` (`manageable`, `wrap`); `src/components/meetings/MeetingPrep.tsx` (rewrite), `SuggestedPeople.tsx` (inline chips), `MeetingTranscripts.tsx` (CanvasSection); `PaperCanvas.tsx` (now renders `RelationProperties` so a future paper relation field isn't hidden by the de-dup); deleted `PromoteTask.tsx`. **Verification:** tsc + eslint clean; dev-auth preview across event (heavy/light/unified), person, and task canvases — sections, inline suggestions, check-off rows, wrapping, relation markers, de-dup all confirmed, no console errors. Bespoke `TaskCanvas`/`ChordCanvas` keep their own rail/stacked layout (module-level, move-fast) and gain the link marker; merging their relations under one "Properties" heading is an optional follow-up.
**Addendum (2026-06-27, consistency pass — Brandon flagged the task rail + popovers weren't skinned):** the skin was opt-in per `CanvasSection`, so any surface with its own heading was missed.
