Swept the rest, splitting by surface class (Brandon's call): **content panels → skin-responsive** — `HistoryPanel` (Version history) and the default canvas's collapsible **Fields** footer now carry the card/divider/flat chrome + the standardized header; `Subtasks` moved onto `CanvasSection`; `ChordCanvas` (song) and `PaperCanvas` (paper) now use the merged Properties section like the default (paper guards on having relation fields). **Compact/transient surfaces → matching headers, NO card chrome** (a popover/menu full of cards reads worse): the `TaskCanvas` right rail merges its relation + scalar fields under one **bare** "Properties" header (the Schedule/Due/Priority rows stay the compact divided list, ADR-108), and `SchedulePopover`'s DATE/TIME/REMINDER/REPEAT labels adopt the shared header text style. `SaveOffline`/`ShareLink` stay headerless action-button rows (a button isn't a section). Verified in dev-auth preview (task + event canvases, heavy): rail Properties, popover labels, Version history, and Fields all consistent; no console errors; tsc/eslint/`next build` clean.

## ADR-125: Body modes (rich / source / preview) + a large-body size gate
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed; **Tyler agreed** before build). **CORE** — touches the type+canvas model and the canonical body contract (how a body is edited/rendered), so both-agree + ADR.
**Context:** Opening very long notes froze or crashed the tab. Measured against production data the cause was unambiguous and entirely client-side: the body always mounts the Tiptap/ProseMirror WYSIWYG editor, which parses the whole markdown into one document and renders it as a single `contenteditable` tree (tens of thousands of nodes), then re-serializes the entire document on every keystroke. Postgres returns the 1MB+ text in milliseconds and the FTS tsvector stays ~13% of its 1 MiB ceiling even for the 2.4M-char outlier (tsvector dedup + the 256-position cap bound it), so neither the DB, search, Neon, nor Vercel is the bottleneck. Real distribution: median body 152 chars, p99 ≈ 96K, with a tail of ~60 notes over 100K and 3 over 1M (Notion-imported books, a scanned magazine, syllabi). Brandon explicitly wants long read-only notes (saving PDFs as text to read) as a permanent first-class use, so "split the data into Pt 1/Pt 2 items" was rejected — the freeze is `contenteditable`, not data size, so the fix is *how* a body renders, not fragmenting the item. Brandon's reframe (the chosen design): build the long-intended **source/preview toggle** now (CLAUDE.md already described the editor as "a markdown-native WYSIWYG ... with a likely source/preview toggle") and let the size gate just *select* it, so the fix is also a general feature available on any note.
**Decision.**
1. **Three body modes over one canonical markdown body (ADR-037), owned by a new client `BodyEditor`** (`src/components/markdown-editor/BodyEditor.tsx`), which `ItemEditor` now renders in place of the inline `tabsEnabled ? TabbedBody : LazyMarkdownEditor` choice — so **every** canvas (markdown, task, link, modules) inherits the behavior, since they all route the body through `ItemEditor`:
   - **rich** — the existing Tiptap WYSIWYG (`TabbedBody` when the type uses tabs, else `LazyMarkdownEditor`). Default for normal-size bodies.
   - **source** — the raw markdown in a plain `<textarea>` (`RawMarkdownEditor`): no contenteditable, no node tree, no per-keystroke serialization, so it holds megabytes without lag. Uncontrolled (`defaultValue` + `onChange`), no syntax highlighting (that would re-introduce the cost). Available on **any** note as a power tool.
   - **preview** — read-only rendered HTML (`MarkdownPreview`) via a new `POST /api/render-markdown` (markdown-it is server-only, so the client fetches the render of its *live* text; styled with `.ledgr-prose`). Owner-scoped, transforms only the text it's handed, touches no row.
2. **Size gate (`LARGE_BODY_THRESHOLD = 100_000` chars, `isLargeBody`, in `src/lib/body.ts`).** At/above it a body is a "document": the rich editor is **never mounted**, it opens in **preview** with a banner explaining why, and **source** is the edit path. Below it, rich is the default with a quiet Rich/Source toggle. 100K ≈ 16k words / ~40 pages, past any real note while leaving ~99% of items on the rich editor (measured p99 ≈ 96K). One tunable constant.
3. **Mode-switch text sync.** Every mode reports markdown through one `handleChange` kept in a `liveText` ref; switching modes snapshots it into `mountText` (the seed for the freshly-mounted child, keyed by mode), so a switch carries the latest text — including unsaved edits — without remounting the child during editing.
4. **Size-aware revisions** (`src/lib/items.ts`, `snapshotRevision`): a large body throttles to a 60-min debounce and a 10-snapshot cap (vs 5-min / 50 for normal), so a multi-MB document can't pile up ~50× its size in history and pressure Neon's ~0.5GB free tier (revisions are 44MB of the 187MB DB today). Small bodies are byte-for-byte unchanged.
**Why / alternatives:** *Bespoke large-note path* — rejected for the unified source/preview toggle: same fix, less code, and it's a feature on every note (Brandon's reframe). *Split monster notes into Pt 1/Pt 2 items* — rejected: fragments search/backlinks/relations and fights the "one document I'm reading" model; the freeze is `contenteditable`, not size. *Separate "raw edit" route with manual save + back button* (Brandon's first sketch) — rejected for inline: the `<textarea>` is already as raw as Notepad, and inline reuses `ItemEditor`'s debounced autosave and keeps the item's context. *Render preview on the client* — rejected: markdown-it is server-only by rule (Principle 5 / markdown-render.ts); a tiny endpoint keeps that seam. *Bound the FTS input now* — deferred: measured tsvectors are ~13% of the limit, so it's a distant ceiling (the lever, `left(body_text, N)` in the generated column, is noted if ever needed). **Known minor gap:** in-app preview doesn't carry the sermon highlight-color CSS (`mark.hl-*` lives in the print/share doc CSS), so highlights show as the browser default in preview; large imported docs rarely use them, and rich mode (where colors are authored) is unaffected. **Tradeoff accepted:** source mode has no @-mention menu / color picker / drag-drop images (you're editing source); the banner makes this explicit, and rich↔source round-trips on normal notes pass through Tiptap's serializer (may re-normalize formatting) — large notes are immune since rich never runs on them, preserving imported text exactly.
**Affects:** new `src/components/markdown-editor/BodyEditor.tsx`, `RawMarkdownEditor.tsx`, `MarkdownPreview.tsx`, `src/app/api/render-markdown/route.ts`; `src/lib/body.ts` (`LARGE_BODY_THRESHOLD`, `isLargeBody`), `src/components/markdown-editor/ItemEditor.tsx` (renders `BodyEditor`), `src/lib/items.ts` (size-aware `snapshotRevision`). No schema change, no migration; fully additive and reversible.

## ADR-126: Page large bodies on the MCP get_item read path
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted. The follow-up ADR-125 explicitly deferred. Touches the **machine/MCP API contract** (CORE), but additively: it adds optional args + an extra output field to one read tool and never changes the `{format, text}` body contract or any write path, so it's a backward-compatible extension rather than a contract change.
**Context:** ADR-125 fixed the *browser* freeze on huge notes but left the MCP read path: `get_item` (the one MCP tool that returns a body; search/list/run_view are all body-free via `rowView`) returned `bodyMarkdown(item.body)` whole. Against production data that means up to ~2.4M characters (~600k tokens) in a single tool result — several items over 1M (imported PDFs/ebooks/syllabi) — which floods the model's context in one read. The DB/FTS aren't the bottleneck (ADR-125 measured that); the cost is purely the size of the text handed to the model.
**Decision.**
1. **Reuse the ADR-125 size gate.** A new `BODY_WINDOW_CHARS` in `src/lib/body.ts` is pinned to `LARGE_BODY_THRESHOLD` (100K), and a new pure `windowBody(text, {offset, limit})` slices a body to one character window — substring math only, **no markdown parsing** (heading-aware sectioning would belong in the server-only `markdown-render.ts` and would break `body.ts`'s client/server portability), clamping `offset`→[0,total] and `limit`→[1,window] so a bad caller gets an empty/whole window, never a throw.
2. **get_item windows only large bodies.** A body below the threshold (and no explicit paging) returns **whole and byte-for-byte unchanged** — the contract and the existing `verify-mcp` assertion both hold. A large body (or any call passing `bodyOffset`/`bodyLimit`) returns at most one window: the slice, a trailing truncation marker (`…[truncated: N of M chars shown (offset a–b). Call get_item again with bodyOffset=b …]`), and a structured `bodyInfo {totalChars, offset, returnedChars, truncated, nextOffset}`. The caller pages by passing the previous `nextOffset` as `bodyOffset`; `bodyLimit` (≤ window) requests lighter reads.
3. **Window == threshold, so the boundaries line up.** A body at the threshold returns whole in one read; the hard cap on any single read is one "document's worth" (~40 pages / ~25k tokens) instead of the multi-megabyte tail. One tunable knob, shared by the editor (ADR-125) and the MCP read path.
**Why / alternatives:** *Heading/section windowing* (the marker text in the brief hinted at it) — deferred: it needs markdown parsing, which `body.ts` deliberately excludes, and character offsets are a robust, dependency-free paging primitive that round-trips exactly (verified by reassembly). A future section param could layer on top server-side if a real need appears. *Summarize/elide instead of paging* — rejected: would put a model in a read path (violates Principle 3, deterministic-by-default) and lose exact text. *A separate `get_item_body` tool* — rejected: more surface for the same job; optional args on the existing tool keep the contract additive. *Lower the per-read cap below the threshold* — rejected: it would truncate sub-threshold bodies that the editor still treats as whole, an awkward split; aligning the window to the gate keeps one mental model.
**Affects:** `src/lib/body.ts` (`BODY_WINDOW_CHARS`, `BodyWindow`, `windowBody`), `src/lib/mcp/tools.ts` (`get_item` schema + handler), new `scripts/verify-mcp-large-body.mts`. No schema change, no migration, no write-path change; fully additive and reversible.

## ADR-127: Discover — deterministic related-item suggestions (a guessing layer over the relations graph)
**Date:** 2026-06-27
**Status:** accepted. **CORE** — it sits on the `relations` substrate (ADR-055), the universal Related panel / `CanvasSection` (ADR-124), and the FTS tsvector (ADR-014). Both-agree satisfied: Brandon designed it through the planning session, **Tyler acked** before merge. Graduates `explorations/related-items-discovery.md` (parked 2026-06-19).
**Context:** The Related panel only shows edges that already exist; finding what *should* link took manual `+ Relate` search. Brandon wanted a surface that, on every item, surfaces items worth linking but not linked yet — ranked, deterministic (Principle 3, no model), with one-click Link — doubling as a "where did I put that" search helper.
**Decision.**
1. **A deterministic scorer** (`src/lib/discovery/score.ts`), pure and strategy-agnostic. Candidate gather is bounded, indexed probes only (Principle 8): an FTS OR-query (`items.search` / `ts_rank`) + `pg_trgm` title similarity → a **text** signal; shared linked neighbors **IDF-damped by neighbor degree** → **cocitation**; same `parent_id` or a shared `select`/`multi_select` value → **sharedAttr**; created/edited closeness → a **temporal** booster. Weights + a min-score **floor** sit in one named constant (`WEIGHTS`, `SCORE_FLOOR`). Co-citation ranks the head when it fires; text/attr carry the cold, unlinked item.
2. **A precomputed cache, built up front** — table `item_relatedness` (migration 0036; `item_id`, `candidate_id`, `score`, `signals`, `computed_at`; both FKs cascade). Derived machinery like `revisions`, **not** user content (rule 2) and deliberately **not** on `items.properties` (would bump `updated_at` → re-export + a rescore loop, and pollute the FTS tsvector). A bounded nightly job (`refresh.ts`, dirty-driven via `updated_at > computed_at` + a rolling stalest cursor, `BATCH`/time-budgeted) writes it; `/api/machine/relatedness` (cron scope) + a daily `vercel.json` cron run it; `/health` carries `lastRelatednessRunAt`.
3. **One stable seam:** `GET /api/items/[id]/suggested-relations` reads the cache, **falling back to a live compute on a miss** so a brand-new item is never blank, and **re-checks current edges at read** so an item linked since the last compute drops out. The UI never knows which path served it.
4. **The panel** (`DiscoverPanel`, under "Linked here" in both canvas layouts) fetches once on mount (a cheap cache read), so it **auto-hides when nothing clears the floor** and the collapsed header shows the count; **Link** writes a generic `related` edge via the existing `relateItems`, and the row graduates up into Linked here. Discovery **never writes a `suggested` edge** — that meaning stays the calendar matchers' (ADR-123/024).
**Why / alternatives:** *Persist guesses as `suggested` edges* — rejected; overloads a confident-claim state with gray noise and forces dedup against real edges. *Compute-on-read only (no cache)* — the plan's interim option; Brandon chose to build the cache immediately, which also makes the auto-hide + future explorer reads cheap. *Score onto `items.properties`* — rejected (the `updated_at`/FTS reasons above). *A dismiss / "not related" control* — deferred for v1 (a bad guess just ranks low and scrolls off). *pgvector embeddings / an AI pass in the read path* — out of scope (a new dependency / a model in a default path); the deterministic layer is the always-on baseline, an on-demand AI "Find connections" can layer on later. **Deferred, designed:** a **Related Explorer** (Phase 2) — the same scorer with `includeLinked` true for a score-sorted, anchor-hopping map (the search-helper case); **Loose Ends** (Phase 3) — the engine inverted across the corpus as a Build › Maintain page + widget.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/discovery/{types,score,refresh}.ts`, `src/app/api/items/[id]/suggested-relations/route.ts`, `src/app/api/machine/relatedness/route.ts`, `src/components/relations/DiscoverPanel.tsx`; migration `0036_keen_exodus.sql` + `itemRelatedness` in `schema.ts`; wiring in `MarkdownCanvas.tsx` + `canvas-layout.ts` (a `discover` card after `related`), a `lastRelatednessRunAt` canary in `health.ts`, the daily `vercel.json` cron, and a `q` prefill on the search page for the handoff. Verification: new `scripts/verify-discover.mts` (19/19 — signals, floor, template/deleted/self exclusions, body-free, score-sorted, cache populate + read, read-time re-filter of a now-linked candidate, owner-scoping); regressions green (`verify-canvas-layout` updated for the new card, `verify-relations`, `verify-lists-search`, `verify-health-check`); `tsc` + lint clean. Additive and reversible (drop the table + the cron entry).
**Phase 2 shipped (2026-06-27, PR #109):** the **Related Explorer** — `/items/[id]/explore` (server page, breadcrumb trail via `?trail`, one score-sorted list of links + candidates with `+ Link` and `Explore →` re-anchoring). `exploreNeighborhood` (`src/lib/discovery/explore.ts`) unions `listRelatedItems` + `scoreRelated({includeLinked:true})`, computed live per anchor (no cache dependency); `ExploreRow` client leaf; entry points in `ItemActionsMenu` + the Discover panel footer. `verify-explore.mts` 9/9; tsc/lint/build green. No schema change. Phase 3 (Loose Ends) remains.
**Phase 3 shipped (2026-06-27, PR #110):** **Loose Ends** — the engine inverted across the corpus. `findLooseEnds` (`src/lib/discovery/loose-ends.ts`) aggregates confirmed non-mention edge degree once, takes the least-connected items (≤3 edges), scores the top ~40 concurrently, returns ~20 that have a real suggestion (true orphans with no candidate are skipped, not shown empty). Build › MAINTAIN page `/build/loose-ends` (`LooseEndCard` renders each item + its top suggestions inline with one-click Link) + a `build-nav.ts` entry. `verify-loose-ends.mts` 7/7; tsc/lint/build green; no schema change. **Deferred (opt-in extras):** a bespoke Loose Ends *dashboard widget* (the page is the home for now) and the on-demand AI "Find connections" Layer 2. With Phases 1–3 in, ADR-127 is delivered.

## ADR-128: Section style honored on grid item views + visible save feedback on the settings form
**Date:** 2026-06-28
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed). **Solo** (UI/UX polish), matching ADR-124's own classification of the heavy/light/unified skins as polish-not-core; this only extends the existing skin's reach and floats a confirmation. No schema, seam, or canvas-model change.
**Context:** Brandon reported the heavy/light/unified Section style setting "isn't working — wrong style, and no Saved message." Investigation against production: the setting was **saving correctly** (GET/PATCH 200, value persisted). Two display problems made it look broken. (1) The settings form's single shared "Saved" confirmation rendered only at the *bottom* of a long form, so a mid-form control (Section style sits ~middle) flashed its 1.2s confirmation below the fold — invisible. (2) The skin (ADR-124) is applied by CSS scoped `.canvas-section:not(.canvas-section-bare)`. Types with a saved `canvasLayout` (note, project, hiring_candidate — note is among the most-opened) render their panels `bare` inside read-only grid cards, which are deliberately chrome-free (the arrange grid adds the frame; read-only reads like a document). So the skin never reached them and the setting was silently inert on exactly those types.
**Decision.**
1. **Floating save confirmation** (`SettingsForm.tsx`): the "Saved" pill is now `fixed bottom-4 right-4`, visible from any control regardless of scroll position, instead of an inline line at the form's end.
2. **Grid cards honor the section style** (`globals.css`): apply the same three weights (heavy = bordered card, light = top rule, unified = flat) to **every** read-only grid card — `[data-section-style=…] .layout:not(.dash-edit) .canvas-card-content`. "Every card" (body editor included) was Brandon's explicit call over "panel cards only," so a grid item reads as a uniform set of cards; it also sidesteps the fact that bare panels share no marker class (Properties renders a plain `<section>`, Related/Meeting render `.canvas-section-bare`), which made a panels-only CSS selector inconsistent. Scoped to `:not(.dash-edit)` so the arrange grid keeps its edit frame; the existing `.canvas-card-content > *` chrome-strip keeps the weight on the card, not doubled inside it.
**Why / alternatives:** *Panels-only skin (match stacked)* — rejected by Brandon; needs a marker-class code change and mixes boxed/unboxed cards on one item. *Leave grid inert + document it* — rejected; the setting reading as dead on the most-common type is the actual bug. *Treat as core (ADR + Tyler gate)* — initially flagged, then reclassified solo per ADR-124 (the skins are polish; this changes no model or seam).
**Affects:** `src/components/settings/SettingsForm.tsx` (floating pill), `src/app/globals.css` (three grid-card skin rules). Additive, reversible (git revert). Verified server-side (PATCH 200, value persisted); the grid look is to be eyeballed in-browser (CSS-only, low blast radius).

## ADR-129: Notification Center — persisted notifications over the existing Web Push transport
**Date:** 2026-06-28
**Status:** accepted. **CORE** — adds a new `notifications` table (a `schema.md` change). Both-agree satisfied: Brandon designed it this session, **Tyler agreed** before merge. Graduates `explorations/notification-center.md` (raised + resolved 2026-06-28).
**Context:** Web Push (ADR-034) delivers the morning agenda + meeting-prep pings, but delivery is fire-and-forget: once a push goes out it evaporates, with no history, read/unread state, or archive. Brandon asked for a notification center where all notifications live (read + unread), markable read/unread, archivable. Key design call from Brandon: **one row per event** (three tasks notifying at once = three entries), not a rolled-up digest.
**Decision.**
1. **A dedicated `notifications` table** (migration 0037), NOT notifications-as-items. Fields: `id`, `owner_id` (FK `users.id`, owner-scope every query), `kind` (text: `agenda`|`meeting_prep`|`task_due`|`calendar_soon`|`sync_error`|…), `title`, `body` (plain text, null), `url` (in-app deep link, null), `related_item_id` (FK `items.id`, null, cascade with item purge), `state` (`unread`|`read`|`archived`, default `unread`), `read_at`, `archived_at`, `created_at`. Index `(owner_id, state, created_at desc)` powers both the list and the unread-count badge; index `(related_item_id)`. State as one text column + timestamps (not three booleans) keeps the lifecycle linear and the badge query a single `where state='unread'`.
2. **Why a table, not items** (the Principle-2 bend, justified): read/unread does not map onto the `status_category` enum (not_started/in_progress/done/archived) without abuse; notifications are high-churn system ephemera that *point at* items, not content, so as items they would pollute the `items` table, FTS tsvector, search, and Discover/relatedness. Same reasoning that kept `item_relatedness` off `items.properties` (ADR-127) and that justifies `revisions`/`push_subscriptions` as their own tables: derived/system machinery, not user content.
3. **Write path:** a `recordNotification(...)` helper writes a row, called wherever a push fires (Phase 1: the two existing senders) and from silent events later. The push send and the row write are independent: a user with push disabled still accumulates history; a failed delivery still has its row.
4. **Per-source on/off toggles** (Brandon): each source is individually toggleable, stored in `users.settings.notificationPrefs` (the navSlots/favorites/listTabs posture — **no schema**), default all on. `recordNotification` checks the pref for its `kind` and no-ops if off, so **one switch gates both the row and the push**.
5. **UI:** a `/notifications` Work page (Unread / All / Archived filter tabs; per-row mark read/unread + archive; multi-select bulk bar per ADR-118 with Mark read / Mark unread / Archive). A **bell + unread badge** in the Work nav via a new `badgeEligible` built-in destination in `src/lib/nav-slot-options.ts` (Inbox is the only `badgeEligible` destination today, so the count-badge plumbing is reused). Distinct from Inbox: Inbox triages inbound content; the center dismisses events; they coexist.
6. **PWA app-icon badge in v1** (Brandon: wanted ASAP, not deferred): the Badging API — `navigator.setAppBadge(unread)` / `clearAppBadge()`, set from the SW `push` handler (increment) and from the client on read/archive + on load (authoritative count). Works on installed PWAs (desktop Chromium, Android, iOS 16.4+); the in-app bell badge is the universal fallback. Ship both.
7. **Retention:** 30-day auto-purge of archived rows (matches Trash's 30-day), a daily cron sweep.
**Why / alternatives:** *Notifications as items* (Principle 2 literal) — rejected (the enum/pollution reasons in 2). *Three booleans for state* — rejected (linear `state` + timestamps is a simpler query + lifecycle). *Rolled-up digest rows* — rejected by Brandon (one row per event). *App-icon badge deferred to v2* — rejected by Brandon (wanted ASAP). *No per-source toggles* — rejected by Brandon (each area on/off).
**Affects (planned):** new `notifications` table in `schema.ts` + `schema.md` + migration 0037; new `src/lib/notifications/` (`recordNotification`, queries, prefs); `src/lib/push/notify.ts` (call `recordNotification` alongside each send); `src/lib/nav-slot-options.ts` (the bell destination); `/app/notifications/page.tsx` + a client list leaf; the SW (`setAppBadge` on push) + a client badge sync + an unread-count endpoint; User Settings (per-source toggles); a daily purge cron in `vercel.json` + `/api/machine/*`. Phase 2: the three new sources (task_due, calendar_soon, sync/health) as pref-gated callers. Phase 3: MCP tools (`list_notifications`/`mark_read`/`archive_notification`). Verification: new `scripts/verify-notifications.mts`. Additive and reversible (drop the table + cron entry; the prefs key is tolerant-parsed).

## ADR-130: Pause the notification center (detach UI + crons; keep everything recoverable)
**Date:** 2026-06-29
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed). **Solo / per-instance** — a per-instance feature enable flip, not a core change: the `notifications` table, migration 0037, `schema.md`, the push provider interface, and the whole Web Push transport (ADR-034) are all **untouched**. Brandon's instance only; Tyler's instance keeps the center if he wants it (heads-up to Tyler via COLLAB suggested, but not a both-agree gate since no shared schema/seam/contract moves). This pauses, it does not reverse, ADR-129.
**Context:** With the per-task reminder dropdown now offering "At time of event"/lead options and the published ICS feed (ADR-079) firing those alarms precisely, offline, on-device, Brandon observed the subscribed calendar already gives him reminders *and* a per-device notification history — making the recently-built in-app notification center redundant for his use. He asked to delete or detach it; per the project's **defer-by-hiding-not-deleting** rule (and his own "in case I want a more powerful app later"), detach won over delete. Scope confirmed with Brandon: **all off** — hide the in-app center AND stop both push crons (morning-agenda + meeting-prep phone pushes go quiet too), not just hide the list.
**Decision.**
1. **One flag, db-free leaf module:** `src/lib/notifications-enabled.ts` exports `NOTIFICATION_CENTER_ENABLED = false` with a full re-enable runbook in its header. Lives apart from `notifications.ts` (which imports the db) so client components can read it without dragging server-only code into the client bundle; `notifications.ts` re-exports it for the server callers.
2. **Gated app surfaces:** the two senders in `push/notify.ts` early-return (so even a manual cron dispatch is a no-op — no rows, no pushes, no `prepNotifiedAt` stamps); the `/notifications` nav destination is filtered out of `nav-slot-options.ts`; the More-menu link + `AppBadgeSync` mount are conditional in `NavShell.tsx`; `Nav.tsx` skips the unread query (badge 0); the Settings "Notifications" section is hidden in `SettingsForm.tsx`; the `/notifications` page `redirect("/")`s so a stray pin/bookmark lands safely.
3. **Crons disabled in config:** `notify-agenda` entry removed from `vercel.json` (strict JSON, no comment — git + this ADR are the record); `notify-prep.yml`'s `schedule:` commented out, `workflow_dispatch` kept so it stays hand-runnable.
4. **Kept intact, recoverable:** the `notifications` table + migration 0037, `src/lib/notifications.ts`, the API routes (`/api/notifications*`), the `/notifications` page + `NotificationList`, the SW badge handlers, and the entire Web Push transport (subscriptions, VAPID, `PushToggle`, `web-push.ts`). The daily `purge` cron keeps running (harmless; no new archived rows accrue). Nothing destructive; this is the feature-side analog of soft-delete.
**Why / alternatives:** *Delete the center + drop the table* — rejected (defer-by-hiding rule; Brandon may build a more capable notifications app later). *Hide UI only, keep the agenda/prep phone pushes* — offered, Brandon chose all-off (the ICS feed carries what he needs). *Scatter comment-outs instead of a flag* — rejected; one named, documented flag is more legible and is a one-line re-enable.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/notifications-enabled.ts`; edits to `src/lib/notifications.ts` (re-export), `src/lib/push/notify.ts` (guards), `src/lib/nav-slot-options.ts`, `src/components/nav/NavShell.tsx`, `src/components/nav/Nav.tsx`, `src/components/settings/SettingsForm.tsx`, `src/app/notifications/page.tsx`, `vercel.json`, `.github/workflows/notify-prep.yml`. Reversible: flip the flag, restore the two cron configs, redeploy.

## ADR-131: Planner — a `views.display` jsonb for the interactive drag-to-schedule calendar
**Date:** 2026-06-29
**Status:** accepted. **Core (both-agree + ADR):** adds a column to the `views` table and a field to the View Definition contract, so it's on the frozen-core list (the data model / `schema.md`). **Brandon + Tyler agreed** before merge (Tyler's agreement recorded 2026-06-29). The new column is the *only* core touch in the Planner feature; the renderers, the drag hook, and the Unscheduled rail are UI (solo).
**Context:** Tasks already carry a scheduled day (`scheduled_date`) and an optional floating time block (`properties.scheduledTime`, ADR-091 / `scheduled-time.ts`), but there was no surface to *place and shuffle* that work on a calendar — dates were set one task at a time in a detail panel. The Planner is a calendar surface with two modes (a month grid and a multi-day time-grid) where tasks are dragged to plan when they'll be done. The `calendar` view layout already exists (a static month grid in `ViewRenderer`); the Planner replaces that branch with an interactive client island. The open question was *where the calendar's interactive options live* (mode, day count, slot size, place-by, work-hours), since a saved view needs to remember them per-view. (Full plan + the six resolved design questions: the 2026-06-29 brainstorm; design follows the Ledgr theme + the built-in accent from `users.settings`, ADR-053.)
**Decision.**
1. **One additive column.** `views.display` (jsonb, nullable) — migration `0038_third_cyclops.sql` (`ALTER TABLE "views" ADD COLUMN "display" jsonb;`). `null` = the layout's defaults (`DISPLAY_DEFAULTS` in `views.ts`), so every pre-existing calendar view is unchanged. No backfill.
2. **The shape (`ViewDisplay`):** `mode` (`month` | `timegrid`), `dayCount` (1–7), `slotMinutes` (15 | 30 | 60), `placeBy` (`scheduled` | `due`), `workStartHour` / `workEndHour`, `showWeekends`. All optional; the renderer resolves gaps from `DISPLAY_DEFAULTS` (month · 7 days · 30-min · scheduled · 7a–7p · weekends on).
3. **Place-by = scheduled, by default.** A drag writes `scheduled_date` (+ an optional time block) — the Planner plans *work*, it does not move the *deadline* (`due_date`). A per-view `placeBy: "due"` flips a calendar to operate on the deadline for the occasional due-date calendar.
4. **Tolerant parse (`parseDisplay`).** Same discipline as `parseColumns` / `parseGrouping`: unknown keys dropped, out-of-range numbers clamped, an inverted work-window's end dropped, an empty result collapsed to `null`. A stale or hand-edited row can never wedge a render. Threaded through `parseViewInput`, `rowToDefinition`, `createView`, `updateView`; the MCP `create_view` contract gains an optional `display` and is otherwise unchanged.
5. **Time stays in `properties.scheduledTime` for now.** No column promotion (`scheduled_at` / `scheduled_minutes`) yet; the Planner is the surface that will earn that later ADR once the shape is proven.
**Why / alternatives:** *Reuse the existing `grouping`/`filter` jsonb* — rejected; overloads fields with an unrelated meaning. *URL + localStorage only (no column)* — rejected; an ad-hoc planner can't remember per-view settings, and a seeded default Planner view needs to persist its config. *A bespoke `planner_settings` table* — rejected; the config belongs to a view, one nullable jsonb is the lightest additive step (rule 5). *Make the calendar a new layout enum value* — unnecessary; `month`/`timegrid` is a display mode of the existing `calendar` layout, not a different query.
**Affects (this slice):** `src/db/schema.ts` (`views.display`), `drizzle/0038_third_cyclops.sql` + journal, `src/lib/views.ts` (`ViewDisplay`/`DISPLAY_DEFAULTS`/`parseDisplay` + `ViewDefinition`/`ViewInput`/CRUD wiring), `scripts/verify-planner.mts`. Schema doc update + the interactive renderers (`PlannerCalendar`, `MonthGrid`, `TimeGrid`, `UnscheduledRail`, `usePlannerDrag`) and the `ViewRenderer` calendar-branch swap land in the following Phase-1 slices. Reversible: drop the column (no readers depend on it until the renderer ships).

## ADR-132: Type cue on the item view + move an item between types
**Date:** 2026-06-29
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, built). **Touches core — Tyler agreed before merge (2026-06-29).** No schema change (no migration), but the *move-between-types semantics* and a new **MCP tool** touch the frozen-core type model and the machine/MCP contract, so this is a both-agree + ADR item. Part A (the cue) is plain additive UI and is solo-safe on its own; it's bundled here for one review.
**Context:** Two gaps on the individual item view (Brandon, 2026-06-29). (1) Nothing on an open item said what *type* it was — the only trace was the raw type key buried in the grid-layout Fields card (`canvas-fields.ts`). (2) There was no way to *move* an item to another type. The data layer already allowed it (`updateItem` accepts a `type` change via `assertTypeExists`), but it was unreachable from the UI and did nothing about properties the new type doesn't declare. Brandon's worry — that a retype silently loses properties/relations — and his ask to keep orphaned values **visible and editable** (not just silently parked in jsonb) drove the design. A `/visual-plan` (local-files render) settled four questions before build.
**Decision.**
1. **Type cue (Part A) — zero extra vertical space.** A quiet, non-interactive `TypeCue` (`src/components/canvas/TypeCue.tsx`) = the type's own nav icon (`NavGlyph`, the same `types.icon` source the nav, type builder, and @-mentions read) + its label, muted. It rides chrome that's already on screen: the full-page breadcrumb row in `ItemCanvas` (after the trash button, a `·` before any ancestor chain), and the modal header beside "Trash" in `Modal` (fed `typeLabel`/`typeIcon` by the modal page). Chosen over a dedicated row above the title (added height, rejected) and a non-editable title-line adornment (Option B, shares the title line — kept as the runner-up). An unset icon falls back to the generic glyph; an unregistered type shows its key as the label.
2. **Move between types (Part B) — one server helper, three callers.** `moveItemType(ownerId, id, targetType, { dryRun })` in `items.ts` is the single reconciliation path behind the dialog preview, the REST endpoint, and the MCP tool — so the preview can never drift from the commit. It reconciles **only the SOURCE type's declared `propertySchema` properties**: keys the target also declares **carry over** untouched; keys it lacks are **surfaced** into the body as a fenced YAML block (`# carried over from <Type>`). System/sync keys (`locked`, `recurrence`, todoist/ms ids) and anything not on the type schema are **never touched and never surfaced** — they aren't "the type's fields". Relation-kind properties hold no jsonb value (their value is the edges), so they're skipped, and **relation edges are never read or written** — they survive the move and keep showing in the related list. (Decided: do **not** re-emit relations as @-mentions; mentions create edges via sync, so that would duplicate them.)
3. **Decided knobs (the four open questions).** Surfacing format = **fenced YAML** (visible, copyable). Orphaned values are **retained in `items.properties`** as a recoverable backup *and* surfaced to the body, so a move-back re-renders the original fields. The cue lives in the **top chrome line** (Option A). And the move **is exposed to MCP** (`move_item_type`) so Claude can retype with the same reconciliation.
4. **Surfacing writes through `updateItem`,** so a body change snapshots a revision (the pre-move state stays restorable) and refreshes `body_text`. A move with no orphaned properties changes only `type` (no body write, no revision — trivially reversible).
**Why / alternatives:** *Silently keep orphaned props in jsonb only* — rejected by Brandon: functionally fine but "lost to me," can't see/copy/edit them. *Clear orphaned props after surfacing* — rejected; retain gives both the safety net and a clean move-back. *Compute orphaned from all jsonb keys* — rejected; would dump system keys (`locked`, `recurrence`) into the body. Reconciling only the source type's declared properties is the correct boundary. *Overload `update_item` MCP to accept `type`* — rejected; a dedicated `move_item_type` with a `dryRun` preview is clearer and keeps the reconciliation in one place.
**Verified (dev-auth preview + prod DB):** cue renders on the full page ("Trash · Note"), no console errors; actions menu shows "Change type…"; dialog opens with the current type excluded; dry-run preview matches; a throwaway Event→Note move surfaced `location: Test Hall` as a YAML block at the top of the body, retained `location` in jsonb, set `type=note`, then cleaned up.
**Affects:** new `src/components/canvas/TypeCue.tsx`, `src/components/canvas/ChangeTypeDialog.tsx`, `src/app/api/items/[id]/move-type/route.ts`; edits to `src/components/canvas/ItemCanvas.tsx`, `src/components/canvas/Modal.tsx`, `src/app/@modal/(.)items/[id]/page.tsx`, `src/components/canvas/ItemActionsMenu.tsx`, `src/lib/items.ts` (`moveItemType` + `MoveTypeSummary` + YAML helpers; new `relations`/`ne`/`or` imports; dynamic `getType` import to dodge the items↔types value cycle), `src/lib/mcp/tools.ts` (`move_item_type`). No migration. Reversible: remove the dialog/menu entry + endpoint + MCP tool; the cue is independent.

## ADR-133: Planner — read-only calendar overlay (plan tasks around what's already scheduled)
**Date:** 2026-06-29
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, built). **Not core — solo-movable.** Adds a read query over the existing `calendar_events` cache, an additive `ViewDisplay.showCalendar` flag (same nullable `views.display` jsonb from ADR-131, no migration), and UI. The **calendar provider seam is untouched** — no new Graph fetch, no new scope — so the frozen-core "calendar provider interface" line doesn't trip. This realizes the parked **Planner slice 5** (the busy/overlay half) and `explorations/calendar-time-blocking.md` option 2 ("Ledgr-native calendar view overlay").
**Context:** Brandon: when planning work on the Planner (month grid or multi-day time-grid), he wants to *see what's already on his calendar* so he can schedule tasks around it — and that overlay should be a toggle available on any calendar view, not just the Planner. Calendar events are already in Ledgr: `runCalendarSync` (ADR-023/094) mirrors Microsoft Graph events into the `calendar_events` cache (real-instant `start_at`/`end_at`, `meta`, `is_cancelled`, deduped on `ms_event_id`), and `listCalendarFeed` already reads the *un-promoted* feed for `/events`. So the overlay is a render problem, not an integration problem.
**Decision.**
1. **Source = the `calendar_events` cache, not `event`/`meeting` items.** New `listCalendarEventsForRange(ownerId, start, end)` (`src/lib/calendar/feed.ts`) returns **all** non-cancelled events in a window — promoted *and* un-promoted — because the overlay is the *whole* calendar to plan around, not just the items that have been added into Ledgr. Owner-scoped, index-backed (`calendar_events_feed_idx`), body-free.
2. **Resolve to app-tz day + wall-clock on the server.** Events are real instants; tasks place on UTC-midnight calendar days + a floating `HH:MM` (ADR-008/091). The helper emits each event as an `OverlayEvent { id, title, ymd, start, durationMinutes, location }` with `ymd`/`start` already formatted in `APP_TIMEZONE`, so the client grids bucket and position events with no timezone math. **All-day is inferred** (starts at local midnight + whole-day duration) since the synced `meta` doesn't carry Graph's `isAllDay`; a rare midnight timed event lands in the all-day band, which is acceptable.
3. **Read-only, never interactive.** Overlay blocks carry no drag handlers and never PATCH. In the time-grid they're `pointer-events-none` and painted behind the task blocks, so a task can still be dropped onto the slot underneath an event. Styled muted with a sky (`#38bdf8`) left bar to read as "calendar, not task," distinct from the accent-colored task chips.
4. **A toggle on any calendar view.** A session toggle ("Show calendar") in `PlannerCalendar` (off by default, persisted to `localStorage` `planner:showCalendar`, mirroring the existing `showUnscheduled` pattern), **seeded from** an additive per-view `ViewDisplay.showCalendar` so a saved calendar view can default it on. Pages that render a *writable* calendar (`/planner`, the `/tasks` Planner tab, and `/views/[id]` when the date property is scheduled/due/plan) fetch the window with the pure `overlayWindow(month)` helper and pass `calendarEvents` through `ViewRenderer` → `PlannerCalendar` → the grids. Fetch is server-side and unconditional on those pages (one cheap indexed query), so toggling is instant with no refetch.
**Why / alternatives:** *Overlay the synced `meeting` items by `meeting_at`* (the original slice-5 sketch) — rejected; that only shows events promoted into Ledgr, missing the rest of the calendar, which defeats "plan around what's there." Reading the cache shows everything. *A client fetch behind the toggle* — rejected; adds an API route + loading state + client tz logic for no gain over a cheap server query. *Add `isAllDay` to the sync meta now* — deferred; the midnight heuristic is good enough and avoids a re-sync to backfill. *Write blocks onto the real Outlook calendar* — out of scope (read-only stays the default; would need a new Graph write scope, see the time-blocking exploration).
**Constraint to note:** the overlay only reaches as far as calendar sync has pulled. The sync window `DEFAULT_WINDOW_DAYS` was bumped 14 → **28** (`sync.ts`) to give the overlay a 4-week planning horizon (Brandon, 2026-06-29); beyond that the grid shows no events and `PlannerCalendar` renders a one-line "no synced events in this range" hint when the toggle is on and the window is empty. The meeting-import feed (`listCalendarFeed`) is **bounded to 2 weeks** (`FEED_WINDOW_DAYS`) so the wider cache doesn't lengthen its suggestion list — the two horizons are intentionally decoupled. (Hard-deleted *future* events that Graph stops returning linger in the cache as ghosts until they age out of the date window; this pre-existing behavior now spans 4 weeks instead of 2. Cancellations are still detected — Graph returns them flagged.)
**Verified (dev-auth preview, prod DB):** month grid shows muted sky-bordered events with time prefixes ("9:30 AM Mike Pick-up") + a "+N events" overflow above the task chips; multi-day grid positions 18 timed event blocks at their real times, all `pointer-events: none`; the "Show calendar" toggle sits beside "Show unscheduled"; no console or server errors.
**Affects:** new `src/lib/calendar/overlay.ts` (`OverlayEvent` type + `overlayWindow`), `src/lib/calendar/feed.ts` (`listCalendarEventsForRange`); `src/lib/views.ts` (`ViewDisplay.showCalendar` + `DISPLAY_DEFAULTS` + `parseDisplay`); `src/components/views/ViewRenderer.tsx`, `src/components/planner/{PlannerCalendar,PlannerMonth,PlannerTimeGrid}.tsx`; `src/app/planner/page.tsx`, `src/app/tasks/page.tsx`, `src/app/views/[id]/page.tsx`; plus the window bump in `src/lib/calendar/sync.ts` (`DEFAULT_WINDOW_DAYS` 14 → 28) and the feed bound in `src/lib/calendar/feed.ts` (`FEED_WINDOW_DAYS`). No migration. Reversible: drop the prop + the toggle; the read helper has no other callers.

## ADR-134: Cross-device edit guard — optimistic body-conflict detection + refresh-on-focus
**Date:** 2026-06-30
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, built). **Touches core** (the machine/REST API contract: a new optional request field, a new 409 outcome, a new read route), so logged here; the change is **purely additive and back-compatible** — a caller that sends nothing behaves exactly as before. Heads-up to Tyler in `COLLAB.md`.
**Context:** Ledgr's body autosave is a debounced `PATCH /api/items/:id` carrying the **whole** body markdown, and `updateItem` was an unconditional last-write-wins overwrite with **no version check**. So the real lost-update Brandon flagged: open a meeting on device 1, edit the body on device 2, then (without reloading device 1) type on device 1 — device 1's stale full-body PATCH silently clobbers device 2's work, with no indication anything had changed. Custom properties already merge per-key (ADR-069 `propertyPatch`), so the wholesale-overwrite fields — **body** (and title) — were the exposed surface. The safety net (revisions, ADR snapshots) is timing-dependent (5-min debounce), so it can't be relied on to recover the clobbered version.
**Decision.** Two independent, complementary pieces:
1. **Content-based optimistic guard on the body write (the correctness fix).** The body editor remembers the markdown it last *synced* with (a `syncedBodyText` ref, distinct from the on-open dedup baseline) and sends `expectedBodyDigest` — a short, dependency-free non-crypto digest (`bodyDigest` in `src/lib/body.ts`, djb2-xor, length-tagged, pure so client and server agree) of that synced body — alongside each guarded body PATCH. `updateItem` refuses the write with `ItemError("conflict")` → **409** when a *real* body write carries a digest that no longer matches the stored body. **Content-based on the body specifically, NOT `items.updated_at`,** on purpose: it ignores sibling writes to status/properties/title on the same item, so editing a field on one device never trips a false body conflict on another (an `updated_at` token would). The phantom on-open re-emit is a no-op (`writeBody` false) and never reaches the check, so opening an item can't conflict — only a genuine body change does. The digest is omitted by MCP, batch ops, and the field-only writers, so they keep last-write-wins untouched.
2. **The 409 is surfaced, never silent.** On a 409 the editor latches a global `conflict` state (extended `save-status.ts`) and stops auto-retrying (a retry would just 409 again), holding the pending body. The canvas's one `SaveStatusIndicator` shows a banner with **"Keep mine"** (re-send without the token — an informed overwrite; the other version is still in revision history) and **"Reload."** So the worst case is now an explicit, recoverable choice rather than silent data loss.
3. **Refresh-on-focus (the "no indication" fix).** When the canvas tab regains visibility/focus, `SaveStatusIndicator` re-reads the new lightweight `GET /api/items/:id/version` (`getItemVersion` — one `updated_at`, no body, owner-scoped) and, if it moved past what this canvas last saw, shows a dismissible "Updated on another device — Reload" banner. The baseline lives in `save-status.ts` (`knownVersion`), seeded at mount and advanced by every successful body save (exact, from the PATCH response) plus a `localSaveSinceSync` flag that absorbs the canvas's *own* writes so a refocus right after editing never reads your own change as remote. One tiny request per refocus, gated on `document.visibilityState`, so an idle tab costs nothing. No polling interval (a single user physically switches devices; focus is the signal).
**Why / alternatives:** *`If-Match`/`updated_at` optimistic token* — rejected as the body mechanism: every sibling control on the canvas (status, due, priority, properties) bumps `updated_at`, so a per-surface token would false-409 against your *own* device's field edits unless all ~12 hand-rolled writers refreshed it; content-hashing the body sidesteps that entirely. *Realtime sync (SSE / WebSocket / Postgres LISTEN-NOTIFY)* — rejected: long-lived connections fight Vercel's serverless model and it's a heavy dependency for a single user (principles 5, 8). *CRDT / Yjs co-editing* — rejected: large dependency for a problem that is "two stale tabs," not live multi-cursor. *Rely on revisions to recover clobbers* — rejected as the primary fix: it's a timing-dependent backstop, and "silently lose then maybe restore" is worse than "detect and ask."
**Scope boundary (defer-by-hiding):** the hard guard covers the markdown body editor (`ItemEditor` — notes/tasks/meetings, the scenario). Chord/Paper bodies (`useItemAutosave`) don't send the token yet; they advance the focus baseline on save (so no false stale banner) and rely on the refresh-on-focus alert, not the hard guard. Title clobber (both devices editing the title) stays last-write-wins, covered by the focus banner. Both are reasonable v1 boundaries; extending the token to them is additive later.
**Verified:** `scripts/verify-concurrent-edit.mts` against live Neon (throwaway owner, cleaned up) — `bodyDigest` determinism/sensitivity/format-agnosticism; matching digest writes; stale digest → 409 with the stored body untouched; resynced digest writes; no-token = last-write-wins; identical-body PATCH with a stale token is a safe no-op; `getItemVersion` returns `updated_at` and is owner-scoped. Plus the full HTTP round-trip in the dev-auth preview against a scratch note (since the Tiptap canvas doesn't hydrate under dev streaming): device-2 write 200 → device-1 stale guarded write **409, body preserved** → "Keep mine" (no token) **200, overwrites**; the `/version` route returns 200. tsc + eslint clean.
**Affects:** `src/lib/items.ts` (`ItemError` gains `"conflict"`; `ItemPatch.expectedBodyDigest`; the guard in `updateItem`; new `getItemVersion`), `src/lib/api.ts` (409 mapping), `src/lib/body.ts` (`bodyDigest`), `src/lib/item-input.ts` (parse `expectedBodyDigest`), `src/lib/save-status.ts` (conflict state + force-save registry + focus baseline), `src/components/markdown-editor/ItemEditor.tsx`, `src/components/canvas/SaveStatusIndicator.tsx` (+ props from `ItemCanvas.tsx`), `src/components/chord-editor/useItemAutosave.ts`; new route `src/app/api/items/[id]/version/route.ts`; new `scripts/verify-concurrent-edit.mts`. No migration (uses existing `items.updated_at`). Reversible: the request field and 409 are additive; reverting the client stops sending the token and the server falls back to last-write-wins.

## ADR-135: Multi-select on related panels + meeting "Open tasks" on the lens system
**Date:** 2026-06-30
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, built). **Not core** — UI/view-rendering layer only: the view engine (`queryViewItems`/`ViewFilter`) is untouched, no schema/migration, no machine-API change. Solo-movable.
**Context:** PR #129 gave every related-type group on an item ("Linked here") the owner's chosen **lens** (the type's saved lenses/views rendered through the shared `ViewRenderer`). Brandon flagged two gaps when viewing a **meeting**: (1) the lens treatment didn't reach the tasks he actually works from there, and (2) there was no multi-select on those tasks. Root cause on (1): a meeting's tasks mostly surface in the **"Open tasks"** panel (`MeetingPrep`), which is **rule-pulled** (tasks related to the event's people, or by tag — ADR-094 E4), not directly related to the meeting — so it rendered through a bespoke client list (`PrepTaskList`) with an old lightweight sort/filter bar, bypassing the lens path entirely. On (2): even "Linked here" (`RelatedGroupView`) called `ViewRenderer` **without** `selectable`, so the multi-select standard (ADR-118 — "every list surface") had an unintentional gap across all related panels.
**Decision.** Three reuse-first moves, no new rendering machinery:
1. **`ViewLensBody` becomes the one selectable view-body**, gaining an optional `rowActions` pass-through. It already wrapped `ViewRenderer` in `SelectionProvider` + `SelectModeToggle` + `BulkActionBar` (gating board/calendar out per ADR-118); adding `rowActions` lets the related panels reuse it verbatim instead of calling `ViewRenderer` directly.
2. **`RelatedGroupView` routes through `ViewLensBody`** and takes an optional `bulkConfig`. A related group is always one type, so the caller passes that type's **full** `bulkConfigForType` (status/date/select + Move + Delete) — richer than a mixed surface's Move+Delete. `RelatedPanel` resolves each group's `typeDef` and hands down its config; a type that fails to resolve renders read-only. The leading select checkbox and the trailing relation controls (un-relate, @-marker) **coexist** in the list/table layouts.
3. **Meeting "Open tasks" joins the lens path** via a new `resolveProvidedGroup(rows, typeKey, lens, hideCompleted)` (`related-views.ts`): it renders an **already-resolved** row set (membership decided by the pull rule, not a `ViewFilter`) through the same `ViewLensData` shape, applying the lens's order **in memory** (`sortInMemory`, mirroring the engine's nulls-last rules; `mostLinked` keeps the rule's order since a body-free row carries no relation count). `MeetingPrep` then renders the standard `CanvasSection` ("Open tasks" + the existing `TaskPullControl`) with the lens picker in the section's action slot and `ViewLensBody` for the rows. `PrepTaskList` is deleted (fully replaced).
**Why / alternatives:** *Restrict the Open-tasks picker to SORT lenses* (not view lenses) — chosen deliberately: a saved **view** lens carries its own `filter`, and applying that filter to a rule-chosen set would silently drop tasks the rule deliberately pulled in; a view lens's `relatedTo` wouldn't even match (these tasks relate to the *people*, not the meeting). Sort lenses contribute order only, which composes cleanly. *Add an `ids`/multi-`relatedTo` filter to `ViewFilter`* so the rule-pull rides the real query engine — rejected: that's a change to the shared/core view engine (both-agree + ADR) for what is a presentation need; in-memory sort of an in-hand, body-free, capped row set is cheap and keeps this solo. *One panel-wide `SelectionProvider` with mixed-type Move+Delete config* — rejected: each related group is single-type, so per-group providers give the richer, type-appropriate bulk actions Brandon wants for tasks (set status, reschedule); the floating bar only appears for the group you're selecting in. The Open-tasks lens choice shares the `(event:task)` key with any Linked-here task group, so "how I view this meeting's tasks" stays one setting.
**Verified:** dev-auth preview against the prod DB on a real meeting ("Brandon/Roger Check-in", 21 pulled tasks): the Open-tasks panel shows the **Lens** picker (Recent/Newest/A→Z/Most linked — view lenses correctly excluded) + a **Select** toggle (off by default, ADR-121); switching to "A→Z" re-sorts the rows alphabetically and persists; entering select mode reveals 21 row checkboxes and the floating bar (**Set… → Status To Do/Done/Archived + Due date + Scheduled date, Move…, Delete, Clear**). The "Linked here" Person group shows its own Select toggle, and a row carries **both** the select checkbox and the un-relate (✕) control. Clean reload = exactly two toggles, both off. No console/server errors; tsc + eslint clean.
**Affects:** `src/components/lists/ViewLensBody.tsx` (`rowActions`), `src/components/relations/RelatedGroupView.tsx` (→ `ViewLensBody`, `bulkConfig`), `src/components/relations/RelatedPanel.tsx` (per-group `bulkConfigForType`), `src/lib/related-views.ts` (`resolveProvidedGroup` + `sortInMemory`/`sortKey`), `src/components/meetings/MeetingPrep.tsx` (Open tasks → lens path + multi-select); deletes `src/components/meetings/PrepTaskList.tsx`. No migration. Reversible (UI wiring only). **Scope boundary (defer-by-hiding):** Open tasks stays the `list` layout (rule-pulled rows don't need board/calendar); board/calendar layouts remain non-selectable per ADR-118.

## ADR-136: Calendar feed + event timeline as bespoke lenses; unify events onto `/list/event`
**Date:** 2026-07-01
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, built). **Core-adjacent** — extends the shared `Lens` union (`list-lenses.ts`, first defined ADR-105) with two new *kinds*, which is shared code both instances use, so it gets an ADR + a `COLLAB.md` heads-up to Tyler. But the two new kinds' **bodies and defaults are event-module internals** (Microsoft calendar adapter + the event timeline), enabled only for the `event` type; no schema/migration, no view-engine or machine-API change. Solo-movable in practice.
**Context:** The calendar-import feature (browse upcoming Outlook meetings, click **Add** to pull each into Ledgr as an `event` to take notes on — ADR-094 E3) went missing from Brandon's view. Root cause was a **routing split** the lens era introduced, not a deletion: the feed + the Upcoming/Past/No-date timeline lived only on the bespoke `/events` page (which had **no** lens tab strip), while the destination picker (`nav-slot-options.ts`) mapped the `event` type to the *generic* `/list/event` page (which had lenses but **no** feed). Navigating to "Events" landed on the lensed page and the feed silently fell out of view. Two divergent events pages was the real problem.
**Decision.** Unify onto the generic `/list/event` page (Brandon's call over keeping two pages) and make the two event surfaces **lenses**:
1. **Two bespoke lens kinds** on the shared `Lens` union — `{kind:"calendar"}` (the un-promoted upcoming feed + one-click **Add**, external data) and `{kind:"timeline"}` (the Upcoming/Past/No-date grouping by `meetingAt`). Both carry only `id`+`label` (no sort/source); the list page branches on `kind` to pick the body. Neither is expressible as a sort or view lens (external data / bespoke grouping), which is why they earn their own kinds rather than riding `view`.
2. **`defaultLenses(typeKey?)` is now type-aware:** `event` gets `[Calendar, Timeline, Recent, Newest, A→Z, Most linked]` (Calendar default/leftmost); every other type keeps the four generic sorts unchanged. Hiding/reordering is the ordinary Build → Types tabs editor (`ListTabsEditor`), which also offers an **"Event views"** group to re-add Calendar/Timeline after removal, and resets to the event defaults.
3. **The generic list page** (`/list/[type]`) fetches `listCalendarFeed` for the calendar lens (with an empty state, since it's the default landing) and the meeting-time-ordered split for the timeline lens (wrapped in the standard `SelectionProvider`/`SelectModeToggle`/`BulkActionBar`). The feed + timeline rendering moved out of the retired page into `CalendarFeed`/`EventTimeline` components + a shared `event-format.ts`. The bespoke `/events` route becomes a `redirect("/list/event")` (defer-by-hiding, not deleted) and `ListTabs` points events at `/list/event` (tab key aligned to the type key `event`, mirroring `person`).
**Why / alternatives:** *Just fix nav to re-point at the bespoke `/events`* — rejected by Brandon; leaves two divergent pages and keeps lenses off events. *Rebuild the feed/timeline as saved **view** lenses instead of new kinds* — the calendar feed reads external `calendar_events` (not `items`), so no `ViewFilter` can express it; the timeline's Upcoming/Past grouping is bespoke. New kinds are the honest model. *Let bespoke lenses flow into related panels* — rejected: a calendar feed or timeline inside a host item's "Linked here" makes no sense, and `event` is now the first default lens (so it would become the related-group default). Fixed with `relatedLensCandidates()` — related panels offer/​default to **sort + view lenses only** — and `resolveRelatedGroup` defaults a stray bespoke lens to `updatedAt desc` instead of asserting non-null.
**Verified:** dev-auth preview against the prod DB. `/list/event` strip reads **Calendar · Timeline · Recent · Newest · A→Z · Most linked**, Calendar active by default, showing 12 real upcoming events each with **Add**; Timeline lens renders Upcoming/Past; `/events` redirects to `/list/event`; Build → Types → Event shows the six event defaults and the re-addable "Event views" options; `/list/person` still shows only the four generic sorts (no leak). No console/server errors; tsc + eslint clean.
**Affects:** `src/lib/list-lenses.ts` (union + `defaultLenses(typeKey)` + `relatedLensCandidates` + parse), `src/app/list/[type]/page.tsx` (kind branches), `src/components/calendar/CalendarFeed.tsx` + `src/components/events/EventTimeline.tsx` + `src/lib/event-format.ts` (extracted bodies), `src/app/events/page.tsx` (→ redirect), `src/components/lists/ListTabs.tsx` (events → `/list/event`), `src/components/build/ListTabsEditor.tsx` (badges/describe/reset/re-add), `src/components/relations/RelatedPanel.tsx` + `src/lib/related-views.ts` (bespoke-lens guards). No migration (lenses live in `users.settings.listTabs`). Reversible.

## ADR-137: AI Memory — a `memory` type + always-on "stumps" + `remember`, read over MCP, behind a setting
**Date:** 2026-07-01
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, built; **Tyler pre-cleared** — a `COLLAB.md` heads-up pairs with this). **Core** — it extends the machine/MCP API contract (two new tools + one resource) and adds a cross-cutting owner setting, so it takes an ADR + both-agree. The `memory` type itself is a bespoke type (not a schema change), and everything else reuses existing libs (items/relations/views/settings), so the surface area is small.
**Context:** Brandon wanted his AI's memory to live in **his** system, not a provider's, so it's portable across AI vendors and unifies with everything else Ledgr holds. The design (worked out in-session) landed on a two-layer model: tiny always-on **stumps** (an index the assistant carries each session) over deep, **linked** memories pulled on demand — where Ledgr's existing relation graph is the serendipity engine (a memory about a person is a doorway into everything related to that person). Key sub-decisions: keep it *deterministic* (the AI decides what to remember; no model in the plumbing); make the whole thing opt-in so a plain MCP client is unchanged; and let recall follow the graph with judgment rather than a fixed depth.
**Decision.** Five reuse-first pieces:
1. **A `memory` item type** (migration `0040_memory_type.sql` + `seed.mjs`, additive `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`). Bespoke, `hidden=true` — so it's out of every Work surface, the destination picker, and the generic MCP `list_types` (an AI/system concern, like `unmarked`), while `getType` still renders `/list/memory` and Build → Types (`includeHidden`) still lets the owner add their own properties on top. Built-in properties: `kind` (user|feedback|project|reference), `horizon` (evergreen|seasonal|episodic), `pinned` (checkbox). "About" links use the **universal** relations, not a typed relation field, so a memory can point at a person *and* a project *and* a note.
2. **Two gated MCP tools** (`src/lib/mcp/tools.ts`): `get_memory_stumps` (body-free index — id/title/kind/horizon/pinned + up to 4 linked neighbours via the batched `relatedSummaryFor`; default returns the always-on set, `includeAll` the whole store) and `remember` (one call: create the memory + set the facets + link `about` ids). `getMemoryStumps` lives in a new `src/lib/memory.ts`, shared with the Build page. Reads/writes go through the same `queryViewItems`/`createItem`/`relateItems` as the rest of the app.
3. **A `memory-protocol` MCP resource** (`ledgr://guide/memory-protocol`, `guide.ts`): the recall rule and write conventions written once so any connected AI follows them.
4. **A master setting `aiMemoryEnabled`** (default **off**, `users.settings` jsonb). Off ⇒ `listToolDefs`/`callTool` filter the two tools, `resources/list`+`resources/read` hide the protocol, and the Build sidebar drops the entry — a vanilla MCP client sees nothing. A toggle in User Settings; `listToolDefs` became owner-aware (async) to gate.
5. **A Build → AI Memory surface** (`/build/memory`, MAINTAIN, labelled to read as an AI/maintenance tool, not Work). Shows the live stump index (always-on vs pull-only) and links to `/list/memory` for full CRUD (generic list + multi-select for free). Gated: off ⇒ an enable prompt; the sidebar entry is hidden via a new `gatedBy` field on `BuildEntry`, threaded `Nav → NavShell → BuildSidebar`.
**Recall model (in the protocol resource): a rising bar, not a hop cap.** Follow a link only when it may change what you'd say/do; the bar rises with each hop out; relevance outranks distance; stop at diminishing returns. Chosen over a fixed "≤N hops" so a rich trail can run long while a cold one is refused early.
**Why / alternatives:** *Store memories as local Markdown files* (the built-in memory feature) — rejected as the deep store: flat files have no relation graph, which is the whole point; kept only as the model for orphan working-preferences, which gain nothing from links. *A `SessionStart` hook that queries Ledgr* — deferred: the stump read is one cheap body-free call at session start, cached thereafter, and Ledgr-direct works identically on every device (phone included) with no per-machine cron or sync; a local cache is a later optimization if session-start latency ever bites. *A typed relation field for "about"* — rejected: typed fields lock to one target type; universal relations let a memory link anything. *A hard hop limit for recall* — rejected for the rising-bar heuristic (more serendipity, still bounded). *Show the memory type in normal type lists* — rejected: `hidden=true` keeps it out of Work while staying editable in Build and browsable at `/list/memory`. *Episodic facts as memories* — discouraged in the protocol: a one-time event is better as an ordinary linked item; memories are the durable distillations.
**Verified:** `tsc --noEmit` clean; `verify-mcp.mts` updated for the async `listToolDefs(ownerId)` and asserts the memory tools are **absent** for a settings-less owner (gating on by default-off). Full end-to-end (toggle on → tools/resource appear, `remember` writes a linked memory, `get_memory_stumps` returns it, Build page renders) pending the verify phase; the additive migration is applied to prod on Brandon's explicit go (local env = prod DB).
**Affects:** new `drizzle/0040_memory_type.sql`, `scripts/seed.mjs` (type row); new `src/lib/memory.ts`; `src/lib/settings.ts` (`aiMemoryEnabled`); `src/components/settings/SettingsForm.tsx` (toggle); `src/lib/mcp/tools.ts` (2 tools + owner-aware gating), `src/lib/mcp/server.ts` (await + resource gate), `src/lib/mcp/guide.ts` (protocol resource); `src/lib/build-nav.ts` (`gatedBy` + entry), `src/components/nav/{BuildSidebar,NavShell,Nav}.tsx` (thread the flag); new `src/app/build/memory/page.tsx`; `scripts/verify-mcp.mts`. Reversible: the setting defaults off (feature invisible); the type row is additive and its items soft-delete like any other. **Scope boundary (defer-by-hiding):** no local stump cache, no `remember`-by-name create-on-miss (link by id for now), and the power-user surfaces (destination picker, command palette, `describe_workspace`) still list the Build entry when the feature is off — only the sidebar doorway + the tools/resource/page are gated. All additive later.

### ADR-137 addendum (2026-07-02) — AI Memory improvements: activation + hygiene
**Status:** accepted (Brandon-directed, built). Additive-only within the existing ADR-137 contract; **Tyler heads-up in `COLLAB.md`** (touches the MCP instructions/resource text, still gated behind `aiMemoryEnabled`, no new tool/schema/protocol-version). Follows a review of the subsystem: the design was sound but had an activation gap and no maintenance loop.
**Decision.** Four reuse-first changes:
1. **Owner-aware connect-time instructions.** `server.ts` gains `buildInstructions(ownerId)`; `initialize` now returns the base `INSTRUCTIONS` plus a short **memory addendum** (call `get_memory_stumps` at session start, file with `remember`, read the protocol resource) **only when `aiMemoryEnabled`**. This is the fix that actually gets the feature used: the connect-time instructions are the one surface every MCP client reliably shows the model, whereas tool descriptions are only read once a tool is under consideration and resources are rarely fetched unprompted. When AI Memory is off, the instructions are **byte-identical** to before (verified), so a vanilla client is unchanged.
2. **A "Maintain the store" section in the memory protocol** (`guide.ts`): update-over-duplicate (check loaded stumps before filing a near-duplicate; `update_item` the existing one), enrich links with `relate_items`, touch a still-true seasonal memory to keep it always-on, correct-in-place / flag-for-owner-removal (no silent drops), and prefer few dense memories over many thin ones. Closes the write-only gap — the protocol taught *when to remember* but never *how to revise*.
3. **Per-horizon aging windows** (`memory.ts`): the single 45-day always-on window split into `seasonal: 45` / `episodic: 10` (evergreen/pinned still never age). "A moment" now actually ages faster than "a while."
4. **`remember` partial-link hardening**: new exported `assertOwnedItems(ownerId, ids)` (one batched owner-scoped existence check) validates every `about` id **before** the memory is created, so a bad/hallucinated id fails the whole call instead of leaving a memory created-but-unlinked.
**Also:** a one-off live-data fix — the seeded memory titled `Trellis &amp; Vine…` had a double-escaped ampersand in its title (stored literally as `&amp;`); corrected to `Trellis & Vine…` via `update_item` (revision snapshotted). The seed source is a one-off loader outside the repo, so there was no in-repo source to fix; the other 20 titles were clean.
**Explicitly deferred (defer-by-hiding):** AI-initiated retirement (a `forget` tool / MCP soft-delete) — the protocol's "flag it to the owner" path stands until it proves annoying; aging-by-recall (touch on pull); automated consolidation + a Build-page "always-on set is large" nudge; and (unchanged from ADR-137) the local stump cache / SessionStart hook. The privacy angle (a per-memory pull-only/quiet flag so sensitive memories stay searchable but never auto-load) was **declined** as overbuilding, consistent with ADR-075.
**Gating boundary (recorded on purpose):** toggling AI Memory off hides the tools, the protocol resource, the instructions addendum, and the sidebar doorway — but existing `memory` items remain reachable via the generic `search_items`/`get_item` (they're ordinary hidden-type items). "A vanilla client sees nothing" is a statement about the memory *tools/resource*, not about filtering the type out of generic search; data-level hiding was not added.
**Verified:** `tsc --noEmit` + eslint clean; `verify-mcp.mts` extended (now covers: instructions omit the addendum when off / gain it when on; memory tools gated; `remember` rejected when off; a bad-`about` `remember` errors and creates **no** memory; the happy path links + `get_memory_stumps` returns it always-on with its neighbour; seasonal survives 11 days while episodic ages out but stays visible via `includeAll`) — **ALL PASS** on the dev Neon branch.
**Affects:** `src/lib/mcp/server.ts` (`buildInstructions` + memory addendum), `src/lib/mcp/guide.ts` (Maintain section), `src/lib/memory.ts` (per-horizon windows), `src/lib/relations.ts` (`assertOwnedItems`), `src/lib/mcp/tools/memory.ts` (pre-validate `about`), `scripts/verify-mcp.mts`. No schema, no migration, no new tool, no protocol-version change, no new dependency.

## ADR-138: Project Type & widget-composed homepages — PJ1: containment + activity log
**Date:** 2026-06-29
**Status:** accepted
**Context:** Tyler's last open v1.0 goal — a Project type that's a hub for tasks/notes/meetings. The PRD (`ledgr-project-type-prd.md`) reframes it as the first adopter of a universal capability: **Types become widget-composed**, where the same widget runs in two scopes (unscoped on a Dashboard, bound to the current record on a Type page). CORE (touches `items`/`relations`/`types`, the type/canvas model, a new platform layer); Brandon agreed to proceed (2026-06-29). Tyler expanded scope: the composable homepage is a per-type capability, not Project-only. Decisions resolved with Tyler: reuse the existing dashboard widget engine (record page = a dashboard focused on the record) not the canvas_layout field grid; Digest ships push-first (outbound email isn't built); fresh installs default the project status_schema to Planning/Active/On Hold/Done while Tyler keeps his Todoist buckets. Built as a slice series **PJ1–PJ11**, one PR each (the E/TPL/T precedent). This entry covers **PJ1** (the spine: containment + the activity log); later PJ slices append their own notes here.
**Decision (PJ1):**
1. **`relations.home boolean not null default false`** + a partial unique index `relations_one_home_per_source_uq ON (source_id) WHERE home`. The containment residence bit from PRD §1: on a child→parent edge, `home=true` is the child's primary residence; `home=false` is surfaced-elsewhere. Orthogonal to `role` (what kind of edge) and `match_state` (trusted vs suggested); the `(source,target,role)` unique is unchanged. "A note is still a note" — containment is purely this edge, no per-parent schema fork. A record has at most one home parent (the partial unique). Default false leaves every existing edge (tags, mentions, typed relation fields, the existing `task→project` edge) untouched and non-home.
2. **Containment via relations, not `parent_id`.** `parent_id` stays reserved for subtasks + recurrence occurrences (schema.md §10). A Project contains tasks/notes/meetings/milestones/typed records through home edges. New `setHome(ownerId, child, parent, role="contains")` (tasks keep `role="project"`); `relateItems` gains an optional `{home}`; both clear any prior home edge first so the invariant holds. `homeParentOf()` resolves the single home parent.
3. **`activity_events` table** (+ `activity_kind` pgEnum) — the append-only, owner-scoped log the PRD calls its most important table; Recent Activity, the Digest, and the Story weave all read from it. Subject = the record narrated (a project); actor = what triggered it (a completed task) when distinct. Indexed `(subject_id, occurred_at)`, `(owner_id, occurred_at)`, and a partial `WHERE kind='checkin_reviewed'`. `subject_id` cascades on delete (purge stays complete); `actor_id` SET NULL.
4. **Emission in the server write paths** (`src/lib/activity.ts` + `items.ts`/`relations.ts`, best-effort/never breaks a save): `record_created` (tracked types), `status_changed` (a tracked record's own status, payload from/to), `task_completed` (a contained item moving to the done category, on its tracked home parent), `task_added`/`note_added`/`milestone_added`/`record_related` (containment via `setHome`). A "tracked subject" is `isTrackedSubjectType` = `project` for now (pursuit + Digest-on types join later). **Inbox items with no tracked home parent log nothing** — keeps the log a project narrative, not a global firehose.
5. **`last_reviewed_at` is derived** (max `occurred_at` of `checkin_reviewed`, served by the partial index), not a column; `reviewCheckin()` writes the event and resets the staleness clock the Digest (PJ7) keys off.
**Why / alternatives:** *Reuse the dashboard engine over extending canvas_layout* — the dashboards engine already models the PRD's "same widget two scopes" via `focusItemId`/`applyFocus`, so a record page is a focused dashboard with no widget-side Type-branching; canvas_layout's cards are fields of one item (wrong granularity, no query/focus). *`home` as a boolean not a `home|referenced` enum* — it's one bit; boolean default-false is migration-cheap and avoids a pgEnum extension later. *`activity_kind` as pgEnum (vs text like `status`)* — activity kinds are a closed, code-owned vocabulary, so an enum gives the narrator switch compile-time exhaustiveness. *Derive `last_reviewed_at`* — matches Ledgr's derive-don't-store discipline (ADR-109 plan-date). *Don't log inbox-task completions* — the log is a container narrative; logging homeless items would make it a firehose.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-containment.mts` 11/11 + `scripts/verify-activity-log.mts` 13/13 on live Neon (home set/move/invariant, Related panel carries home, containment activity on tracked-only parents, owner-scoping; record_created/status_changed/task_completed emission gated correctly, checkin resets the derived clock, newest-first). `verify-relations`/`verify-items`/`verify-recurrence` regress green; tsc/eslint/`next build` clean. Migration 0034 applied to Neon.
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts` (`activity_kind` enum, `relations.home` + index, `activity_events` table), `drizzle/0034_solid_leech.sql`, new `src/lib/activity.ts`, `src/lib/items.ts` (emission in createItem/updateItem), `src/lib/relations.ts` (`setHome`/`clearHomeEdges`/`relateItems({home})`/containment emission + `home` in the Related select), `scripts/verify-containment.mts` + `scripts/verify-activity-log.mts`. Merged to main (2026-06-29; Tyler dropped the both-agree merge gate for this chunk — Brandon agreed to proceed).

### PJ2 (2026-06-29) — record base fields + project status default
**Decision:** `items.next_action_task_id` (uuid → items, ON DELETE SET NULL) + `items.next_action_text` (the record's single pinned next step — a task pointer that auto-advances on completion, or free text); `items.composition` jsonb (Layer 3 per-record widget override, null = inherit) + `types.default_widgets` jsonb (Layer 2 per-type default composition). All three `items` columns ride `itemColumns` (getItem only, never lists). New `initialStatusKey(schema)` (`src/lib/status.ts`): a new item prefers the schema's first explicitly-default NON-terminal status, so a type whose working default is `in_progress` (a Project's Active/Ongoing) starts there instead of a `not_started` bucket; `createItem` uses it (task/note unchanged). Project status (migration 0035 data step): fresh/unused instances adopt the PRD §5 default **Planning/Active/On Hold/Done**; in-use instances keep their buckets but the category-mapping bug is fixed (working status `not_started`→`in_progress`). Non-destructive + idempotent; `seed.mjs` default updated.
**Why / alternatives:** *Next Action as columns* — the PRD puts it on the base; it's hot and a free-text variant has no edge home. *Project status keep-vs-replace* — resolved with Tyler: new users get the generic PRD states, existing users keep their buckets (mapping fixed); `NOT EXISTS project items` + `@> ongoing` guards discriminate without clobbering a customized schema. *`archived`* — deferred to Brandon's `items.archived_at` axis (PJ7), not forked.
**Verification:** `scripts/verify-record-base.mts` 18/18 on Neon; `verify-statuses`/`verify-items`/`verify-project`/`verify-views` regress green; tsc/eslint/`next build` clean. Migration 0035 applied. (Fixed a pre-existing dev-DB drift: the project type's `property_schema` had been emptied — restored repo/liveurl/stack per 0031.)
**Affects:** `src/db/schema.ts`, `drizzle/0035_overrated_warpath.sql`, `src/lib/items.ts`, `src/lib/item-input.ts`, `src/lib/status.ts`, `scripts/seed.mjs`, `scripts/verify-record-base.mts`.

### PJ3 (2026-06-29) — widget registry + composition layers + home-scoped queries
**Decision:** New pure, client-safe `src/lib/widgets.ts` — the `WidgetDefinition` catalog (PRD §6, 14 widgets: overview/status/tasks/notes/meetings/milestones/relatedRecords/links/people/mindmap/nextAction/progress/recentActivity/timeline) with `kind`/`requires`/`cardinality`/`scope`/`options`/`recordQuery`, plus **Layer-1 derived availability**: `availableWidgets(type)` returns the WHOLE catalog for every type by construction (every `requires` key is satisfiable — universal base properties + universal containment + global log/relations), so a new Type inherits the catalog with zero widget authoring.
